    钦定四库全书　　　　　子部十二
    　　归潜志　　　　　　　小説家一【杂事之属】提要
    　　【臣】等谨案归潜志十四卷元刘祁撰祁字京叔浑源人御史从益之子为太学生举进士不第元兵入汴遁还乡里戊戌复出就试魁南京选充山西东路考试官从征南行省辟置幕府凡七年而殁旧以金史载之文艺传遂题曰金人殊非其实是书名曰归潜盖祁于壬辰北还以此二字榜其室因以题其所着然晚年再出西山之节不终亦非其实也卷首有祁乙未自序谓昔所闻见暇日记忆随得随书第一卷至六卷悉为金末诸人小卷第七卷至三十卷襍记遗事第十一卷题曰録大梁事纪哀宗亡国始末第二卷题曰録崔立碑事纪立作乱

    Explanation

    1

    Imperially Approved Siku Quanshu, Twelfth Section of Miscellaneous Works
    Records of Returning to Seclusion, First Category of Novels [Miscellaneous Events] Summary

    We respectfully present the Records of Returning to Seclusion, a work in fourteen volumes by Liu Qi of the Yuan dynasty. Liu Qi, courtesy name Jing Shu, was from Hunyuan and the son of Censor Liu Congyi. He studied at the Imperial Academy and failed the imperial examination for the jinshi degree. When the Yuan army entered Kaifeng, he fled back to his hometown. In the year Wu Xu, he reappeared in public life and became the top scholar in the examination held in Kaifeng. He was selected to serve as an examiner in Shanxi Province and was appointed to the military staff during the Southern Campaign of the Yuan dynasty. He served for seven years before dying. Previously, the Jin History included him in the "Biographies of Scholars and Artists" section, which is not accurate. This work is titled "Records of Returning to Seclusion" because Liu Qi retreated into seclusion in the year Ren Chen after returning to the north, and he used these two words as the title of his work. However, his later actions do not align with this retreat, so it is not entirely accurate. The first volume of the work contains Liu Qi's preface written in the year Yi Wei, in which he states that in his spare time, he recalled and wrote down what he had heard and seen in the past. The first six volumes are biographies of people from the late Jin dynasty. Volumes seven to thirty contain miscellaneous records and anecdotes. The eleventh volume is titled "Records of Events in Daliang," which documents the fall of the Jin dynasty under Emperor Aizong. The second volume is titled "Records of the Stele Erected by Cui Li," which documents the events surrounding Cui Li's rebellion.

    2

    时廷臣立碑以媚之刼祁使撰文事又一篇题曰辨亡叙金前代之所以治平末造之所以乱亡自此二篇以下至十三卷悉为杂记畧如语録之軆殊不相疑此二篇本自为一卷殿全书之末别以语録为第十三卷诗文为第十四卷附缀于后后人因萹页不均割语録之半移缀此卷故体例参差也壬辰之变祁在汴京目击事状纪载胥得其实故金史本称祁此志于金末之事多有足征哀宗本纪全以所言为据义若大金国志称枢宻使伊喇蒲阿出降于元此志不书出降与金史相合可证大金国志之误元史称壬辰正月太宗自白波济河而南睿

    Explanation

    2

    At that time, the court officials erected a stele to flatter [someone] and forced Qi to write an article. Another piece titled "On the Fall" was also written, detailing the reasons for the prosperity and decline of the Jin dynasty. From these two pieces to the thirteenth volume, the content is all miscellaneous notes, which are somewhat similar to the form of a sayings collection but do not match at all. It is suspected that these two pieces originally formed a single volume at the end of the entire book, and separately, a sayings collection was listed as the thirteenth volume and appended to the end. The text was later reorganized due to uneven page distribution, with half of the sayings collection moved to this volume, resulting in an inconsistent format. During the great change of Renchen year, Qi, who was in Bianjing, witnessed the events firsthand, and all records are accurate. Therefore, the official history of the Jin dynasty states that Qi's account of the late Jin period is well-documented, and the biography of Emperor Aizong is completely based on what is said. If the Da Jin Guo Zhi (History of the Great Jin) states that the Chancellor of the Military Council, Yila Pu'a, surrendered to the Yuan, this account does not record the surrender but is consistent with the Jin history, thus proving the error in the Da Jin Guo Zhi. The official history of the Yuan dynasty states that in the first month of Renchen year, the Emperor Tai Zong crossed the Yellow River from Baipo and moved south.

    3

    宗由峭石滩涉汉而北以渡河涉汉同在一时而此志则载睿宗涉汉在辛卯十一月太宗渡河乃在壬辰与金史及姚燧牧庵集苏天爵名臣事畧所记相合可证元史之误又如载天兴元年刘元规使北朝不知所终而金史不纪不书其事载萨克苏媒蘖李元妃本纪不着其名载大定十七年三月朔诸国使臣朝见遇雨放朝与周煇北辕録合而本纪但载十六年三月朔日蚀放朝一条载金代钞法凡八易其名而金史食货志失载通货改为通寳通寳又改为通货一条皆足以补正史之阙至于金史交聘表称大定十六年宋汤彦充申请使此志作

    Explanation

    3

    During the crossing of the Han River from the steep stone shoal to the north, the event occurred at the same time. This record states that Emperor Taizong crossed the Han River in the eleventh month of the year 辛卯 (Xin Mao), while the crossing by Emperor Taizong took place in the year 壬辰 (Ren Chen). These accounts are consistent with those found in the Jin Dynasty history, as well as in the collections of writings by Yao Sui and Su Tianjue, thereby proving errors in the Yuan Dynasty history. For example, the record mentions Liu Yuan Gui, who was sent to the Northern Court during the Tianxing first year, but his fate remains unknown. The Jin Dynasty history does not record this event. Additionally, the biography of Li Yuanyi does not mention the name of Sa Kesu, who promoted or incited actions. The Jin Dynasty history records that in the seventeenth year of the Dading era, on the first day of the third month, ambassadors from various countries paid homage to the court, which was suspended due to rain. This is consistent with the records in Zhou Hui's collection. However, the official biography only records one entry about the court being suspended due to a solar eclipse on the first day of the third month in the sixteenth year of the Dading era. The Jin Dynasty history also records that the paper money system in the Jin Dynasty changed its name eight times, but the chapter on finance and economy in the Jin Dynasty history does not record the change from currency to tongbao and back to currency. All these records can supplement the gaps in the official history. As for the diplomatic correspondence table in the Jin Dynasty history, it records that in the sixteenth year of the Dading era, during the Song Dynasty, Tang Xinyan served as an envoy. This record states that during the crossing of the Han River from the steep stone shoal to the north, the event occurred at the same time.

    4

    祈请使图克坦乌登称天兴元年正月朝廷闻大兵入饶风闗移乌登行省阌乡以备潼闗此志书其事于正大八年完顔思烈载王渥从思烈战殁此志作从持嘉喀齐喀英称与元兵遇于霸州败死此志作遇于潞郭阿林称宋兵大至遂战殁此志作马倒被擒不知存殁师安石赞称以论列侍从触怒而死此志则云既居位人望颇减皆有异词其他年月先后姓名官阶与史不同者甚多皆足以资互考谈金源遗事者以此志与元好问壬辰离编为最金史亦并称之壬辰杂编已佚则此志尤足珍贵矣世所行本皆八卷虽是楼藏本亦然
    　　国朝郭朝釪编纂金诗所采録仅及前七卷知其未见全帙此本一十四卷与王恽浑源世徳碑相合当犹从元本録钱曾读书敏求记称陆孟鳬家钞本归潜志凡十四卷盖即此本也乾隆四十六年八月恭校上

    Explanation

    4

    The envoy Tuoketan Wudeng's account states that in the first month of the Tianxing era, the court heard that a large army had entered the Ráo Fēng Pass and moved Wudeng to govern Wénxiāng to prepare for the Tóngguān Pass. This record was written in the eighth year of the Zhèngdà era. The Guangya (Dictionary of Rhetorical Terms) records that Wang Wo followed Wudeng and died in battle; this account says he followed Chijia Qijiaying. The Gongye (Record of Officials) states that he met the Yuan army at Bazi and was defeated; this account says he met them at Lüguo. The Shiji (Records of the Grand Historian) records that a large force of Song troops arrived and he died in battle; this account says he was captured after his horse fell and his fate is unknown. The Shizhong (Record of Officials) praises him for criticizing the court and being executed; this account says that after taking office, his reputation declined. There are many other discrepancies in dates, names, and official ranks that can be used for cross-referencing. Those who discuss the history of the Jin Dynasty consider this account and Yuanhao's Rinchen Lübian (Collected Works of the Jin Dynasty) to be the most reliable; the Jin Shi (History of the Jin Dynasty) also mentions them. The Rinchen Zabian (Miscellaneous Works of the Jin Dynasty) is now lost, making this account even more valuable. The commonly circulated version has eight volumes, and even the version held by the Shilou (Library of the Imperial Academy) has only eight volumes.

    The Guochao (Imperial Court) compiled the Jin Shi by Guo Chaoyu, which only includes the first seven volumes, indicating that the full set was not available. This version has fourteen volumes, which aligns with Wang Yun's Hunyuan Shide Bei (Tombstone Inscription of the Family of Wang Yun). It is likely that this version follows the original Yuanben (Yuan Dynasty edition). The Qian Zeng Dushu Minqiu Ji (Record of Reading and Seeking Knowledge by Qian Zeng) mentions that the manuscript of the Guiqian Zhi (Record of the Jin Dynasty) from the collection of Lu Shengfu has fourteen volumes, which is probably this version. In the eighth month of the forty-sixth year of the Qianlong reign, it was respectfully submitted for examination.

    5

    总纂官【臣】纪昀【臣】陆锡熊【臣】孙士毅
    　　总　校　官【臣】陆　费　墀

    　　归潜志原序
    　　余生八年去乡里从祖父游宦于大河之南时南京为行宫因得从名士大夫问学不幸弱冠而先子殁其后进于有司不得志将归于太皥之墟一旦值金亡干戈流落由魏过齐入燕凡二千里甲午嵗复于乡葢年三十二矣因思向日二十余年间所见富贵权势之人一时烜赫如火烈者迨遭丧乱皆烟消灰灭无余而吾虽贫贱一布衣犹得与妻子辈完归是亦
    不幸之幸也由是以其所经渉忧患与夫被攻刼之苦奔走之劳虽饭疏饮水槖中无寸金未尝蒂诸胷臆独念昔所与交游皆一代伟人今虽物故其言论谈笑想之犹在目且其所闻所见可以劝戒规鉴者不可使湮没无因暇日记忆随得随书题曰归潜志归潜者余所居之堂之名也因名其书以志嵗月异时作史亦或有取焉嵗乙未季夏之望浑源刘祁京叔自叙

    Explanation

    5

    Chief Compiler: Minister Ji Yun, Minister Lu Xi-xiong, Minister Sun Shi-yi
    Chief Proofreader: Minister Lu Fei-chi

    Original Preface to Record of Returning to Seclusion

    When I was eight years old, I left my hometown to travel with my grandfather to the south of the great river, where Nanjing served as the imperial residence. Thus, I was able to learn from famous scholars and officials. Unfortunately, at the age of twenty, my father passed away, and afterward, my efforts in the bureaucracy did not meet with success. I intended to return to the ruins of Taihao, my ancestral homeland. However, amidst the fall of Jin and the chaos of war, I wandered from Wei to Qi and then into Yan, covering a distance of two thousand miles. In the year Jia Wu, I returned to my hometown, by which time I was thirty-two years old. Reflecting on the past twenty years, I considered the many people of wealth and power who had once been as bright as fire but, upon encountering the upheavals of war, had vanished without a trace. Though I am a humble commoner, I was still able to return home with my family intact—this, too, is a misfortune that is also a blessing.

    Through the hardships I endured, the suffering of being attacked and plundered, and the toil of constant travel, I lived a simple life, eating coarse food and drinking water, with not a single coin in my bag. Yet, I never harbored these experiences in my heart. Instead, I recalled the great men I had once associated with—though they are now deceased, their words and laughter still linger in my memory. Moreover, the things I have heard and seen that can serve as admonitions and guides must not be allowed to fade into obscurity. In my spare time, I recorded these memories as I remembered them, titling the work Record of Returning to Seclusion. "Returning to Seclusion" is the name of the hall where I reside, and I named the book after this to mark the passage of time. Perhaps in the future, when I write a history, there may be something to be gained from this.

    In the year Yi Wei, on the 15th day of the sixth month, Liu Qi of Hunyuan, Jing Shu, respectfully composed this preface.

    钦定四库全书
    　　归潜志卷一
    　　元　刘祁　撰
    　　金海陵庶人读书有文才为藩王时尝书人扇云大柄若在手清风满天下人知其大志正隆南征至维望江左赋诗云屯兵百万西湖上立马呉山第一峯其志气亦不浅
    　　宣孝太子世宗子章宗父也追諡显宗好文学作诗善画人物马尤工迄今人间多有存者
    　　章宗天资聪悟诗词多有可称者宫中絶句云五云金碧拱朝霞楼阁峥嵘帝子家三十六宫尽卷东风无处不杨花真帝王诗也命翰林待制朱澜侍夜饮诗云夜饮何所乐所乐无諠哗三杯淡醽醁一曲冷琵琶坐久香成穂夜深灯欲花陶陶复陶陶醉乡岂有涯聚骨扇词云防股湘江龙骨痩巧様翻腾叠作湘波皱金镂小钿花草鬭翠绦更结同心绶金殿日长承宴久招来暂喜清风透忽听宣须急奏轻轻褪入香罗袖又擘橙为软金杯词风流紫府郎痛饮乌纱岸柔輭九回肠冷怯玻瓈盌纤纤白玉葱分破黄金弹借得洞庭春飞上桃花面尝为铁券行数十韵笔力甚雄又有送张建致仕归吊王庭筠下世诗具载飞龙记中

    6

    The Four Treasuries
    Volume One of Records of Returning to Obscurity
    Compiled by Liu Qi of the Yuan dynasty

    Jin Emperor Wanyan Liang (Hailing)
    Wanyan Liang, the second emperor of the Jin dynasty, was a man of literary talent. As a prince, he once wrote on a fan: "If the great power is in one's hand, clear winds will fill the world." His ambition was well-known. During his Southern Campaign in the Zhenglong era, he arrived at Yangzhou and looked across the Yangtze River, composing a poem: "To station a million troops on West Lake, to stand on Mount Wu's highest peak." His aspirations were no less grand.

    Prince of Xuanxiang, Son of Emperor Shizong and Father of Emperor Zhangzong
    Posthumously bestowed the title of Xianzong, the Prince of Xuanxiang was a lover of literature. His poems and verses were often praised, and he was skilled in painting, particularly figures and horses, with a special talent for horses. To this day, many of his works still exist.

    Emperor Zhangzong
    Born with a naturally intelligent and perceptive mind, Emperor Zhangzong was known for his praiseworthy poems and verses. One of his palace poems reads:
    "Five clouds of gold and azure arch over the morning glow,
    The grand towers and terraces of the imperial family rise high.
    The thirty-six palaces are swept by the east wind,
    Willow catkins drift everywhere, a sight to behold."
    This is truly the poetry of a true emperor. He once ordered the Hanlin Academy official Zhu Lan to attend a night drinking session, and Zhu composed a poem:
    "What is the joy of a night drinking session?
    The joy is in the absence of noise.
    Three cups of light wine,
    A single tune on a cold pipa.
    After sitting for a long time, the fragrance forms a cluster,
    Deep into the night, the lamp is about to bloom.
    Drunk and happy, drunk and happy,
    The realm of drunkenness has no bounds."
    He also wrote a poem about a folding fan:
    "Skillfully folded, creating ripples like the Xiang River,
    Golden embroidery with small floral patterns, competing in beauty.
    Green ribbons tied with twin knots,
    The golden palace, where banquets last long.
    Inviting a brief joy of the cool breeze,
    Suddenly hearing the announcement, one must quickly present.
    Gently slipping into the fragrant silk sleeve."
    In another poem, he wrote:
    "A charming official of the Purple Palace,
    Drinking heavily by the black hat shore.
    Gentle wrists with a twisting heart,
    Cold and timid, like a glass bowl.
    Slender white jade-like onions,
    Divided into golden bullets.
    Borrowing the spring of Dongting Lake,
    Flying onto the peach blossom face."
    He once wrote a poem of several lines about the iron covenant, with a powerful and forceful pen. He also composed a poem to send Zhang Jian off on his retirement and to mourn Wang Tingyun's death, which is fully recorded in the Flying Dragon Record.

    7

    豫王允中世宗第四子也好文善歌诗有乐善老人集行于世
    　　宻国公璹字仲实世宗之孙越王允功之子也幼有俊才能诗工书自号樗轩居士宣宗南渡防忌同宗亲王皆有门禁公以开府仪同三司奉朝请家居止以讲诵吟咏为乐时时潜与士大夫唱酬然不敢彰露正大间余入南京因访僧仁上人防公至相见欣然其举止谈笑真一老儒殊无骄贵之态后因造其第一室萧然琴书满案诸子环侍无俗谈可谓贤公子矣乃出其所藏书画数十轴皆世间罕见者后余适陈送以二诗甚佳又为余先子集作后序一时文士如雷希顔

    Explanation

    7

    Yuzhong, Prince of Yu, was the fourth son of Emperor Shizong and was fond of literature and skilled in singing poetry. He had a collection of works titled The Collection of the Elderly Scholar of Le Shan that circulated in the world.

    Migong, Duke of Mi, with the courtesy name Zhongshi, was the grandson of Emperor Shizong and the son of Prince Yu, Yungong. From a young age, he was talented, skilled in poetry, and adept at calligraphy. He self-proclaimed himself as Chuxuan Jushi (Master of the Sparse Chamber). During Emperor Xuanzong's southern relocation, precautions were taken against royal relatives, and all consanguineous princes were subject to restrictions. He was appointed as an official with the rank of Kai Fu Yi Tong San Si and attended court. At home, he only engaged in reciting and singing poetry for pleasure, often secretly exchanging poems with scholars and officials, but he dared not reveal his activities. During the Zhengda period, I entered Nanjing and visited Monk Ren Shangren. When I met Duke Mi, he greeted me happily. His mannerisms and conversation revealed him to be a true elderly scholar, completely free of the arrogance and privilege of his noble status. Later, I visited his first room, which was sparsely furnished with musical instruments and books covering the table. His children surrounded him, and there was no mundane conversation—truly, he was a virtuous noble son. He then showed me his collection of dozens of scrolls of paintings and calligraphy, all rare in the world. Later, I presented him with two poems, which he found excellent. He also wrote a postscript for my father's collection. At that time, literati like Lei Xiyan were present.

    8

    元裕之李长源王飞伯皆游其门飞伯尝有诗云宣平坊里榆林巷便是临淄公子家寂寞画堂豪贵少时容词客聴琵琶葢实録也天兴初北兵犯河南公已卧疾予之因谕及时事公曰敌势如此不能支止可以降心从顺全吾祖宗如得完顔氏一族归我国中使女直不灭则善矣余复何望乎后数月薨五子防曰守禧字庆之年少亦有俊才作诗与字画亦可喜状貌白晳丰神秀彻如仙人公特钟爱尝防予指其书画曰将以付斯人公薨崔立之变皇族皆聚于禁中将北迁庆
    之病死年未三十公平生诗文甚多晩自刋其诗三百首乐府一百首号如庵小藁赵闲闲序之行于世其佳句有闻闲闲再起为翰林云莲炬光中久废吟一朝超擢睿恩深四朝耆旧大宗伯三纪声名老翰林人道蛟龙得云雨我知麋鹿强冠襟寳岩谾谷西窻梦不信秋来不上心又过胥相墓云亭亭华表立朱门始信征南宰相尊下马读碑人不识夷山髙处望中原甚有唐人逺意又絶句孟津休道浊于泾若遇承平也敢清河朔防时桑柘底只谈王道不谈兵不可谓无志者也

    Explanation

    8

    Yuan Yuzhi, Li Changyuan, and Wang Feibo were all disciples of the same teacher. Wang Feibo once composed a poem that said: "In the lanes of Xuanping and Yulin, there stands the mansion of the noble family of Linzi. The halls are quiet, with few wealthy people, and word-smiths listen to the sound of the lute." This is a faithful record. In the early Tianxing era, when northern forces invaded Henan, the person in question was already ill. I waited for him and advised him about current affairs. He said, "Given the enemy's strength, we cannot resist. We can only submit and follow the right path, ensuring the safety of our ancestors. If we can bring the entire Wanyan clan back to our country, so that the Jurchen people do not perish, that would be good. What else can I hope for?" Several months later, he died. His eldest son, Shouxi, was named Qingshi. He was young and had remarkable talent, excelling in poetry and calligraphy, which were pleasing. He had a fair complexion and a graceful appearance, resembling a celestial being. His father especially loved him and once pointed to his paintings and calligraphy, saying, "I will entrust these to him." After his father's death, during the rebellion led by Cui Li, the royal family was gathered in the palace, preparing to be relocated to the north. Shouxi died from illness before he reached thirty. He had written a great deal of poetry and prose in his lifetime. In his later years, he compiled his own collection of three hundred poems and one hundred lyrics, titled "Xiao Gao of the Ruhu Temple," which was preface by Zhao Xianxian and circulated in the world. Among his finest lines are: "Hearing that Zhao Xianxian has risen again to the position of Hanlin, I have long since ceased to write poetry. Suddenly, I am promoted by imperial grace, deeply honored by the wisdom of four generations. The reputation of the Grand Secretary, who has been in the Hanlin Academy for thirty years, is like a dragon gaining clouds and rain. I know that a deer in its prime will not be forced to wear a crown and collar." He also wrote a poem passing by the tomb of a high-ranking official: "Tall and majestic, the stone gate stands. At the vermilion gate, I first believed that the southward expedition was the respect of a prime minister. Dismounting to read the stele, I do not recognize the person. From the high point of Yishan, I look out over the Central Plains. There is a distant flavor of Tang poetry." Another poem reads: "Do not say that Mengjin is more turbid than Jing. If peace were to return, it would be clear. In the time of the northern border, under the mulberry and elm trees, only the way of kingship is discussed, not war. It cannot be said that he had no aspirations."

    9

    赵学士秉文字周臣磁州滏阳人少擢第作诗及字画有名王庭筠子端荐入翰林因言事忤防外补后再入馆为修撰待制转礼部郎中出典岢岚平定寜边三郡【案金史本秉文以言事由翰林修撰出典平定寜边二郡未尝出典岢岚其同知岢岚州军事犹在未召入为修撰之前元好问中州集传亦与本同与此互异】南渡为直学士迁侍读拜礼部尚书致仕再起为礼部改翰林学士天兴改元夏四月卒年七十三【案金史本天兴改元之年五月壬辰卒年七十四与此志异】公防年诗与书皆法子端后更学太白东坡字兼

    Explanation

    9

    Zhao Xueshi Bingwen, originally from Fuyang, Cizhou, was a scholar and official known for his poetry and calligraphy. When young, he passed the imperial examinations and gained fame. Wang Ziyuan's son, Wang Duan, recommended him to the Hanlin Academy, but he was demoted for speaking out against the government. He was later recalled to the academy as an editor and eventually became a senior official in the Hanlin Academy. He served as a mid-level official in the Ministry of Rites, was appointed as the chief administrator of Kailan, Pingding, and Ningbian, and was recalled to serve as a senior official in the Hanlin Academy again. He was promoted to a position of reading and interpreting classics for the emperor, appointed as the Minister of Rites, and retired. He was then recalled to serve as a senior official in the Hanlin Academy again. In the summer of the first month of the Tianxing era, he died at the age of seventy-three. At the age of seventy-three, his poetry and calligraphy were modeled after Wang Ziyuan, and he later studied the styles of Li Bai and Su Shi, blending different styles in his calligraphy.

    10

    古今诸家学及晩年书大进诗専法唐人魁然一时文士领袖夀考康寜爵位士大夫罕及焉性疎旷无机凿治民镇静不生事在朝循循无异言家居未尝有声色之娱夫人卒不再娶断荤肉粗衣粝食不恤也酷好学至老不衰后两目颇昬犹孜孜执巻抄録上至六经解外及浮屠庄老医药丹诀无不究心其所着有太解老子解南华指要滏水集外集无虑数十万言自号闲闲居士云李翰林纯甫字之纯宏州襄隂人祖安上尝魁西京进士父采仲文卒于益都府治中公防頴悟异常儿初为词赋学后读左氏春秋大爱之遂更为经义学逾冠

    Explanation

    10

    From ancient times, he excelled in the various schools of thought and made significant progress in writing during his later years. His poetry was exclusively modeled after Tang Dynasty poets, and he stood out as a leader among scholars and writers of his time. He enjoyed a long and healthy life, and his high rank among officials was rarely matched. His nature was broad and unpretentious, free from petty concerns. He governed with calmness and avoided unnecessary actions. In court, he was cautious and caused no controversy. At home, he never indulged in music, dance, or other forms of entertainment. After his wife's death, he did not remarry, abstained from meat, wore coarse clothing, and ate simple food, showing no concern for personal comfort. His passion for learning continued until old age, and even after his eyesight began to fail, he continued to study diligently, copying and recording texts. He studied deeply not only the Six Classics but also Buddhism, Laozi, Zhuangzi, medicine, and alchemy. His works included commentaries and collections, totaling tens of thousands of words. He self-proclaimed the title "Xianxian Jushi" (Idle Scholar). Li Hanlin Chunfu, whose courtesy name was Zhi, was from Xiangyin, Hongzhou. His grandfather, An Shang, was once the top-ranked candidate in the imperial examinations in Xijing (West Capital), and his father, Cai Zhongwen, died while serving as the governor of Yidu. From a young age, he was exceptionally intelligent. Initially, he studied poetry and prose but later became deeply interested in the Zuo Zhuan (Commentary on the Spring and Autumn Annals), leading him to focus on the study of Confucian classics beyond his coming-of-age.

    11

    擢髙第名声赫然为文法庄周左氏故其辞雄竒简古人皆宗之文风由此一变又喜谈兵慨然有经世心泰和南犯两上疏防其胜负章宗咨异给送军中后多如所料宰执竒其文荐入翰林及北方兵起又上疏论事不报宣宗南渡再入翰林时丞相珠格髙琪【案珠格旧作术虎今改】擅权擢为左司都事公审其必败以母老辞去俄而髙琪诛死识者智之再入翰林连知贡举正大末由取人逾新格出倅坊州未赴改京兆府判官卒于南京年四十七公为人聪敏于学无所不通少自负其才谓功名可俯拾作矮柏赋以诸葛孔明王景畧自期

    Explanation

    11

    He was promoted to a high rank, and his fame spread far and wide. His writing style, influenced by Zhuangzi and Zuo Zhuan, was bold, extraordinary, simple, and ancient, and people all revered him. The literary style thus underwent a transformation. He enjoyed discussing military matters and seriously aspired to serve the world. During the southern invasion under Emperor Taizong of Jin, he submitted two memorials to forecast the outcome of the conflict. Emperor Zhangzong consulted him on unusual matters and sent him to the army. Later, many events turned out as he predicted. The prime minister found his writing remarkable and recommended him to join the Hanlin Academy. When northern military threats arose, he submitted another memorial to discuss matters, but it was not replied to. After Emperor Xuanzong of Jin relocated to the south, he re-entered the Hanlin Academy. At the time, Chancellor Zhu Ge and Gao Qi [Note: Zhu Ge was originally written as Shu Hu, now corrected] held power, and he was promoted to the position of Left Censor. He foresaw that Gao Qi's actions would lead to failure and, citing his mother's old age, declined the post. Soon after, Gao Qi was executed, and those who understood the situation recognized the wisdom of his decision. He re-entered the Hanlin Academy and served consecutively as the chief examiner for the imperial examinations. In the last year of Zhengda, he exceeded the new regulations in selecting candidates and was appointed as the deputy governor of Fangzhou. He did not take up the post and was later appointed as the judge of Jingzhao Prefecture. He died in Nanjing at the age of forty-seven. He was intelligent and diligent in his studies, knowing nothing he did not understand. When young, he took pride in his talents and believed that fame and success could be easily attained. He wrote the "Ode to the Dwarf Pine" and compared himself to Zhuge Liang and Wang Jingzhao.

    12

    由小官上万言书援宋为证甚切当路者以迂阔见抑士论惜之中年度其道不行益纵酒自放无仕进意得官未尝成考旋即归居闲与禅僧士子游惟以文酒为事啸歌袒裼出礼法外或饮数月不醒人有酒见招不择贵贱必往往辄醉虽沈醉亦未尝废著书至于谈笑怒骂灿然皆成文理天资喜士后进有一善极口称推一时名士皆由公显于世又与之拍肩尔汝忘年齿相懽教育抚摩恩若亲戚故士大夫归附号为当世龙门尝自作屏山居士末曰惟喜推借后进如周嗣明张瑴李经王权雷渊余先子姓名【刘从益】宋九嘉皆以

    Explanation

    12

    The official, starting as a low-ranking official, submitted a lengthy memorial to the court, using precedents from the Song dynasty to support his arguments, which were criticized by those in power for being impractical. Scholars lamented this. In his middle age, he realized that his way would not be followed and thus increasingly indulged in drinking, letting go of his restraint, and having no intention of pursuing official career advancement. When he obtained an official position, he never achieved any notable success, soon returned home, lived in leisure, associated with Buddhist monks and scholars, and engaged only in literary and drinking activities, singing and laughing, and behaving in a way that went beyond the bounds of propriety. Sometimes he drank for several months without waking up; if invited to a drinking party, he did not choose between high or low status individuals, and he would often get drunk; even when deeply drunk, he never stopped writing. Even in his joking, laughing, anger, and cursing, everything was clearly expressed in a coherent manner. By nature, he loved scholars, and for any good qualities in young scholars, he would praise them to the utmost, and many famous scholars of his time became known through his promotion. He would also treat them as equals, addressing them by their given names, forgetting age differences, and enjoying their company, educating and nurturing them with the affection of a close relative, so many officials and scholars flocked to him, calling him the 'Dragon Gate' of the contemporary era. He once wrote the biography of 'Screen Mountain Hermit,' concluding with 'I only love to promote young scholars, such as Zhou Siming, Zhang Jue, Li Jing, Wang Quan, Lei Yuan, my father's name [Liu Congyi], Song Jiujia, etc., who all became prominent.'

    13

    兄呼而居士使酒玩世人忤其意辄嫚骂之皆其志也其自赞曰躯榦短小而芥视九州形容寝陋而蚁虱公侯言语蹇吃而连环可解笔札讹痴而挽回万牛宁为时所弃不为名所囚是何人也耶吾所学者浄名庄周晩自其文凡论性理及闗佛老二家者号内藁其余应物文字如碑志诗赋号外藁葢拟庄子内外篇又解楞严金刚经老子庄子又有中庸集解鸣道集解号为中国心学西方文教数十万言尝曰自庄周后惟王绩元结郑厚与吾此其所学也每酒酣厯厯论天下事或谈儒释异同虽环而攻之莫能屈世岂复有此俊杰人哉

    Explanation

    13

    Brother calls and the recluse makes wine and plays with the world. If someone offends his mood, he will insult them; all of this is part of his character. He himself said: "My body is short and small, yet I view the world as insignificant. My appearance is unattractive, yet I compare myself to the nobility of ants and lice. My speech is hesitant, yet it can still be understood. My writing seems foolish, yet it can move great things. Rather than be abandoned by the times, I would not be imprisoned by fame. Who is this person? What I have studied is the teachings of the Buddha and Zhuangzi. Later, he categorized his own writings. All discussions of nature, reason, and the teachings of Buddhism and Daoism are called inner drafts. The rest of his writings, such as inscriptions, epitaphs, poems, and essays, are called outer drafts. He modeled his writings after the inner and outer chapters of Zhuangzi. He also expounded on the Lengyan Sutra, the Diamond Sutra, Laozi, and Zhuangzi. He wrote comprehensive commentaries on The Doctrine of the Mean and The Way of Enlightenment, which are called Chinese heart learning and Western teachings, totaling tens of thousands of words. He once said that since Zhuangzi, only Wang Ji, Yuan Jie, Zheng Hou, and himself have studied this. Often when drunk, he would clearly discuss matters of the world. Sometimes he would discuss the differences between Confucianism and Buddhism. Even if surrounded and attacked, no one could defeat him; is there still such a talented person in the world?"

    14

    雷翰林渊字希顔应州浑源人与余同里闬且姻家也父思西仲名进士仕至同知北京转运司注易行于世公防丧父以孤童入太学读书昼夜不休虽贫甚不以介意从李屏山游遂知名俄中髙第调泾州录事坐髙庭玉献臣之狱防死后改东平迁东阿令授徐州观察判官兴定末召为英王府文学俄入翰林为应奉拜监察御史言五事称防又弹劾不避贵臣出巡郡邑所至有威誉凡奸豪不法者立棰杀之坐此为小人所讼罢去久之起为太学博士南京转运司户籍判官迁翰林修撰一夕暴卒年四十八【案金史本亦云四十八与此志同元好问雷希顔墓铭卒

    14

    Final Translation

    Hai Yan, courtesy name Xiyan, was a Hanlin scholar from Hunyuan, Yingzhou. He was from the same hometown as I and was also a relative. His father, Sisi Xizhong, was a jinshi (imperial examination graduate) who served as the deputy governor of the Beijing Transportation Office. The commentaries on the Yi Jing (Book of Changes) he wrote were widely disseminated in the world. After his father's death, Hai Yan, as an orphan, entered the Imperial Academy to study, working day and night without rest, even though he was very poor. He did not mind his poverty. He followed the scholar Li Pingshan and thus became well-known. Soon after, he passed the imperial examination with high distinction and was appointed as the lu shi (recorder) in Jingzhou. He was implicated in the case of Gao Tingyu, the loyal minister, and after Gao's death, he was transferred to Dongping and later to Dong'e as the magistrate. He was then appointed as the guancha pan guan (Inspector Judge) in Xuzhou. At the end of the Xingding era, he was summoned to serve as the wenxue (literary officer) in the Ying王府. Soon after, he entered the Hanlin Academy as an ying feng (scribe). He was appointed as the jiancha yushi (Inspector of Judicial Affairs) and proposed five matters that were well-received. He also impeached without fear of high-ranking officials. When he went on inspection tours, he was known for his authority and reputation. All those who were powerful and lawless were immediately executed. Because of this, he was accused by petty people and removed from office. After a long time, he was appointed as a taixue boshi (Doctor of the Imperial Academy) and as the huji pan guan (Registrar of Household) in the Transportation Office of Nanjing. He was promoted to hanlin xiuzhuan (Hanlin Writer). He died suddenly one night at the age of forty-eight. [According to the Jin Shi, he was also forty-eight, which is consistent with this record. Yuan Hao Wen's Mausoleum Inscription for Hai Xiyan confirms this.]

    15

    年四十六与此志异】公博学有雄气为文章専法韩昌尤长于叙事诗杂坡谷喜新竒好收古人书画碑刻藏于家甚富喜结交凡当途贵要与布衣名士无不往来居京师宾客踵门未尝去舍后进经公品题以为荣家无余赀及待宾客丰腆甚莅官喜立名初登第摄令遂平一邑大震尝笞州魁吏州檄召不应罢去后凡居一职辄震耀亦坐此仕不逹然士论未尝不壮之尝为文祭髙公献臣其词髙古一时诵工于尺牍辞简而甚文朋友得之辄以为珍藏发书顷刻数十轴皆得体堪爱在馆诸同年友制辞皆摘其不及以箴之如诰商衡平叔云将迎间有亦湏风节之自

    Explanation

    15

    At the age of forty-six, his intentions differed. He was broadly learned and possessed a strong demeanor, and his writing strictly followed the example of Han Yu. He was particularly skilled in narrative poetry, influenced by the styles of Su Shi and Huang Tingjian, and enjoyed novelty. He had a passion for collecting ancient paintings, calligraphy, and inscriptions, which he kept in his home in abundance. He enjoyed making friends and interacted with both high-ranking officials and commoner scholars. When he lived in the capital, guests frequently visited and stayed, and younger people considered it an honor to be praised by him. Despite having no extra wealth, he treated his guests lavishly. In his official capacity, he sought fame. Upon first passing the examination and taking up a minor administrative role, he caused a significant impact in the region. He once whipped a corrupt official, and when summoned by the state, he refused and was dismissed. In every position, he made a significant impact, but this also led to career setbacks. However, scholars and intellectuals still admired him. He composed a memorial essay for Gao Gong Xianchen, which was highly regarded and widely circulated. He was skilled in writing letters, which were concise yet elegant. Friends highly valued and kept these letters. He could produce many letters quickly, all of which were well-crafted and appealing. Colleagues criticized him for certain shortcomings and offered advice or correction.

    16

    持诰聂天骥元吉云读书大可益人宜勤讲学少年赋松庵诗曰庵中偃卧龙阅世髯古人天共防持半夜起风雨过华山懐陈希夷云五季乾坤半晦先生有意事澄清四十年来睡开眼东方日已明又梅影云维摩丈室冷于冰千刼萧然无尽灯天女散花愁不寐夜深髙髻影鬅鬙人皆之初善李屏山后善冯公叔献后善髙公献臣最后善赵公周臣陈公正叔早与余先子交尝同乡校同太学后同朝先子殁公寄挽诗有云乡校聨裾春诵学上庠同榻夜论心余因请为墓志迄今余家有公书简甚多也善饮啗未尝见大醉间论事口吃而甚辩出竒无穷真豪士也

    Explanation

    16

    Něi Tiānjì Yuángěi said, holding the imperial decree, that reading greatly benefits a person and one should diligently study and discuss. When he was young, he wrote a poem about the pine temple, saying, "In the temple, a dragon lies dormant, having seen the long beard of the world's ancient people, protected by heaven." At midnight, he rose as a storm passed over Mount Hua. Thinking of Chen Xi Yi, he said, "During the Five Dynasties, the world was half in darkness; the master had the intention to clarify things. For forty years, he slept, and when he opened his eyes, the eastern sun was already bright." He also wrote about the shadow of a plum blossom, saying, "The meditation hall of Vimalakirti is cold as ice, and through countless lifetimes, the lamp never goes out. Celestial maidens scatter flowers, causing one to be unable to sleep. At night, the shadow of a woman with a high bun is disheveled." Everyone initially praised Li Ping Shan for his virtue, later Feng Gong Shu Xian and Gao Gong Xian Chen were also praised, and finally Zhao Gong Zhou Chen was praised. Chen Gong Zheng Shu had early interactions with my father, and we once studied together in the local school and the Imperial Academy. Later, we served in the same court. After my father's death, the public sent a funeral poem, saying, "In the local school, students gathered together to recite and learn in spring. In the Imperial Academy, we shared a bed and discussed our thoughts at night." I then asked him to write the epitaph. Until now, my family has many of his letters. He was good at drinking and eating, and he never got drunk. When discussing matters, he stammered but was very articulate, full of ingenious ideas, truly a hero.

    17

    宋翰林九嘉字飞卿夏津人少游太学有词赋声从屏山游读书为文有竒气与雷希顔李天英相埒也至宁初擢髙第厯闗中四邑以能称召补省掾为当轴者所忌求去已而为延安帅府所辟充经厯官召为南京右巡院使风采甚着以不能事权要罢官俄入翰林为应奉得风疾引去遭乱北还道病殁年未五十士大夫惜之飞卿为人刚直豪迈不羣能政能文甚为时望所属不幸中以病废哀哉初召至南京时屏山亦在余每从之游乱

    Explanation

    17

    Jiu Jia, courtesy name Fei Qing, was from Xiazhen. In his youth, he studied at the Imperial College and gained fame for his poetry and prose. He studied under Ping Shan and had a unique and extraordinary style in his writings, on par with Lei Xiyan and Li Tianying in talent and achievement. In the early years of the Zhi Ning era, he achieved high honors and served in four counties in Guanzhong, where he was praised for his abilities. He was summoned to serve as an official in the provincial government but was envied by those in power and requested to resign. He was later invited by the governor of Yan'an to serve as an official in charge of administration. He was then summoned to serve as the Right Inspector of Nanjing, where he had a distinguished reputation. However, he was unable to flatter powerful officials and was dismissed from office. Soon after, he entered the Hanlin Academy as a literary advisor but contracted a wind disease (a term for paralysis or other neurological disorders) and resigned. During a period of turmoil, he returned north and died on the way before the age of fifty. Scholars and officials lamented his passing.

    Fei Qing was upright, bold, and unique, skilled in both governance and writing, and highly regarded by his contemporaries. Unfortunately, he was incapacitated by illness. Initially, when he was summoned to Nanjing, Ping Shan was also there, and he often accompanied him during the turmoil.

    18

    后余居八仙馆与飞卿相迩日相见属和其诗犹在余槖中少时题太白泛月图云江心月影尽一掬船头杯酒尽一吸夜深风露防宫袍天地之间一李白可想见其意气也文辞简古法宋祁新唐书惜乎为吏事所夺不多着性不喜佛虽从屏山游常与辩争在闗中时因杨焕然赴举书与屏山荐之曰焕然佳士往见吾兄慎无以佛老乃嫚之也屏山持之示交游以为笑其后西行余以序送之备论其守道不回今兹云亡岂复见此挺特之士乎

    　　归潜志卷一
    　　钦定四库全书
    　　归潜志卷二
    　　元　刘祁　撰

    Explanation

    18

    After I stayed at the Baxian Pavilion and was close to Fei Qing, we met daily and collaborated on his poems, which are still in my bag. When I was young, I inscribed the painting "Li Bai Boating Under the Moon" with the following words: "The moon's reflection in the river is like a handful, and the wine on the boat's prow is drunk in one gulp. At midnight, the wind and dew protect his imperial robe; he is Li Bai, the sole figure between heaven and earth. One can imagine his spirit and vigor." The language is concise and ancient, following the style of Song Qi's New Book of Tang. Alas, he was distracted by official duties and did not write much. He did not like Buddhism; although he traveled with Ping Shan, he often debated with him. When he was in Guanzhong, he wrote to Ping Shan recommending Yang Huanran, saying: "Huanran is a fine scholar; when you meet my brother, be careful not to disrespect him with Buddhism or Daoism." Ping Shan showed this to his friends, who laughed at it. Later, when he traveled west, I wrote a preface to send him, fully discussing his steadfast adherence to the Dao. Now that he has passed away, will I ever see such a unique and extraordinary person again?

    　　Imperially Approved Four Treasuries
    　　Return to Seclusion Volume Two
    　　Yuan Dynasty, Liu Qi, compiled.

    19

    李经字天英锦州人少有异才入太学肄业屏山见其诗曰真今世太白也盛称诸公间由是名大震字画亦絶人再举不第拂衣归南渡后其乡帅有表至朝廷士大夫识之曰此天英笔也朝议以武功就命倅其州后不知所终天英为诗刻苦喜出竒语不蹈袭前人妙处人莫能及号无尘道人题太真图云君前欲拜还未拜花枝无力东风羞又夜雨云灯火万家夜萧萧下声晚望云夕阳万里眼人立秋黄中夜起云夜半不得月河汉空星辰又歩云意云一片昆仑心夕阳小烟树又四言云老峯蹙云壁立挽秀林隂洒雨苍苍玉鬭虚明满镜夜气成昼此其诗体也
    　　张瑴字伯玉许州人伯英运使弟也少有俊才美风姿髯齐于腹为人豪迈不羁竒士也初入太学有声从屏山游与雷李诸君及余先子善雅尚气任侠不肯下人再举不中遂辍科举计居许之郾城有园有田宅甚丰日役使诸侄治生事而已则以诗酒自放偃然为西州豪侠魁邑令过使皆下之喜称人善交游有患难极力挈扶俗子少不惬意辄嫚骂年四十余不娶有一妾因小过以铁简杀之

    19

    Li Jing, courtesy name Tian Ying, was from Jin Prefecture. From a young age, he possessed extraordinary talent and entered the Imperial Academy to study. Screen Mountain saw his poetry and said, "Truly the Li Bai of today," and highly praised him among the scholars of the time. Thus, his reputation greatly increased, and his calligraphy was also extraordinary. He failed the imperial examinations twice and waved his sleeves and returned home. After the Southern Migration, his local commander presented a memorial to the court. Scholars recognized it and said, "This is the work of Tian Ying." The court appointed him as the deputy of his state due to his military achievements. Later, his fate is unknown. Tian Ying was known as the Daoist Master Without Dust. He inscribed on the painting of Tai Zhen saying, "About to bow before the ruler but not yet bowed, the flower branches were weak, and the east wind was ashamed." He also wrote about night rain, saying, "A thousand lights in the night, the wind howling, looking up at the clouds in the evening, standing in the eye of the sun, a thousand miles away, rising in the middle of the night, the autumn leaves yellow." In the middle of the night, unable to see the moon, the Milky Way is empty, stars are scattered. He also wrote in four-character verse, "The old peak gathers clouds, standing walls pull the beautiful forest, sprinkling rain, the jade bowl is clear, the empty clarity fills the mirror, the night air turns into day." This is the style of his poetry.

    Zhang Ruo, courtesy name Bo Yu, was from Xu Prefecture and the brother of Bo Ying, the Transport Commissioner. From a young age, he was talented, handsome, and had a full beard. He was bold and unrestrained, a remarkable man. Initially, he entered the Imperial Academy and gained fame, traveling with Screen Mountain and becoming friends with Lei, Li, and other scholars, as well as my father. He valued courage and chivalry, would not bow to others, and failed the imperial examinations again, giving up on them. He lived in Yancheng, Xu Prefecture, with a large garden, fields, and houses. He employed his nephews to manage his affairs and otherwise indulged in poetry and wine, becoming a prominent hero in the west. All officials and travelers bowed to him. He liked to praise others' good qualities and helped friends in times of trouble. Ordinary people who displeased him were often insulted. He remained unmarried until he was over forty and had a concubine whom he killed with an iron rod for a minor offense.

    20

    尝衣紫绮裘半醉坐堂上人望之如神迨酒酣兴发引纸落笔往往有天仙语后病脑疽死年未五十麻九畴知防为文以祭辨其为人大畧少时与屏山饮燕市有诗云日日饮燕市人人识张胡西山日来好饮酒不下驴又云昨日上髙楼西山翡翠堆今晩上西楼西山如死灰想见屏山老疗饥西山隈餐尽西山色髙楼空崔嵬又赋古镜云轩姿古镜黒如漆锦华鳞皴秋雨湿人以为不减李长源云
    　　周嗣明字晦之真定人叔昻字徳卿名士文章气势一时流辈推之屏山最爱之尝曰若徳卿操履端重学问淳深真韩欧辈人也晦之为人有学长于议论自号放翁屏山尝与作真赞与雷宋张李辈颉颃同余先子擢第后从其叔北征在军中军败俱缢死屏山赘谈晦之序也屏山送李天英诗云髯张元是人中龙喜如俊鹘盘秋空怒如怪兽拔枯松更着短周时缓颊智囊无底眼如月斫头不屈面如铁一説未终复一説勍敌相阨已铮铮二豪同运又连衡屏山真欲树降旌那得人间有阿英阿英魁竒天下士笔头风雨三千字醉倒谪仙元不死时借竒兵攻二子可想见三人者也

    Explanation

    20

    尝衣紫绮裘半醉坐堂上人望之如神迨酒酣兴发引纸落笔往往有天仙语后病脑疽死年未五十麻九畴知防为文以祭辨其为人大畧少时与屏山饮燕市有诗云日日饮燕市人人识张胡西山日来好饮酒不下驴又云昨日上髙楼西山翡翠堆今晩上西楼西山如死灰想见屏山老疗饥西山隈餐尽西山色髙楼空崔嵬又赋古镜云轩姿古镜黒如漆锦华鳞皴秋雨湿人以为不减李长源云

    Translation:
    Once, he wore a purple silk robe and sat half-drunk on a platform, appearing divine to those who looked upon him. When the wine reached its height and inspiration struck, he would take paper and pen, often producing words that seemed like those of a celestial being. Later, he fell ill with a brain abscess and died before the age of fifty. Ma Jiu Chou wrote an article to eulogize and distinguish his character. In his youth, he drank with the mountain (Screen Mountain) in the market of Yan and wrote poetry, including lines such as: "Every day I drink in the market of Yan, and everyone recognizes Zhang and Hu. The West Mountain has been coming for a long time, and I enjoy drinking without needing to ride a donkey." He also wrote: "Yesterday, I climbed to a high building, and the West Mountain was a pile of jade; tonight, I climbed to the West Tower, and the West Mountain was as gray as ashes. I wish to see the old man of the Screen Mountain, who can provide sustenance in the corner of the West Mountain, and who has consumed all the colors of the West Mountain, leaving the high building empty and towering." He also wrote a poem about an ancient mirror, describing it as: "The ancient mirror is black like lacquer, with a surface like fish scales and wet as autumn rain. People thought it was no less than Li Changyuan."

    周嗣明字晦之真定人叔昻字徳卿名士文章气势一时流辈推之屏山最爱之尝曰若徳卿操履端重学问淳深真韩欧辈人也晦之为人有学长于议论自号放翁屏山尝与作真赞与雷宋张李辈颉颃同余先子擢第后从其叔北征在军中军败俱缢死屏山赘谈晦之序也屏山送李天英诗云髯张元是人中龙喜如俊鹘盘秋空怒如怪兽拔枯松更着短周时缓颊智囊无底眼如月斫头不屈面如铁一説未终复一説勍敌相阨已铮铮二豪同运又连衡屏山真欲树降旌那得人间有阿英阿英魁竒天下士笔头风雨三千字醉倒谪仙元不死时借竒兵攻二子可想见三人者也

    Translation:
    Zhou Siming, known by the courtesy name Hui Zhi, was from Zhending. His younger brother, Shuang Ang, known by the courtesy name De Qing, was a famous scholar whose literary style and momentum were admired by his contemporaries. Screen Mountain loved him most and once said, "If De Qing maintains a dignified conduct and profound learning, he is truly a man of the caliber of Han and Ouyang." Hui Zhi was well-learned and skilled in debate, calling himself Fang Weng. Screen Mountain once wrote a formal praise for him, rivaling those of Lei, Song, Zhang, and Li. After my father passed the imperial examination, he followed his uncle north to campaign. They both died by hanging in the army after defeat. Screen Mountain added a postscript to his eulogy for Hui Zhi. In a poem he wrote to Li Tianying, he said: "The bearded Zhang is a dragon among men, joyful like a graceful hawk circling in the autumn sky, angry like a fierce beast tearing down a dead pine tree. With a brief pause, he speaks with the wisdom of an inexhaustible mind, eyes as bright as the moon, unyielding even when faced with death, a face as hard as iron. His words flow continuously, and in a fierce struggle, two great men work together in harmony. Screen Mountain truly wishes to raise a white flag, but where can one find such a person as Ying in the world? Ying is a remarkable person among the world's elite, with a pen that writes with the force of a thousand words in a storm. Even when drunk, he is like a demoted immortal who is still alive and vibrant

    21

    王权字士衡真定人又名之竒从屏山游屏山称之为人跌宕不羁喜功名博学无所不览酣饮放歌人以为狂屏山为作狂真赞与余先子同年进士然仕宦连蹇晩召入朝为部勾当官俄辞为县令未赴家鲁山为县吏所辱愤惋发疾死贞祐初余先子摄许州幕时屏山二张伯英伯玉雷魏诸公皆在焉日防饮为乐忽髙公献臣将赴河南来过诸公诣之及夕独希顔士衡留宿髙既去未防为主帅所诬陷以有异志逮捕诸党与符下颍川械二公赴洛狱榜掠万端防赦方得免然自兹士衡无仕进之意矣

    Explanation

    21

    Wang Quan, also known as Shi Heng, was from Zhending and had another name, Zhiqi. He traveled with Bing Shan, who praised him for being unrestrained and free-spirited, ambitious, widely learned, and knowledgeable. He enjoyed drinking deeply and singing freely, and people thought he was crazy. Bing Shan wrote a praise for Wang Quan's wild and true nature, and he was a Jinshi (imperial scholar) in the same year as the author's father. However, his career was full of setbacks. He was called to serve in the imperial court late in his life as a department official but soon declined an appointment as a county magistrate and did not take up the position. In Lushan, he was humiliated by a county clerk, which caused him to become depressed and fall ill, leading to his death.

    In the early years of the Zhenyuan era, the author's father served as an acting official in Xuzhou. Wang Quan, Zhang Boying, Zhang Boyu, Lei, and Wei were all present. They enjoyed drinking and socializing. Suddenly, Gao Xianchen, who was going to Henan, came to visit and stayed overnight with Wang Quan and others. After Gao left, Wang Quan was falsely accused of having ulterior motives, arrested along with others, and sent to Luoyang prison. They were severely tortured, but were eventually released after a general amnesty. However, from then on, Wang Quan lost interest in officialdom.

    22

    麻九畴字知防初名文纯易州人防颖悟善草书能诗号神童既长入太学刻苦自厉为赵闲闲李屏山所知南渡后居郾蔡间入遂平西山读书为经义学精甚兴定末试开封府词赋乙经义魁再试南省复然声誉大振南都妇人小儿皆知名及廷试以误绌士论惜之已而居不为科举计正大初门人王説王采苓俱中第上以其年防怪而问之且知知防为师近臣言其有才学平章政事侯公挚翰林学士赵公秉文俱荐之特召赐进士第以病不拜官告归病已赴调授太常寺太祝俄入翰林后以病去居郾久之北兵入河南知防挈其孥入确山避乱后复出为兵士所得驱之北边至广平病死知防

    Explanation

    22

    Ma Jiuchou, courtesy name Zhifang, originally named Wen Chun, was from Yizhou. He was insightful and quick-witted, skilled in cursive script, capable of poetry, and known as a child prodigy. After he grew up, he entered the Imperial Academy and worked hard to discipline himself. He was known to Zhao Xianxian and Li Pingshan. After the Southern Migration, he lived in Yancheng and Caizhou, entered the West Mountain of Suiping to study, and excelled in the study of Confucian classics. At the end of the Xingding era, he won first place in the poetry and prose section of the Kaifeng Prefecture examination, passed the provincial examination again, and his reputation greatly increased. Even women and children in the Southern Capital knew of him. When he took the final imperial examination, he failed due to a mistake, and scholars lamented it. Afterward, he retired to live in seclusion and did not pursue the imperial examinations. In the early Zhengda era, his disciples Wang Shuo and Wang Cailing both passed the examination. The emperor was surprised by his young age and asked about him, and knew that Zhifang was recommended by a close minister who spoke highly of his talent and learning. Pingzhangzhengshi Hou Gongzhi and Hanlin Xueshi Zhao Gongbingwen were recommended by him, and he was specially summoned and granted the title of Jinshi. Due to illness, he did not take office and returned home. After recovering, he was appointed as Taichangshi Taizhu. Soon, he entered the Hanlin Academy but left due to illness. He lived in Yancheng for a long time. When northern soldiers invaded Henan, Zhifang took his family to Queshan to avoid the chaos. Later, he came out and was captured by the soldiers, driven north to Guangping, where he died of illness.

    23

    为人耿介清苦虽居贫不妄干求卓然以道自守然性隘狭交游少不惬意辄怒去葢处士之刚者也初因经义学易后喜邵尧夫皇极书因学数又喜卜筮射覆之术晩更喜医方与名医张子和游尽得其学为文精宻巧健诗尤竒峭妙处似唐人常作透光镜篆韵诗人争冩后以避谤畏时忌持戒不作诗益潜心为易学与张伯玉宋飞卿雷希顔李钦叔及余先子善先子初摄令郾城日与唱酬为友后知防试开封先子为御史监试而王翰林从之李翰林之纯为有司因相与读举子之文见其有雄丽者相谓曰是必知防因擢为魁已而果然士林以得人相贺晩景为赵闲闲所知有送麻徴君序并诗云

    Explanation

    23

    A Man of Integrity, Simplicity, and Learning

    This person was upright, straightforward, and lived a simple, austere life, even though he was poor. He did not frivolously seek things and maintained a high moral standard by adhering to the Way. However, he was narrow-minded and had few friends; if he was not satisfied, he became angry and left immediately. He was a rigid recluse, known for his strict adherence to principles.

    Initially, he studied the Yijing (Book of Changes) through the lens of Confucian teachings. Later, he became interested in the Huangji Shu (Book of the Supreme Polarity) by Shao Yong and began to study numerology. He also enjoyed divination and guessing games, which were popular in ancient China. In his later years, he became particularly interested in medical formulas and associated with the famous physician Zhang Zihe, learning all his knowledge.

    His writing was precise, skillful, and vigorous, and his poetry was especially strange and sharp, with a touch that resembled that of Tang dynasty poets. He often composed poems in the style of the intricate patterns of a "light-transmitting mirror," which were widely circulated among poets. Later, to avoid slander and fear the times' taboos, he refrained from writing poetry and devoted himself more deeply to the study of the Yijing.

    He was friends with Zhang Boyu, Song Feiying, Lei Xiyan, Li Qinsu, and the author's late father. The author's late father, who was temporarily governing Yancheng, exchanged poems with him and became friends. Later, when overseeing the imperial examinations in Kaifeng, the author's late father served as a censor supervising the exams, while the Hanlin scholar followed him, and the pure Hanlin scholar served as an official. Together, they read the essays of candidates and found one particularly brilliant and magnificent. They said, "This must be a knowledgeable person," and selected him as the top candidate. Indeed, he was, and the scholars congratulated each other on finding the right person.

    In his later years, he was known by Zhao Xianxian, who wrote a preface and poem for Ma Zhengjun, a reclusive scholar, in his honor.

    24

    辛愿字敬之河南人自号女几野人又号溪南诗老幼嗜书苦学坐环堵数年由是六经百家无不通贯喜作诗五言尤工人以为得少陵句法平生不为科举计且未尝至京师砉然中州一逸士也为人质古不娴世事麻绦草履或倚杖读书市中人讶之亦不恤尝谓王郁飞伯曰王侯将相世所共嗜者圣人有以得之亦不避然得之不以道与夫居之不能行己之志是欲澡其身而伏于厠也此言他人难闻子宜保之此可见其志也贞祐

    Explanation

    24

    Xin Yuan, courtesy name Jingzhi, was from Henan. He styled himself "Nüji Yeren" and also "Xinan Shilao." As a child, he loved books and studied diligently, spending many years in a small, walled room. As a result, he had a thorough understanding of the Six Classics and the writings of a hundred schools. He enjoyed writing poetry, especially five-character verse, and people thought he had mastered Du Fu's style. He never sought to pass the imperial examinations and had never been to the capital. He was a remarkable recluse in the Central Plains. He was a simple, ancient-minded person who was not skilled in worldly affairs. He wore a hemp sash and straw sandals, sometimes leaning on a staff to read in the market, and people were astonished, but he didn’t care. He once said to Wang Yu Feibo: "Duke, king, general, and prime minister—these are things the world commonly desires. Sages have ways of obtaining them, and they do not avoid them. However, if one obtains them without the right path, or if one cannot act according to one’s own aspirations while holding these positions, it is like wanting to cleanse oneself but being buried in a latrine." These words are difficult for others to hear, but you should preserve them. This shows his aspirations.

    25

    初先子主长葛簿敬之素不识闻名来谒相得甚懽及别厚赠之归而买牛使其子躬耕以自给居女几山下往来长水永宁间惟以吟咏讲诵为事朝士大夫愿交而不得也正大中先子令叶复来游后归洛下病殁有诗数千首常在行槖中其佳句有云院静寛留月牕虚细度云又莺衔晩色啼深树燕掠春隂入短墙又波揺朗月浮金镜岭隔华星断玉绳又箕山颍水春风里唤起巢由酒一杯又黄绮暂来为汉友巢由终不是唐臣真处士诗也
    　　赵宜禄字宜之忻州人防举童子第及壮病目失明自号愚轩居士髙才能诗其所读书皆自少时不忘居西山下以吟咏为乐名士无不与游赵李诸公甚重之屏山尝赋愚轩云我虽有眼不如无安得恰似愚轩愚后病殁有愚轩集其题嵩阳归图云风烟万顷一椽第丘壑端能傲市朝窈窕云山三兔穴飘飖风树一鸠巢本来无取亦无与只合自渔还自樵三十六峯俱可愿从君后不湏招送辛敬之云李白久矣骑长鲸后五百嵗之纯生

    Explanation

    25

    At first, my father served as the magistrate of Changge and was named Jingzhi. We had never met before, but he came to visit after hearing of his reputation, and we got along very well. Upon parting, he gave him a generous gift. He then returned home and bought a cow, making his son till the land to support themselves. He lived in the foothills of Nüji Mountain, traveling between Changshui and Yongning, engaging only in poetry, singing, and recitation. Court officials wished to befriend him but could not. During the reign of Emperor Wuzong, my father went to Ye again and later returned to Luoyang, where he died of illness. He had thousands of poems, always carried in his travel bag. His best lines are as follows: "The courtyard is quiet and wide, the moon lingers; the window is empty, thin clouds pass. Again, the oriole carries the evening color, singing in the deep trees; the swallows skim the spring shade, entering the short walls. The waves sway, the bright moon floats like a golden mirror; the mountains separate the brilliant stars, cutting through the jade cords. In the spring breeze, the Jishan and Yingshui rivers, calling forth Chao You with a cup of wine. Huang and Qi temporarily came as friends of Han, Chao You were never truly Tang officials. These are true recluse poems."

    Zhao Yilu, courtesy name Yi, from Xinzhou, passed the imperial examination as a child. When he grew up, he lost his sight and called himself Mr. Yu Xu. He was talented and skilled in poetry, and all the books he read as a child he never forgot. He lived in the west mountains, finding joy in poetry and singing. Scholars all wished to be his friends, and the scholars of Zhao and Li highly esteemed him. Pingshan once wrote about Yu Xu, saying, "I have eyes but they are useless; how I wish I could be as foolish as Yu Xu." After he died, there was a collection of Yu Xu's works. In his poem titled "Returning to Songyang," he wrote, "In the vast expanse of wind and smoke, a small thatched cottage; the hills and ravines can truly disdain the market and court. The graceful clouds and mountains, three rabbit holes; the swaying trees in the wind, a magpie's nest. Originally, I have nothing to gain or lose; I should only fish and chop wood for myself. All thirty-six peaks can be climbed; I wish to follow you after your death, no need to summon." Sending a poem to Xin Jingzhi, saying, "Li Bai has long ridden the great whale; after five hundred years, a pure birth."

    26

    史学字学优河南人昆弟三人兄才长亦知名学优之学长于史地理工诗絶句殊妙年五十擢南省魁后中廷策得主武阳簿颇有政声再倅卢氏令病卒兴定末与余同试于廷始识之中夜棘围谈至旦后先子令叶学优复来游先子殁学优寄挽诗未防亦下世有诗数百首其七夕云箱牛回驭锦机闲天下悲欢亦梦间月夜并肩人不见萧萧风叶满骊山又絶句石壁城头夜斩闗软红尘底晓催班道人一笑那知此门外清溪屋上山又哭屏山云张侯新作九原人【伯玉】梁子今为战血尘【仲泾父】四海交游零落尽白头扶杖哭之纯
    　　李献能字钦叔河中人先世以武功显仕至金吾卫上将军时号李金吾家迨钦叔昆弟皆以文学有名从兄钦止献卿先擢第继以钦叔又继以从兄钦若献诚从弟钦用献甫故李氏有四桂堂钦叔苦学博览无不通尤长于四六南渡擢南省魁后中宏词遂入翰林为应奉攷满再留出为鄜州观察判官再入选修撰正大末授河中

    Explanation

    26

    A man from Henan who excelled in history and philology, he had three brothers. His elder brother was talented and also famous. The man who excelled in learning was particularly skilled in history, geography, and biography. He was especially skilled in writing short poems. At the age of fifty, he was selected as the top scholar in the provincial examination. Later, he passed the imperial examination and became the magistrate of Wuyang, where he had a good reputation in governance. He later served as the deputy magistrate of Lushi but died of illness. At the end of the Xingding era, I took the same imperial examination with him, and we first met in the middle of the night, surrounded by thorny barriers, and talked until dawn. Later, my father sent Ye Xueyou to visit me again. After my father's death, Ye Xueyou sent a mourning poem, but he also passed away soon after. He had hundreds of poems. His poem on the Qixi Festival goes:

    "The cowherd returns, and the loom of silk is idle.
    The joys and sorrows of the world are like dreams.
    On a moonlit night, the person standing shoulder to shoulder is no longer there.
    The wind rustles through the leaves, filling the Lishan mountains."

    Another short poem goes:

    "At night, the city walls are cut open.
    In the soft red dust, the morning calls for duty.
    The monk smiles, unaware of this.
    Outside the door, the clear stream; on the roof, the mountains."

    Another poem mourning Pingshan goes:

    "Zhang Hou, the new resident of the Nine Graves.
    Liangzi is now covered in the dust of battle.
    All my friends from across the land have scattered.
    I, with white hair and a cane, mourn him sincerely."

    Li Xian'neng, courtesy name Qin Shu, was from Hedong. His ancestors were renowned for their military prowess and had served as generals of the Gold Bird Guard, earning them the title "Li Jinwu." By the time of Li Xian'neng, he and his brothers had all gained fame for their literary achievements. His elder brother, Li Qin Zhi, and his younger brother, Li Qin Ruo, were also distinguished scholars. Thus, the Li family had the Four Guitang Hall. Li Xian'neng studied diligently, reading extensively and mastering all subjects, particularly excelling in the eight-part essay. After the Southern Crossing, he was selected as the top scholar in the provincial examination and later passed the imperial examination, entering the Hanlin Academy as a secretary. After serving his term, he was retained and later appointed as the observer of Fuzhou. He was then promoted to the position of historian, and at the end of the Zhengda era, he was granted the post of governor of Hedong.

    27

    帅府经厯官北兵来攻军败奔陜又为陜府经厯官天兴改元陜乱见杀年四十三钦叔为人小而黒色颇有髯善谈论每敷説今古声铿亮可听作诗有志于风雅又刻意乐章在翰林院应机敏捷号得体赵闲闲李屏山尝曰李钦叔天生今世翰院材故诸公荐之不令出馆尝谓人曰吾防梦官至五品夀不至五十后竟如其言异哉
    　　冀禹锡字京父恵州龙川人防聪明絶伦年十九擢大兴魁入太学有声弱冠登髙第时雷希顔宋飞卿皆同榜号为得人京父入仕以能称遇事风生老吏莫及初主沈丘簿以年少喜交游饮酒遂为其令所乗坐废再调考柘二城皆主簿又以治闻由前过终不得京官朝士屡荐之为当途者所沮居闲日与诸公宴游昭雪得扶风丞因客睢阳为行枢宻院辟为都事末帝东迁擢为应奉翰林文字

    Explanation

    27

    As the official in charge of the administrative affairs of the military command post, he faced an attack by northern troops and his army was defeated, leading him to retreat to Shaanxi. He then served as the official in charge of the administrative affairs of the Shaanxi command post. During the era name Tianxing, a rebellion broke out in Shaanxi, and he was killed at the age of forty-three. Qinsu, a man who was short, dark-skinned, and had a beard, was skilled in conversation and could eloquently discuss ancient and modern times. His voice was clear and resonant, making him an enjoyable listener. He dedicated himself to writing poetry in the style of the Book of Songs (Shijing) and focused on composing musical pieces. While serving in the Hanlin Academy, he was quick-witted and able to respond appropriately. Zhao Xianxian and Li Pingshan once remarked, "Li Qinsu was naturally suited for the Hanlin Academy." Therefore, he was recommended by many but not allowed to leave the academy. He once said to someone, "I had a dream predicting that I would reach the rank of a fifth-rank official and live no longer than fifty years." Eventually, the prediction came true, which was indeed strange.

    Ji Yuxi, also known as Jingfu, was from Longchuan, Huizhou. He was exceptionally intelligent and excelled in the imperial examinations at the age of nineteen, gaining fame in the Imperial College. After reaching adulthood, he achieved high ranks in the imperial examinations. At the time, Lei Xiyuan and Song Feiqing were in the same examination batch and were considered successful candidates. Ji Yuxi, upon entering government service, was known for his abilities and quick thinking, even surpassing experienced officials. Initially, he served as the magistrate of Shenqiu but was demoted due to excessive socializing and drinking. He was later transferred to Ka and Zhe cities, where he served as a magistrate and gained a reputation for good governance. Due to his previous mistakes, he never became a central government official. Scholars repeatedly recommended him, but he was hindered by those in power. During his leisure time, he spent with officials and, after being exonerated, became the magistrate of Fufeng. He was invited to serve as a deputy in the Military Council in Suizhou and was promoted to the position of a scholar in the Hanlin Academy during the emperor's eastern relocation.

    28

    充尚书省都事富察古纳【案旧作蒲察官奴今改】之变与宰相李蹊同见杀年四十三【案中州集传云自投水中与此作见杀异又云年四十二与此作四十三异】京父少年作诗锻链甚工写画亦劲健可喜其赠先子诗有云忠策万言忧国献好诗千首课儿抄又哭先子云大才自古无髙位吾道何人主后盟又醉乡广大寛留地仕路﨑岖小作程散文亦精致尝作余先子哀词雷丈希顔善之
    　　王渥字仲泽后名仲泽太原人家世贵显少游太学有词赋声屡中髙选南渡后擢第为时帅所知故多在兵间后辟令宁陵有治迹召为省掾因使宋至州应对华敏宋人重之回为太学助教充枢宻院经歴官俄迁右司都事稍见信用天兴改元从持嘉喀齐喀【案旧作赤盏合喜今改】提兵出援武仙郑州西遇北兵大战殁于阵【案金史完顔思烈思烈行省邓州以渥为左右司员外郎从行故思烈自邓入援

    Explanation

    28

    Fu Cha Gu Na, who served as a high-ranking official in the Shangshu Province, was killed in a significant event along with Chancellor Li Xi at the age of forty-three. According to the Zhongzhou Collection, there is a discrepancy in the records: some accounts state that he committed suicide by drowning, while others say he was killed, and his age is recorded as forty-two in some versions and forty-three in others. His son, a young man, was known for his skillful poetry and painting, which were both powerful and appealing. In a poem he wrote to his father, he said: "I offered thousands of words of advice for the state, and taught my children by copying a thousand poems." In a poem mourning his father, he wrote: "Great talent has never been recognized with high positions; who will lead the way after me? The land of drunkenness is vast and accommodating, but the path of officialdom is difficult and requires small steps. My prose is also refined and well-crafted. I once wrote an elegy for my father, which was praised by Lei Zang Xiyang."

    Wang Wo, whose courtesy name was Zhongze and later changed to Zhongze, was from Taiyuan, a family of noble birth and prominence. He was young when he studied at the Imperial Academy and was known for his talent in poetry and prose. He was often selected for high-ranking positions. After the Southern Crossing, he passed the imperial examination and was known to the military leaders of the time, so he often served in military affairs. Later, he was appointed as the magistrate of Ningling, where he demonstrated good governance. He was then summoned to serve as a provincial clerk. On a mission to Song, he arrived in Yangzhou, where his responses were graceful and impressive, earning the respect of the Song people. He returned to serve as an assistant teacher at the Imperial Academy and was appointed as an official in the Military Council. He was soon promoted to the position of Right Secretary of the Right Office and began to gain trust and favor. In the first year of Tianxing, he followed Jia Kajikai (formerly known as Chizhan Hexi) to lead troops in support of Wu Xian in the west of Zhengzhou. They encountered northern forces and engaged in a major battle, where Wang Wo was killed in action. According to the History of the Jin, Wanyan Silie, who served as the provincial governor of Dengzhou, had Wang Wo appointed as a deputy secretary of the left and right offices and accompanied him on his campaign. Therefore, Wanyan Silie entered the relief effort from Dengzhou.

    29

    渥在军中谏勿躁进防为思烈所杀后战殁思烈之阵然则渥所从者思烈非持嘉哈希与此志异】性明俊不羁博学无所不通长于谈论使人聴之忘倦工尺牍字画遒美有晋人风作诗多有佳句其过颍亭云九山西络烟霞去一水南吞涧壑流宾主唱酬空翠琰干戈横絶自沧洲又赠李道人云簿领沈迷嫌我俗云山放浪觉君贤又颍川西湖云破除北客三年恨惭愧西湖五月春又过龙门云诗成一大笑浩浩洪波东
    　　李汾字长源先名让字敬之太原人少游秦中喜读史书览古今成败治乱慨然有功名心工于诗専学唐人其妙处不减太白崔颢为人尚气跌荡不羁颇褊躁触之辄怒以是多为人所恶尝以书谒行台胥相国鼎胥未之礼也长源后投以书尽发胥过恶胥大怒然以其士人容之元光间游梁举进士不中能诗声一日动京师诸公辟为史院书写时赵闲闲为翰林雷希顔李钦叔皆在院长源不下之诸公怒将逐去亦不屑后以病目免归后入南京上书言时事不报出客唐邓防北兵入境恒山公武仙

    Explanation

    29

    Wò, while in the army, advised against rash advances to prevent being killed by Sīliè, but later died in battle in Sīliè's ranks. Thus, Wò followed Sīliè, not holding to the good Hashi, which differed from this intention. He was intelligent, handsome, and unrestrained, broadly learned and knowledgeable in all things, skilled in conversation, making people forget their fatigue when listening. He was skilled in writing letters or documents, his handwriting strong and beautiful, with the style of the Jin people. His poetry often contained excellent verses. When passing by Yingting, he said, "The Nine Mountains flow with smoke and clouds, a river flows south, swallowing the streams and valleys, the host and guests recite poetry back and forth, the green mountains and the sound of weapons, as if they were in a distant place." He also wrote a poem to Li Dàorén, saying, "Buried in official duties, they despise my vulgarity, wandering in the clouds and mountains, I feel your virtue." He wrote another poem about West Lake in May, saying, "Breaking the three-year resentment of the northern guest, ashamed of the spring of West Lake in May." When passing by Longmen, he said, "When the poem is finished, a great laugh, the vast waves flow eastward."

    Li Fén, courtesy name Chángyuán, originally named Ràng, courtesy name Jìngzhī, was from Taiyuan. He traveled in Shaanxi when young, liked reading historical books, observed the rise and fall, governance and disorder of past and present, and had a strong desire for fame and success. He was skilled in poetry, studying exclusively the Tang people, and his skill was not inferior to Tàibái and Cuī Hào. He was proud and unrestrained, quite narrow-minded and quick to anger, and because of this, he was often disliked by others. Once he wrote a letter to seek an audience with Xū Xiàngguó Dǐng, the Chancellor of the Imperial Secretariat, but Xū did not treat him with courtesy. Chángyuán later wrote a letter exposing all of Xū's faults, and Xū became very angry but tolerated him because he was a scholar. During the Yuánguāng period, he traveled to Liang and failed the imperial examination for the jinshi degree. His poetry gained fame quickly in the capital, and officials appointed him as a writer in the Historical Bureau. Zhào Xiánxián was a Hanlin scholar, and Léi Xīyán and Lǐ Qīnshū were also in the bureau, but Chángyuán did not respect them. The officials were angry and wanted to expel him, but he did not care. Later, he was excused from his post due to eye disease and returned home. Later, he went to Nanjing and submitted a memorial on current affairs, but it was not responded to. He served as a guest in Táng and Dèng, guarding against northern invaders.

    30

    署为掌书记在军中金国亡长源劝仙归宋未防为仙麾下所杀【案金史本传仙与防知政事完顔思烈相异同颇谋自安惧汾言论欲除之汾觉遁泌阳仙令总帅王徳追获之锁养马平絶食而死又末帝本纪天兴元年六月丁丑恒山公武仙杀士人李汾中州集恒山惧长源言论欲除之遁之泌阳竟为所害则杀李汾者武仙而此志其名于麾下与金史及中州集互异】年未四十【案金史本与此志同而中州集载李汾感寓述史杂诗五十首引曰正大庚寅予行年三十有八攷之此志汾卒

    Explanation

    30

    Changyuan was appointed as a secretary in the military during the fall of the Jin Dynasty. He advised Xian to return to the Song Dynasty, but was unexpectedly killed by someone under Xian's command. [According to the Jin History, Xian and Fang had differing views with Wang Yan Si Lie, a high-ranking official, and were plotting to ensure their own safety, fearing that Fan's words might lead to his removal. Fan realized the danger and fled to Biyang. Xian ordered General Wang De to pursue and capture Fan, who was then locked in a stable and died by refusing to eat. The Jin History also records that in the first year of the Tianxing era of the Jin Dynasty, Wu Xian, the Prince of Hengshan, killed the scholar Li Fan. The Zhongzhou Collection states that Wu Xian feared Changyuan's words and wanted to remove him, so Changyuan fled to Biyang but was ultimately harmed. The Jin History and Zhongzhou Collection differ in attributing the killing of Li Fan to Wu Xian or his subordinates.] Changyuan was less than forty years old. [According to the Jin History, this is consistent with this account, but the Zhongzhou Collection records that Li Fan, in his poem "Reflections on History," wrote that in the year Zhengda Gengyin, he was thirty-eight years old, which suggests that Changyuan died at that age.]

    31

    于金亡之后金以天兴三年亡正大庚寅下距天兴三年凡五年则汾卒之年当四十有三四矣此志与本均云年未四十疑误】哀哉平生诗甚多不自收集故往往散落其再过长安有云三辅楼台失归燕上林花木怨啼鹃空余一掬伤时泪暗堕昭陵石马前又下第絶句云学劔攻书事两违回头三十四年非东风万里衡门下依旧中原一布衣望少室云圭影静涵秋气老劔锋横倚斗杓寒夏夜云鸦衔暝色投林急萤曳余光入草深鹳雀楼云白鸟去边红树小断云横处碧山多乐府歌行尤雄峭可喜

    Explanation

    31

    After the fall of the Jin dynasty, which occurred in Tianxing Year 3 (1234), it was five years later, in Zhengda Gengyin (1230), when Fen passed away at the age of forty-three. However, both the biography and the record mention that he was not yet forty, which may be an error. Alas, throughout his life, Fen composed a great many poems, but he did not collect them himself, so they often became scattered. When he passed through Chang'an for the second time, he wrote: "The towers of the Three Auxiliaries lose their returning swallows, the flowers and trees in the imperial gardens lament the cries of cuckoos, leaving only a handful of tears for the times, which silently fall before the stone horses of the Zhaoling mausoleum." In another poem, after failing an imperial examination, he wrote: "Studying martial arts and scholarship, two paths that diverged; looking back, thirty-four years have passed, the east wind blows far and wide, but I remain just a commoner in the Central Plains." Gazing at the Shaoshi mountain, he wrote: "The shadow of the ritual tablet quietly absorbs the autumn atmosphere, the sword blade horizontally leans against the handle of the Big Dipper, cold and still." In a summer night, he wrote: "Crows carry the twilight color into the forest quickly, fireflies drag their remaining light into the deep grass." At the Stork Tower, he wrote: "White birds fly away from small red trees, broken clouds across the landscape reveal many green mountains." His folk songs and ballads, in particular, were robust and impressive, and highly enjoyable.

    32

    李夷字子迁后名倵字季武陈郡人出于兵家能刻苦为学喜读史书究古今成败治乱尤喜武事习兵法击劒驰射有志于功名累举词赋不中改试经义复不售后将弃二科以武举进身无何陈防死年四十二子迁为人介特自守不羣然尚气使酒刚甚平居循谨惟恐伤人既醉虽王公大人嫚骂不恤为文尚竒涩喜唐人作诗尤劲壮多竒语然不为乡里所知贞祐末先子为陈幕一见喜之为延誉诸公间后为麻知防雷希顔所重东方后进皆推以为魁若侯季书伯威王飞伯杜仲梁曹通甫辈皆以兄事与余最深子迁既死余尝为哀词道其为

    Explanation

    32

    Li Yi, originally named Zi Qian and later known as Zi Ji Wu, was from Chen County and came from a military family. He was able to endure hardship in his studies, enjoying reading historical books and studying the successes and failures, order and chaos of past and present. He especially enjoyed military affairs, studying military strategies, fencing, horseback riding, and archery, with aspirations for military glory. He repeatedly failed in literary examinations and eventually decided to pursue a military career. Chen Fang died at the age of forty-two. Li Yi was a person of integrity, self-disciplined, and not part of the crowd, but he was very proud and often drank excessively. In his daily life, he was cautious and careful, always afraid of hurting others. Once drunk, he would not hesitate to insult even high-ranking officials. In writing, he preferred strange and obscure styles, enjoyed Tang dynasty poetry, and often used bold and unusual expressions. However, he was not well-known in his hometown. At the end of the Zhenyou era, my father, who was in Chen Fang's entourage, met him once and was impressed, recommending him to various officials. Later, he was highly regarded by Ma Zhi and Lei Xiyan, and Eastern scholars of his generation all considered him a leader. Scholars like Hou Jishu, Wang Fei, Du Zhongliang, and Cao Tongfu all treated him as an elder, and I had the deepest connection with him. After Li Yi's death, I wrote an elegy to commemorate him.

    33

    人之详平生诗不甚多不如意辄毁去尝赋古镜诸公称之其诗曰盘盘古皇州梦断繁华缺一鞭春事忙耕山陇头月土蚀背花暗蹄涔骇龙蹲髯殆欲张不敢着手扪星环紫极位劒外十三字细看清用文【其篆文云为清日用】溟漠君墓志夀堂鏁菱花引得阿紫家榛烟夕霏时防照拂双鸦神物汚虽久一日落吾手夀光阅人多常有此客不呵呵吾戏云雅志踵先民镜里春风面泉下今日尘九原不可作哲弟师有若摩挲一面铜便有亲炙乐又吊张伯玉云匣内青蛇亦悲吼意慿谁识抉云材又赠赤腿王云石鼎夜聮诗句健布囊春醉酒钱麄

    Explanation

    33

    The poet's lifetime works are not many, and if not satisfactory, he would destroy them. He once composed a poem about an ancient mirror, which was praised by the scholars. The poem reads:

    In the ancient imperial capital, the dream of prosperity is broken, and the spring activities are busy. Farming under the moonlight, the back of the mirror is eroded by soil, the hooves of horses splash water, causing dragons to cower, and the beard seems about to spread out, but dare not touch the star ring. The central position of the emperor, outside the sword, thirteen characters are carefully examined for the clear use of characters. The tombstone inscription for the mysterious figure, the lock shaped like a water lily on the tombstone, the smoke rising from the thicket, the evening mist, the two crows, even if it has been long, it will fall into my hands one day. In the place with many people, often there is such a guest who does not laugh, noble aspirations follow the ancients, the face reflected in the mirror, the dust in the grave, the ancient burial ground, the wise and respected teacher or mentor, rubbing a piece of copper, then there is the joy of close association. He also composed a poem to mourn Zhang Boyu, which reads:

    The green snake in the box also cries out in sorrow, who can understand the meaning of the cloud-like material. He also composed a poem to gift Red Leg Wang, which reads:

    The stone tripod used at night to connect strong poetic lines, the cloth bag filled with coarse wine money.

    归潜志卷二
    　　钦定四库全书
    　　归潜志卷三
    　　元　刘祁　撰
    　　侯策字季书先字君泽中山人少不喜学鬭鸡走狗雄乡里南渡后慨然有为学心与一时名士游尽絶少年事喜作诗刻苦自学自汉魏六朝唐宋人诸集无不研究初为李子迁所知荐于余先子亦喜之王飞伯负其材素少许可一见季书诗即加敬为人任侠尚气然修谨无过失与余交最深久之居南顿家甚贫遇朋友倾所有共乐天兴改元陈乱失妻独走大梁诣余防疾作数月死诸朋友为买棺西城余为志其墓
    刻石平生诗甚多同王飞伯唱和南顿同余唱和梁园又喜效西昆体甚有得其吊一贵人云歌翻薤露刍灵逺门掩秋风甲第深又云峯前雨送闺中梦【峯一作蓬】楼上云凝扇底歌又明月花楼闲玉凤秋风桂漏戞铜龙又九疑湘瑟悲龙竹子夜秦箫隔凤楼又幽鸟防音花覆地断虹沈影水明河又咏雨云势侵书帙湘芸润声入旌蜡炬清又和飞伯云世事催人南去早梦魂失路北归迟置之唐人集中谁复疑其非也
