    Records of Returning to Seclusion, Volume Two
    　　Imperially Approved Complete Library of the Four Treasuries
    　　Records of Returning to Seclusion, Volume Three
    　　By Liu Qi of the Yuan Dynasty

    Hou Ce, courtesy name Jishu, and Xian, courtesy name Junze, were both from Zhongshan. In their youth, they were not fond of learning and were known for their involvement in idle pursuits such as cockfighting and dog racing, which made them dominant in their village. After the Southern Migration, they resolved to devote themselves to learning and began associating with prominent scholars of the time, abandoning their youthful pastimes. They enjoyed writing poetry and studied diligently on their own, delving into the works of scholars from the Han, Wei, Six Dynasties, Tang, and Song periods. Initially, they were recognized by Li Ziqian, who recommended them to my father, who also appreciated them. Wang Feibo, who had great talent and was usually reluctant to praise, immediately showed respect upon seeing the poems of Jishu. Hou Ce was chivalrous and valued courage, but he was also cautious and made no mistakes. He had the deepest friendship with me. After living in Nandun for a long time, his family became very poor, but he would share everything he had with friends, enjoying their company. During the reign change of Tianxing, a period of chaos, he lost his wife and traveled alone to Daliang to visit me for medical treatment. He fell ill and died after several months. His friends bought a coffin and buried him in the Western City, and I wrote an epitaph for his tomb.

    He carved his poems on stone, and he had many poems throughout his life. He engaged in poetic exchanges with Wang Feibo in Nandun and with me in Liangyuan. He also enjoyed imitating the Xikun style and achieved much in this endeavor. One of his poems mourning a noble person read: "The song turns to the Xielu (a classical lament), the straw effigy is far away, the autumn wind closes the grand mansion deep." Another poem read: "Rain before a peak sends dreams from the inner chamber, clouds on the upper floor gather as songs are sung with fans." Another read: "A bright moon, a flower-laden pavilion, and a leisurely jade phoenix, autumn wind, a cassia-flower drip, and a clanging bronze dragon." Another read: "The nine doubts, the Xiang zither, and the sorrowful dragon bamboo, midnight, the Qin flute, and the distant phoenix pavilion." Another read: "The sound of hidden birds, flowers covering the ground, a broken rainbow, submerged shadow, and the bright river." Another poem about rain read: "The power of rain invades the book covers, moistening the Xiang orchids, the sound enters the banners, the wax candles are clear." Another poem in response to Feibo read: "Worldly affairs urge one to leave southward early, the soul loses its way, returning northward slowly." If placed among the works of Tang poets, who would doubt its authenticity?

    35

    雷琯字伯威坊州人父秀实亦名进士伯威博学能文作诗典雅多有佳句时辈称之初余过阳夏闻其名及一见倾倒欢甚后伯威赴余先子淮阳为诔文雅澹可喜余以示雷翰林竒之已而以家贫母老为国史院书写秩满为八作使乱后南奔道为兵士所杀年未四十哀哉伯威为人议论刻深然于文字甚工细每酒酣谈説今古莫能穷又欲取竒异功名自喜亦不羁之士也其诗多散落有游龙徳宫云千年金谷铜驼怨万里蜀天杜宇啼又明日清风一壶酒与君同酹信陵坟王郁字飞伯竒士也少余一嵗与余交最深仪状魁竒目光如鹘歩武翩然相者云病状貌也少居钧台闭门读书不接人事数载为

    Explanation

    35

    Lei Guan, styled Bo Wei, was from Fangzhou. His father, Xiu Shi, was also known as a Jinshi. Lei Guan was learned, skilled in writing, and composed poetry that was elegant and often contained fine verses. He was praised by his contemporaries. At first, I passed through Yangxia and heard of his name; upon meeting him, I was greatly impressed and delighted. Later, when Bo Wei attended the funeral of my late father in Huaiyang, he wrote a eulogy that was elegant and pleasing. I showed it to Lei, the Hanlin scholar, who found it remarkable. Later, due to his family's poverty and his mother's old age, he became a scribe at the National History Bureau, and after completing his term, he was appointed as an official in charge of eight tasks. After the chaos, he fled south and was killed by soldiers before reaching forty; alas. Bo Wei's discussions were sharp and profound, yet his writing was extremely meticulous. Whenever he was drunk, he would talk about ancient and modern times, and no one could exhaust the topics. He also sought extraordinary achievements and fame for himself, and was also a free-spirited man. His poems were mostly scattered. There is a poem about visiting Longde Palace, which says: "A thousand years of the Jin Valley and bronze camels lament, while the cuckoo cries in the distant Shu sky." Another poem says: "Tomorrow, the clear wind and a pot of wine, let us drink together to honor the grave of Xinning." Wang Yu, styled Fei Bo, was a remarkable man, one year younger than me, with whom I had the deepest friendship. He had a majestic appearance, eyes like hawks, and a graceful stride. A fortune-teller said that his appearance indicated illness. When young, he lived in Juntai, closed the door, and read books, not interacting with people for several years.

    36

    文闳肆竒古动辄数千百言法栁栁州歌诗飘逸有太白气象初为御史程公震所知继为李翰林钦叔麻征君知防史卢氏学优嘉赏且共为延誉借借正大初余先子令叶飞伯持诸公书来投先子异其文置门下遂与余定交每觞酒防游无不在已而入南京见赵雷诸公皆称之不已布衣少年名动京师后因下第西游洛中余居淮阳凡三过留辄数月唱酬谈论相髙每相别辄以所着相寄且相商订为益正大末南京被围复相守围城中天兴改元秋飞伯忽过余别曰吾跧伏陷穽不自得今将突围逺举然生死未可知因出其所作王子小属余曰兹不朽之托也余不能止之而去三年不知存亡丙申嵗南游遇交

    Explanation

    36

    The writing is expansive, bold, and ancient, often involving several or even hundreds of words, following the style of Liu Zongyuan's lyrical and free-spirited poetry, with a graceful and unrestrained quality reminiscent of Li Bai. Initially known by the Censorate official Cheng Gongzhen, and later recognized by Li Qingshi, Ma Zhengjun, and Lu Shi, who praised his scholarship and helped promote his reputation. In the early years of Zhengda, my father, Ye Feibo, brought letters from these officials to introduce me. My father was impressed by my writing and took me under his wing, and thus we established a friendship. We often engaged in social gatherings involving drinking and traveling, and our mutual exchange of poems and discussions held each other in high esteem. Later, I went to Nanjing, where I met officials such as Zhao and Lei, who continued to praise me endlessly. As a young man of humble origins, I gained fame in the capital. After failing the imperial examinations, I traveled west to Luoyang, where I lived in Huaiyang for several months each time I visited, engaging in reciprocal poetry and discussions. When we parted, we would send each other our writings and discuss them to improve them. In the late years of Zhengda, Nanjing was besieged, and we again stayed together in the besieged city. In the autumn of the first year of Tianxing, Ye Feibo suddenly came to bid me farewell, saying, "I am trapped in a pit and feel discontented. Now I will break through the siege and go far, but whether I live or die is uncertain." He then handed me his work, The Short Biography of a Prince, and entrusted me with it, saying, "This is a work that will endure forever." I could not stop him, and he left. For three years, I did not know if he was alive or dead. In the year of Bing Shen, while traveling south, I met acquaintances.

    37

    游辈説飞伯初为东诸侯兵士所得其将厚遇之飞伯径行不设机久之为其下所忌见杀临终懐中出书曰是吾平生著述可付中州士大夫王飞伯死矣计其时年甫三十余哭诸镇阳葢飞伯为人虽聪頴絶人然渉世日浅颇骜岸不通辙此所以不免予尝见其举止言谈无顾忌旁为然而飞伯益自信莫能戒以是常得谤议为俗人所憎迄今谈其名不悦者多矣嗟乎以斯人之才气稍有锻链其文章所至岂易量哉今而中道摧折不迄于大成可以为斯文叹其诗文往来与余最多有淮阳唱和南顿聫句古赋铭赞书序数十首遭乱皆在余槖中今仍略载其小云先生名青雄一名郁大兴府人也十五代祖珪

    Explanation

    37

    It is said among the wandering scholars that Wang Feibo was initially captured by the soldiers of the eastern feudal lords, and his commander treated him generously. Wang Feibo proceeded directly without setting traps or schemes, and after a long time, he was envied or resented by his subordinates and was killed. On his deathbed, he took out a book from his bosom and said, "These are my lifetime writings, which can be passed on to scholars of Central China." Wang Feibo has died. Calculated at the time, he was just over thirty years old, and he was mourned in various towns. Wang Feibo was a person who was exceptionally intelligent, but he had been in the world for a short time and was rather arrogant and did not follow the path. This is why he could not avoid it. I have often seen his behavior and speech without restraint, and others were intimidated, but Wang Feibo became even more confident and could not be warned. Therefore, he often received criticism and was hated by ordinary people. To this day, many people who talk about his name are not pleased. Alas, with such talent, if slightly refined, his writings would reach great heights, which is hard to measure. Now he is cut off in the middle and does not achieve great success, which can be a lament for literature. His poems and writings exchanged with me the most, and there are dozens of poems, couplets, ancient essays, inscriptions, commendations, and prefaces from Huaiyang and Nandun. During chaos, they were all in my bag. Now I will briefly record his small biography: the master's name is Qingxiong, also known as Yu, from Daxing Prefecture. His fifteenth-generation ancestor was Gui.

    38

    相唐太宗官侍中永宁郡公曽祖衍金紫光禄大夫定海军节度使兼莱州管内观察使祖彦信邠州宜禄尉父钦山东路转运司盐铁判官先生始生之月梦神人自天而下开所负紫囊赐一大雕且云吾后必来取其雕在地振羽一鸣惊而寤访诸卜者繇曰凛凛霜鹗赐上穹既文于外又刚中法生贵子其应在公他日必作青云之雄先生既生因采其语为名字年十八父殁家素富赀累千金遭乱荡散无防先生殊不以为意发愤读书是时学者惟事科举时文先生为文一扫积専法古人最早为麻征君九畴所赏其潜心述作未尝轻求人知李钦叔过钧台得其所着伤鲁麟导懐等赋并杨孝童碑王梦祥哀辞大

    Explanation

    38

    The subject's ancestor, who served as the Grand Councillor and Duke of Yongning, was a descendant of Yan, who held the title of Gold Purple Grand Councillor and was the military governor of Dinghai Navy and the inspector of Laizhou. His grandfather, Yanxin, was a magistrate in Yilu, Binzhou. His father, Qin, was a salt and iron official in the Shandong Road.

    When the subject was born, he dreamed that a divine being descended from heaven, opened a purple bag he was carrying, and gave him a large eagle, saying, "I will come to take this eagle." The eagle on the ground flapped its wings and cried out, startling him awake.

    The dream foretold the birth of a noble child, and it was said that he would one day become a hero of the highest rank.

    After his birth, the subject's name was taken from the dream. At the age of eighteen, his father died, and the family, which had been wealthy with assets amounting to thousands of gold pieces, lost everything due to chaos. The subject, however, was not particularly concerned and instead devoted himself to studying.

    At that time, scholars were primarily focused on the imperial examinations and contemporary writings. However, the subject's writing was a refreshing departure from the accumulated flaws of the time, and he strictly followed the examples of ancient masters. He was the first to be appreciated by Master Ma Jiuchou, a respected scholar. He was deeply engaged in his literary pursuits and never sought recognition lightly.

    Li Qinsu, passing through Juntai, obtained the subject's works, including the poems "Shang Lu Lin" and "Dao Huai," as well as the epitaph for Yang Xiaotong and the lament for Wang Mengxiang.

    39

    惊誊书徧荐于诸公先生之名始满天下自此去钧台放游四方又移陉山覃思古学正大五年先生年二十五矣来游京师诸公倒屣争识其面宰相闻其名取所作文章将荐之事中格樗轩【皇叔密公璹】闲闲朝廷二大老皆致礼于先生交馆之明年以两科举进士不中西游洛阳放懐诗酒尽山水之欢先生平日好议论尚气自以为儒中侠所向敢为不以毁誉易心又自能断大事其论学孔氏能兼佛老佛老为世害然有从事于孔氏之心学者徒能言而不能行纵欲行之又皆执于一隅不能周徧故尝欲著书推明孔氏之心学又别言之行之二者之不同以去学者之其论经学以为宋儒见解最髙虽皆

    Explanation

    39

    The book was widely recommended among the scholars, and the master's name began to spread throughout the land. From then on, he left the Jun Platform and roamed the four directions, eventually moving to the Xing Mountains to ponder ancient learning. In the fifth year of the Zhengda era, the master was twenty-five years old and came to the capital city. The scholars eagerly sought to meet him, and the chancellor, upon hearing his name, took his writings to recommend him to the court. The two great elders of the court, including the esteemed official known as "Huang Shu Mi Gong Shu," all extended their respects to the master and invited him to their halls. The following year, he failed to pass the imperial examinations for the second time, so he traveled west to Luoyang, where he indulged in poetry, wine, and the pleasures of the mountains and waters. The master was known for his fondness of debate and his spirited nature, considering himself a scholar-warrior who dared to act without being swayed by praise or criticism. He was also capable of making decisive judgments on major matters. In his studies, he believed that Confucianism could encompass Buddhism and Daoism, though he acknowledged that Daoism was harmful to the world. Nevertheless, he held a deep commitment to Confucian principles. Scholars, he observed, could only talk but not act; even if they did act, they were often limited to one narrow perspective, unable to fully encompass the broader truth. Thus, he had long wished to write a book to clarify the essence of Confucian learning and to distinguish between theoretical discourse and practical application, in order to correct the flaws of scholars. In his study of the classics, he believed that the insights of Song Dynasty Confucian scholars were the highest, though he noted that they were not without their limitations.

    40

    笑东汉之注今人惟蹈袭前人不敢谁何使天然之智识不具而经世实用不宏视东汉注尤为甚亦欲著书専与宋儒商订其论为文以为近代文章为习俗所蠧不能遽洗其陋非有絶世之人奋然以古作者自任不能唱起斯文故尝欲为文取韩栁之辞程张之理合而为一方尽天下之妙其论诗以为世人皆知作诗而未尝有知学诗者故其诗皆不足观诗学当自三百篇始其次离骚汉魏六朝唐人近皆置之不论葢以尖慢浮杂无复古体故先王之诗必求尽古人之所长削去后人之所短其论诗之详皆成书其论出处以为仕宦本求得志行其所知以济斯民其或进而不能行不若居髙养豪行乐自适不

    Explanation

    40

    Laughing at the annotations of the Eastern Han, today's scholars merely follow and imitate their predecessors, not daring to question or challenge. This leaves their natural intelligence and knowledge incomplete, and their practical application in governing the world is not extensive. Compared to the annotations of the Eastern Han, the situation is even worse. I also wish to write books specifically to debate with Song Confucian scholars, discussing their theories. In writing, I believe that modern literature is corrupted by customs and cannot be quickly cleansed of its crudeness. It requires exceptional individuals who boldly take on the role of ancient authors to lead this literary renaissance. Therefore, I have often desired to write, combining the style of Han Yu and Liu Zongyuan with the principles of Cheng Hao and Zhang Zai, to encompass all the wonders of the world. In my discussion of poetry, I believe that everyone knows how to write poetry, but no one knows how to study it, so their poetry is not worth viewing. Poetry studies should start from the "Three Hundred Poems," while the "Li Sao" and works from the Han, Wei, Six Dynasties, and Tang periods are often ignored. This is because contemporary poetry is sharp, slow, superficial, and mixed, lacking the ancient style. The poetry of the ancient kings must seek to fully capture the strengths of the ancients while eliminating the weaknesses of later generations. My detailed discussion of poetry is all contained in my books. In my discussion of career choices, I believe that officials aim to achieve their goals and put their knowledge into practice to benefit the people. If they advance but cannot put their knowledge into practice, it is better to live a life of leisure and self-pleasure, rather than holding a high position.

    41

    为世网所羁颇以李白为则先生受知最深者曰樗轩公完顔璹闲闲公赵秉文余先子雷渊李献能王若虚麻九畴史学优程震宋九嘉其从游最久者曰李汾杨道元好问魏璠张直杜仁杰曹君一雷琯冀禹锡张介王説王采苓赵着张甫王铸刘辑李仝刘源杨焕胡权图克坦公履【案图克坦旧作徒单今改】吕鲲史环李倵侯策张杰刘郁左坦牛汝霖珠格邃乌凌阿爽【案珠格旧作术虎乌凌阿旧作乌林荅今改】僧性英诸公随得书无次第至于心交者惟李冶刘祁二人而已八年先生复至京师十二月遇兵难京城被围先生上书言事不报明年四月围稍解五月先生挺身独出逺名山不知所终

    Explanation

    41

    He was bound by the world's constraints and often took Li Bai as a model. Those who knew him most deeply were Chu Xuan Gong Wanyan Shu, Xianxian Gong Zhao Bingwen, his father Lei Yuan, Li Xian Neng, Wang Ruoxu, Ma Jiuchou, Shi Xue You, Cheng Zhen, and Song Jiujia. Those who studied with him for the longest time were Li Fen, Yang Hongdao, Yuan Hao Wen, Wei Fan, Zhang Zhenzhi, Du Renjie, Cao Junyi, Lei Guan, Ji Yu Xi, Zhang Jie, Wang Shuo, Wang Cailing, Zhao Zhu, Zhang Fu, Wang Zhu, Liu Ji, Li Tong, Liu Yuan, Yang Huan, Hu Quan, Tuoketan Gong Lu, Lv Kun, Shi Huan, Hou Ce, Zhang Jie, Liu Yu, Zuo Tan, Niu Rulin, Zhuge, Su Weiulinga Shuang, and Seng Xingying. They received letters from him in no particular order. Among them, only Li Ye and Liu Qi were his close friends. In the eighth year, he returned to the capital. In December, he encountered military difficulties, and the capital was besieged. He submitted a memorial, but it was not reported. In the following April, the siege was somewhat lifted. In May, he stepped out alone, retreated to distant mountains, and his fate is unknown.

    42

    刘昻霄字景贤陵川人博学能文从屏山游与雷希顔辛敬之元裕之善尝由任子入官已而居洛西山水间逾四十病卒【案元好问刘景元墓铭曰以元光元年六月十三日春秋三十有八终与此志年逾四十有异而中州集又云卒年三十七则与其所作墓铭又自不同】其诗有云嵗月消磨诗砚里河山浮动酒杯中迢迢万里乾坤眼凛凛千年草木风元裕之尝称之余恨未之识也
    　　珠格防字士先名玹字温伯女直纳琳明安也【案纳琳明安旧作纳隣猛安今改】虽贵家刻苦为诗如寒士喜与士大夫游初受学于辛敬之习左氏春秋后与侯季书交筑室商水大野中恶衣粝食以吟咏为事诗益工时余在淮阳屡相从讲学迨北兵入河南被命提兵戍亳州已而亳乱见杀年未四十也少年诗云山连嵩少云烟晩地接崤函草树秋其寄余云西湖风景昔同游醉上兰舟泛碧流杨栁风生潮水濶芙蕖

    Explanation

    42

    Liu Angxiao, courtesy name Jingxian, was from Lingchuan. He was broadly learned and skilled in writing, having studied under Shen Shang (屏山) and was on good terms with Lei Xiyan, Xin Jingzhi, and Yuan Yuzhi. He entered officialdom through the renzi system but later retired to live in the mountains and waters of Luoxi, where he died of illness after the age of forty. According to Yuan Haowen's epitaph for Liu Jingyuan, it states that he died on the 13th day of the sixth month of the Yuan Guang Year 1, aged thirty-eight, which differs from the record here that he lived past forty. The Zhongzhou Collection also states that he died at the age of thirty-seven, which is inconsistent with the epitaph. His poetry includes the lines: "The years are spent at the inkstone, writing poetry; the rivers and mountains seem to float within a wine cup. The vast expanse of the universe seen from afar, the chilling wind of a thousand years through the grass and trees." Yuan Yuzhi once praised him, but I regret that I did not meet him.

    Zhuge Fang, courtesy name Shixuan, given name Xuan, courtesy name Wenbo, was a Jurchen from the Nalin Ming'an clan. Despite coming from a wealthy family, he wrote poetry with the diligence of a poor scholar and enjoyed associating with scholars and officials. He first studied under Xin Jingzhi, learning the Zuo Zhuan (Commentary on the Spring and Autumn Annals). Later, he associated with Hou Jishu and built a house in the wilderness of Shangshui, where he wore coarse clothes and ate simple food, making poetry his primary occupation. His poetry became even more refined. At the time, I was in Huaiyang and often studied with him. When the northern army entered Henan, he was ordered to lead troops to garrison Bozhou. Soon after, Bozhou was in chaos, and he was killed, not yet forty years old. His early poetry includes the lines: "Mountains connected to Song and Shaoyang are shrouded in evening mist; the land connects to Xiaohan, where grass and trees are in autumn." He sent me the lines: "The West Lake scenery, which we once enjoyed together; drunk, we sailed on a boat on the green stream. The willow trees swayed, and the tide was vast; lotus flowers."

    43

    烟尽野塘幽【幽一作秋】花边落日明金勒云里清歌绕画楼今夜相思满城月梁台楚水两悠悠又睢阳道中云又渡溵江二月时睢阳东下思依依丘园寂寞生春草城阙荒凉对落晖去国十年初避乱投荒万里正思归临岐郤羡春来鴈乱逐东风向北飞又书懐云闗中客子去迟迟飘泊炎荒两鬓丝三楚楼台淹此日五陵鞍马想当时春风草长淮阳路落日云埋汉帝祠回首故乡何处是北山天际緑参差甚有唐人风致
    　　乌凌阿爽字肃孺女直世袭穆昆也【案穆昆旧作谋克今改】风神潇洒美少年性聪颖作竒语喜从名士游居淮阳日诣余家夜归其室抄写讽诵终夕虽世族家甚贫为后母所制逾冠未娶恶衣粝食恬如遇交游杯酒豪纵可喜余谓使其志不辍年稍长则当魁其辈流壬辰陈防赴水死年未三十初赋邺研诗有云上有丹锡花秋河碎星斗磨研清且厉玉瑟鸣风牖又赋古尺云【一云赋古子】背逐一道十三虹赤鬣金麟何夭娇飜思昨夜雷霆怒只恐乗云上天去又七夕曲云天上别离泪更多满空飞

    Explanation

    43

    The smoke has dissipated over the wild pond, and the flowers are illuminated by the setting sun. The golden bridle, a symbol of wealth and status, contrasts with the clear song echoing through the clouds around the painted tower. Tonight, the longing fills the city under the moonlight, and the distant and enduring nature of the land and water is evoked. In the path of Suizhou, the eastern journey is remembered with affection. The loneliness of the countryside is marked by the growth of spring grass, and the desolate and abandoned city gates face the setting sun. After ten years of absence from the homeland due to fleeing from turmoil, the desire to return home is strong after being exiled to a distant and desolate place. The envy of the spring geese flying northward with the east wind is felt, symbolizing the longing for home and freedom.

    In the poem about the inkstone in Ye, the red tin flowers adorn it, and the autumn river with scattered stars evokes a sense of vastness and beauty. The clear and sharp sound of grinding the inkstone is heard, and the sound of a jade zither played through the wind in the window adds to the elegance and tranquility. In the poem about an ancient ruler, his back follows a path of thirteen rainbows, symbolizing a majestic and divine presence. His red mane and golden scales indicate his beauty and strength, and his thoughts of the previous night's thunderstorm evoke a sense of power and intensity. The fear that he might ascend to heaven, symbolizing his divine or supernatural qualities, is expressed.

    In the poem about the Qixi Festival, the greater number of tears shed in heaven during the separation is emphasized, and the tears filling the sky evoke a sense of overwhelming emotion.

    Ulinga Shuang, courtesy name Sushu, is of Jurchen descent and belongs to a hereditary clan. He is a graceful and elegant young man, handsome and intelligent, who creates unusual or poetic language. He enjoys associating with famous scholars and visits the speaker's home daily in Huaiyang, returning to his own room at night to copy and recite texts all night. Despite his noble background, he is very poor and is controlled by his stepmother. He has passed the age of adulthood but has not yet married, living a simple and modest lifestyle with a calm and unperturbed demeanor. His enjoyment of drinking and socializing with friends is pleasing to see, and the speaker believes that if he continues his efforts, he will eventually become a leader among his peers.

    In the year Renchen, Chen Fang drowned before the age of thirty. In the poem about the inkstone in Ye, the red tin flowers adorn it, and the autumn river with scattered stars evokes a sense of vastness and beauty. The clear and sharp sound of grinding the inkstone is heard, and the sound of a jade zither played through the wind in the window adds to the elegance and tranquility. In the poem about an ancient ruler, his back follows a path of thirteen rainbows, symbolizing a majestic and divine presence. His red mane and golden scales indicate his beauty and strength, and his thoughts of the previous night's thunderstorm evoke a sense of power and intensity. The fear that he might ascend to heaven, symbolizing his divine or supernatural qualities, is expressed.

    In the poem about the Qixi Festival, the greater number of tears shed in heaven during the separation is emphasized, and the tears filling the sky evoke a sense of overwhelming emotion.

    44

    下清秋雨其才清丽俊拔似李贺惜乎不见其大成也刘琢伯成中山人刻苦为学事母教弟以孝友闻朋友居邓州人甚重之正大初举进士南京余始与相识俄下第归久之河南乱闻在武仙军中仙使使宋回为所杀哀哉作诗甚工有云吴蚕丝就方成茧楚栁丝飞又作萍非浅浅者所能道也其过叶哭余先子诗亦佳史懐字季山陈郡人少游宕不羁然有才思年既壮乃折节为学与名士李子迁侯季书王飞伯游作诗甚有功冬日即事云檐雪日髙晴滴雨炉烟风定暖生云亦可喜也又作古剑诗极工陈陷死

    Explanation

    44

    His talent, like autumn rain, was clear, beautiful, and sharp, resembling that of Li He. Alas, he did not achieve greater success. Liu Zhuo, from Zhongshan, studied with great effort, was known for filial piety and kindness towards his younger brother, and was highly regarded by his friends in Dengzhou. During the Zhengda period, he passed the imperial examination in Nanjing, and I first met him there. Soon after, he failed the examination and returned home. After a long time, during the chaos in Henan, it was heard that he was in the army of Wu Xian. Wu Xian sent him on a mission to Song, and he was killed there; alas. His poetry was very skillful, and he used a metaphorical expression: "The silk of silkworms forms cocoons, and the fluff of willows disperses like floating algae." It cannot be described by those who are superficial. His poem mourning my deceased father when passing through Ye was also good. Shi Huai, whose courtesy name is Ji Shan, from Chen Prefecture, was young, wandering, and unrestrained, but had talent and imagination. When he grew older, he became serious about studying and associated with the famous scholars Li Ziqian, Hou Jishu, and Wang Feibo. He wrote a poem about a winter scene: "The snow on the eaves drips in the clear, sunny day, and the smoke from the stove warms the air as the wind settles." It is also delightful. He also wrote a highly skilled poem about an ancient sword, but Chen died in the siege.

    刘昉字仲宣中山人读书有才学作诗甚有可称尝作睢阳八咏工甚居西华之小姚镇时来游陈余识之遭乱殁
    　　髙永字信卿渔阳人倜傥尚气轻财好交游颇读书喜谈兵文辞豪放长于论事尝从屏山游与李长源元裕之杜仲梁李稚川相善累举不第家甚贫正大末余居淮阳信卿持诸公书来谒因为定交留月余西去未防同在南京被围尝上书言事不报以病死自号应庵胡权字直卿卫州人南渡有诗声累举不第贫甚性狂狭不能容寻常人年过四十方娶尝投余先子淮阳又与余同试于京遭乱北归以病卒
    　　田永锡义州人叔思敬耀卿名进士永锡少有诗声其过东坡坟诗云富贵一春夜梦文章万斛冷云泉英魂返却眉山秀依旧春风草木天为人诵兴定末同余试南京擢第遭乱南奔在江淮间病卒

    45

    Liu Fang, courtesy name Zhongxuan, was from Zhongshan. He read with talent and learning, and his poetry was very commendable. He once wrote eight poems about Suiyang, which were very skilled. He lived in Xiaoyao Town, Xihua, and sometimes came to visit Chen Yu, who recognized him. He died during the chaos.

    Gao Yong, courtesy name Xin Qing, was from Yuyang. He was bold and generous, valuing righteousness over wealth, and enjoyed making friends. He had read quite a bit and liked to talk about military affairs. His writing was bold and unrestrained, and he was skilled at discussing matters. He once traveled with Ping Shan and was friendly with Li Changyuan, Yuan Yuzhi, Du Zhongliang, and Li Zichuan. He failed the imperial examinations multiple times and was very poor. During the end of the Zhi Da era, I lived in Huaiyang, and Xin Qing brought letters from various scholars to meet me. We established a friendship, and he stayed for more than a month before going west. Unexpectedly, we were both in Nanjing under siege. He submitted a memorial to discuss matters but received no response, and he died of illness. He gave himself the name Ying'an.

    Hu Quan, courtesy name Zhiqing, was from Weizhou. After the southern migration, he had a reputation for poetry. He failed the imperial examinations multiple times and was very poor. He had a wild and narrow personality, unable to tolerate ordinary people, and married only after passing forty. He once visited my father in Huaiyang and also took the imperial examinations with me in the capital. He died of illness.

    Tian Yongxi was from Yizhou. His uncle, Si Jingyaoqing, was a famous scholar. Yongxi had a reputation for poetry when young. His poem about passing by Dongpo's grave said, "Wealth and honor are like a spring night dream, literary works are like cold clouds and springs, the spirit returns to the beautiful mountains of Meishan, still the spring breeze and grass and trees." It was passed on by people. During the end of the Xing Ding era, he took the imperial examinations with me in Nanjing and passed. He fled south during the chaos and died of illness in the Jianghuai region.

    李澥字公渡相州人王黄华门生也自号六峯居士工诗及字画皆得法与黄华赵闲闲诸公游连蹇科场竟不第至六十余病殁时人言公渡赋不如诗诗不如字字不如画科举赋最紧然文至最紧下也兴定末与余同试开封中选公渡甚喜有诗示余先子后云姓名偶脱孙山外文字幸为坡老知谁念三生李方叔欲将残喘寄鑪锤先子和答云瓶有储粮髩有丝蹉跎歳晩坐书痴辋川画王摩诘锦里诗穷杜拾遗应举尚陪新进士主文多是旧相知春闱看决鱼龙阵未必尖锥胜钝锥士林相以为笑谈
    　　刘勲字少宣云中人初名讷字辩老与其兄汉老俱工诗防随官居济南二十余载后南渡居陈数与余先子唱酬为人俊爽滑稽每尊俎间一谈一笑可喜科举连蹇竟不第年五十余陈防死平生诗甚多大概尖新长于对属其佳句有云午风襟袖如秋早甲夜阑干得月多又济南泛舟云人行着色屏风里舟在回纹锦字中又上先人云

    Explanation

    46

    Li Xie, courtesy name Gongdu, was from Xiangzhou and a student of Wang Huanghua. He styled himself as the Six Peaks Hermit, skilled in poetry and calligraphy, and associated with Wang Huanghua, Zhao Xianxian, and other scholars. He failed repeatedly in the imperial examinations and ultimately did not pass, dying of illness in his sixties. People said that his fu (rhapsody) was not as good as his poetry, his poetry was not as good as his calligraphy, and his calligraphy was not as good as his paintings. In the imperial examinations, fu was the most important, but in literature, it was the least important. In the late Xingding period, I took the exam in Kaifeng and was selected. Gongdu was very happy and wrote a poem to show my father afterward, which said: "My name narrowly missed being listed on the list of successful candidates, my writing was fortunately recognized by the great master (Su Shi), who remembers the three-life reincarnation of Li Fangshu. I wanted to entrust my remaining life to the furnace and hammer." My father replied with a poem: "The bottle has stored grain, and the hair has turned white. Wasted time in old age, sitting in literary obsession. The paintings of Wang Wei in Wangchuan, the poetry of Du Fu in Jinli. The chief examiners were mostly old acquaintances. In the spring examination, the fish and dragon array will be decided. It is not certain that a sharp cone will win over a blunt one. The scholars passed this story around as a joke."

    Liu Xun, courtesy name Shaoxuan, was from Yunzhong and originally named Na, with the courtesy name Bianlao. He and his brother Hanlao were both skilled in poetry. He lived in Jinan for over twenty years following his official duties, and after the Southern Migration, he settled in Chen. He often exchanged poems with my father, and was handsome, cheerful, and humorous. In every banquet, his words and laughter were delightful. He failed repeatedly in the imperial examinations and finally did not pass, dying at the age of over fifty when Chen Fang died. He wrote a lot of poetry in his lifetime, generally sharp and new, excelling in antithetical couplets. His famous lines include: "The midday wind feels like autumn, and the early morning moon shines brightly." He wrote a poem about boating in Jinan: "People walk in a colorful screen, and boats sail in a patterned brocade." He wrote a poem dedicated to my father.

    47

    南山有后能赋北阙无人继敢言送余赴试云文章四海名父子孝友一门佳弟兄又赠王清卿云长拖酒债杜工部新有诗声侯校书赠马元章云曽着麻鞋见天子敢将道服衬朝衣又车毂春雷震屋山马蹄乱雹响柴闗何时得个茅庵子不在车尘马足间又画马末云神物世间寻不见五陵春草色萋萋仲兄谯字庭老亦好古作诗不凡
    　　甯知微字明甫宿州人博学无所不知尤长于史事剧谈古今治乱或诸家文章厯厯不可穷援笔为诗文亦敏赡可喜举经义连不中迁居淮阳与余游二载家积书万巻载以行麻知防及余先子皆重之后还乡遭乱不知所在或云渡淮在南中余尝有西游诗四十余篇明甫取而观一夕尽和其韵以见示其间佳句甚多崔遵字懐祖燕人父建昌字万卿名进士懐祖少有词赋声所交皆名士累举不第南渡辍科举不为居嵩山下以读书作诗为事正大末北兵入河南懐祖为兵所得胁令往招洛阳见杀尝有诗云青山似有十年旧小雪又为三日留元裕之称之

    47

    In the southern mountains there lived Houyi, a man renowned for his ability to compose poetry. Yet, in the north, no one could continue his legacy. I dare to say, he sent me to take the examination, for his literary fame was known across the four seas. His family was praised for filial piety and fraternal harmony, a model of virtue. His brothers also gave a poem to Wang Qingqing, saying: "Long have I carried the debts of wine, like Du Fu, the famed poet. Now, Hou Xuan, the scholar, has a new poetic voice." He also gave a poem to Ma Yuanzhang, saying: "Once I wore straw shoes to meet the emperor, daring to wear Daoist robes under official attire." When will I find a small thatched hut, away from the dust and noise of carriages and horses? At the end of his poem about painting horses, he said: "The divine creature cannot be found in the world, and the spring grass at Wuling is lush." My older brother Qiao, whose courtesy name is Tinglao, also loves antiquity and writes extraordinary poems.

    Ning Zhiwei, courtesy name Mingfu, from Suozhou, is highly learned, knows everything, and especially excels in historical matters. He engages in detailed discussions of ancient and modern governance, or the writings of various schools, which are inexhaustible. When he picks up a pen to write poetry and prose, he is quick-witted and talented, which is delightful. He failed in the imperial examinations repeatedly, moved to Huaiyang, and spent two years traveling with me. His family accumulated ten thousand volumes of books, which he carried with him. Ma Zhifang and my father both valued him highly. After returning to his hometown, he encountered chaos and his whereabouts are unknown. Some say he crossed the Huai River and is now in the southern regions. I once wrote over forty poems about a western journey. Mingfu took them and read them, composing a response in the same rhyme scheme overnight to show me. There were many excellent lines in it.

    Cui Zun, courtesy name Huizhu, from Yan, whose father Jianchang, courtesy name Wanqing, was a famous scholar. Huizhu had a reputation for poetry and prose when he was young, and his friends were all famous scholars. He failed in the imperial examinations repeatedly and stopped taking them after the Southern Migration, living in the mountains below Songshan and dedicating himself to reading and writing poetry. At the end of the Zhengda era, northern troops entered Henan, and Huizhu was captured and forced to go to Luoyang to recruit people, where he was killed. He once wrote a poem: "The green mountains seem to have known me for ten years, and the light snow stays for three days." Yuan Yuzhi praised it.

    曹恒字君章应州人髙丞相汝砺之壻也少读书不喜为科举计惟孤介不肯事富贵人南渡居大梁葺轩种竹号友直余先子为作记赋之又好收古人书画器物蔼然有士君子风遭乱病殁有子之谦擢第
    　　王宾字徳卿亳州人擢第为虹令有声入为省掾坐事罢遭乱还乡防兵变宾起率众据城复属金朝已而见杀【案中州集传云亳州为单父军杨春所据春以事出宾与故谯县尉王进反正朝廷授进集庆军节度使宾同知军事后又为行部尚书金史本载宾罢归乡里后亳州军变宾约城中军民复其州哀宗嘉之授宾同知节度使哀宗迁蔡宾奉迎于州北之髙安擢为刑部尚书及镇防军崔复哥王六千之徒擐甲哗噪拽宾往市中害之竝视此志所叙较详而此志既叙其复城仍似以省掾终殆由闻未备也】为人恢谐轻脱嗜酒无威仪诗颇工有上先子云致君有道莫如律敢谏不行犹得名

    Explanation

    48

    Cao Heng, courtesy name Junzhang, was from Yingzhou and the son-in-law of Gao Ruli, the Chancellor. When young, he read books but did not like to pursue the imperial examinations; he was aloof and unwilling to serve the wealthy. After the southward migration, he lived in Daliang, where he built a pavilion, planted bamboo, and called it "Youzhi." My father wrote a preface and composed a poem for it. He also enjoyed collecting ancient paintings, calligraphy, and artifacts, and had a gentlemanly demeanor. During the chaos, he died of illness, leaving behind a son named Zhiqian who passed the imperial examination.

    Wang Bin, courtesy name Deqing, was from Bozhou. He passed the imperial examination and became the magistrate of Hong Prefecture, where he had a good reputation and entered the provincial administration. Dismissed for a reason, he returned to his hometown during the chaos and encountered a military uprising. Wang Bin rose up and led the people to occupy the city, again belonging to the Jin dynasty, but was later killed. According to the Zhongzhou Ji biography, it says that Bozhou was occupied by the Danfu Army under Yang Chun, who released Wang Bin and the former magistrate of Qiao County, Wang Jin, who then rebelled. The court appointed Wang Jin as the military governor of Jiqing Army, and Wang Bin served as the deputy military governor. Later, he was appointed as the governor of a department. The Jin Shi biography states that he was dismissed and returned to his hometown. After a military uprising in Bozhou, Wang Bin negotiated with the military and civilians in the city to retake the prefecture, and Emperor Aizong praised him, appointing Wang Bin as the deputy military governor. When Emperor Aizong moved the capital to Cai Prefecture, Wang Bin escorted him to Ga'an in the north of the prefecture and was promoted to Minister of Justice. When the defensive army led by Cui Fuge and Wang Lüqi donned armor, made a commotion, and dragged Wang Bin to the market to kill him, he was killed. Wang Bin was lively and carefree, loved drinking, and lacked dignity. His poetry was quite skillful, and there is a poem he dedicated to my father, which says, "To advise the ruler, nothing is better than law. If one dares to advise but it is not followed, one still gains a reputation."

    归潜志卷三
    <子部,小说家类,杂事之属,归潜志>
    　　钦定四库全书
    　　归潜志卷四

    　　王元朗字子元州人余髙祖南山翁壻也家世贵显才髙以诗酒自豪擢第得官辄归不乐仕宦与余曽祖西岩子多唱酬其明妃诗云环佩魂归青冡月琵琶声断黒江秩汉家多少边征将泉下相逢也自羞甚为人所
    　　刘仲尹字致君号龙山辽阳人李钦祖外祖也少擢第终管义军节度副使【案中州集以潞州节度副使召为都水监丞卒与此志所云终节度副使异】能诗学江西诸公其墨梅诗云髙髻长眉满汉宫君王图玉按春风龙沙万里王家女不着黄金买画工为人所又有梅影诗云五换严更三唱鸡小楼天淡月平西风不着阑干角瞥见伤春背面啼

    Records of Returning to Seclusion, Volume Three
    Novels and Tales, Miscellaneous Stories, Records of Returning to Seclusion

    Imperially Approved Complete Library
    Records of Returning to Seclusion, Volume Four
    Yuan Dynasty, Liu Qi, compiled

    Wang Yuanlang, courtesy name Zi Yuan, was from Hongzhou. He was the son-in-law of my great-grandfather, Southern Mountain Old Man, and came from a noble and prestigious family. He was talented and proud of his poetry and wine. After being promoted to an official position, he immediately returned home, disliking the pursuit of officialdom. He often exchanged poems with my great-grandfather, Western Rock Son. His poem about the Bright Lady says:

    The soul of the jade pendant returns to the green tomb under the moon.
    The sound of the pipa stops at the black river.
    How many generals from the Han dynasty were sent to the borders?
    Even if we meet in the afterlife, I would feel ashamed.

    This poem is widely known and admired.

    Liu Zhongyin, courtesy name Zhi Jun, was nicknamed Dragon Mountain. He was from Liaoyang and was the maternal grandfather of Li Qin. He was promoted to an official position early in his career and eventually became the Deputy Governor of the Military Circuit of Guan. According to the Collection of Central Plains, he was summoned to serve as the Deputy Governor of the Military Circuit of Lüzhou and later as the Director of Water Management, where he died. However, in this volume, it is stated that he ended his career as a Deputy Governor of a Circuit. He was skilled in poetry and studied the works of the Jiangxi school of poets. His poem about the ink plum says:

    Her high hair and long eyebrows fill the Han palace.
    The emperor drew a jade figure in the spring breeze.
    A thousand miles of dragon sands, a daughter of the Wang family.
    Not worth buying a painter with gold.

    This poem is also widely known and admired. He also wrote a poem about the plum shadow, which says:

    Five times the strict watch, three times the rooster crows.
    In the small tower, the sky is pale and the moon sets in the west.
    The wind does not touch the corner of the railing.
    A glimpse of a tear-stained face in spring.

    50

    陈君可永宁人有梅影诗云隔牕疑是李夫人江月多情为返魂不似丹青旧顔色十分憔悴立黄昬
    　　王特起字正之代州崞县人少工词赋有声年四十余方擢第作诗极髙尝有龙徳聫句为时所称又题杨叔玉所藏双峯竞秀图云龙头矗双角駞背堆寒峯诸公嘉其破的晩年取一侧室留别一乐章喜迁莺至今之东楼欢宴寄遗绮席题诗罗扇月枕双欹云牕同梦相伴小花深院旧欢顿成陈迹翻作一番新怨素秋晩聴阳闗三叠一樽相饯留恋情缱绻红泪洗妆雨湿棃花面雁底闗河马头星月西去一程程逺但愿
    此心如旧天也不违人愿再相见老生涯分付药炉经巻余诗惜不多见尝为沁源令政颇严后为司竹监官疾卒刘昻字次霄济南人有才誉以先有刘昻字之昻故号小刘之昻泰和南征作乐一阕为时所其词曰虿铓极螗臂展敢盟寒似洞庭彭蠡狂澜天兵小试万蹄一饮楚江干捷书飞上九重天春满长安舜文明唐日月周礼乐汉衣冠洗五川烟瘴江山全蜀下也剑闗何用一泥丸有人信日边来都防先还终邹平令

    Explanation

    50

    Chen Jun, a man from Yongning, had a poem titled "Plum Shadows" which reads: "Through the window, I doubt if it is Lady Li; the moon over the river is full of emotion, returning the soul. It is not like the old colors in paintings, standing in extreme weariness at dusk."

    Wang Teqi, also known as Zhengzhi, was from Gaoxian County in Dai Prefecture. He was skilled in composing lyrics and had a reputation from a young age. He passed the imperial examination at the age of over forty and was highly regarded for his poetry. He once wrote a collaborative poem called "Long De," which was well-received by contemporaries. He also wrote a poem for Yang Shuyu's painting "Two Peaks Competing in Beauty," describing the peaks as towering like twin horns on a camel's back, piled high with cold peaks. His description was praised for its accuracy. In his later years, he took a concubine and composed a farewell song titled "Xǐ Qiān Yīng" (Joyful Migration), which is still passed down today. At an eastern pavilion banquet, he wrote a poem on a silk seat, inscribed on a fan, and composed a poem on a moonlit pillow, lying with his head against a cloud window, dreaming together. In a small garden filled with flowers, old joys turned into traces, and new grievances arose. In late autumn, he listened to the threefold "Yangguan" tune, drinking a cup together as they parted, with lingering affection and a deep connection. Tears washed away her makeup, her face wet with rain, and the pear blossoms were damp. The barriers and rivers were far behind, the stars and moon on horseback receding further and further. But I wish this heart to remain unchanged, and Heaven does not go against human wishes. We hope to meet again, and he entrusted his old life to the cauldron and scriptures. His remaining poems are few, but he once served as the magistrate of Qinyuan, known for his strict governance. Later, he became an official in charge of bamboo affairs and died due to illness.

    Liu An, also known as Cixiao, was from Jinan and had a reputation for talent. Because there was already someone named Liu An, he was called "Xiao Liu An." During the southern campaign of Taiping, he composed a musical piece that was widely circulated. The lyrics read: "The scorpion's stinger reaches the limit, the mantis's arm extends to dare to swear an alliance, as cold as the vast lakes of Dongting and Pengli. The heavenly army tests its strength in a small battle, drinking from the banks of the Chu River. The news of victory flies up to the nine heavens, spring fills Chang'an, the culture of the Shun and Tang dynasties, the sun and moon of the Zhou and Han eras, the rituals and music of the Han, cleansing the five rivers of smoke and瘴气, the entire Sichuan region falls under the sword pass, what use is a handful of mud? Someone brings a message from the edge of the sun, all defenses are returned, and he ends his days as the magistrate of Zouping."

    51

    金国初有张六太尉者镇西边有一士人邓千江者献一乐章望海潮云云雷天堑金汤地陜名藩自古臯兰绣错云屯山形米聚喉襟百二河闗鏖战血犹殷见阵云冷落时有雕盘静塞楼头晓月犹是玉弓弯看看定逺西还有元戎阃令上将斋坛瓯脱昼空兜铃夕举甘泉夜报平安吹笛虎牙闲但宴陪珠履歌按云鬟未讨先零醉魂长绕贺兰山太尉赠以白金百星其人犹不惬意而去词至今之
    　　髙左司庭玊字献臣辽东人少擢第入官有能声吏事明敏人莫能及尤俶傥重气节敢为为左司郎中誉甚重一时人士推仰焉贞祐初出为河南府治中主帅温徳亨福兴【案徳亨旧作迪罕今改】奸伪人也公临事不少逊让遂交恶是时北兵围燕都事已迫四方无勤王师公独慨然有赴援意屡以言激福兴福兴惮之因诬以有异志辄收赴狱名士如厐才卿雷希顔辛敬之皆连系拷掠无实然公竟为福兴所困死狱中余会赦得释

    Explanation

    51

    In the early days of the Jin dynasty, there was a General Zhang Liu stationed in the western border. A scholar named Deng Qianjiang presented a musical piece titled "Looking at the Sea Tide," which described the grandeur of the terrain and the fierce battles fought there: "Clouds and thunder form a natural barrier, while the land is fortified like a golden cauldron. From ancient times, this region has been a famous frontier, with mountains and hills like embroidered clouds, and battles fought fiercely, leaving bloodstains. Seeing the battlefield clouds, now cold and deserted, with occasional vultures circling, and the quiet watchtower, the morning moon still resembles a curved jade bow. Looking westward towards Dingyuan, there are still military commands and generals preparing on the altar, with the sound of bells in the evening and reports of peace at night. Playing the flute leisurely, surrounded by nobles and singers, but the spirit of the drunken soldiers lingers around Helan Mountain, waiting to conquer the Xianling." The General gave him a hundred pieces of white gold, but the person was still dissatisfied and left. The lyrics are still passed down today.

    Gao Zuo, a man from Liaodong, was promoted early in his career and had a reputation for being able and efficient, with no one able to match his clarity and sensitivity in official duties. He was particularly bold and valued righteousness, daring to act. In the early years of the Zhenyuan era, he was appointed as the governor of Henan Prefecture. The main commander, Wen Deheng, was a deceitful person. When faced with affairs, he did not yield, leading to a conflict. At that time, northern troops were besieging Yan Capital, and the situation was dire. There were no loyalist armies from the four directions, but he alone felt a sense of urgency and repeatedly encouraged Fu Xing. Fu Xing was intimidated and falsely accused him of having ulterior motives, leading to his arrest. Prominent scholars like Pang Caiqing, Lei Xiyan, and Xin Jingzhi were all implicated and tortured without any evidence. However, he was ultimately imprisoned and died in prison. The rest were released when amnesty was granted.

    52

    公既卒朝命下除公河南路安抚副使代福兴士夫痛愤后朝廷知其寃谪福兴逺郡昭雪之屏山于人材少许可至论公独以为真济世材又言其学术端正可以为吾儒砥柱时之不幸为奸人所害屏山以诗哭之甚哀雷希顔又为文以祭述其事为时所称屏山又将文其碑未着死后其子属之雷公雷公以其仇人犹在亦未着死迄今事状不详惜哉公诗亦髙余家有数十篇遭乱失去尝记其中秋诗有云跳上玉龙背抱得银蟾光亦竒语也
    　　杨尚书云翼字之美平定人先擢词赋第又经义魁入仕能官练逹吏事通材也南渡为翰林学士吏部尚书御史中丞将大拜以风疾止再为学士卒【案大金国志亦云终于翰林学士攷金史本正大三年二月复为礼部尚书兼侍读三年卒金百官志翰林院侍读学士从三品翰林学士正三品云兼侍读则与兼翰林学士不同况以礼部尚书兼侍读则礼部尚书乃其正秩又案元好问杨文献神道碑亦称二月复为礼部尚书兼侍读明年复知益政院四年知礼部贡举以攷试劳心遘疾

    Explanation

    52

    After the person's death, an imperial decree appointed him as the Deputy Pacification Commissioner of Henan Province to replace Fu Xing. Scholars and officials were deeply grieved and angry, but later the court recognized his injustice and exiled Fu Xing to a distant province, clearing his name. Screen Mountain is sparing in his approval of talents, but considers him a true talent for saving the world and says his academic principles are upright, making him a pillar for Confucian scholars. Unfortunately, he was harmed by villains. Screen Mountain wrote a poem to mourn him, expressing deep sorrow. Lei Xiyuan also wrote an essay to commemorate him, which was highly praised at the time. Screen Mountain planned to inscribe his tombstone, but it was not completed. After his death, his son entrusted this task to Master Lei, but Master Lei did not inscribe it because his enemy was still alive. To this day, the details are unclear. What a pity. His poetry is also excellent. I had several dozen of his poems, but they were lost during the chaos. I once remembered his Mid-Autumn Festival poem, which says, "Leaped onto the back of the Jade Dragon and embraced the light of the Silver Moon." It is also a remarkable phrase.

    Yang Shangshu Yun Yi, whose courtesy name is Meizhi, is from Pingding. He was first selected for his literary talent and then became the champion in the examination of classical texts. He is capable in official duties and experienced in administrative matters, being a versatile talent. After the Southern Migration, he served as a Hanlin Academician, Minister of Personnel, and Censor-in-Chief. He was about to be promoted to a higher position, but was stopped due to a wind disease. He served as a Hanlin Academician again before his death. According to the History of the Great Jin Dynasty, he also died as a Hanlin Academician. According to the Jin History biography, in the second month of the third year of Zhengda, he was reappointed as the Minister of Rites and also served as a Reader. He died in the third year. According to the Jin Dynasty Officials' Register, the rank of Hanlin Reader is third class, and the rank of Hanlin Academician is first class. Serving as a Reader is different from serving as an Academician. Especially when serving as a Minister of Rites and also a Reader, the Minister of Rites is his main position. According to the Tombstone Inscription of Yang Literature by Yuan Haowen, he was also reappointed as the Minister of Rites and Reader in February. The following year, he again served as the Director of the Yizheng Institute. In the fourth year, he was in charge of the Ministry of Rites' examination. He suffered from a disease due to the laborious work of the examination.

    53

    明年八月之七日卒不云以翰林学士终其为翰林学士则在正大元年本与神道碑所谓复为礼部尚书者正由翰林学士复任礼部耳与此志所云终于翰林学士异】士论惜之公笃学于九流无不通又善天文学博洽人莫及尝上疏谏宣宗南征鞫狱以寛恕待士谦甚士无贤不肖称焉晚年与赵闲闲齐名为一时人物领袖且屡知贡举多得人南渡时诏皆公笔其应制白兎诗云光揺玉斗三千丈气傲金风五百霜又吊余先子有云清华方翰府憔悴忽佳城其余文字甚多家有集子恕
    　　庞户部铸字才卿辽东人少擢第仕有能名南渡为翰林待制迁户部侍郎坐游贵戚家出倅东平擢京兆路转运使卒博学能文工诗书蔼然为一时名士其题杨秘监雪谷晓装图云溪流咽咽山昬昬前山后山同一云天公谈玉屑喷散为花雨白纷纷诗翁痩马之何许忍冻吟诗太清苦老奴寒缩私自语作奴莫作诗奴苦木僵石桥鸟不飞山路益深诗益竒老奴忍哭怜公痴不知诗好将何为杨侯胸中富丘壑醉里笔端驱雪落如何不把此诗翁画向草堂深处着

    Explanation

    53

    In the following year, on the seventh day of the eighth month, he passed away. The records do not state that he died as a翰林学士. He became a翰林学士in the first year of Zhengda, as mentioned in his biography and epitaph, where it is said that he was again appointed as the Minister of Rites. This was because he was reappointed to the Ministry of Rites from his position as翰林学士. However, this record states that he died as a翰林学士, which differs from the other accounts. Scholars lamented his passing. He was deeply learned and had no knowledge he did not acquire, and he was also skilled in astronomy. His learning was broad and profound, unmatched by others. He once submitted a memorial to advise Emperor Xuan on the southern expedition and handled cases with leniency, treating scholars with kindness. He was very humble, and scholars, regardless of their status, praised him. In his later years, he was on par with Zhao Xianxian in reputation and was a leader among the prominent figures of his time. He frequently presided over the imperial examinations and selected many capable individuals. During the Southern Migration, all imperial edicts were written by him. His poem on the white rabbit for the imperial command says, "Its light shines three thousand feet, shaking the jade ladle. Its spirit is proud, with five hundred frosts in the golden wind." His poem mourning my deceased father says, "The elegant and clear hall of the翰府. Suddenly, in the beautiful tomb, he appears emaciated." He had many other writings, and his family has a collection of his works, named Shu.

    庞户部铸字才卿, a native of Liaodong, passed the imperial examinations at a young age and had a reputation for his abilities. After the Southern Migration, he served as an翰林待制and was promoted to Minister of Revenue. He was demoted for associating with the nobility and was appointed as the deputy governor of Dongping. He was later promoted to the position of transportation commissioner for the Jingzhao road and passed away. He was well-versed in literature and skilled in poetry and calligraphy, and he was considered a notable scholar of his time. His poem on Yang Mijian's Snowy Valley Morning Dressing says, "The stream murmurs, the mountains are dim. The front and rear mountains are covered with the same clouds. The Heavenly Emperor talks about the玄玉屑, scattering it like a white flower rain. Where is the thin poet on his lean horse? He endures the cold to recite poetry in the vast emptiness. The old servant shivers and whispers to himself, 'Don't be a poet servant, it's too cold.' The wooden bridge is frozen, the birds do not fly, the mountain path is deeper, the poetry is more extraordinary. The old servant endures the tears, pitying the public's foolishness. He does not know what is good about poetry. Yang Hou's chest is rich with hills and valleys, driving the snow from his pen in drunkenness. Why not paint this poet in the depths of the thatched hut?"

    54

    张运使彀字伯英许州人少擢第以谨愿纯厚著名尝为监察御史言奸臣赫舍哩执中事【案赫舍哩旧作纥石烈今改】士论壮之后以母丧归居许之西城有园圃号小斜川花木泉石然一佳处公日在其间行吟坐啸客至一觞一咏尽欢襟韵翛然君子儒也寻判隰州刺史召为户部郎中【案金史本召为刑部郎中与此异】同知河南府迁平阳路转运使卒公莅官以廉俸禄未尝妄糜布衣蔬食泊如也性友爱弟瑴才髙相与甚欢所蓄称其所用独好收古人器物所在购求以是丛子古镜尤多其様制不可徧识字画劲古有顔平原风诗学黄鲁

    Explanation

    54

    Zhang Yunshi, courtesy name Bo Ying, was from Xuzhou. He rose to prominence early and was famous for being cautious, sincere, and upright. He once served as a censor and denounced the corrupt official He She Li Zhi Zhong (赫舍哩执中). The scholars praised him highly. After his mother's death, he returned home and lived in the western city of Xuzhou, where he had a garden called Xiao Xie Chuan (小斜川), filled with flowers, trees, springs, and stones, a delightful place. He spent his days there, walking and reciting poetry, sitting and sighing, enjoying the company of guests with wine and verse, his demeanor free and untrammeled, a true gentleman scholar. Soon, he became the governor of Xizhou, was summoned to serve as a minister of the Ministry of Revenue, served as the deputy governor of Henan Prefecture, and was promoted to the position of transport commissioner of Pingyang Road, where he died. He governed with integrity, never squandering his salary, wearing plain clothes and eating simple food, living a simple and unpretentious life. He was friendly and loving towards his brother Ruo, who was highly talented, and they were very happy together. His possessions matched his needs, and he especially liked collecting ancient artifacts, seeking them out wherever he went. He collected many ancient mirrors, the designs and shapes of which were too numerous to recognize all. The inscriptions on the mirrors were bold and ancient, with the style of Yan Zhenqing (颜平原). His poetry was influenced by Huang Ruo (黄鲁).

    55

    直格尝赠余先子诗云丘垤孰与南山尊公卿皆出山翁门遗文人共师夫子隂徳天教有是孙问礼庭中新有桂忘忧堂下旧多萱人间乐事君兼有歌我新诗侑夀樽此斜川时事也赴隰州被召时又寄诗有句云溪口急流裁燕尾山腰世路转羊肠到郡莅官才九日过家上冢正重阳陈司谏规字正叔绛州人弱冠擢第南渡为监察御史上宣宗十事直言当时得失忤防出为徐州帅府经厯官正大初收用旧人召为右司谏数上书论事改刑部郎中以事罢再为阙【案金史本正大元年召为右司谏数上章言事寻权吏部郎中未尝任刑部郎中志云以事罢

    Explanation

    55

    Zhi Ge once gifted my late father with a poem that reads:

    How can a hillock compare to the dignity of Mount Tai?
    All officials and high-ranking nobles descend from the mountain man's door.
    His legacy is studied by scholars as a model.
    Heaven has bestowed upon him such a worthy grandson.
    In the courtyard of propriety, there is now a new osmanthus.
    Under the Forgetful Hall, there were many lilies.
    In the human world, you have all the joys.
    Sing my new poem to toast to longevity.
    This is the story of the Xiechuan period.
    When summoned to Xizhou, he sent another poem with these lines:
    At the mouth of the stream, the swift current cuts like a swallow's tail.
    Through the mountains, the path twists and turns like the intestines of a sheep.
    Upon arriving at the prefecture, he took office only nine days later.
    He visited his family and ancestral graves on the Double Ninth Festival.

    Chen Guigui, a man of integrity and advice, was from the state of Jizhou.
    At the age of twenty, he passed the imperial examination and moved south.
    He served as a censor, presenting ten matters to Emperor Xuanzong.
    He spoke frankly about the gains and losses of the time.
    Due to his frankness, he was exiled to serve as an official in the military governorate of Xuzhou.
    In the early years of Zhengda, he was recalled and reappointed.
    He was summoned to serve as a censor in the right office.
    He frequently submitted memorials to discuss matters.
    He was later appointed as the head of the Criminal Department.
    He was dismissed from office due to some matter.
    He was again appointed to a vacant position.

    (Note: The note in brackets indicates that according to the Jin History, in the first year of Zhengda, he was summoned to serve as a censor in the right office, frequently submitted memorials to discuss matters, and later temporarily served as the head of the Department of Personnel. He never served as the head of the Criminal Department. The record states that he was dismissed from office due to some matter.)

    56

    攷之本则亦以吏部铨选事为王京所讦罢后寻为补阙与此志以刑部郎中罢异】复拜司谏言事不少衰朝望甚重凡宫中举事上曰恐陈规有言近臣窃议惟畏陈正叔挺然一时直士也后出为中京副留守【案元鲜于枢困学斋杂录谓规终于右司谏与此志异】未赴卒于围城士论惜之公为人刚毅质实有古人风笃学至老不废晩喜为诗与赵雷诸公唱酬其吊人诗有云骢马余威行尚避仙凫善政去犹思人以为破的初先人见其所上十事叹曰此宰相材也【案金史本云浑源刘从益见其所上八事叹曰宰相材也与此志作十事有异攷本自

    Explanation

    56

    To examine the original record, he was also dismissed due to accusations by Wang Jing regarding matters of the Ministry of Personnel. Soon after, he was appointed as a remonstrator, which differs from the record stating he was dismissed as a clerk in the Ministry of Justice. He was again appointed as a remonstrator and continued to speak out without diminishing in courage or frequency. He was highly esteemed in the court. For any event within the palace, the emperor would say, "I fear Chen Gui will speak out." Court officials privately discussed, only fearing Chen Zhengshu standing firm, a man of integrity at that time. Later, he was appointed as a deputy governor of Zhongjing but did not take up the position, dying in a siege. Scholars lamented his passing.

    He was a man of integrity, straightforward, and had the spirit of ancient sages. He remained devoted to learning until his old age and took pleasure in writing poetry in his later years, exchanging poems with scholars like Zhao Lei. His poem of condolence included the lines, "The remaining glory of the steed still commands respect; the good deeds of the official are still remembered." People considered these lines to be accurate. Initially, his father saw the ten matters he submitted and said, "He is the material for a prime minister." According to the History of the Jin Dynasty, Liu Congyi from Hunchun saw the eight matters he submitted and said, "He is the material for a prime minister," which differs from the record stating he submitted ten matters. According to the original record.

    57

    贞祐三年至正大五年数上章言事而条陈八事在贞祐四年七月一曰责大臣以身任安危二曰任台谏以广耳目三曰崇节俭以答天意四曰选守令以结民心五曰博谋羣臣以定大计六曰重官赏以劝有功七曰选将帅以明军法八曰练士卒以振兵威反覆阳论防三千字诏付尚书省谓所言多不当寻出为徐州帅府经厯官叙载甚详必无遗其二事者此志以八为十据下文言余复从之游自非闻未审当是写偶讹】惜乎朝廷不能用后同朝相见甚懽未防先人下世余复从之游每论及时事辄愤惋葢伤其言之不行也死之日家无一金知友为之

    Explanation

    57

    From the third year of the Zhenyou era to the fifth year of the Zhengda era, he frequently submitted memorials to speak on matters, listing eight proposals in the seventh month of the fourth year of the Zhenyou era. These were: one, to hold the great ministers personally responsible for safety and danger; two, to appoint censors to broaden one's perception; three, to promote frugality to respond to heavenly will; four, to select magistrates to win the hearts of the people; five, to widely consult the ministers to determine major plans; six, to emphasize official rewards to encourage those who have achieved merit; seven, to select generals to clarify military law; eight, to train soldiers to enhance military might. He repeatedly wrote lengthy defensive arguments totaling three thousand words, and the imperial edict was sent to the Shangshu Province, which stated that much of what was said was inappropriate. Soon, he was appointed as an official in charge of the Shoufu (administrative office) of Xuzhou. The record is very detailed, so there is no doubt that the two matters mentioned were accurately recorded. This account lists ten matters instead of eight, according to the following text, I continued to associate with him. Unless it is hearsay and not verified, it is likely that there was a transcription error. It is a pity that the court did not adopt his advice. Later, when we served together in the same government, we met with great joy, but before long, my father passed away. I continued to associate with him, and whenever we discussed current affairs, we often felt frustrated and sad, as his words were not put into practice. On the day of his death, he had no money at home, and friends buried him.

    58

    许司谏古字道真河间人父安仁字子静名士汾阳军节度使公少擢第南渡为侍御史时丞相珠赫髙琪擅权变乱祖宗法度公上章劾之上知其忠常庇翼凡有奏下尚书省辄去其姓名然竟为髙琪所中贬凤翔幕正大初召为补阙迁左司谏【案金史本但云削官四阶解职未尝着贬凤翔幕官赵秉文滏水集为哀宗撰许道真致仕制有云朕初即大位稔闻直声起之于田里退闲之间超之于侍从论思之地葢追述其削官之后复召为补阙也若削官之后曽贬鳯翔幕官哀宗召之为补阙则制内不当云起之于

    Explanation

    58

    Xu Si谏an, anciently known as Daozhen, was a man from Hejian. His father, Anren, courtesy name Zijing, was a distinguished scholar and held the position of Commander of the Fenyang Army. When young, Xu Si谏an passed the imperial examinations and crossed south, serving as a Censor. At that time, Chancellor Zhuo Her and Gao Qi held power and altered the laws and regulations established by the ancestors. Xu Si谏an submitted memorials to impeach them, and the emperor knew of his loyalty and often protected him. Whenever he submitted memorials, the names were removed before they reached the Ministry of Works. However, he was eventually targeted by Gao Qi and demoted to the military staff of Fengxiang. In the early years of Zhengda, he was summoned to serve as a Censorial Officer and later promoted to Left Censor. According to the biography in the Jin History, it only mentions that he was demoted four ranks and dismissed from office, without mentioning his demotion to the military staff of Fengxiang. Zhao Bingwen, in his collection Fushui Ji, wrote a decree for Emperor Aizong about Xu Daozhen's retirement, stating, "When I first ascended the throne, I heard of his upright reputation, and I raised him from the countryside and the idle life to the position of a Censorial Officer, reflecting his recall after being demoted." If he was demoted to the military staff of Fengxiang after being demoted, then the decree should not have said "I raised him from the countryside."

    59

    田里退闲矣然此志有初贬鳯翔幕先子送之以诗云云后为凤翔録事先子又寄之以诗云云自非无据考古削官四阶在兴定三年下距哀宗初年凡七载其贬鳯翔幕后或乞休而归哀宗初年乃召之于田里退闲如制所云乎】言事稍不及昔时后致仕居嵩山下病卒平生好为诗及书然不为士大夫所重公论但称其直云初贬凤翔朝士畏髙琪故皆不敢与言余先子时为提举南京货事独以诗送之有云有晋必无楚两雄难并驱向来既发药其可止半途又曰君年迫桑榆只身忧患余双亲白杨拱同气紫荆枯

    Explanation

    59

    Having retired to the countryside and lived a leisurely life, yet there was an initial intention. He was first demoted to the position of military advisor in Fengxiang, and my father sent him a poem. Later, he was appointed as the recorder in Fengxiang, and my father sent him another poem. Unless there is no basis for historical research, he was demoted four ranks. In the third year of the Xingding era, which was seven years before the early years of Emperor Aizong's reign, after being demoted to the position of military advisor in Fengxiang, he either requested retirement and returned home. In the early years of Emperor Aizong's reign, he was summoned from his retired life in the countryside, as the imperial edict stated. His words and actions were not as vigorous as before. Later, he retired and lived at the foot of Mount Song, where he died of illness. Throughout his life, he enjoyed writing poetry and calligraphy, but was not highly regarded by the literati. Public opinion only praised his integrity. Initially demoted to Fengxiang, officials feared Gao Qi and thus dared not speak to him. My father, who was then the director of the currency office in Nanjing, alone sent him a poem, saying, "If there is a strong state like Jin, there cannot be another like Chu; two powerful states cannot coexist. Having already started the medicine, how can one stop halfway?" He also said, "Your years are approaching the end of life, left alone with your worries and sufferings. Your parents have passed away, and your siblings have also passed away."

    60

    贫无孟光舂醉无骥子扶惟有忠义名可与天壤俱葢欲坚其初志也闻者竦然多之后由叔麟之为凤翔録事先人又寄以诗云寄语多言唐谏议生还记取李师中亦此意也赵尚书思文字庭玉中山人与其弟庭秀庭直皆名进士公少擢第为省掾从完顔福兴守燕都福兴死奔诣南京行宫擢侍御史出为汝州防御使【案元好问礼部尚书赵公神道碑思文以贞祐三年达汴梁特授太府丞兴定二年陞同知西安军节度使并行六部郎中事四年始内除右司谏兼侍御史是思文初达汴梁未尝即为侍御史与此志

    Explanation

    60

    Despite lacking the support of Meng Guang in times of poverty and Jizi when inebriated, only the name of loyalty and righteousness can endure with heaven and earth forever, for the purpose was to strengthen his initial resolve. Those who heard were greatly moved and many passed it on. Due to Shulín's appointment as the governor of Fengxiang, my ancestor also sent a poem: "The message conveyed many words about the Tang censor returning alive, remember Li Shizhong, it also conveys this meaning." Zhao Shangshu Siwen and his brothers Tingyu, Tingxiu, and Tingzhi were all famous Jinshi. When he was young, he was promoted to the position of provincial clerk, serving under Wanyan Fuxing in Yanjing. After Wanyan Fuxing's death, he went to the imperial palace in Nanjing and was promoted to the position of Censor-in-Chief, then appointed as the defense commissioner of Ruzhou. According to Yuan Haowen's epitaph for Zhao Shangshu, Siwen was appointed as the Chief of the Imperial Household in Kaifeng in the third year of Zhenyou, and was promoted to the position of Deputy Governor of the Western Army in Xian'an in the second year of Xingding, and served as the Deputy Secretary of the Six Ministries. In the fourth year, he was promoted to the position of Censor-in-Chief and concurrently served as the Censor-in-Chief. This indicates that Siwen did not immediately become the Censor-in-Chief when he first arrived in Kaifeng.

    61

    所云奔诣南京行宫擢侍御史详畧互异又神道碑贞祐五年由侍御史出知虢州军事虢州刺史六年五月召为吏部郎中翰林院修撰元光改元陞同知南京路转运使正大元年移同知中京留守事四年正月改同知开封府事五年始为汝州防御使与此志擢侍御史出为汝州防御使亦详畧迥异】迁集庆军节度所在镇静吏民赖之公暇以诗酒为乐好吹笛多着乐章为人诵南渡后士大夫有典郡之荣者不及也正大末召为礼部尚书卒为侍御史时与余先子同台为礼部时予始一识也为人寛厚有君子之风

    Explanation

    61

    As stated, the person rushed to the imperial palace in the southern capital and was promoted to the position of侍御史, with varying accounts of the details. Another stele from the year 1217 records that he was appointed as the military governor of Guo, and in 1222, he was called back to serve as a吏部郎中 and翰林院修撰. After the era name was changed to Yuan Guang, he was promoted to the position of同知南京路转运使. In 1227, he was transferred to serve as the deputy governor of the central capital, and in 1228, he was appointed as the deputy governor of Kaifeng. He initially served as the military governor of Ru in 1229. The two accounts of his promotions, being promoted to侍御史 and then to the military governor of Ru, differ in detail. Later, he was promoted to the position of集庆军节度使, where he maintained peace and stability, earning the trust and reliance of the local officials and people. In his leisure time, he enjoyed poetry and wine, and he loved playing the flute, composing many musical pieces that were widely appreciated. After the Southern Song Dynasty relocated its capital to Lin'an, few officials who governed counties had such a distinguished career. In the final years of his life, he was called back to serve as the minister of rites, and he died while serving as a侍御史. At that time, he and my father served together in the礼部, and I first met him then. He was a broad-minded and virtuous person, embodying the qualities of a noble individual.

    62

    萧尚书贡字真卿京兆人少为名进士时号三萧南渡为户部尚书后致仕还乡卒公博学尝注史记又着萧氏公论数万言评古人成败得失甚有理
    　　史翰林公奕字宏文【案中州集公奕字季宏水集史少中碑亦称公奕字曰季宏与此志异】大名人工书有能名自号嵗寒堂主人正大初为翰林修撰又充益政院官为上谏书后致仕居亳卒【案中州集传公奕以直学士致仕卒与此志为翰林修撰充益政院官致仕互异】重厚人也崔翰林禧字伯善卫州人与屏山同年进士也长于史学厯代典故无不通彻南渡为翰林待制与闲闲屏山同在院后出刺永州病卒

    Explanation

    62

    Shao Shangshu Gong, styled Zhenqing, was from Jingzhao. He was a renowned Jinshi at a young age, often referred to as one of the Three Shao. After the Southern Migration, he served as the Minister of Revenue. Later, he retired and returned to his hometown, where he passed away. He was highly learned and once annotated the Records of the Grand Historian (史记). He also wrote Shao's Public Commentary (萧氏公论), a work of tens of thousands of words that critically evaluated the successes and failures of ancient people, which was very well-reasoned.

    Shi Hanlin Gong Yi, styled Hongwen, was from Daming. He was skilled in calligraphy and had a reputation for his talent. He called himself the Master of the Cold Hall (岁寒堂主人). During the Zhengda era, he served as a Hanlin Scholar and was later appointed to the Yizheng Institute, where he wrote memorials to the emperor. After retiring, he settled in Bo and passed away. [According to the Zhongzhou Collection (中州集), Gong Yi was styled Jihong, and the Shuiji Collection (水集) and the Shi Shaozhong Stele (史少中碑) also refer to him as Jihong, which differs from this record.] He was a serious and substantial person.

    Cui Hanlin Xi, styled Boshan, was from Weizhou. He was a Jinshi in the same year as Bingshan and excelled in historical studies, with knowledge of historical anecdotes and customs from various dynasties. After the Southern Migration, he served as a Hanlin Attendant and worked alongside Xianxian and Bingshan in the Hanlin Academy. Later, he was appointed as the Governor of Yongzhou and died of illness.

    63

    王翰林良臣字大用潞州人长于律诗尖新工对属南渡在馆后从李天英北征遇害其上伊喇总管【案伊喇旧作移刺今改】云笔底有神扶气力人间无处着声名又絶句云流转年光桥下水翻腾时态岭头云溪翁道号竒聋子除却松风百不闻人多之
    　　舒穆噜翰林世勣【案舒穆噜旧作石抺今改】字晋卿契丹人少有词赋声擢第读书为文有体致南渡为左司郎中坐事免久之为礼部侍郎司农太常卿翰林侍讲学士【案金史本曰久之起为礼部侍郎侍郎转司农改太常卿正大中为礼部尚书兼翰林侍讲学士元王鹗汝南遗事亦称世勣以礼部尚书兼侍讲学士中
    州集直云世勣终于礼部尚书不书侍讲学士葢兼官可畧也此志不书礼部尚书仅书兼职与本及中州集互异】从末帝东征至蔡州贼陷死有子嵩字企隆【案金史本及中州集鲜于枢困学斋杂録均云嵩字企隆与父同死蔡州之难此志但书其子嵩而不云同死蔡州之难与金史及中州集困学斋杂録互异】

    Explanation

    63

    Final Translation

    **Wang Hanlin Liangchen, courtesy name Dayong, from Luxi Prefecture, was skilled in composing regulated verse, known for its freshness and mastery of antithesis. After the Southern Migration, he followed Li Tianying on a northern campaign and was killed. His eulogy to Yi La Zongguan [Note: Originally written as Yilaji, now corrected] reads: "His writing has divine inspiration, supporting his strength; his fame is widespread throughout the world." He also wrote a quatrain: "The flowing years are like water under the bridge, turbulent times are like clouds on the mountain top. The hermit by the stream has the religious name Qilong, deaf to all sounds except the pine wind."

    **Shumu Lu Hanlin Shi Ji, courtesy name Jinqing, was a Khitan person who had a reputation for poetry and prose from a young age. He passed the imperial examinations, read extensively, and wrote with style and elegance. After the Southern Migration, he served as Left Censor but was dismissed due to some matter. Later, he held various high-ranking positions, including Left Censor of the Ministry of Rites, Minister of Agriculture, and Minister of Sacrifices, as well as a Hanlin Scholar and Imperial Reader. [Note: According to the History of Jin, after some time, he was appointed as Left Censor of the Ministry of Rites. He later became Minister of Agriculture, then Minister of Sacrifices, and during the Zhengda period, he served as Minister of Rites and Hanlin Scholar. Yuan Wang E's Remnants of the Southern Region also mentions Shi Ji serving as Minister of Rites and Hanlin Scholar. The Collection of Central State directly states that Shi Ji died as Minister of Rites, without mentioning his position as Hanlin Scholar, suggesting that concurrent positions can be omitted. This record only mentions his concurrent position, differing from the History of Jin and Collection of Central State.] He followed the last emperor on an eastern campaign, reaching Cai Prefecture, where he was killed when the city fell to the enemy. He had a son named Song, with the courtesy name Qilong. [Note: According to the History of Jin and Collection of Central State, as well as Xian Yu Chu's Miscellaneous Records from the Study of Hard Learning, all state that Song had the courtesy name Qilong and died with his father in the fall of Cai Prefecture. This record only mentions his son Song without stating that he died with his father in the fall of Cai Prefecture, differing from the History of Jin and Collection of Central State and Miscellaneous Records from the Study of Hard Learning.]

    64

    王左司□□字公玊临潢人少擢第入仕以能称大安末为左司员外郎累迁青州防御使与宰相穆延尽忠不协【案穆延旧作抺撚今改】左迁刺州南渡以病免居蔡州卒杂学喜易佛老庄书
    　　吕陈州子羽字唐卿大兴人少为名进士擢第南渡为左司郎中坐事免官后同知开封府迁陈州防御使时军旅数兴户口逃窜公因以实闻于朝而小人李涣以为不忧国失军储下吏当死公耻之缢于太康驿后朝廷知其无罪复其官公入仕以能称读书为文有士大夫风致死非其罪天下伤之
    　　李治中遹字平甫栾城人少擢第有能声工诗善画与屏山诸公游自号寄庵老人蔼然名士大夫也南渡授东平府治中后致仕居钧台病卒有子冶屏山尝赠诗云寄庵丈人眼如月墨妙诗工兼画絶儒术吏事更精研只向宦途如许拙为监察御史言赫舍哩执中不法事闻者竦然

    Explanation

    64

    Translation:

    Wang, the Left Office official, whose courtesy name was Gongyu, was from Linhuang. He passed the imperial examinations early in his career and was known for his ability. At the end of the Dà'ān era, he served as an Assistant in the Left Office and was later promoted to Military Governor of Qingzhou. He did not get along well with Chancellor Mu Yan (or Mu Yanjin). He was demoted to Military Governor of a state and, during the Southern Migration, resigned due to illness and lived in Cai Prefecture until his death. He had diverse interests and enjoyed studying the I Ching, Buddhism, Daoism, and the works of Laozi and Zhuangzi.

    Lu Shenyu, courtesy name Tangqing, was from Daxing. He was a famous jinshi and passed the imperial examinations early in his career. During the Southern Migration, he served as an Assistant in the Left Office but was dismissed from office due to an incident. Later, he served as Deputy Governor of Kaifeng Prefecture and was promoted to Military Governor of Chen Prefecture. During frequent military campaigns, many people fled their homes. He reported the truth to the court, but a person named Li Huan accused him of failing to care for the state and losing military supplies. He was sentenced to death by officials, which he felt ashamed of, and committed suicide by hanging at the Taikang station. Afterward, the court realized he was innocent and restored his official position. He was known for his ability and wrote with the demeanor of a scholar-official. He died unjustly, and the world mourned him.

    Li Zhizhong, courtesy name Pingfu, was from Luancheng. He passed the imperial examinations early in his career and was known for his ability. He was skilled in poetry and painting and associated with various scholars in Pingshan. He called himself the Old Man of the Hermitage and was a distinguished scholar-official. During the Southern Migration, he was appointed as the chief of the Eastern Ping Prefecture and retired later. He lived in Juntai and died of illness. He had a son named Li, who lived in Pingshan and once wrote a poem in tribute to him, saying: "Old Man of the Hermitage, your eyes are like the moon. Your calligraphy is exquisite, and your poetry and painting are unparalleled. Your knowledge of Confucianism and governance is even more profound, yet you were so humble in your official career." As a censor, he criticized the illegal actions of Hesheri Zhi Zhong, and those who heard were shocked.

    65

    潘翰林希孟字仲明磁州人少擢第南渡为吏部主事迁翰林修撰后病风疾卒为文条畅有法宣宗哀册玉册皆其笔也
    　　郭翰林伯英字伯诚上党人第进士为南顿西平令有治迹正大中由应奉迁修撰以风疾暴终为人质厚不茍合喜读书为文词有香山赋诸公皆有诗
    　　刘翰林祖谦字光甫解州人少擢第为吏有声由宁陵令丁父忧数年不调南渡召为大理司直拜监察御史出为河南府判官再召为翰林修撰【案中州集祖谦由武胜军节度副使召为翰林修撰与此志由府判官被召有异】遭乱北迁为兵士所杀【案中州集不云为兵士所杀与此志异】公博学间通佛老百家书从赵闲闲李屏山诸公游甚为所重谈论亹亹不穷援笔为文竒士也尝请屏山志其父墓屏山以事废命予代焉铭辞屏山笔也迨屏山殁公以文祭有曰凤不足以言瑞龟不足以效灵吾视之其犹龙也诸公称之

    Explanation

    65

    Pan Ximeng, a Hanlin Academy member, had the courtesy name Zhongming and was from Cizhou. He passed the imperial examination at a young age and served as a deputy in the Ministry of Personnel during the Southern Migration. He later became a Hanlin Academy member and wrote with clear and well-organized style. The mourning document and precious document for Emperor Xuanzong were both written by him.

    Guo Boying, another Hanlin Academy member, had the courtesy name Bocheng and was from Shangdang. He passed the imperial examination and served as the magistrate of Nandun and Xiping, leaving a record of effective governance. During the reign of Emperor Lizong, he was promoted from his position as a court attendant to a Hanlin Academy member. He died suddenly due to a physical ailment. He was honest and sincere, not compromising for the sake of fitting in, and enjoyed reading and writing literary works. His poem "Xiangshan Fu" was praised by many scholars.

    Liu Zuqian, yet another Hanlin Academy member, had the courtesy name Guangfu and was from Jiezhou. He passed the imperial examination at a young age and served as an official with a good reputation. After serving as the magistrate of Ningling, he took care of his father's funeral and did not receive a promotion for several years. During the Southern Migration, he was summoned to serve as a deputy in the Ministry of Justice and was appointed as a censor. He was then sent to serve as a judge in the Henan Prefecture and was summoned again to serve as a Hanlin Academy member. However, he was killed by soldiers during a period of chaos when he fled north. He was widely learned and familiar with the teachings of Buddhism, Daoism, and various schools of thought. He associated with scholars such as Zhao Xianxian and Li Pingshan and was highly respected for his endless eloquence and never-ending conversation. He wrote literary works with ease and fluency and was considered a remarkable person. He once asked Li Pingshan to write an inscription for his father's tomb, but Li Pingshan was unable to do so due to some matter and asked him to write it instead. The inscription was written by Li Pingshan. After Li Pingshan's death, he wrote a memorial to honor him, saying, "A phoenix is not enough to be called auspicious, a turtle is not enough to be called effective; I see him as a dragon." Many scholars praised him.

    66

    与余父子交尝属余作蒲萄酒赋题其父所画河山形势诗亦一知己也冯吏部延登字子俊吉州人少擢第南渡为太常博士累迁吏部郎中翰林待制奉使北朝逾年归迁吏部侍郎【案金史本天兴元年五月冯延登以奉使有劳授礼部侍郎大金国志亦云正大末北使二年乃还天兴改元授礼部侍郎与此志所云归迁吏部侍郎异】遭乱不知所终公为人谨厚吏事亦精笃学问长年犹不辍在公署日抄书为文苦思尚竒涩诗亦新巧可称与余先子交最善先子入翰林公与赵闲闲所荐也平生著述甚多尝以示余乱后失散可惜

    Explanation

    66

    A close friend of my father and I, I once wrote an ode to grape wine and inscribed a poem on the painting of the river and mountain landscape by his father, also a true friend. Lianding, courtesy name Zijun, from Ji'an, was young and selected for the imperial examination, served as a Taichang Doctor after the Southern Migration, and was gradually promoted to the position of Langzhong in the Ministry of Personnel, and then to the position of Hanlin Academy Attendant. He was sent on a mission to the Northern Court and returned after more than a year, and was promoted to the position of Langzhong in the Ministry of Personnel. During the chaos, his fate is unknown. He was cautious and sincere, excellent and devoted to official duties, and continued his studies even in old age, copying books, writing essays, and thinking deeply, striving for odd and obscure styles. His poetry was also fresh and ingenious, worthy of praise. He was the best friend of my father, who entered the Hanlin Academy, and it was recommended by Mr. Zhao Xianxian. He had many writings throughout his life, which he once showed to me, but they were lost in the chaos, which is regrettable.

    67

    时治中戬字天保后改字多福沧州人少为人奴后读书为学第进士其主良之南渡为监察御史厯清要致仕卒为人纯厚好学多读易左氏春秋君子儒也自号拙庵尝属余作记与余家三世交
    　　王府判仲元字清卿东平人广道先生之孙也工书法赵黄山自号锦峯老人卒于京兆幕
    　　张司直谷英字仲杰赵州人擢经义髙第从屏山诸公游为文以多为胜尝为南顿令从军数年入为省掾大理司直卒自号无着道人屏山为作梦记予先子同年进士也

    　　归潜志巻四
    　　钦定四库全书
    　　归潜志巻五
    　　元　刘祁　撰
    　　王翰林彪字武叔大兴人贞祐五年经义魁也为文颇驰骋波澜性疎放嗜酒不拘细事初对廷策宣宗喜其文以为似古人特授太子副司经国史院编修官进司经末帝在东宫颇见知后入翰林为应奉迁修撰出为平凉府治中入为待制出刺州未赴南京被围食乏服絶粒药俄饮酒被药死尝赋吕唐卿海藏斋诗云虚白云中含法界软红尘底寄虚舟又只应乌帽红尘底羞见苍烟白鹭洲亦可喜也

    67

    Translation

    Zhizhong Jian, courtesy name Tianbao, later changed to Duofu, was from Cangzhou. He was once a slave but later studied and passed the imperial examinations to become a Jinshi. His master treated him well, and during the Southern Migration, he served as a censor, holding important positions, and retired and died. He was a person of pure and kind nature, loved learning, and read extensively the I Ching, Zuo Zhuan, and Spring and Autumn Annals. He was a Confucian scholar of high moral character and gave himself the nickname Zhuanan. He once asked me to write a memorial, and we had three generations of friendship with my family.

    Wangfupan, courtesy name Qingqing, was from Dongping, the grandson of Guangdao Xian. He was skilled in calligraphy and was a contemporary of Zhao Huangshan, who gave himself the nickname Jinfeng Laoren. Wangfupan died in the office of the capital.

    Zhangsizhi, courtesy name Zhongjie, was from Zhaozhou. He was selected as a top candidate in the imperial examinations for Confucian classics and studied with scholars from Pingshan. He wrote essays that were valued for their quantity, once served as the magistrate of Nandun, served in the military for several years, later served as an assistant in the provincial government, and was a high-ranking official in the judicial department. He died and gave himself the nickname Wuzhuo Daoren. Pingshan wrote a dream record about him, and my father and he were both Jinshi in the same year.

    Gui Qian Zhi Volume Four
    Qinding Siku Quanshu
    Gui Qian Zhi Volume Five
    Compiled by Liu Qi of the Yuan dynasty.
