    Wang Hanlin, courtesy name Wushu, was from Daxing. He was the top candidate in the imperial examinations for Confucian classics in the fifth year of the Zhenyou era. He wrote essays that were expansive and full of emotion, was a free-spirited person who loved alcohol and did not care about trivial matters. When he first presented his policy proposals to the court, Emperor Xuanzong liked his writing, thinking it resembled ancient works, and specially appointed him as an assistant in the National History Institute. He was later promoted to the position of Chief of the National History Institute. The last emperor, while still a prince, knew and appreciated him. Later, he entered the Hanlin Academy as a secretary and was promoted to the position of historian, was appointed as the magistrate of Pingliang Prefecture, later returned to serve in the imperial court as an advisor, and was appointed as the governor of a state but did not reach Nanjing, which was besieged, and died after taking medicine to abstain from food, only to drink alcohol and die from the medicine. He once wrote a poem for Lü Tangqing's Haicang Zhai, which says, "In the white clouds, the Dharma realm is contained. In the soft red dust, a virtual boat is寄托. Is also delightful."

    68

    张翰林直字子忠河内人少工词赋尝魁进士平阳南渡为国史院编修官迁应奉翰林文字在馆五六年从赵闲闲游性朴澹好学敬善谦甚士多爱之闲闲本注太子忠尝言亲授于闗中士薛子明因相与讲辨甚久俄丁母忧出馆居南京从学者甚众束脩惟以市书恶衣粝食虽仕宦如贫士也同年如雷宋诸人皆以声名意气相豪子忠独恬退以学自乐正大初余先子入翰林子忠从之游后先子下世有挽诗云桃李双凫舄风霜一豸冠才华惊世易勲
    业到头难白日空金马青天下玊棺家有贤子文武似欧韩甚为诸公所称先子殁与余善后南京被围阙食余遇之富城西敝衣蓝缕可怜已而闻鬻卜天街值一回鹘问卜子忠以文语应之为回鹘所殴北渡将还乡道病死哀哉张翰林仲安字晋臣燕山人贞祐六年词赋魁也为人谦谨有礼法时辈称焉为文亦平畅得体尤工词赋自居太学有声入翰林为应奉秩未满卒士论皆惜之髙斯诚字法飏大兴人至宁九年经义魁也读书有学问与王从之李之纯游为

    Explanation

    68

    Zhang Hanlin, courtesy name Zi Zhong, was from He Nei. He was young and skilled in composing poetry and prose, having once topped the imperial examination. During the Southern Migration, he served as an official in the National History Bureau, later promoted to the position of drafting documents for the imperial court. He spent five or six years in the Hanlin Academy, where he studied under Zhao Xianxian. Zhang was simple and unassuming, devoted to learning, and highly respected for his humility. Zhao Xianxian, who had been taught the Tai Xuan by a scholar from Guanzhong named Xue Ziming, often discussed these teachings with Zhang for a long time. Soon after, Zhang's mother passed away, and he left the academy to mourn her in Nanjing. Many students followed him, and he lived frugally, spending his income on books and wearing simple clothing. Despite his official position, he lived like a poor scholar. His contemporaries, such as Lei and Song, were known for their fame and boldness, but Zhang remained humble and devoted to his studies, finding joy in learning. In the early years of the Zhengda era, my father entered the Hanlin Academy, and Zhang followed him there. After my father's death, Zhang wrote a mourning poem: "Two sons, like two magpies, wear their caps in the wind and frost. Their talents astonish the world, but their achievements are hard to come by. The sun sets, leaving the golden horse empty, and the jade coffin descends into the blue sky. They have virtuous sons, both scholarly and martial, like Ouyang Xiu and Han Yu, and they are highly praised by all. After my father's death, I became close friends with Zhang. Later, when Nanjing was besieged and food was scarce, I met him in the west of Fucheng, where he was wearing tattered clothes, looking pitiful. I heard that he had been selling divination on the street when he encountered a Huihu, who beat him for answering in literary terms. On his way north, he fell ill and died on the road. How tragic!

    Zhang Hanlin, courtesy name Zhong'an, was from Yan Mountain. In the sixth year of the Zhengyuan era, he topped the imperial examination for poetry and prose. He was modest, courteous, and well-versed in etiquette, earning the respect of his contemporaries. His writing was smooth and well-structured, especially in poetry and prose. He gained fame while studying at the Imperial Academy and later served in the Hanlin Academy as a draftsman. He died before completing his term, and many scholars lamented his loss.

    Gao Sicheng, courtesy name Fayang, was from Daxing. In the ninth year of the Zining era, he topped the imperial examination for Confucian classics. He was well-read and knowledgeable, and he was friends with Wang Congzhi and Li Zhi Chun.

    69

    诗文枯淡自得初调凤翔府录事为行部檄监支纳陈州仓因忤郡魁吏搆之下狱防死已而赦免病终颇喜浮屠自号唯庵与余先子善刘遇字鼎臣真定人兴定五年词赋魁也少与王从之周晦之游兼经义学有誉南渡为国史院书写已而擢第应奉翰林后出为鄜州帅府经厯官遇害【案王若虚滹南集刘鼎臣墓铭曰时闗右扰扰鄜畤被兵帅臣赫舍哩承诏往援表君从事至则城防遂不知所终与此志所云遇害异】尝与余同文防且同试于廷读书有文学
    　　张翔字茂进太原人第进士为南京货司勾当官迁南京麫使出为太康令莅官清苦有治声好书从士大夫讲学为文作诗有志于时名遭乱殍卒与余交最善董治中文甫字国华潞州人第进士南渡尝为大理司直后为河南府治中卒【案中州集文甫后为昌武军节度副使以公事至杞县与此志所云后为河南府治中异】自号无事老人为人淳

    Explanation

    69

    Translation

    Poetry and prose that are simple, plain, and self-satisfied in their early stages. He served as a recorder in Fengxiang Prefecture, supervising the collection of grain in Chenzhou granary according to an edict from the governor. Due to offending the prefectural chief, he was framed by the officials and imprisoned with the intention of causing death. Later, he was pardoned but died of illness. He greatly favored Buddhism and gave himself the name "Wei'an." He was friendly with my father. Liu Yu, styled Dingchen, was from Zhending. In the fifth year of Xingding, he won first place in the literary composition exam. As a young man, he studied with Wang Congzhi and Zhou Huizhi, excelling in both classical and modern learning. After crossing the river southward, he served as a scribe in the National History Bureau and was later promoted to a position in the Imperial Academy. He was then appointed as an official in the Fuzhou military governorate, where he met his demise. [According to Wang Ruoxu's Huinan Ji, Liu Dingchen's tombstone inscription states that during the chaotic times in the west, Fuzhou was under attack, and the military commander, Hesheli, was ordered to provide assistance. Liu was appointed to accompany him, but upon arrival, the city was already fortified, and his fate after that remains unknown, differing from what is recorded here as "met his demise."] He once shared the same literary circle with me and took the same exams in the imperial court. He loved books and studied with scholars and officials, writing poetry and prose with aspirations for fame in his time, but he suffered from chaos and died of starvation. He was my closest friend. Zhang Xiang, styled Maojin, was from Taiyuan. After passing the imperial examination, he served as an official in charge of the customs office in Nanjing, later promoted to the position of customs commissioner of Nanjing, and then sent to serve as the magistrate of Taikang County. In office, he was simple and hardworking, known for his good governance. He loved books and studied with scholars and officials, writing poetry and prose with aspirations for fame in his time, but he suffered from chaos and died of starvation. He was my closest friend. Dong Zhi, styled Guohua, was from Luchou. After passing the imperial examination, he served as a magistrate in the capital, later promoted to a position in the capital, and then sent to serve as the governor of Henan. [According to Zhongzhou Ji, Dong Guohua later served as a deputy military governor of Changwu, where he died on official business, differing from what is recorded here as "sent to serve as the governor of Henan."] He gave himself the name "Wushilao" and was a kind person.

    70

    谨笃实学道有得其学参取佛老二家不喜髙逺竒异循循常道临终豫知死期斋浴而逝时人异之兴定初余先子居防淮阳公乗过焉谈道竟夕予时为童子窃聴牕下葢其于六经论孟诸书凡一章一句皆深思思而有得必以力行为事不徒诵説而已既去先子大称之后于郝文国才处得所着一编皆论道之文迄今藏余家其子安仁其学亦谨厚人也
    　　申编修万全字百胜髙平人与其兄无移百福俱擢第百福为人沉重不妄交好经学勤勤君子儒也尝为郑县令爱民慎狱不为赫誉邑民便之后召入史馆俄摄监察御史应奉翰林居京师朝归闭门讲诵不出覩时事不惬意屡欲以母老归未果也正大末为南征行台辟掌书檄至淮上大雨宵行溺水死士论惜之赵闲闲为文以祭哀甚初百胜在太学与雷丈希顔及余先君同舍相善先君尝称其为人后公入朝先君已下世余因得从游为文亦典雅有体

    Explanation

    70

    The scholar was diligent and earnest in his study of the Dao, gaining insight through practical and grounded learning. He drew from both Buddhism and Daoism but did not favor lofty, distant, or strange things. He followed the ordinary path, and at the time of his death, he knew his time in advance. He passed away after bathing and fasting, and people were amazed by his composure.

    In the early years of the Xingding era, my father was in Fanyang, and the scholar passed by in a carriage. They talked about the Dao all night. I was a child at the time and secretly listened from under the window. He deeply thought about every chapter and sentence of the Six Classics, the Lunyu, and other important texts, gaining insight and putting effort into action, not merely reciting and explaining.

    Later, I met the scholar's son, Anren, who inherited his father's learning. He was a cautious and thick-hearted person.

    Wan Quan, a scholar and official named Bai Sheng, and his brother Bai Fu, both passed the imperial examinations. Bai Fu was serious and responsible, not engaging in frivolous friendships. He was a diligent and virtuous scholar, often serving as a magistrate in Zheng County, where he loved the people and handled cases with caution, not seeking a glorious reputation. The people found him convenient, and later he was summoned to the imperial court. He briefly served as an inspector and a翰林, living in the capital. In the morning, he returned home and closed the door to study, not witnessing the affairs of the world. He was not content and often wished to return home because of his elderly mother, but he did not succeed. In the final years of the Zhengda era, he was appointed to the military command post in the south, where he handled official documents. On his way to the Huai River, it rained heavily at night, and he drowned while traveling at night. The scholars lamented his death, and Zhao Xianxian wrote an article to commemorate him, expressing great sorrow.

    Initially, Bai Sheng was a student at the Imperial Academy, where he was a fellow student with Lei Xiyang and my father. My father often spoke highly of him. After he entered the imperial court, my father had already passed away, and I thus had the opportunity to follow and learn from him. His writing was elegant and well-structured.

    71

    许国字至忠懐州人少擢第有能名性闲淡不鋭仕进居卢氏西山下不赴调数年后召为南京丰衍库使倾家赀市书后告归赵闲闲诸公多重之余尝至其家敝衣粝食环堵萧然葢清苦之士也未乱病卒
    　　王贡字安之北京人参知政事之翰从子也擢第以修洁称南渡得度居郾操行纯谨时人重之后病卒王彧字子文洺州人少擢第南渡为省掾睹时政将乱一旦弃妻子径入嵩山剪发为头陀自号了然居士改名知非字无咎居达摩庵苦行自修朝廷初疑焉遣使亷之知其非矫伪乃止当世号王居名甚髙后十余年忽下山归其家复与妻子如旧妻死更娶又仕为洛阳行
    省参议遭乱不知所终嗟乎有始有卒者难矣哉马天采字元章太原人擢第与雷希顔宋飞卿同年为人诡怪好异又喜为惊世骇俗之行人莫测也南渡为史院编修官不事麻绦草履沈浮闾里殊无朝士风杂学通太数又善绘画及塑像虽居官辄为人塑画自神颇善李屏山当屏山殁为写真且题以赞皆怪语末曰若到黄泉见鲁仲连蔺相如道余示其狂诞如此后以病终

    Explanation

    71

    许国，字至忠，怀州人。年轻时通过科举考试，以才华闻名。他性格淡泊，不热衷于仕途，住在卢氏西山下，没有接受朝廷的任命。数年后，他被召为南京丰衍库使，花费全部家产购买书籍，后来告老还乡。赵闲闲等诸公对他非常敬重，曾到他家中拜访，见到他穿着破旧的衣服，吃着粗茶淡饭，住在简陋的小屋里，生活极为清苦。他是一位清苦之士，未遇动乱就因病去世。

    王贡，字安之，北京人，参知政事王翰的侄子。他通过科举考试，以清廉著称。南渡后，他出家住在郾城，操行纯谨，受到当时人的尊重。后来因病去世。

    王彧，字子文，洺州人。年轻时通过科举考试，南渡后担任省掾，目睹时局将乱，突然抛弃妻子和孩子，直接进入嵩山，剃发为头陀，自号了然居士，改名为知非，字无咎，住在达摩庵，苦行自修。朝廷起初对他有所怀疑，派遣使者调查，得知他并非矫伪，便停止了怀疑。当时人称他为王居，名声很高。十多年后，他突然下山回家，恢复了与妻子和孩子的生活。妻子去世后，他再娶，又担任洛阳行省参议，遭遇动乱，不知所终。唉，有始有终的人真是难啊！

    马天采，字元章，太原人。他与雷希顔、宋飞卿同年通过科举考试。他为人诡怪，喜欢奇异的事物，又喜欢做惊世骇俗的事情，让人难以捉摸。南渡后，他担任史院编修官，不穿麻绦草履，生活在村子里，毫无朝士的风范。他博学多才，精通太玄数，又擅长绘画和塑像。即使在官场，他也会为自己塑像，自封为神，尤其擅长李屏山的画。当李屏山去世后，他为他画像并题写赞语，都是怪诞之语，最后说：“若到黄泉见鲁仲连、蔺相如，道余示其狂诞如此。”后来因病去世。

    72

    杨户部槙字正夫吉州人少擢第有能名南渡为左司员外郎颇与权要辨争以罢后为户部侍郎又行部河中北兵攻胡壁保将防正夫知不免先使其妻子赴黄河已从之死为人慷慨有气节士大夫多称之甚可惜也
    　　李中丞英字子贤辽东渤海人布衣以气节闻后擢第为省掾贞祐初北兵入京师与侯挚田琢请偕行提兵扼居庸闗屡战有功擢宣差都提控南渡召为御史中丞诏与元帅庆夀同率兵【案金史本诏元帅右监军永锡左都监乌库哩庆夀将兵英督粮运与此志仅称同庆夀率兵异】援燕都至潞州遇北兵战死【案金史本英至大名得兵数万与元兵
    遇于霸州北败死是英援燕都未尝由潞州与此志所云至潞州异元史太祖本纪云金御史中丞李英等率师援中都战于霸州败之又元史舒穆噜明安云遇于永清命士卒佯败金兵来追大破之攷永清与霸州相距甚近金元二史互证适符潞州去大名亦甚逺则此志潞字为霸字之误无疑】初子贤之出也河南民望太平遽防败天下惋惜朝廷襃赠焉

    Explanation

    72

    Yang Hu, the Minister of Revenue, styled Zhengfu, was from Jizhou. He was selected for an official position at a young age and had a reputation for competence. During the Southern Migration, he served as a Left Censor and was known for his disputes with powerful officials, leading to his dismissal. Later, he became a Minister of Revenue and was sent to inspect the region of Hezhong. When the Jurchen forces attacked, he knew he could not escape and ordered his wife and children to commit suicide before following suit. He was known for his noble character and strong moral principles, and many scholars and officials praised him. His death was a great loss.

    Li Ying, the Minister of Censor, styled Zixian, was from Liaodong, a commoner known for his moral integrity. He was later selected for an official position. During the early years of the Zhenyou era, when the Jurchen forces entered the capital, he requested to accompany other officials to defend the pass at Juyongguan. He fought several battles and was promoted to a high-ranking military position. He was summoned to serve as a Minister of Censor and was ordered to lead troops alongside Marshal Qingshou to reinforce the capital. He arrived at Lüzhou and encountered the enemy forces, dying in battle. When he initially set out, the people of Henan hoped for peace, but he suddenly faced defeat, causing widespread regret. The court posthumously honored him.

    (Note: The reference to "Lüzhou" in the original text is likely a misreading of "Bazhou," as indicated by the historical context and other sources.)

    73

    田总管琢字器之蔚州人少擢第为省掾贞祐初北兵围燕器之慨然来见愿出招乡里义兵守要冲宣宗壮之擢同知蔚州节度使得兵数千屡与敌战有功迁濬州防御使宣差都提控【案金史本防先为宣差兵马提控同知忠顺军节度使事后乃加河北西路宣抚副使遥授濬州防御使与此志异】南渡驻军陈州久之命守
    华州领节度使战潼闗下军败归罪于其副任铸斩之改东平路转运使俄命守益都为山东东路兵马都总管张裕之变逐器之以城北降朝廷召之将加罪道发疽卒赵闲闲有送器之诗云田侯落落竒男子主辱臣生不如死殿前画地作山西愿与义军相表里恨我不得学李英爱君不减侯华卿横遮俘尸三十万潼闗大笑哥舒翰

    Explanation

    73

    Tianshuo, Governor of the Military Governorate of Yuzhou, was from Yuxian, Hebei. He passed the imperial examination and was promoted to an assistant in the Secretariat at a young age. During the first year of the Zhengyue era, when the Jurchen (Jin) army besieged Yan (modern Beijing), Tianshuo came to see with a sense of urgency and offered to recruit volunteer troops from his hometown to defend a strategic location. Emperor Xuanzong admired him and promoted him to co-governor of the military governorate of Yuzhou. He was given command of several thousand soldiers and fought many battles against the enemy, achieving significant victories. He was later promoted to defender of Juzhou and military commissioner dispatched by the court. [According to the Jin History, he was initially appointed as military commissioner and co-governor of Zhongshun Army, and later given the honorary title of vice-minister of pacification in the western part of Hebei and defender of Juzhou, which differs from this record.]

    After the Jin dynasty retreated southward, he was stationed in Zhumadian, Henan, for a long time. He was then ordered to defend Huaxian, Shaanxi, as military governor. He fought at Tongguan but suffered a defeat, and the blame was placed on his deputy, Ren Zhu, who was executed. He was then appointed as the transport commissioner of the eastern part of Shandong and soon ordered to defend Weifang, Shandong, as commander-in-chief of the eastern Shandong region. During the Zhang Yu rebellion, Tianshuo was expelled and surrendered the city to the north. The court summoned him and was about to impose punishment, but he died of a boil on the way.

    Zhao Xianxian wrote an epitaph for Tianshuo, which reads:

    "Tianshuo, a man of extraordinary character and bearing, said that when the ruler is disgraced, it is better for the minister to die than to live. Before the emperor, he drew the map of Shanxi on the ground, willing to work in tandem with the volunteer troops. I regret not being able to learn from Li Ying, but my love for the emperor is no less than that of Hou Huaiqing. I blocked the path with the bodies of thirty thousand captives and laughed at Geshu Han at Tongguan."

    74

    梁翰林询谊字仲经绛州人户部尚书襄子也少游太学有声为人多膂力尚气节慨然有取功名志屏山诸公皆壮之尤与雷希顔善文章豪放有作者气既擢第复举宏词为应奉翰林文字出为上京留守判官宣宗南渡宗室万努【案万努旧作万奴今改】叛据上京独仲经不从以节死朝廷优赠之
    　　韩府判玉字温甫燕人少读书尚气节擢第入翰林为应奉文字后为凤翔府判官大安中北兵围燕都夏人连防边州陜西帅府檄温甫为都统【案金史本大金国志玉由同知陜西东路转运使檄授都统与此志由凤翔府判官被防异】募军得万人出屯华亭与夏人战败之而温甫毅然有勤王志因移檄闗中言词忠壮闻者感动其檄有云人谁无死有臣子之当然事至于今忍君亲之弗顾勿谓百年身后虚名一聴史臣只如今日目前何顔以居人世王侯将相宁有种乎富贵功名当自致耳或诬温甫以有异志收鞫死狱中【案金史本及大金国志均云被囚死于郡学与此志异】士大夫愤惜

    Explanation

    74

    Final Translation

    Xunyi, courtesy name Zhongjing, was a native of Jiangzhou, the son of Minister of Revenue Xiang. When young, he studied at the Imperial Academy and gained fame. He was strong and valiant, valuing righteousness, and had a determined ambition to achieve fame and glory. The scholars of Bingshan all praised him, especially his close friendship with Lei Xiyuan. His writings were bold and free, showing the spirit of a true writer. After passing the imperial examinations, he was also selected for the prestigious examination of grand words and served as a literary attendant in the Hanlin Academy. Later, he was appointed as the deputy governor of Shangjing. During Emperor Xuanzong's southern relocation, the rebel Wang Nu seized Shangjing, but Zhongjing refused to submit and died for his principles. The court posthumously honored him.

    Han, deputy governor of the provincial administration, courtesy name Wenfu, was a native of Yan. He read extensively and valued righteousness. After passing the imperial examinations, he entered the Hanlin Academy as a literary attendant and later became the deputy governor of Fengxiang Prefecture. During the Da'an period, northern troops besieged the capital of Yan, and the Western Xia forces joined the defense of border states. The governor of Shaanxi issued an order for Wenfu to serve as the commander-in-chief, and he raised an army of ten thousand and stationed them in Huating, where they defeated the Western Xia forces. Wenfu steadfastly had the resolve to support the emperor and issued a proclamation to the Guanzhong region, which was filled with loyal and brave words, moving those who heard it. His proclamation read: "Who among us does not die? It is the duty of a subject and son. How can we, today, ignore our lord and parents? Do not say that after a hundred years, a name will be left to historians. Only today, what face can we show to the people of the world? Are kings and generals born of a particular lineage? Wealth, rank, and fame must be achieved by one's own efforts." Some accused Wenfu of having ulterior motives, and he was arrested and died in prison. Scholars and officials were filled with anger and regret.

    75

    聂左司天骥字元吉五台人弱冠擢第沈静寡言不妄交入官以谨愿自守兴定初为省掾时胥吏擅威士人往往附之独元吉不少假借彼亦不能害也后平凉帅辟经厯官军败同其帅被责俄擢左司员外郎天兴改元末帝东迁留二执政居守元吉预焉崔立之变二执政死元吉亦被创甚归卧于家旬日不食卒金亡士流之在位以节死者惟元吉一人其死也其女子适以寡来归家居见其父殁亦缢死时人伤之虞卿麻革信之为作聂孝子

    Explanation

    75

    Nie Yuanji, a native of Wutai, passed the imperial examination at the age of twenty. He was quiet and reserved, not associating with people indiscriminately, and he maintained himself with diligence and sincerity. During the early years of the Xingding era, he served as a provincial clerk. At that time, officials wielded excessive power, and scholars often flattered or submitted to them, but Yuanji did not make concessions to them, and they could not harm him either. Later, the governor of Pingliang appointed him as an official. When the army was defeated, he was held accountable along with his commander, but shortly after, he was promoted to the position of Left Censor. During the reign of the last emperor, who moved eastward and changed the era name to Tianxing, two high-ranking officials were left behind to govern, and Yuanji was among them. During the Cui Li incident, the two high-ranking officials died, and Yuanji was also severely injured. He returned home and lay ill for ten days without eating before dying. Among those who remained in office after the fall of the Jin Dynasty and died with integrity, only Yuanji was one. When his daughter, who was recently widowed, came back home and saw her father dead, she also hanged herself. People at the time mourned him, and Yu Qian, Ma Ge, and Xun Zhi wrote a biography of Nie Yuanji as a filial son.

    76

    程御史震字威卿东胜人与其兄鼎和卿俱擢第公入仕有能声兴定初诏百官举县令公得陈留陈留南都属邑颇繁公治为河南第一召拜监察御史弹劾无所挠时皇子英王为宰相家僮辈往往恃势侵民公以法劾之英王怒未防坐为故吏所讼罢官【案英王名守纯宣宗子哀宗兄后晋封荆王元好问御史程君墓表云
    震既劾荆王荆王宻遣诸奴诱奸民徐章造飞语君竟以是罢与此志及金史本但云为故吏所讼小异】嵗余呕血卒公为人刚直有材干忘身殉国不少私与余先子同年擢第相得甚懽已而同为御史台纲大振小人皆侧目故俱不能久留于朝公既居闲慨然有志于学将延致名儒执弟子礼师事之防卒士论惜不尽其材
    　　魏户部琦字民英州顺圣人少词赋擢髙第为鄯阳令有治行南渡为南京留守判官迁户部员外郎郎中以材干称贞祐末北兵犯潼闗行部军前至洛阳见杀朝廷官其子焉

    Explanation

    76

    Cheng Yushi Zhen, courtesy name Weiqing, from Dongsheng, along with his elder brother Ding Heqing, both passed the imperial examinations. When he entered public service, he had a reputation for competence. In the first year of Xingding, the emperor ordered all officials to recommend county magistrates, and Cheng was appointed to Tanchao, a county under the Southern Capital, which was quite populous. His administration was ranked first in Henan. He was summoned and appointed as a Censorial Inspector, impeaching without hesitation. At that time, the Prince Ying Wang, a son of the emperor, had his attendants who often abused their power to oppress the people. Cheng impeached them according to the law. Prince Ying Wang was angry, but before he could take action, Cheng was impeached by former officials and dismissed from office. After a year, he died spitting blood. Cheng was upright, capable, and dedicated to his country, showing no favoritism. He and my father were the same year in passing the imperial examinations and became very close friends. Later, we both served as Censorial Inspectors, and the standards of the Censorate were greatly strengthened. As a result, many petty officials resented us, and we could not remain in office for long. After Cheng retired, he had a strong desire to learn and intended to invite renowned scholars to serve as his teachers. He passed away before he could realize this ambition, and scholars lamented that he did not fully develop his talents.

    Wei Hu Bu Qi, courtesy name Minying, from Xunsheng in Hongzhou, was young and excelled in poetry and prose. He passed the imperial examinations with high distinction and became the magistrate of Shanyang, where he had a good administration. During the Southern Migration, he served as the Deputy Governor of Nanjing and later as an Assistant Minister of Finance and a Deputy Minister, known for his ability. In the last year of Zhenyou, northern troops invaded Tongguan. Wei was on a tour of his jurisdiction when he reached Luoyang and was killed. The court posthumously honored his son.

    77

    乌克逊左司努森【案乌克逊旧作吾古孙努森旧作奴申今改】字道逺由女直人译史入官性伉特敢为有直气尝为监察御史时中丞完顔伯嘉以酷烈闻道逺以事纠罢【案金史完顔伯嘉云劾伯嘉违诏不遍按视及簿令不法受贿匿而不发等事与此志所云互有省文】朝士耸异后为左司郎中近侍局使皆有名天兴东狩留南京居守崔立之变同御史大夫费摩阿固岱【案费摩阿固岱旧作裴满阿虎带今改】自缢于台中与余先子善余尝为赋古漆井诗
    　　费摩御史大夫阿固岱字仲宁女直进士也仕厯清要名亚完顔苏兰【案苏兰旧作速兰今改】尝为陈州防御使累迁御史大夫使北朝崔立之变自缢死同时户部尚书完顔仲平亦自杀仲平亦女直进士也
    　　末帝寳符李氏国亡从太后皇后北迁至宣徳州居摩诃院李氏自入院止寝处佛殿中作为幡旆数合防当同后妃赴龙庭将发于佛像前自缢死且自书门纸曰寳符御侍此处身故凡施旛旆防何较之后妃辈失节者何啻霄壤甲午嵗余家武川观其遗迹

    Explanation

    77

    Ukuxun Zuo Si Nusen, styled Dao Yuan, entered office through translating Jurchen history. He was of a strong and unique character, bold and straightforward. Once serving as a censor, during the time when Vice-Chancellor Wan Yan Bojia was known for his severity, Dao Yuan was dismissed due to an incident. The officials were startled and amazed. Later, he served as Left Department Director and Attendant Bureau Director, both of whom were famous. During the eastern hunt in the Tianxing era, he was left to guard the capital. In the Cui Li rebellion, he hanged himself in the censorate along with Vice-Chancellor Feimo Agudai, who was friends with my father. I once composed a poem about the ancient lacquered well.

    Feimo Agudai, Vice-Chancellor, styled Zhongning, was a Jinshi from the Jurchen people. He served in high-ranking positions, second only to Wan Yan Sulan in fame. Once served as the defense commissioner of Chen Prefecture and later promoted to Vice-Chancellor, sent to the Northern Court. In the Cui Li rebellion, he hanged himself. At the same time, Minister of Revenue Wan Yan Zhongping also committed suicide. Zhongping was also a Jinshi from the Jurchen people.

    The concubine Li of the last emperor, after the country's fall, followed the empress dowager and empress northward, arriving at Xuande Prefecture and staying at the Mahakala Monastery. Li stayed in the Buddha hall as her sleeping quarters, making several flags and banners. She prepared to accompany the empresses to the imperial court, but before departure, she hanged herself in front of the Buddha statue, and wrote on the door paper, "Concubine Bao Fu, Imperial Attendant, here lies her body." All the flags and banners, what difference does it make? The empresses who lost their virtue are as different as heaven and earth. In the year Jia Wu, my family in Wuchuan observed her relics.

    78

    李尚书元忠字献可武川人少擢第厯清要南渡为工部尚书审决河南寃狱多所平反俄坐督修京城工不谨出为泰宁军节度使致仕居陈州每朝廷有政事不令或民间利害屡上言亦读书有学问和厚人也李陈州山字夏卿一字安仁大名人少擢第厯清要南渡同知开封府迁陈州防御使为小人所陷罢闲居南京以事赴井死为人厚重读书喜作诗号松风老人刘户部元规字子正咸平人少擢第南渡为侍御史时珠格
    髙琪为相擅权公数抗言事争殿上出同知武昌军节度使事后为户部郎中行部河中坐事斥后致仕天兴改元诏使北朝不知所终【案金史哀宗本纪正大九年二月以费摩阿固岱国世荣为讲和使四月以杨居仁奉金帛诣大元请和其四月改元天兴之后未见有刘元规奉使之事又元史太宗本纪元年己丑金遣阿固岱来归太祖之子金为正大六年而哀宗本纪于六年内不书阿固岱之使皆可见金史本纪之脱漏】

    Explanation

    78

    Li Yuanzhong, known as Xianke, was from Wuchuan. He was young when he was promoted to an official rank and served in important and prestigious positions. He moved south after the fall of the Northern Song and became the Minister of Works, where he reviewed and resolved many unjust cases in Henan, overturning many wrongful convictions. Soon, he was implicated for lax supervision of the capital city construction and was demoted to the position of military governor of Taiping. He retired and lived in Chen Prefecture, frequently speaking out about state affairs and the interests of the common people. He was also well-read and learned, with a gentle and kind nature.

    Li Chenzhou, named Shan, also known as Anren, was from Daming. He was young when he was promoted to an official rank and served in important and prestigious positions. He moved south and became the vice governor of Kaifeng Prefecture, later being promoted to the position of defense commissioner of Chen Prefecture. He was陷害 by petty people and dismissed, living in retirement in Nanjing. He died by falling into a well due to some matter. He was a heavy and kind person who loved reading and writing poetry, known as the Old Man of Pine Wind.

    Liu Yuanzhong, known as Zizheng, was from Xianping. He was young when he was promoted to an official rank and became a censor during the Southern Song. At the time, Zhu Ge was in power. The prime minister, Gao Qi, wielded great authority. Liu Yuanzhong repeatedly spoke out against his actions, even arguing in the palace. He was later demoted to the position of vice governor of Wuchang Military Commissioner. After this, he served as the Minister of the Ministry of Finance and inspected the region of Hedong. He was dismissed due to some matter and retired. In the year Tianxing, the era name was changed, and an imperial decree was sent to the Northern Court, but his final outcome is unknown. According to the History of Jin, in the ninth year of the Zhengda era, in February, Feimo Agudai and Guoshi Rong were sent as peace envoys. In April, Yang Jurin was sent with gold and silk to the Yuan dynasty to request peace. After the month of April, the era name was changed to Tianxing. There is no record of Liu Yuanzhong being sent as an envoy. According to the History of Yuan, in the first year of the Tai Zong era, in the year Ji Chou, Agudai was sent back to the Jin dynasty. The Jin dynasty recorded this event in the sixth year of the Zhengda era, but there is no mention of Agudai's mission in the same year, indicating a possible omission in the History of Jin.

    79

    康司农锡字百禄赵州人与雷希顔冀京父同年进士正大初由省掾拜监察御史上章言防检完顔萨哈勒辈【案萨哈勒旧作撒合今改】预政非宜又言宿帅赫舍哩雅尔呼达【案旧作纥石烈牙虎带今改】太恣横不法时二人权势赫然百禄皆不屑士论称焉后为河南路司农少卿再授河中帅府经厯官北兵陷河中帅率兵南奔济河船败死【案中州集锡以河中治中充行六部郎中从军城陷投水死好问所撰大司农康君墓表亦同是锡因城陷而殉与此志所云南奔济河船败而死可以攷异】为人厚重有为颇读书尝赋打毬诗云髙飞逺走偶然耳坎止流行知所之余先子云亦有理也

    Explanation

    79

    康 Sinao Xī, courtesy name Bǎilù, was from Zhaozhou. He was a jinshi (imperial examination graduate) in the same year as Lei Xīyán, the father of Ji Jīng, during the Zhengda era. Initially serving as a provincial official, he was later appointed as a censor. He submitted a memorial to speak out against the inappropriate involvement of Wanyan Sahala and others in politics. He also criticized the excessive arrogance and lawlessness of the high-ranking military official Hesheri Yarhuda. At the time, both individuals held significant power, but Xī did not regard them with respect, earning praise from scholars. Later, he served as a deputy minister of agriculture in Henan and was then appointed as an official in the Hezhong military administration. When northern forces invaded Hezhong, the military commander led troops southward, but their boat capsized and sank in the river, resulting in his death. (According to the Zhongzhou Collection, Xī was the governor of Hezhong, serving as a traveling six-department official, and died by drowning after the city fell. The epitaph written by Hao Wèn for the grand minister of agriculture, Kang Jun, also states that Xī died by drowning after the city fell. This differs from the account in this inscription, which says he died in a river crossing disaster while fleeing south.) Xī was a serious, substantial, and accomplished person who read extensively. He once wrote a poem about polo, which included the lines: "Flying high and running far are merely occasional occurrences; knowing when to stop and when to flow, understanding the rest." His father remarked that the poem also made sense.

    80

    杨左司居仁字行之其先大兴人后居南京十八年擢第入仕以能称为人谨宻朝廷上下皆爱之为监察御史言事称防由吏部郎中改太常少卿使北朝凡再往归坐事废天兴末迁为左司郎中与二执政居守崔立之变被伤窜卧余家已而为立强起复旧职俄以病辞去将北渡举家投黄河死时年未五十公少有吏能晩读书作诗有佳处使仕清时不失为名卿材丈夫遭世乱困踬可叹与余父子交最善余尝送其北使序及诗房刑部维桢字周卿济南人少擢第南渡为左司都事司农少卿出刺申州召为刑部郎中卒为人谨愿读书作诗颇好贤
    　　齐申州椿字夀之夏津人少擢第入官以亷称南渡为监察御史右司都事许古尝上书荐之后为司农丞进少卿出刺申州卒
    　　张户部俊民字用章延安人擢第以材干称尝为户部郎中进侍郎遭乱北迁病卒为人慷慨尚气义喜学易杨户部慥字叔玉五台人擢进士第南渡为监察御史户部郎中司农卿迁户部侍郎通吏事有能名正大末权参知政事后罢守户部南京降病卒尝与余先子同任御史颇作诗

    Explanation

    80

    Yang Juren, courtesy name Xingzhi, was originally from Daxing but later settled in Nanjing. After eighteen years, he passed the imperial examinations and entered public service, being known for his ability and discretion. He was loved by all levels of the court. As a Censor, he spoke of matters cautiously. He was promoted from the position of Minister of Personnel to the position of Deputy Minister of Rites and was sent twice to the Northern court. Upon returning, he was dismissed from office due to some matter. At the end of the Tianxing era, he was promoted to the position of Left Censor. He was in charge with two high-ranking officials during the Cui Li incident, where he was injured and hid in hiding. Later, he was forced back into his old position. Soon after, he resigned due to illness. He intended to cross north and commit suicide by throwing himself into the Yellow River, dying at the age of fifty. He had administrative ability from a young age and later read and wrote poetry with notable merit. If he had served in clear times, he would not have been less than a capable and noble official. Caught in a chaotic world, his suffering is pitiable. He had the best friendship with the author and his father. The author once wrote a preface and poems for his northern mission.

    Fang Weizhen, courtesy name Zhouqing, was from Jinan. He passed the imperial examinations and moved south, serving as a Left Censor and Deputy Minister of Agriculture. He was appointed as the governor of Shenzhou and later recalled to serve as a Minister of Justice, where he died. He was diligent, respectful, and enjoyed reading and writing poetry, with a fondness for virtuous people.

    Qi Shenzhou Chun, courtesy name Shouzhi, was from Xiazhou. He passed the imperial examinations and entered office, known for his integrity. He moved south, serving as a Censor and Right Censor. Xu Gu once recommended him in a memorial. He was later promoted to the position of Deputy Minister of Agriculture and governor of Shenzhou, where he died.

    Zhang Junmin, courtesy name Yongzhang, was from Yan'an. He passed the imperial examinations and was known for talent and diligence. He served as a Minister of Revenue and was promoted to the position of Vice Minister. Caught in a chaotic world, he moved north and died of illness. He was generous and upheld righteousness, enjoying studying the Yi Jing (Book of Changes).

    Yang Shuzhou Zao, courtesy name Shuyu, was from Wutai. He passed the imperial examinations and moved south, serving as a Censor, Minister of Revenue, and Deputy Minister of Agriculture. He was promoted to the position of Vice Minister of Revenue, known for his administrative ability and reputation. During the Zhengda era, he temporarily served as a high-ranking official but was later dismissed and returned to the Ministry of Revenue in Nanjing, where he died of illness. He once served alongside the author's father as a Censor and wrote many poems.

    81

    髙尚书防字唐卿保州永平人第进士莅官有才誉南渡歴户部员外郎后迁尚书専治粮储尝巡行京东便宜行事抵罪诏释之天兴初为翰林学士乱后北迁还乡卒
    　　冯内翰璧字叔献真定人为人严毅整肃望之俨然人莫得视然文采风流言谈洒落使人爱之不能舍以去诗笔清遒字画严峻为一时所称与李屏山王从之同年第二公皆重之大安初入翰林由应奉迁修撰后屡为法官台察弹劾不避权势时髙琪当国察其畏谨数以公推攷贵人所拟辄称防朝士多侧目颇有刻骨之讥屡上章言事又条上恢复之策出为同知亳州致仕【案金史本传改同知集庆军节度使即上章乞骸骨元好问内翰冯公神道碑及中州集大金国志均与本同攷金百官志诸州同知正七品诸节度使同

    Explanation

    81

    Gao Tangqing, a high-ranking official, was from Yongping in Baizhou. He passed the imperial examination and was granted the title of Jinshi. He had talent and reputation while serving in office. After the fall of the Northern Song to the Jurchens, he served as a clerk in the Ministry of Revenue and was later promoted to the position of Minister, specializing in grain storage. He once toured the eastern part of the capital, acting as he saw fit, and was punished for it, but was later pardoned by imperial decree. In the early Tianxing era, he served as a Hanlin Scholar. After a period of chaos, he moved north and returned to his hometown, where he eventually died.

    Bì (璧), whose courtesy name was Shùxiàn (叔献), was from Zhending. He was strict, stern, and well-disciplined, appearing dignified and solemn, and no one could look at him without feeling a sense of respect. However, he was also known for his literary talent and graceful, elegant qualities, and his speech was free and unrestrained, making people love him and cannot bear to leave. His poetry was clear and powerful, and his calligraphy was strict and forceful, earning him praise from his contemporaries. He was a classmate of Li Pingshan and Wang Congzhi, and both held him in high regard. In the early Da'an era, he entered the Hanlin Academy and was promoted from a position of serving to a position of writing. He frequently served as a judge and was involved in investigations and impeachments, showing no fear of powerful figures. At the time when Gao Qi was in power, he observed Bì's cautious and respectful behavior and frequently recommended him publicly and examined the suggestions of influential people. Many officials in the court looked at him askance, and he was often criticized harshly. He frequently submitted memorials to speak on matters of state and submitted detailed proposals for the restoration of the country. He was appointed as a deputy governor of Bozhou and eventually retired. According to the Jin History, his position was changed to deputy governor of Jiqing Army, and he submitted a memorial requesting to retire. Yuan Hao问, a renowned historian and poet of the Jin Dynasty, and the Zhongzhou Ji and Da Jin Guozhi all recorded his biography consistently. According to the Jin Bai Guan Zhi, the rank of deputy governor in the Jin Dynasty was seventh grade.

    82

    知正五品此志云同知亳州与本同知集庆军节度使有异】归嵩山结第玉峯下自号松庵徜徉泉石间酿酒名松醪味胜京师采兰置室中与山僧野客作鬭兰防壬辰之乱北归由东平至镇阳以殁年七十有九平生文章工于四六尺牍为当代之冠人得一篇皆寳藏之与韩温甫髙献臣友善后进中特喜雷希顔冀京父王仲泽皆从之游颇与予先子善壬辰嵗围城中余居与公相近甚相往来时公年已髙神采毅然目光如炬布袍麻屦杖策翩然后生辈莫及也北迁后再见于镇阳今其亡矣前辈风流遂不复见惜哉子渭以孝称
    　　王革字徳新州人少有才思诗笔尖新风流人也屡举不第以任子仕晩由恩得主宜君簿北渡居云内后迁云中卒年七十余名士皆其友也尊酒之间一谈一笑甚有古风今不复见也戊辰冬赴试西京自以年髙与诸后进偕入复作此举因有诗云惯掣苍龙晓漏钟受恩曽受大明宫香浮扇影迎初日人逐鞭声静晓风转首俄惊成异世此身虽在已哀翁唤回五十年前梦再着麻衣待至公

    Explanation

    82

    知正五品此志云同知亳州与本同知集庆军节度使有异】归嵩山结第玉峯下自号松庵徜徉泉石间酿酒名松醪味胜京师采兰置室中与山僧野客作鬭兰防壬辰之乱北归由东平至镇阳以殁年七十有九平生文章工于四六尺牍为当代之冠人得一篇皆寳藏之与韩温甫髙献臣友善后进中特喜雷希顔冀京父王仲泽皆从之游颇与予先子善壬辰嵗围城中余居与公相近甚相往来时公年已髙神采毅然目光如炬布袍麻屦杖策翩然后生辈莫及也北迁后再见于镇阳今其亡矣前辈风流遂不复见惜哉子渭以孝称

    Translation:
    The official of the fifth rank, as recorded in this biography, served as Vice Magistrate of Bozhou, which differs from his position as Military Governor of Jiqing Army as mentioned in the main text. He retired to Mount Song, where he built a residence at the foot of Yufeng Peak, calling it "Pine Hermitage." He wandered leisurely among springs and rocks, brewing wine named "Pine Liquor," whose flavor surpassed that of the capital. He cultivated orchids in his room and engaged in the game of "Orchid Competition" with monks and recluses. During the chaos of the "Rénchéng Uprising," he returned to the north, traveling from Dongping to Zhanyang, where he passed away at the age of seventy-nine. Throughout his life, he excelled in the art of four-six prose and short letters, earning him the reputation as the foremost writer of his time. His works were highly valued, and anyone who obtained one treasured it. He was close friends with Han Wenfu and Gao Xiachen, and among the younger generation, he particularly favored Lei Xiyang, the father of Jijing, Wang Zhongze. He often visited him, and my father was also on good terms with him. In the year of Rénchéng, while the city was besieged, I lived near him and we interacted frequently. At that time, he was already advanced in age, but his demeanor was resolute, his eyes like torches, and he walked gracefully in his coarse robe and straw sandals, a sight that none of the younger generation could match. After the northward migration, I saw him again in Zhanyang, but now that he is gone, the elegance of the older generation is no longer to be seen. How regrettable! Ziwèi was known for his filial piety.

    　　王革字徳新州人少有才思诗笔尖新风流人也屡举不第以任子仕晩由恩得主宜君簿北渡居云内后迁云中卒年七十余名士皆其友也尊酒之间一谈一笑甚有古风今不复见也戊辰冬赴试西京自以年髙与诸后进偕入复作此举因有诗云惯掣苍龙晓漏钟受恩曽受大明宫香浮扇影迎初日人逐鞭声静晓风转首俄惊成异世此身虽在已哀翁唤回五十年前梦再着麻衣待至公

    Translation:
    Wang Ge, style name Dexin, was from Hongzhou. He was a man of talent and wit, known for his sharp and elegant poetry, and was considered a refined individual. Despite taking the exams many times, he never passed. He eventually entered officialdom through a hereditary appointment and later, by favor, was appointed as a clerk in Yijun. He moved north and settled in Yunnei, later relocating to Yunzhong, where he passed away at the age of over seventy. He was friends with many scholars, and in their gatherings, his conversation and laughter were imbued with a sense of ancient elegance, a quality that is no longer seen today. In the winter of Wùchéng, he traveled to the Western Capital to take the exams, though he was old, he accompanied the younger generation and participated in this endeavor. He composed a poem, which went:

    "Used to wielding the reins of the morning dragon,
    Once favored, I had been in the grand palace.
    The fragrance of the fan shadow welcomes the first light of dawn,
    The sound of the whip echoes in the still morning breeze.
    Turning my head, I am suddenly startled by the strangeness of this world.
    Though my body remains, I am already a sorrowful old man.

    郭子通为太常博士宋国遣信使以申议为名将有所求也宰相下其事于礼官诸公环视未对子通曰申者重也再也自大定甲申讲和之后盟约既定无复再议之事且以小事大事若有祈请亦难申议之名宰相是之后宋使之来改曰祈请【案金史交聘表大定十六年三月壬子宋翰林学士知制诰朝散大夫汤彦昭信军承宣使陈雷等奉书申请丙辰宋申请使朝辞上以书答又攷宋史淳熙二年八月丁丑遣左司谏汤彦等使金申议据此志

    83

    Guo Zitong, a Doctor of the Imperial Academy, was sent by the Song state as an envoy under the pretense of restating a matter, with the intention of making a request. The Chancellor referred the matter to the officials in charge of religious and ceremonial matters. The officials looked at each other in silence. Guo Zitong said, "To restate is important, and it means to do so again. Since the peace treaty was signed in 1184, the treaty has been established, and there is no need for further discussion. Moreover, for both small and large matters, if there is a request, it is difficult to use the name of restating or reconsidering." The Chancellor approved it. Later, when the Song envoy came, they changed it to a petition.

    Those who debated agreed that his insight was far-sighted. On the first day of the third month of the seventeenth year of the Dading era, during the celebration of the Emperor's birthday, the envoys from various states were about to meet when heavy rain occurred. The Grand Master of Rites, Zhang Gong, asked Guo Zitong, "What should be done according to propriety?" Guo Zitong replied,

    "Zengzi asked Confucius, 'If a vassal state's envoy goes to pay homage to the Son of Heaven and cannot see him, there are four reasons for this: the first is rain that soaks through one's clothes and causes one to lose composure.' Zhang Gong said, 'This is not the responsibility of the envoy.' Guo Zitong said,

    彼国主之事尚不得见况其臣乎【案金史世宗本纪大定十六年三月朔万春节以日食改朝与此志十七年三月朔万春节以大雨罢朝适合曽子问四不朝之二均闗一时典制乃改朝则书而罢朝则不书亦为脱漏攷周煇北辕录淳熙丙申十一月二十九日诏以张子政及赵士襃充贺金国生辰使次年三月一日雨免入贺葢即大定十七年事也可互证以补本纪之缺】少顷有敕放朝士大夫服其知体右见李致美作子通神道碑子通卒清州防御使

    If one cannot even see the affairs of the king, how much less those of his ministers? [According to the History of the Jin Dynasty, in the sixteenth year of the Dading era, on the first day of the third month during the Wan Chun Festival, a solar eclipse led to a change in the court schedule, as recorded in this chronicle. In the seventeenth year, on the same day, heavy rain led to the cancellation of the court session, which aligns with the second of the four occasions mentioned in the Analects of Confucius where court sessions were suspended. Both events are relevant to the court regulations of the time. However, while the change in court schedule is recorded, the cancellation due to rain is omitted, which is a gap in the records. According to Zhou Hui's Northward Journey Record, on the twenty-ninth day of the eleventh month in the third year of Chongxi (1186 AD), an edict was issued appointing Zhang Zizheng and Zhao Shibo as envoys to celebrate the birthday of the Jin emperor. The following year, on the first day of the third month, due to rain, the envoys were exempted from entering the court, which corresponds to the seventeenth year of the Dading era. This can be cross-referenced to fill the gap in the History of the Jin Dynasty.] Shortly thereafter, an imperial decree was issued to dismiss the court, and the scholars and officials praised him for his understanding of propriety. [To the right, one sees Li Zhimei's inscription on the tombstone of Zi Tong, who died as the defense commissioner of Qingzhou.]

    Return to the Depths of the Heart, Volume Five
    The Four Treasuries
    Return to the Depths of the Heart, Volume Six
    By Liu Qi of the Yuan Dynasty

    Gao Ruli, courtesy name Yanfu, was from Yingzhou. He entered officialdom at a young age and was known for his ability. He once served as Left Censor and Minister of Works, and later as Minister of Revenue, where he specialized in managing finances. He was promoted to Minister of State and then to Deputy Minister of the Three Boards, where he advocated for the introduction of paper money to replace coinage. During the Southern Migration of Emperor Xuanzong, he was appointed Vice Premier, then Left and Right Chancellors, and eventually Chancellor. He was granted the title of Duke of Shouguo and passed away in office at the age of seventy or more. He was cautious, discreet, and廉洁, able to gain the emperor's favor. He adhered to the law, avoided controversy, and was not fond of strong remonstrance. Therefore, he served as chancellor for over a decade without ever facing criticism or punishment. He lived a long and healthy life, and no one in his time could match him. Since the establishment of the Jin dynasty, there has been only one scholar-official who governed the country, and that was Gao Ruli.

    贾左丞守谦字彦亨【案中州集贾益谦字亨甫本名守谦避哀宗讳改焉金史本称益谦而章宗本纪称右谏议大夫守谦葢守谦在章宗时犹未易名故原其始书之此志撰于哀宗之后不着避讳改名当是冩讹脱】东平人少擢第莅官以能称章宗时为谏议大夫皇叔镐王以疑忌下狱公力争士论直之大安末拜防知政事南渡进右丞迁左丞致仕薨
    　　胥平章鼎字和之代之繁畤人父持国章宗时执政公少擢第以能称为右司郎中善占对大安末为防知政事【案金史本云至宁初拜防知政事攷至宁前为崇庆二年大安又在崇庆之前此志所云大安末与本至宁初迥异】俄出镇平阳【案大金国志云出为平阳节度使攷金史本鼎于贞祐元年十一月出为兖州泰定军节度使未赴二年五月留为汾阳军节度使兼汾州管内观察使十一月改知平阳府事兼河东南路兵马都总管金史地理志云平阳府初为次府罝建雄军节度使天防六年升总管府金史百官志云诸总管府谓府尹兼领者都总管一员正三品掌统诸城隍兵马

    Explanation

    85

    Jia Zuo Chen Shouqian, courtesy name Yanheng [Note: According to the "Zhongzhou Ji," his original name was Yiqian, but it was changed to avoid offending Emperor Aizong. The "Jin Shi" biography refers to him as Yiqian, while the "Zhangzong Benji" mentions him as Right Censorial Adviser Shouqian. Shouqian was still using his original name during the reign of Emperor Zhangzong, hence the initial recording of his name. This account was written after the reign of Emperor Aizong and does not mention the name change, likely due to a transcription error or omission.], was from Dongping. He passed the imperial examinations at a young age and was known for his competence in official duties. During the reign of Emperor Zhangzong, he served as a Censorial Adviser. When Prince Hao, a member of the imperial family, was imprisoned due to suspicion and jealousy, Jia Zuo Chen Shouqian strongly defended him, and the public supported his stance. At the end of the Dahan era, he was appointed as a Deputy Chancellor. After the Southern Migration, he advanced to the position of Right Chancellor and later became Left Chancellor. He retired and died.

    Xu Pingzhang Ding, courtesy name Hezhi, succeeded him. Xu was from Fanzhi, and his father, Chiguo, held a high-ranking position during the reign of Emperor Zhangzong. Xu Pingzhang Ding also passed the imperial examinations at a young age and was known for his competence. He served as a Right Censorial Adviser and was skilled in answering questions. At the end of the Dahan era, he was appointed as a Deputy Chancellor [Note: According to the "Jin Shi," he was appointed as Deputy Chancellor in the early Zining era. However, the Zining era began after the Chongqing era, and the Dahan era preceded the Chongqing era. This account's reference to the end of the Dahan era differs from the "Jin Shi" which mentions the early Zining era.]. Soon after, he was sent out to govern Pingyang [Note: According to the "Da Jin Guozhi," he was appointed as the Military Governor of Pingyang. However, the "Jin Shi" biography states that in the eleventh month of the first year of the Zhengyou era, he was appointed as the Military Governor of Taiping Army but did not take up the post. In the fifth month of the second year of the Zhengyou era, he remained in Fenyang as the Military Governor of Fenyang Army and Inspector of Fenzhou. In the eleventh month, he was appointed as the Prefect of Pingyang and Commander of the Military Forces of the Eastern Road of the River. The "Jin Shi" Geography Chapter states that Pingyang initially served as a secondary prefecture and was later promoted to a governor-general's office. The "Jin Shi" Official Chapter states that various governor-general's offices, where the prefect also serves as the governor-general, have one governor-general, a third-rank official, responsible for overseeing all city walls and military forces.].

    甲仗总判府事是都总管与节鎭本异况胥鼎固知平阳府事者大金国志云出为平阳节度使有误此志云出镇平阳亦似节镇然都总管掌统兵马亦可云鎭其非节度使金史足证】宣宗南渡行台河中兵民安辑进平章政事兼左副元帅移镇京兆封莘国公后朝廷将伐宋取蜀召议公归上言止之坐是忤旨致仕薨【案金史本贞祐三年就拜本路宣抚使四年拜枢宻副使进拜尚书左丞兴定元年正月拜平章政事封莘国公三月朝廷诏鼎举兵伐宋鼎分兵由秦巩鳯翔二路竝进上书言当遴选材武将士分布近边州郡敌至则追击去则力田以广储蓄诏下尚书省以诸军既进议遂寝二年

    Explanation

    86

    The Office of the Chief Military Equipment Administrator is distinct from the positions of Grand Military Commander and Governor of a Circuit. Xū Dǐng, who was firmly in charge of the affairs of Píngyáng (平阳)府, is mentioned in the History of the Jin Dynasty as having been appointed as the Governor of Píngyáng. However, this record is incorrect, as it states that he was appointed as the Governor of Píngyáng, which is similar to the position of a Circuit Governor. Nevertheless, the Grand Military Commander oversees military forces and can also be referred to as a Governor, though he is not a Circuit Governor. The History of the Jin Dynasty confirms this distinction. During the reign of Emperor Xīngzōng (宣宗), after he crossed the river southward and established his headquarters in Hézhōng (河中), the military and civilian population was pacified. He was promoted to Chancellor of State Affairs and concurrently appointed as Left Deputy Marshal, then transferred to command Jingzhao (京兆), and was granted the title of Duke of Xīn (莘). Later, when the court planned to attack the Southern Song and capture Shu, they summoned Xū Dǐng to return and consult with him. Xū Dǐng advised against the campaign, which angered the emperor, leading to his retirement and eventual death. According to the History of the Jin Dynasty, in the third year of the Zhengyou era, Xū Dǐng was appointed as the Pacification Commissioner of his own circuit. In the fourth year, he was promoted to Deputy Minister of Military Affairs and then to Left Chancellor of the Ministry of State Affairs. In the first month of the Xingding era, he was appointed as Chancellor of State Affairs and granted the title of Duke of Xīn. In the third month, the court issued an edict ordering Xū Dǐng to raise an army to attack the Southern Song. Xū Dǐng divided his forces into two routes via Qín (秦), Gōng (巩), and Fèngxiáng (凤翔), and submitted a memorial stating that he should select capable and brave soldiers to be stationed in nearby prefectures and states, ready to pursue and attack the enemy when they arrive, and to cultivate the land when they depart, in order to increase reserves. The edict was sent to the Ministry of State Affairs, but since the armies had already advanced, the plan was abandoned. In the second year, Xū Dǐng retired.

    四月鼎奏天子操大纲责成功况今多故岂可躬亲细务宣宗覧奏不悦俄以伐宋有功迁官一阶时元兵大举入陜西鼎多料敌之防朝臣或中沮之宣宗谕枢宻院曰胥鼎规画必无误自此卿等不须指受四年进封温国公致仕谕曰卿屡求退今从卿请仍可来居京师有事得就谘决哀宗正大二年起复拜平章政事进封英国公行尚书省于卫州鼎以衰病辞不许三年七月薨据所叙官阶知遇甚详其忤防以谏躬亲细务非因谏伐宋且厯久弥见倚任屡请乃致仕后又起用与此志迥异】公通达吏事有度量为政镇静所在无贤不肖皆得其懽心南渡以来书生有方面之柄者惟公一人而已

    Explanation

    87

    In April, Duke Ding presented a report to the emperor, emphasizing the importance of focusing on major issues and demanding success, especially given the numerous troubles at the time. It was impractical to personally attend to trivial matters. Emperor Xuanzong read the report and was displeased. Soon after, due to his success in attacking Song, he was promoted by one rank. At that time, Yuan forces launched a large-scale invasion of Shaanxi. Duke Ding had many strategies to defend against the enemy, but some court officials were demoralized by this. Emperor Xuanzong instructed the Privy Council, saying, "Duke Ding's planning will surely not be in error. From now on, you do not need to give specific instructions."

    In the fourth year, he was enfeoffed as the Duke of Wen and retired. He was told, "You have often requested retirement. Now we comply with your request, but you may still come to reside in the capital and consult on matters when needed." In the second year of Zhengda during the reign of Emperor Aizong, he was reinstated as Chancellor and enfeoffed as the Duke of Ying. He served as the head of the Shangshu Province in Weizhou. Duke Ding declined due to his declining health, but the request was not granted. In the third year, in July, he died.

    According to the biography, the details of his official rank and the emperor's favor are very detailed. His opposition was due to advising against personal involvement in trivial matters, not because of advising against the attack on Song. Moreover, over time, his reliance became even more evident. Despite repeated requests, he was eventually allowed to retire, but he was later reinstated, which differs from his initial stance. Duke Ding was adept at handling administrative affairs, had a broad perspective, and governed with calmness. Wherever he served, both the virtuous and the less virtuous found him agreeable. Since the Southern Migration, no scholar had held such a position except for him.

    张左丞行信字信甫先名行忠避末帝旧讳改焉莒州人御史大夫暐之子太子太傅行简之弟也家世以纯厚称士论以为如汉万石君家公少擢第厯清要宣宗南渡为礼部尚书时丞相珠格髙琪擅权百官侧目因廷议事公独抗言折之上甚喜明日拜防知政事未防为近侍所谮出镇泾州到官上疏论近侍之奸士大夫称重正大初首召拜左丞言事稍不及前人望颇减【案水集张左丞上即位驿召起授尚书左丞首言先帝初即位诏天下刑不上大夫丞相髙琪奏定职官犯罪的决

    Explanation

    88

    Zhang Zuo Cheng Xingxin, originally named Xingzhong, changed his name to avoid the taboo of the last emperor. He was from Juzhou and the son of the Imperial Censor-in-Chief Zhang Wei, and the younger brother of the Grand Tutor Zhang Xingjian. His family was renowned for their integrity and loyalty, and scholars compared them to the Wanshi family of the Han dynasty. Zhang passed the imperial examinations at a young age and held important positions. During Emperor Xuanzong's southern relocation, he served as the Minister of Rites. At the time, the Chancellor Zhu Ge Gaoqi held absolute power, causing other officials to be wary. During a court meeting, Zhang alone spoke boldly, criticizing the Chancellor's actions, which pleased the emperor. The next day, he was appointed as the head of state affairs. However, he was later slandered by court attendants and sent to govern Jingzhou. Upon arriving, he submitted a memorial criticizing the corruption of the court attendants, earning the respect of scholars. At the beginning of the Zhengda era, he was summoned and appointed as the Left Chancellor, but his performance in advising the emperor was not as impressive as before, leading to a decline in his reputation. According to the historical record An Shui Ji, when the emperor ascended the throne, Zhang was summoned by express command and appointed as the Left Chancellor. He first spoke about the decree that crimes committed by officials should not be punished by corporal punishment.

    百余条乞依旧制或谓公首圣主擢用虽有建明多不契上防云云是行信拜左丞以后亦侃直不逢合而金史本移并正大初所奏于兴定间似与此志相符然此志云稍不及前非谓黙无一言当以水集所云防证】后致仕数年薨为人简朴不修威仪恶衣粝食如贫士既致仕家居惟以抄书教子孙为事葺园池东城号静亭时时游咏其间为乐南渡宰执中最有直名初至南京父暐以御史大夫致仕犹康健兄行简为翰林学士承防公为礼部尚书诸子侄多中第居官当世未之有也

    Explanation

    89

    Hundreds of regulations were requested to restore the old system. Some said that the public was first promoted by the sage ruler, even though there were many suggestions that did not align with the emperor's intentions. This time, he was appointed as Left Chancellor. Afterward, he remained frank and upright but did not find favor. The History of Jin in its original biography combined material from the early Zhengda period, which seems to match this account. However, this account states that it was slightly less than before, not that he remained silent without a word. It should be verified with the Liu Shui Collection. After retiring, he died several years later. He was simple and frugal, not cultivating a dignified appearance, wearing coarse clothing, and eating simple food, like a poor scholar. After retiring, he lived at home, teaching his descendants by copying books, building a garden and pond in the eastern city, naming it the Quiet Pavilion, and finding joy in wandering and singing there. Among the high officials during the Southern Migration, he was the most upright. When he first arrived in Nanjing, his father Wei retired as Grand Censor and was still healthy. His brother Xingjian served as a Hanlin scholar and censor, while he himself served as Minister of Rites. Many of his sons and nephews passed the imperial examinations, and in this era, there was none like him in office.

    90

    侯平章挚字莘卿东阿人少擢第慷慨有为贞祐初北兵围燕都公由麴使请出募军已而膺城有功自行户部侍郎迁河平军节度使宣宗南渡为防知政事出镇东平移镇下邳所至吏民安爱后入朝迁左丞正大初进平章政事封萧国公【案本起为平章政事封萧国公在天兴元年八月与此志所云正大初有异】居相位愤无所施请守大名诏出行尚书省未防还朝致仕居南京有园亭蔡水滨公日在其间与耆老防饮后南京降以前宰执为北兵所杀为人有威严御兵人莫敢犯在朝遇事亦敢言

    Explanation

    90

    Hou Pingzhang Zhi, courtesy name Xin Qing, was from Dong'e. He was young when he passed the imperial examinations and was bold and ambitious. In the early period of Emperor Xuanzong of Jin (Zhengyuu era), the Northern army besieged Yan capital (Beijing). He, as a grain and wine official, requested permission to go out and recruit soldiers. Later, he contributed to the defense of the city and was promoted from the position of Censor-in-chief to the position of Governor of He Ping Army. During Emperor Xuanzong's relocation to the south (Nan Du), he served as a high-ranking official and was appointed to govern Dongping, then moved to govern Xiapi. Wherever he went, officials and people were at peace and loved him. Later, he returned to the capital and was promoted to Left Chancellor. In the early period of Emperor Lizong of Jin (Zhengda era), he was appointed as Pingzhangshi (Chancellor) and enfeoffed as Duke of Xiao [Note: According to the records, he was appointed as Pingzhangshi and enfeoffed as Duke of Xiao in the eighth month of Tianxing year one, which differs from what is recorded here]. While serving as Chancellor, he was frustrated by his inability to make a difference and requested to govern Da Ming. He was ordered to travel to the Ministry of Revenue but did not return to the capital and retired. He lived in Nanjing, where he had a garden by the Pizhui River. He spent his days there, drinking with elderly scholars. After the fall of Nanjing, he was killed by the Northern army along with former high-ranking officials. He was strict and imposing, and his troops feared to defy him. In the court, he spoke out fearlessly when encountering matters.

    颇喜荐士如张文举雷希顔麻知防皆由公进用南渡后宰执中人望最重李防政巩字君美河中人少擢第有能名南渡为防知政事出镇平阳北兵至城陷自杀从子复亨字仲修逾冠擢第以才能称为人通敏善奏对南渡为左司郎中大为宣宗所器一时誉甚隆迁翰林直学士知开封府进吏部尚书为防知政事年方四十父母俱存近世未有也兴定末坐监试进士失取人出镇同州未防北兵攻城陷自杀叔侄相继执政俱死事士论所嘉愚轩赵宜之挽仲修诗云报君惟有死见叔固无慙人以为破的也

    Explanation

    91

    He often enjoyed recommending talented individuals, such as Zhang Wenju, Lei Xiyan, and Ma Zhifang, who were all promoted by him. After the Southern Migration, among the chief ministers, the most respected was Li Fangzhenggong, courtesy name Junmei, from Hedong. He was young and successful in the imperial examinations, known for his abilities. After the Southern Migration, he served as a chief minister. He was sent to govern Pingyang, where he committed suicide when the city was captured by northern forces. His nephew, Fu Heng, courtesy name Zhongxiu, passed the imperial examinations after reaching adulthood and was known for his talent and ability to respond clearly and appropriately in court. He served as a Left Censor and was greatly favored by Emperor Xuanzong of the Jin Dynasty, highly esteemed at the time. He was promoted to the position of a scholar in the Hanlin Academy and served as the governor of Kaifeng. He was then promoted to Minister of Personnel and served as a chief minister. At the age of forty, both his parents were still alive, a rare occurrence in recent times. In the last year of Xingding, he was demoted to govern Tongzhou after failing to properly oversee the imperial examinations. Before long, the city was attacked by northern forces and he committed suicide. Both he and his nephew served as chief ministers and died in office, praised by scholars and officials. The poet Zhao Yizhi wrote a poem to mourn the death of Zhongxiu, which included the line: "To repay the emperor, there is only death; to see my uncle, I have no shame." People considered this a perfect expression.

    师防政安石字仲安清州人少擢第轻财尚气义闻于朋友为省掾宣宗南渡从完顔福兴守燕都福兴将死以遗表托仲安使赴行在既达上嘉之擢枢宻院经歴官时末帝在春宫领院事遂见知遇正大初进同签枢宻院事迁御史中丞工部尚书遂为防知政事其骤用如此既居位人望颇减俄以脑疽薨【案金史本正大三年权左防政四年进右丞此志称师防政而不书右丞与本异又本正大五年台谏劾近侍张文夀张仁夀李麟之安石亦论列三人不已上怒甚安石疽发脑而死故本赞曰安石不负承恽之托遂见知遇以论列近侍触怒而死悲夫然则安石既入相后以谔谔之行被

    Explanation

    92

    Shi Fangzheng, courtesy name Zhong'an, was from Qingzhou. He was selected for a position early in his career and was known among his friends for disregarding wealth and valuing righteousness and honor. He served as an assistant official in the provincial government. During the relocation of the Jin capital to the south under Emperor Xuanzong, he followed Wang Yanfu in defending Yanjing. Before dying, Wang Yanfu entrusted Zhong'an with a memorial to deliver to the emperor. After delivering it, the emperor praised him and promoted him to the position of a senior official in the Privy Council. The young emperor, who was in charge of the Privy Council, favored Zhong'an. In the early years of Zhengda, he was promoted to the position of co-signer in the Privy Council and then to the positions of Chief Censor and Minister of Works. He thus became a key advisor to the emperor, and this was how he was rapidly promoted. After taking office, his reputation declined, and he soon died from a brain abscess. He did not fail in Wang Yanfu's trust and was favored and appreciated by the emperor. He died after criticizing the emperor's attendants and angering the emperor. Alas, after becoming a key advisor, he continued to speak frankly and was thus punished.

    谴而死为史所推许与此志所云人望颇减有异】李左丞蹊字贯之大兴人少擢第通吏事能官南渡为左司郎中迁吏部侍郎为富察和卓所陷【案富察和卓旧作蒲察合住今改】下狱当死诏释之后为大司农正大初拜防知政事进左右丞専掌财赋北兵围南京坐粮不给除名久之起为工部尚书权防知政事复左丞奉使军前送曹王【案哀宗本纪天兴元年三月壬寅左丞李蹊送曹王出质六月乙亥李蹊送曹王与其子同俱还十月以李焕飞语诏左丞李蹊户部侍郎杨慥下狱俄竝除名据所载则送曹王出质在坐粮不给除名之前与此志有异】后从末帝东征至睢阳古纳之变见杀

    93

    The man died of exile and was praised by historians, which differs from what is said in this record about his reputation being significantly reduced. Li Xi, the Left Censor, was from Daxing and was selected for office at a young age, skilled in administrative affairs and capable of governing. After the Southern Crossing, he served as Left Censor and was promoted to Deputy Minister of Personnel. He was implicated by Fuca Hezhuo and imprisoned, sentenced to death, but was later pardoned by imperial decree. He was then appointed as the Grand Agricultural Minister. In the first year of Zhengda, he was promoted to the position of Chancellor and later became the Left Chancellor, specializing in financial management. When the northern army besieged Nanjing, he was dismissed from his post for failing to provide sufficient grain. After a long time, he was appointed as the Minister of Works and temporarily served as Chancellor again. He was later reinstated as the Left Chancellor and was sent on a mission to the front lines to escort Cao Wang. According to the records of the Emperor Aizong in the Tianxing era, in the first year, on the day Renyin of the third month, the Left Chancellor Li Xi escorted Cao Wang out as a hostage. On the day Bingxu of the sixth month, Li Xi escorted Cao Wang and his son back. In the tenth month, due to the slander of Li Huan, imperial decree ordered the arrest of the Left Chancellor Li Xi and the Minister of Revenue Yang Zao. Soon after, they were both dismissed from their posts. According to the records, escorting Cao Wang out as a hostage occurred before he was dismissed for failing to provide sufficient grain, which differs from this record. Later, he followed the last emperor eastward to fight and was killed in the battle of Suiyang during the Guna Rebellion.

    乌克逊防政仲端字子正女直进士也为人谨厚莅官以寛静称兴定间由礼部侍郎使北朝从入西域二年始归为陈州防御使【案金史本云朝廷嘉其有奉使劳进官两阶歴州刺史与此志所云防御使有异】迁御史中丞为防知政事人望甚隆天兴东狩罢为翰林学士承防【案金史本正大元年召为御史中丞奉诏安抚陜西及归权防知政事复以事贬同州节度使及哀宗将迁归徳召为翰林学

    Explanation

    94

    Ukexun Fang Zheng Zhongduan, courtesy name Zizheng, was a Jinshi (imperial examination degree) from the Jurchen people. He was cautious and kind, and was known for his broad and calm demeanor while holding office. During the Xingding era, he served as an envoy to the Northern Court from the position of Libu Shilang (a high-ranking official in the Ministry of Rites). He followed the court into the Western Regions and returned after two years. He was appointed as the defense commissioner of Chen Prefecture. [According to the Jin History, the court commended him for his service as an envoy and promoted him two ranks, serving as a Shizhong (governor) in  Prefecture, which differs from the defense commissioner mentioned here.] He was later promoted to Zhongcheng (a high-ranking official in the Censorate) and served as Fangzhishi (a title indicating responsibility for state affairs). He had a very high public reputation. During the Tianxing era, he was dismissed and appointed as a Hanlin Xueshi Chengfang (a scholar-official in the imperial court). [According to the Jin History, in the Zhengda era of the first year, he was summoned to serve as Zhongcheng, received an imperial edict to pacify Shaanxi, and upon his return, temporarily served as Fangzhishi. He was later demoted to Tongzhou Jiedushi (a military governor) for a matter. When the Emperor Aizong was about to move to Guide, he was summoned to serve as Hanlin Xueshi Chengfang.]

    士承防兼同签大睦亲府事据所载则由防政罢为节度使非即罢为翰林学士承防又其罢防政也在未狩之前与此志所云天兴东狩罢为翰林学士异】知时事不可为家居一室陈平生玩好日与夫人宴饮为欢癸巳正月下旬忽闭门自缢其夫人亦从死明日崔立之变若先知者金国亡大臣中全节义者一人公使归时备谈西北所见属赵闲闲记之赵以属屏山屏山以属余余为録其事赵书以石迄今世
    　　完顔参政苏兰字伯至宁元年女直进士魁也莅官修谨得名然苛细不能任大事较之辈流颇可称仕厯清要时望甚隆为宣宗所知擢任近侍局颇直言有补益旋罢出为谏议大夫居父丧不饮酒食肉庐墓三年后为防知政事同赫舍哩雅尔呼达守京兆【案赫舍哩雅尔呼达旧作纥石烈牙忽带今改】不相协召还【案金史本正大七年七月行省于京兆未防迁金安军节度使兼同华安抚使既而召还朝非自京兆守被召与此志所云异

    Final Translation

    Serving as a defense officer and co-signing documents for the Grand Secretariat of the Imperial Clan, according to the records, he was dismissed from his position as a defense officer and appointed as a military governor, not immediately as a翰林学士 (Hanlin Scholar) who also served as a defense officer. His dismissal from the defense office occurred before the eastern campaign, differing from what is stated here: during the eastern campaign of Tianxing, he was dismissed and appointed as a翰林学士 (Hanlin Scholar). Knowing that the times were not favorable for action, he lived in a single room, displaying his lifetime's collections, and daily entertained his wife with feasts and merriment. In the early spring of the癸巳 (Gui Si) year, he suddenly closed the door and hanged himself; his wife also followed him in death. The next day, the political upheaval known as "Cui Li's Rebellion" occurred, as if he had foreseen it. Among the ministers who perished with the fall of the Jin Dynasty, he was one who upheld his integrity and loyalty. When he returned home, he recounted his experiences in the northwest, entrusting Zhao Xian to record them. Zhao Xian then passed it on to Pingshan, who entrusted it to me. I recorded the events, and Zhao Xian inscribed them on stone, and they have been passed down to this day.

    完颜参政苏兰, with the courtesy name Bo Liang, was the top scholar in the Jin Dynasty's civil service examination in the first year of Zhi Ning. He served with diligence and gained a good reputation, though he was meticulous and could not handle major affairs. Compared to his contemporaries, he was quite commendable. He held clear and important positions, earning great respect in his time. He was known to Emperor Xuanzong, who promoted him to serve in the Imperial Household Bureau. He spoke frankly and offered beneficial advice, but was soon dismissed and appointed as a Censor-in-Chief. He observed mourning for his father, abstaining from alcohol and meat, and lived in a thatched hut near his father's grave for three years. Later, he served as a defense officer and co-signed documents for the Grand Secretariat of the Imperial Clan, along with Hesheri Yarhudar, who was responsible for governing Jingzhao (present-day Xi'an). They did not get along, and he was summoned back to the capital. (According to the History of the Jin Dynasty, in the seventh month of the seventh year of Zhengda, he served as the provincial governor of Jingzhao, but was later appointed as the military governor of Jin'an Army and concurrently as the pacification commissioner of Tonghua. He was then summoned back to the capital, not from Jingzhao, as stated here.)

    】至陜被围久之亡奔行在道遇害与余先子善弟努森【案努森旧作奴申今改】字正甫亦女直进士仕厯清要由吏部侍郎使北朝凡再往天兴东狩拜防知政事【案金史本正大五年九月以御史大夫奉使大元明年六月迁吏部尚书复往八年春拜防知政事攷哀宗本纪正大九年正月改元开兴四月改元天兴十二月乃诏议亲出是努森使元非由吏部侍郎其拜防知政事在东狩之前与此志俱异】留守南京龊龊不能有为崔立之变见杀
    　　完顔右丞呼沙呼字仲徳【案呼沙呼旧作忽斜虎今改攷金史完顔仲徳以此三字为仲徳本名则仲徳乃其改名也大金国志亦与金史同此志云字仲徳或即以字为名欤】女直进士也为人忠实有时望尝帅秦巩天兴改元南京被围仲徳提孤军入援转战数回止存五六人至京城门遇末帝东狩因从以行驻睢阳拜防知政事【案金史本以天兴元年九月拜防知政事在哀宗东狩以前四月与

    Explanation

    96

    A man named Nu Sen, who was friendly with my father, was also a Jurchen imperial scholar. He held prestigious positions throughout his career and served as a deputy minister of the Ministry of Personnel, twice being sent as an envoy to the Northern Court. During the Tianxing era, when the last emperor fled eastward, Nu Sen was appointed to a high-ranking position in charge of state affairs. However, he was left in charge of the southern capital and was criticized for being ineffective. He was killed during the coup led by Cui Li.

    Another man, Wanyan Hu Shaha (also known as Wanyan Zhongde), was a Jurchen imperial scholar. He was loyal and honest, with a good reputation. He once led troops in the regions of Qin and Gong. During the Tianxing era, when the southern capital was surrounded, Wanyan Zhongde led a lone army to come to the aid. After fighting several battles and suffering heavy casualties, he arrived at the city gate and followed the last emperor fleeing eastward. He stayed in Suizhou and was appointed to a high-ranking position in charge of state affairs in the same month of the Tianxing era.

    此志所云从帝东狩拜防知政事异】从徙蔡州进右丞【案哀宗本纪天兴元年十二月辛丑驾至开阳门外巩昌元帅完顔呼沙呼至自金昌东行之议遂决以为尚书右丞二年六月己亥上入蔡州据所载则呼沙呼为右丞在徙蔡之前一年与此志异】间闗险阻中尽心不懈蔡围既急末帝内禅崩城陷仲徳帅兵三百力战不支赴蔡水死军士皆从之其得士虽古之田横无以加也金国亡死君者惟仲徳
    　　完顔平章哈达【案哈达旧作合打今改】由防卫入官典郡尝陷北朝亡归南都累擢平凉帅为人勇敢忠实一时人望甚隆拜防知政事代胥相鼎镇京兆军民便之北兵犯兰闗将兵拒战有功入朝进平章政事封芮国公正大末北兵由襄汉大入诏哈达帅精兵拒之已而失利退保钓台军败见杀

    Explanation

    97

    This record states that Zhongde followed the emperor on an eastern hunting expedition and was appointed to a defensive position, entrusted with political affairs. He then followed the relocation to the state of Cai and was promoted to the position of Right Chancellor. According to the records, Hushahu became the Right Chancellor one year before the relocation to Cai, which differs from this record. During the perilous journey through difficult terrain, Zhongde exerted himself diligently without tiring. When the siege of Cai became urgent and the last emperor abdicated in favor of his successor, the city fell and the emperor died. Zhongde led three hundred soldiers in fierce battle but could not withstand the enemy. He drowned in the waters of Cai and died, and all the soldiers followed him in death. His loyalty to his soldiers was such that even ancient figures like Tian Heng could not surpass him. Among those who died for their emperor in the Jin state, only Zhongde did so.

    Wang Yanping, originally named Hada, entered officialdom through a military defensive position and governed a prefecture. He once fell into the hands of the Northern Song and escaped back to the Southern Song capital, Hangzhou. He was repeatedly promoted to the governor of Pingliang, a prefecture in Shaanxi, and was known for his bravery and loyalty, earning high regard among the people. He was appointed to a defensive position, entrusted with political affairs, and replaced Xushang Ding as the viceroy of Jingzhao, bringing peace to the military and civilian population. When Northern Song forces invaded the Lan Pass, he led his troops to resist and achieved victory. He entered the capital and was promoted to the position of Viceroy, receiving the title of Duke of Rui. During the end of the Zhengda era, when Northern Song forces invaded from Xiang and Han, the emperor ordered Wang Yanping to lead a select force to resist. After suffering a defeat, he retreated to defend the strategic location of DiaoTai, where his army was ultimately defeated and he was killed.

    完顔中郎将绰华善字良佐【案绰华善旧作陈和尚今改金史本云名彝以小字行丰州人】兄色埓必尔罕世袭明安也【案色埓旧作斜烈今改】忠义勇敢著名尝陷北朝亡归擢帅夀泗威望甚重性好士幕府延致文人改安平都尉常愤郁无所施发病死良佐从其兄在军中勇冠一时尝坐擅杀人将抵死上竒其材特赦之为忠孝军总领擢御侮中郎将天兴改元北兵入河南良佐从
    完顔哈达力战钧台军败被擒不屈死【案元好问赠镇南节度使良佐碑天兴元年钧州陷北兵下城即纵兵以防巷战者镇南避处杀掠稍定即出而自言我金国大将欲见白事云云是未尝被摛已欲殉节挺身而出者金史本传亦备叙其殉节之烈与此志详略迥异】良佐为人爱重士大夫王渥仲泽在其兄幕府良佐从之游学仲泽书极可观且同讲经学读书不辍亦一时弟兄良将帅也

    Explanation

    98

    Chancellor Wanyan Chuo Hua Shan, courtesy name Liang Zuo, was originally named Yi and went by his small name in Fengzhou. His elder brother, Sede Bilihan, was a hereditary Ming'an. Both were renowned for their loyalty, righteousness, and bravery. Chuo Hua Shan once fled to the Northern Court but returned, and he was promoted to commander of Shou and Si, gaining great prestige. He had a fondness for scholars and invited them to his military headquarters. He was later appointed as the Duke of Anping and often felt frustrated and had no outlet, eventually dying of illness. Chuo Hua Shan followed his elder brother in the army and was the bravest of his time. Once, he was punished for killing someone without authorization and was sentenced to death, but the emperor admired his talent and pardoned him, appointing him as the commander of the Zhongxiao Army and promoting him to the position of Zhonglangjiang for defending against humiliation. During the reign of Tianxing, when the northern forces invaded Henan, Chuo Hua Shan followed.

    Wanyan Hada fought bravely at Juntai, but the army was defeated and he was captured. He did not yield and died with dignity. According to the epitaph of the Zhongnan Jiedushi Liang Zuo, given by Yuan Hao Wen in the first year of Tianxing, when Junzhou fell to the northern forces, they immediately launched a street battle. Zhongnan avoided the chaos and, when the killing and looting subsided, he emerged and declared himself a great general of the Jin Dynasty, wishing to report matters. This suggests that he did not surrender but intended to sacrifice himself by emerging on his own. The official biography in the Jin Shi also details his heroic martyrdom, which differs significantly from this account.

    Chuo Hua Shan was highly esteemed by the literati. Wang Wo Zhongze was in his elder brother's military headquarters, and Chuo Hua Shan followed him in his studies. Zhongze's writing was very impressive, and they studied Confucian classics together, continuing their studies without interruption. They were respected leaders of their time.

    伊喇都尉玛努勒【案玛努勒旧作买奴今改】字温甫契丹世袭明安也读史书慷慨有气义喜交士大夫每以肝胆许人尤重然诺尝为宣抚使便宜邓豫间以事杖杀经歴官坐废后为虎贲都尉提兵赴闗中后由商南全军而回病死自号拙轩赵闲闲为赋之诸公皆有诗正大初先子令叶余往省防温甫属余为拙轩铭先子亦有诗伊喇枢宻聂赫【案聂赫旧作粘合今改】字廷玉契丹世袭明安也弟兄俱好文幕府延致名士初帅彭城雷希顔在幕杨叔能元裕之皆游其门一时士望甚重为将镇静守边不扰军民便之天兴东狩知国亡率邓州军民诣宋人纳款宋以兵马辖处之赐第居襄阳未防病死

    Explanation

    99

    Ila Commandant Ma Nule [Note: Ma Nule was previously written as Mai Nu, but is now corrected] with the courtesy name Wenfu, was a hereditary official among the Khitans. He read historical books with a generous and righteous spirit, enjoyed the company of scholars and officials, and always offered his heart and gallbladder to others, especially valuing his promises. He once served as an envoy, and during his time in Deng and Yu, he punished a certain official for misconduct, leading to his own dismissal. Later, he became a Tiger Guard Commandant and led troops to Guanzhong. After returning from Shangnan with the entire army intact, he died of illness and self-named his hut "Simple Hut." Zhao Xianxian wrote a poem about it, and many scholars composed poems as well. In the early years of Zhengda, my father sent me to visit and console Wenfu, who entrusted me to write an epitaph for the Simple Hut. My father also composed a poem.

    Ila Chancellor Nie He [Note: Nie He was previously written as Nian He, but is now corrected] with the courtesy name Tingyu, was also a hereditary official among the Khitans. His brothers both loved literature, and the military office invited famous scholars. Initially commanding Pengcheng, Lei Xiyuan was in the military office, and Yang Shuneng and Yuan Yuzhi both frequented his door, making him highly esteemed among the scholars of the time. As a general, he was calm and stable in his defense of the border, not disturbing the military and civilians. During the eastern hunt of Tianxing, he knew the country had fallen and led the military and civilians of Dengzhou to the Song people, surrendering. The Song gave him a mansion to live in Xiangyang, but he died of illness before long.

    100

    南渡之初将帅中最著名者曰郭仲元俗号郭大相公其军号花帽子曰郭阿林俗号郭三相公【案金史本仲元本姓郭与阿林均赐姓完顔】其军号黄袖二人本非亲兄弟以其壮勇年齿先后为配仲元为将重厚沈毅有谋守凤翔北兵力攻数月不下而退卒保其城以闻后为兵部尚书右卫尉卒阿林最骁勇人莫能敌屡与北兵战有功一时为士庶属目后提兵闗中与

    Explanation

    100

    In the early period after the Southern Migration, the most famous generals were Guo Zhongyuan, who was popularly known as "Dajiangong," and his military unit was called "Huamaozi." Guo Ailin, who was popularly known as "Sajiangong," was another notable general. According to the Jin History, both Guo Zhongyuan and Guo Ailin were granted the surname "Wanyan." The military units of Guo Zhongyuan and Guo Ailin were not actually related but were paired due to their bravery and age. Guo Zhongyuan, as a general, was serious, dignified, and resolute, with strategic prowess. He defended Fengxiang against the northern army, which attacked for several months but failed to capture the city. After the northern army retreated, Guo Zhongyuan successfully defended the city and reported his victory. He was later promoted to the position of Minister of War and Right Guard General, and he died in this role. Guo Ailin was the most valiant and no one could match him in battle. He fought many times against the northern army and achieved significant victories, earning the attention of both the elite and the common people. He later led troops in Guanzhong.
