Reflecting on the past, he lamented his present state. His beard remained unblemished by age, but he exchanged his grand strategy to pacify the barbarians for a book on planting trees. This poem records his youthful experiences.

    High Chancellor Yanfu, in his position, celebrated his seventieth birthday on the first day of the first month of the Yuan Guang era. He invited his old friends and acquaintances from the village to write poems and essays for him. At the time, my father, who had recently been dismissed from his post as a censor, avoided suspicion and did not attend. I, being in my early twenties, wrote a poem for him, which contained words that criticized him and advised him to retire. Upon receiving the poem, High Chancellor Yanfu was greatly pleased and quickly summoned me to greet him, saying, "You can achieve high office through your own efforts without needing a step-by-step promotion, can you?" He then patted my back and said, "How well you have written your name down here." My poem reads:

    Achieving high office through one's own efforts, without needing a step-by-step promotion. After ten years, one can hold a high position with ease, bearing the weight of the pillars of the hall. Harmonizing opinions is as difficult as seasoning with salt and plum. Diligently serving three consecutive dynasties, reaching seventy years old with good health. Family prosperity increased, having grandchildren, wearing clothes and using a cane, returning home happily.

    Lei Xiyuan wrote a preface for this poem, which also included words suggesting resignation. Later, when I was returning to Huaiyang, I submitted a letter advising him to recommend someone to replace himself, which could lead to his retirement. However, he died in office and could not follow through.

    137

    明昌承安间作诗者尚尖新故张翥仲由布衣有名召用其诗大抵皆浮艶语如矮窻小戸寒不到一炉香火四围书又西风了却黄花事不管安仁两鬓秋人号张了却刘少宣尝题其诗集后云枫落呉江真好句不须多示郑参军盖讥之也南渡后文风一变文多学奇古诗多学风雅由赵闲闲李屏山倡之幼无师为文下笔便喜左氏庄周故能一扫辽宋余习而雷希顔宋飞卿诸人皆作古文故复往往相效法不作浅弱语赵闲闲晚年诗多法唐人李杜诸公然未尝语于人已而麻知几李晨源元裕之辈鼎出故后进作诗者争以唐人为法也

    137

    During the Mingchang and Cheng'an periods, poets still valued sharpness and novelty. Thus, Zhang Zhu, known as Zhongyang, rose from a commoner to fame and was summoned for service. His poetry was largely characterized by flowery and ornate language, such as "a small window and door where the cold does not reach, with a single incense burner surrounded by books," and "the west wind finishes the yellow flower affair, regardless of the autumn of Anren's temples." People called him "Zhang of the Finished Affair." Liu Shaoxuan once inscribed on the back of his poetry collection: "The falling of the paulownia leaves in Wujiang is truly a fine line, but there is no need to show it to General Zheng." This was a critique of him. After the Southern Crossing, the literary style underwent a significant change. Writings became more learned and ancient, and poetry followed the elegance of the classics. This shift was championed by Zhao Xianxian and Li Pingshan. From a young age, they had no teachers to instruct them, so when they wrote, they naturally favored the styles of Zuo Qiuming and Zhuangzi, thus they were able to sweep away the remnants of the Liao and Song dynasties. Many others, such as Lei Xiyan and Song Feiqing, also wrote in the classical style, often imitating each other and avoiding weak and shallow expressions. In his later years, Zhao Xianxian's poetry mostly followed the style of the Tang poets Li Bai and Du Fu, though he never spoke of this to others. Soon after, Ma Zhiji, Li Chenyuan, and Yuan Yuzhi emerged, and thus younger poets competed to emulate the Tang style.

    138

    赵闲闲尝言律诗最难工须要工巧周圆吾闻竹溪党公论以为五十六字皆如圣贤中有一字不经罏锤便若一屠沽子厠其间也又云八句皆要警抜极难一篇中须要一联好句为主后但以意收拾之足为好诗矣又尝与余论诗曰选诗曰南登灞陵岸囘首望长安朔风动秋草边马有归心明月照髙楼流光正徘徊此其含蓄意几何又曰小诗贵风骚今人往往止作硬语非也
    　　赵闲闲少尝寄黄华【王氏庭筠】诗黄华称之曰非作千首其工夫不至是也其诗至今为人传诵且赵以此诗初得名诗云寄语雪溪王处士年来多病复何如浮云世态纷纷变秋草人情日日疎李白一杯人影月郑防三絶画诗书情知不得文章力乞与黄华作隐居

    Explanation

    138

    Zhao Xianxian once said that regulated verse is the most difficult to master, requiring skillful craftsmanship and completeness. I have heard that Dang Gong of the Bamboo Stream opined that every character in the fifty-six syllables of a poem should be as refined as those of the sages; if even one character is not polished, it would be like a butcher or wine seller intruding among the sages. He also said that making each line striking is extremely difficult, and in a single poem, one must have a key couplet as the main focus. After that, one can arrange the rest according to the theme, and that would be a good poem. He also once discussed poetry with me, saying, "In the anthology of poems, 'Ascending the banks of Baling and looking back at Chang'an, the northern wind stirs the autumn grass, and the border horses have homesickness. The bright moon shines on the high tower, and the light lingers in its wanderings.' What is the subtle meaning of this?" He also said, "Short poems value elegance and charm, but nowadays people often write in stiff language, which is not right."

    Zhao Xianxian, when he was young, once sent a poem to Huang Huá (Wang Shiyuan). Huang Huá praised it, saying, "If one does not write a thousand poems, one's effort is not enough." His poem is still widely recited today, and Zhao gained fame with this very poem. The poem reads: "Sending words to Wang Shixian of Snow Stream, how have you been since your many illnesses? The world's fickle nature changes like floating clouds, and human feelings grow increasingly distant each day. With a cup of wine, Li Bai casts a shadow of the moon, and Zheng Fang excels in painting, poetry, and calligraphy. Knowing that one cannot achieve literary success through force alone, I ask to join Huang Huá in seclusion."

    139

    赵闲闲尝为余言少初识尹无忌问久闻先生作诗不喜蘓黄何如无忌曰学蘓黄则卑猥也其诗一以李杜为法五言尤工闲闲尝称其防同乐园诗云晴日明华搆繁隂荡緑波蓬丘沧海逺春色上林多流水时虽逝迁莺暖自歌可怜欢乐极钲鼓散云和又有佳句行云春郭暗归鸟暮天苍野色明残照江声入暮云甚似少陵闲闲又称赵黄山诗云灯暗风翻幔蛩吟叶拥墙人如秋已老愁与夜俱长滴尽堦前雨
    催成镜里霜黄花依旧好多病不能觞此诗信佳诗也又黄山尝于黄山道中作诗有云好景落谁诗句里蹇驴防我画图中世号赵蹇驴余先子翰林尝谈章宗春水放海青时黄山在翰苑扈从既得鹅索诗黄山立进之其诗云鴐鹅得暖下陂塘防骑星驰入建章黄伞轻隂随凤辇緑衣小队出鹰坊抟风玉爪凌霄汉瞥目风毛堕雪霜共喜园陵得新荐侍臣齐捧万年觞章宗览之称其工且曰此诗非宿搆不能至此

    Explanation

    139

    Zhao Xianxian once told me that when he first met Yin Wujie, he asked if he had heard that I did not like to write poetry in the style of Su Shi and Huang Tingjian. Yin Wujie replied that learning from Su and Huang would be vulgar. His poetry takes Li Bai and Du Fu as models, especially in five-character verse. Zhao Xianxian often praised his poem "Fangtong Garden" which reads: "On a sunny day, the flowers are bright; in the shade, the green waves dance. A small island floats in the vast sea; the spring colors fill the imperial garden. The stream flows on, though time passes; the warm spring brings songs of the migrating birds. Alas, the joy is fleeting; the drums and flutes scatter like clouds. There are also fine lines: 'Clouds cover the spring city at dusk; birds return to the twilight sky. The wild colors shine in the setting sun; the river's voice echoes in the evening clouds.' It is very similar to Du Fu's style. Zhao Xianxian also praised Zhao Huangshan's poem which reads: "The lamp dims as the wind flips the curtain; the cricket sings among the leaves. The walls are surrounded by trees; the man is as old as autumn, with sorrow that grows with the night. The rain falls from the steps; the frost forms in the mirror. The yellow chrysanthemums remain the same; the sick man cannot drink wine." This poem is indeed a good one.

    Zhao Huangshan once wrote a poem along the Huangshan Road which reads: "Good scenery falls into whose poem? A slow donkey blocks my picture. The world calls Zhao Huangshan 'Zhao the Slow Donkey.' My father, a member of the Hanlin Academy, once talked about the time when Emperor Zhangzong released the sea eagles in the spring water. At that time, Zhao Huangshan was in the Hanlin Academy, accompanying the emperor. After receiving a goose, he was asked to write a poem. Zhao Huangshan immediately presented this poem: 'The geese find warmth in the pond; the horsemen gallop into the palace. The yellow umbrella follows the phoenix carriage; the green-clad officials leave the eagle training grounds. The eagles soar with their jade claws reaching the heavens; the swift feathers fall like snow and frost. All rejoice at the new offering at the imperial tomb; the court officials present the long-lasting cup of wine.' Emperor Zhangzong read it and praised its excellence, saying, 'This poem could not have been composed on the spur of the moment.'

    140

    赵闲闲平日字画工夫最深诗次之又其次散文也尝语余曰今日后进中作文者颇有三二人至吟诗者絶少字画亦无也以是知公所长然议论经学许王从之散文许李之纯雷希顔诗颇许麻知几元裕之字画颇许麻知几冯叔献也又尝教余学书先法张旭石柱记每曰汝辈幸有天资正不许学古人一防一画写也李屏山雅喜奨援后进每得一人诗文有可称必延誉于人然颇轻许可故赵闲闲尝云被之纯坏却后进只奬誉教为狂后雷希顔亦颇接引士流赵云雷希顔又如此然屏山在世一时才士皆趋向之至于赵所成立者甚少惟主贡举时得李钦叔献能后尝以文章荐麻知几九畴入仕至今士论止归屏山也

    Explanation

    140

    Zhao Xianxian was most skilled in calligraphy, followed by poetry, and then prose. He once told me that among the younger generation, there were only a few who could write essays, even fewer who could recite poetry, and none who could practice calligraphy. From this, I understood his strengths. In terms of discussing Confucian classics, Xu Wang Congzhi followed him; in prose, Li Zhipure and Lei Xiyang; in poetry, Ma Zhiji and Yuan Yuzhi; in calligraphy, Ma Zhiji and Feng Shuxian. Zhao Xianxian also taught me to learn calligraphy by first following Zhang Xu's Stone Pillar Record, saying that we are fortunate to have natural talent and should not imitate every stroke and character of the ancients. Li Pingshan, who was fond of supporting young talent, would always praise anyone whose poetry or prose was commendable. However, he was very lenient in his praise, which led Zhao Xianxian to say that Li Pingshan's excessive praise had misled the younger generation, encouraging them to be wild. Lei Xiyang also actively supported young scholars, and Zhao Xianxian thought that Lei Xiyang was similar in this regard. Despite this, during Li Pingshan's lifetime, all talented scholars tended to follow him. As for Zhao Xianxian, he had very few people he could establish as successful. He only managed to select Li Qinshuxian when he was in charge of the imperial examinations. Later, he recommended Ma Zhiji and Jiu Chou for official positions based on their writings. To this day, scholars' opinions only attribute credit to Li Pingshan.

    141

    李屏山教后学为文欲自成一家每曰当别转一路勿随人脚跟故多喜奇怪然其文亦不出庄左栁蘓诗不出卢仝李贺晚甚爱杨万里诗曰活泼剌底人难及也赵闲闲教后进为诗文则曰文章不可执一体有时奇古有时平淡何拘李尝与余论赵文曰才甚髙气象甚雄然不免有失支堕节处盖学东坡而不成者赵亦语余曰之纯文字止一体诗只一向去也又赵诗多犯古人语一篇或有数句此亦文章病屏山尝序其闲闲集云公诗往往有李太白白乐天语某辄能识之又云公谓男子不食人唾后当与之纯天英作真文字亦隂讥云
    　　赵闲闲论文曰文字无太硬之纯文字最硬何伤王翰林从之则曰文字无软者惟其是也余尝以质诸先人先人以赵论为是

    Explanation

    141

    Li Bingshan taught his students to write with the aim of forming their own unique style. He often said that they should take a different path and not follow others' footsteps, which is why he favored the strange and unusual. However, his writing did not go beyond the styles of Zhuangzi and Laozi, Liu Yuxi, and Su Shi. His poetry did not surpass Lu Tong and Li He. Later, he greatly admired Yang Wanli's poetry, saying it was vivid and lively, surpassing others.

    Zhao Xianxian taught his students to write poetry and prose, saying that writing cannot adhere to one style; sometimes it should be strange and ancient, sometimes plain and simple. Why be confined by Li Bai? He once discussed Zhao's writing with me, saying that Zhao's talent was very high, his style was very grand, but he could not help but have some lapses in judgment, as he had not fully succeeded in emulating Su Shi. Zhao also told me, "True writing has only one style; poetry should only follow one direction." Moreover, Zhao's poetry often repeated the phrases of ancient poets, sometimes having several lines in one poem, which is also a flaw in writing. Li Bingshan once wrote a preface to Zhao's Xianxian Collection, saying that Zhao's poetry often contained the words of Li Bai and Bai Juyi, which I could recognize. He also said that Zhao believed a man should not eat others' spittle, and later he would work with Tian Ying to create true literature, which was also a subtle criticism.

    Zhao Xianxian wrote about literature, saying that there is no overly hard pure writing; the hardest writing is not harmful. Wang Hanlin agreed, saying that there is no soft writing, only what is true. I once discussed this with my father, who agreed with Zhao's view.

    142

    兴定元光间余在南京从赵闲闲李屏山王从之雷希顔诸公游多论为文作诗赵于诗最细贵含蓄工夫于文颇麄止论气象大概李于文甚细説关键宾主抑于诗颇麄止论词气才巧故余于赵则取其作诗法于李则取其为文法若王则贵议论文字有体致不喜出奇下字止欲如家人语言尤以助辞为首与屏山之纯学大不同尝曰之纯虽才髙好作险句怪语无意味亦不喜司马迁史记云失支堕节者多韩退之原道如此好文字末曰人其人火其书太下字
    栁子厚肥皮厚肉柔筋脆骨之此何等语千古以来惟推东坡为第一人多发古名篇中疵病渊明归去来辞前想像后直述不相侔伯伦酒德颂有大人先生是寓言后闻吾风声吾当作其退之盘谷序前云友人后云昌黎韩愈似不相识永叔蘓子美墓志争为人所传既用争字当曰人争传之不然曰为人所传不须争字子瞻超然台记物有以蔽之矣作字好此甚多不可胜纪雷则论文尚简古全法退之诗亦喜韩兼好黄鲁直新巧毎作诗文好与朋友相商订有不

    Explanation

    142

    During the years of Xingding and Yuan Guang (1217-1224) of the Jin Dynasty, I was in Nanjing and associated with Zhao Yishan, Li Pingshan, Wang Congzhi, and Lei Xiyan. We often discussed writing and poetry. Zhao was the most meticulous in poetry, valuing subtlety and restraint, but his prose was more general, focusing only on the overall atmosphere. Li was very detailed in prose, discussing the main points, supporting arguments, and balance, but his poetry was less detailed, focusing on the clever use of language. Wang valued well-structured and meaningful writing, disliked unusual words, preferred simple, everyday language, and emphasized the importance of auxiliary words, differing significantly from Li's approach. Lei valued simplicity and antiquity in literary style, followed Han Yu entirely, also appreciated the new and ingenious aspects of Huang Tingjian's style, and preferred to discuss and refine his work with friends. Liu Zongyuan described people with thick skin, thick meat, soft sinews, and brittle bones, a vivid and unusual description. Throughout history, Su Shi has been regarded as the first in literature, often pointing out flaws in ancient masterpieces. Tao Yuanming's Return to the Fields begins with imagination and then proceeds directly, lacking coherence. Ruan Ji's Ode to the Virtue of Wine features the allegorical figure of "Great Man," which later became known as "I have heard of your reputation, so I came." Han Yu's Original Dao suggests destroying those who deviate from the right path, a harsh statement. Su Shi's Record of the Chao Ruan Terrace mentions that there are things that obscure it, and he preferred clear and concise writing. Such preferences are numerous and too many to count.

    143

    安相告立改之此亦人所难也正大中王翰林从之在史院领史事雷翰林希顔为应奉兼编修官同修宣宗实録二公由文体不同多纷争盖王平日好平淡纪实雷尚奇峭造语也王则云实録止文其当时事贵不失真自作史则又异也雷则云作文字无句法委靡不振不足观故雷所作王多改革雷大愤不平语人曰请将吾二人所作令天下文士定其是非王亦不屑王尝曰希顔作文好用恶硬字何以为竒雷亦曰从之持论甚髙文章亦难止以经义科举法绳之也
    　　雷翰林希顔为人作碑志虽称其德善其疵短亦互见之尝曰文章止是襃与贬初作屏山墓志数处有微言刘光甫读之不能平与宋飞卿交劝令削去及刻石犹存浮湛于酒其性厌怠有不屑为之言余谓碑志本以章其人之善虽不可溢美有媿辞然当实録其善事使传信后世若疵短则不当书也况非作史传何必贬焉且其子孙览之岂得自安也
    　　赵闲闲作南城访道图诸公皆有诗尝有一齐希谦者题云亿刼梦中夸识解一生纸上作风波到今不肯抽头去毕竟南城有甚麽人颇传之

    Explanation

    143

    During the reign of the Jurchen Jin dynasty, Wang Huanlin, a scholar-official, was in charge of historical records in the historical office. Lei Hanyan, another scholar-official, served as a literary attendant and compiler, and together they compiled the official history of Emperor Xuanzong. Due to their different writing styles, they often had disputes. Wang preferred a straightforward and factual style, while Lei favored a unique and sharp style. Wang once said that the official history should only record the events of the time accurately, without embellishment. When writing history, however, the standards are different. Lei, on the other hand, believed that writing should have a clear structure and avoid being weak and unimpressive. As a result, Wang often revised Lei's work, which greatly angered Lei. Lei once said to others, "Please let all the scholars in the world judge the merits of our respective works." Wang, however, did not care for such judgments. He once remarked, "Lei enjoys using harsh and difficult words in his writing, which is not what I consider remarkable." Lei also said that Wang's standards for writing were very high, and it is difficult to apply the criteria of the imperial examinations to literary writing.

    Lei Hanyan, when writing epitaphs, would praise the virtues of the deceased but also mention their flaws. He once said that writing is essentially about praise and criticism. When he first wrote an epitaph for the tomb of Ping Shan, it contained some subtle criticisms. Liu Guangfu read it and was dissatisfied, and together with Song Fei, they advised Lei to remove the criticisms. However, even after the stone was carved, the criticisms remained. Lei was immersed in alcohol and indifferent to such matters. I believe that epitaphs should primarily highlight the virtues of the deceased, even if they cannot be overly praised. However, one should record their good deeds truthfully so that they are passed down to future generations. If there are flaws, they should not be recorded, especially since this is not a historical biography. What would the descendants think if they read such things?

    Zhao Xianxian once painted a picture titled "Visiting the Dao in Nancheng," and many scholars wrote poems about it. There was a man named Qi Xiqian who wrote a poem that said, "In a dream spanning eons, he boasted of his understanding. Throughout his life, he created waves on paper. Even now, he refuses to withdraw. What, after all, is there about Nancheng?" This poem became quite famous.

    144

    赵闲闲以文学名一世于吏事非所长兴定初珠赫髙琪为相恶士大夫有罪辄以军储论加棰杖在位者往往被其苦俄命赵公摄南京转运司未几果坐误粮草事当杖既奏宣宗曰学士岂当棰耶髙琪曰不然无以戒后遂杖四十公大愤焉其后髙琪诛诏适当公笔首曰君臣分严无将之罪莫大夫妇义重不睦之刑何逃曽是一身兼此二恶人谓赵公之仇雪矣
    　　正大初赵闲闲长翰林苑同陈正叔潘仲明雷希顔元裕之诸人作诗防尝赋野菊赵有云冈断秋光隔河明月影交荒丛号蟋蟀病叶挂蟏蛸欲访陶彭泽柴门何处敲诸公称其破的也又分咏古瓶蜡梅赵云苕华吐碧龙文涩烛泪痕疎鴈字横后云娇黄唤起昭阳梦汉苑凄凉草生句甚工潘有云命薄从教官独冷眼明犹喜物双清语亦老也后分忆橙射虎题甚多最后咏道学雷云青天白日理分明亦为题所窘也闲闲同馆阁诸公九日登极目亭俱有诗题云魏国

    Explanation

    144

    Zhao Xianxian was renowned throughout the world for his literary talent, but he was not skilled in official duties. In the early Xingding era, Zhu He and Gao Qi served as chancellors and treated scholars and officials who committed crimes harshly, often punishing them with military provisions and physical beatings. Those in power often suffered from it. Soon after, Zhao was appointed to temporarily take charge of the Nanyang Transport Office. Not long after, he was punished for a mistake in grain and fodder matters and was sentenced to flogging. After reporting this to Emperor Xuanzong, the emperor said, "Is it appropriate to flog a scholar?" Gao Qi replied, "Otherwise, there would be no way to warn future generations," and Zhao was flogged forty times. Zhao was greatly angered by this. Later, Gao Qi was executed, and the imperial edict was appropriately written by Zhao. The edict began, "The distinction between ruler and minister is strict; the crime of rebellion is grave. The bond between husband and wife is strong; what punishment can escape for discord? Once, one person committed both of these evils. People say that Zhao Gong's grudge has been avenged."

    In the early Zhengda era, Zhao Xianxian was the head of the Hanlin Academy and collaborated with Chen Zhengshu, Pan Zhongming, Lei Xiyan, Yuan Yuzhi, and others to compose poetry together. They once wrote a poem about wild chrysanthemums, and Zhao contributed a line: "The autumn light breaks through the mountains, and the moon's reflection crosses the river." The other scholars praised this line as hitting the mark. They also divided into poems about an ancient vase and winter jasmine. Zhao wrote, "The winter jasmine blooms with green, the dragon's text is clear, the candle's tears are sparse, and the goose's words are horizontal." Later, he wrote, "The delicate yellow awakens the dream of the Yellow Emperor, and the Han garden is desolate with grass." His language was also mature. They later divided into poems about recalling oranges and shooting tigers, with many titles. Finally, they wrote poems about the Way, and Lei contributed a line: "The clear sky and bright sun make the principles clear." This was also constrained by the title. Zhao Xianxian and the other officials in the Hanlin Academy climbed the Jigum Pavilion on the ninth day of the ninth month, and all wrote poems with the title "Wei Guo."

    145

    山河残照在梁王楼殿野花开鸥从白水明边没雁向青天尽处囘未必龙山如此防座中三馆尽英才雷希顔云千古雄豪几人在百年怀抱此时开李钦止云连朝倥偬簿书堆辜黄花酒一杯凡作诗和韵为难古人赠答皆以不拘韵字迨宋蘓黄凡唱和须用元韵往返数回以出竒余先子颇留意故与人唱和韵益狭语益工人多称之尝与雷希顔元裕之论诗元云和韵非古要为勉强先子云如能以彼韵就我意何如亦一竒也尝在史院与屏山诸公唱和李唐卿海藏斋
    诗舟字韵往返十余首先子有云绣坼旧图翻短褐朱书小字记归舟屏山大称其工用事也后居淮阳与刘少宣唱和村字韵亦往返数十首最后论诗有云杨刘变体号西昆窃笑登坛子美村大抵俗儒无正眼惟应后世自公言光生杜曲今千丈派出江西本一源此道陵迟嗟久矣不才安敢擅专门又乐府虚传山抹云诗名浪得栁连村九原太白有生气千古少陵无间言登太山巅小天下到昆仑口知河源如君少进可入室顾我今衰不及门少宣以为全不觉用他人韵也

    Explanation

    145

    The setting sun on the mountains and rivers shines upon the grand buildings of Liang Wang, where wildflowers bloom and seagulls disappear into the bright waters, while geese fly back towards the distant blue sky. Perhaps even the majestic Dragon Mountain is not as formidable as this. The three halls are filled with talented individuals. Le Xiyan remarked, "How many of the ancient heroes and warriors still exist? The long-held aspirations of a century are realized now." Li Qinzheng said, "Throughout the day, I am busy with official documents, and I regret wasting a cup of yellow flower wine." Composing poetry in a given rhyme scheme is difficult; ancient poets were not bound by strict rhyme schemes in their exchanges. By the Song Dynasty, poets like Su Shi and Huang Tingjian used the original rhyme scheme in their exchanges, going back and forth several times to achieve something unusual. My father paid close attention to this, so in his exchanges with others, the rhyme scheme became narrower, and the language more refined, earning much praise. He once discussed poetry with Lei Xiyan and Yuan Yuzhi. Yuan said, "Using a given rhyme scheme is not ancient practice and requires effort." My father replied, "If one can use the given rhyme scheme to express their own thoughts, it would be a remarkable achievement." He also composed poetry with Ping Shan at the Hai Cangzhai in the history bureau, using the shi and zhou rhyme scheme, going back and forth more than ten times. My father once said, "The old tapestry is torn apart and replaced with a simple robe; red ink and small characters record the returning boat." Ping Shan highly praised the work for its skillful use of allusions. Later, when he lived in Huaiyang, he exchanged poetry with Liu Shaoxuan using the cun rhyme scheme, going back and forth more than thirty times. In their final discussion of poetry, he said, "The Western Kun style, associated with Yang and Liu, is a poetic style that I secretly laugh at the simple village where the poet Zimei once stood. Generally, common scholars lack proper insight; only future generations can speak truly. The glory of Du Fu's poetry shines like a thousand-foot curve; the origin of Jiangxi poetry is one source. This path has declined for a long time, and how dare I claim expertise in this field? The Yuefu poetry is said to have been inspired by the imagery of clouds brushing against the mountains, and the poet's reputation is falsely gained from the imagery of willows connecting villages. In the nine regions, Li Bai still has vitality, and throughout the ages, Du Fu is without reproach. Climbing the summit of Mount Tai makes the world seem small, and reaching the mouth of Kunlun reveals the source of the river. If you advance a little more, you can enter the inner sanctum; but I am old and cannot reach the threshold." Liu Shaoxuan thought that my father had not noticed using others' rhyme schemes.

    146

    聨句亦诗中难事盖座中立书不暇深思也南京龙德宫赵闲闲李屏山王正之联句王云猴未穷巧穴蚁已失王人多称之余先子亦留意主长簿时与屏山张仲杰防饮坐中有定磁酒瓯因为联句先子首唱曰定州花磁瓯顔色天下白诸公称之屏山则曰轻浮妾玻璃顽钝奴琥珀张则曰器质至坚脆肤理还悦泽后居淮阳冀京父来过雪夜联句先子有云疎见飞霙窻静闻落屑又李钦叔来过李子迁在坐防合聨句先子有首唱曰玉立两谪仙鼎峙三敌国又云三强出竒兵八柱乃八克一老怯大敌三战即三北后自大梁归陈与祁联句先子首云红抛汴梁城緑吸淮阳酒后令叶县中秋夜与郝坊州仲纯王飞伯辈聨句具载蓬门集中

    Explanation

    146

    Collaborative poetry is also a difficult task in poetry, as it requires quick writing in a group setting without time for deep reflection. At the Longde Palace in Nanjing, poets Zhao Xianxian, Li Pingshan, and Wang Zhengzhi engaged in collaborative poetry. Wang once said, "The monkey's tricks have not exhausted their ingenuity, but the ant has already lost its way." This was often praised by others. My father also paid attention to this and, while serving as a clerk in the Chánglǐ Office, collaborated with Pingshan and Zhang Zhongjie during a drinking session. Among them was a porcelain bowl from Dingzhou, and my father composed the first line: "The porcelain bowl from Dingzhou, its color pure white." The others praised it. Pingshan then said, "Light and delicate like glass, sturdy and dull like amber." Zhang added, "Its structure is strong yet brittle, its surface smooth and lustrous." Later, when residing in Huaiyang and Jijing, my father collaborated with a friend during a snowy night. He wrote, "Sparse trees reveal falling snow, quiet windows hear the sound of falling flakes." When Li Qinshu visited, Li Ziqian was present, and they collaborated on a poem. My father composed the first line: "Two exiled immortals stand tall, three rival states stand like a tripod." He also wrote, "Three strong forces emerge with innovative strategies, eight pillars achieve victory. One old man fears a powerful enemy, losing three battles in succession." After returning from Daliang, my father collaborated with Chen and Qi. He composed the first line: "Red is thrown in Bianliang, green is absorbed in Huaiyang." Later, on the Mid-Autumn Night in Yexian, he collaborated with Hao Fangzhou Zhongchun and Wang Feibo, and all these collaborations are recorded in the Pengmen Collection.

    147

    归潜志卷八
    　　钦定四库全书
    　　归潜志卷九
    　　元　刘祁　撰
    　　余先子翰林令叶时同坊州仲纯赋昆阳懐古诗诸公多继作先子有云营屯滍水横陈处计堕刘郎小怯中天上雷风扫妖气人间虎豹畏真龙千秋一片昆溪月曽照堂堂盖世雄郝云战骨至今埋滍水暮云何处是舂陵李长源云颍川南下郁陂陁遐想当年战垒多自是真人清宇宙谁为防子试干戈元裕之云英威未觉消沈尽试向舂陵望郁葱王飞伯云落日一川英气在西
    风万叶战声来后云谁倚城楼吊兴废一声长笛暮云间史学优李钦叔白文举皆有诗余亦作一古诗也古人多有偶得佳句而不能立题者如山谷云清鉴风流归贺八飞跋扈付朱三未知可以赠谁又云人得交游是风月天开图画即江山亦无全篇余先子尝有句云推愁不去若移石呼酒不来如望霓又半生窃禄鱼贪饵四海无家鸟择栖又未解作诗如见画常忧读赋错呼霓

    Explanation

    147

    归潜志卷八
    钦定四库全书
    归潜志卷九
    元 刘祁 撰

    我的父亲当时担任翰林令叶，与坊州的仲纯一同创作了关于昆阳怀古的诗篇，许多学者纷纷效仿。我的父亲写道：营寨沿滍水排列，刘郎的计谋稍显怯懦；天上的雷风扫荡了妖气，人间的虎豹畏惧真龙。千秋万代，一片昆溪月光照耀着堂堂盖世的英雄。郝云说，战死者的白骨至今仍埋在滍水边，暮云笼罩下，何处是舂陵？李长源说，颍川南下，郁郁的陂陁让人遐想当年的战垒众多，这是真人的清宇，谁敢与之较量？元裕之说，英威未觉消沉尽，试向舂陵望郁葱。王飞伯说，落日映照一川英气，西风卷起万叶战声，后云谁倚城楼吊古，一声长笛在暮云间响起。史学优李钦叔、白文举都有诗作，我也写了一首古诗。古人多有偶得佳句而不能立题者，如山谷云：清鉴风流归贺八，飞飏跋扈付朱三，未知可以赠谁？又云：人得交游是风月，天开图画即江山，亦无全篇。我的父亲曾有句云：推愁不去若移石，呼酒不来如望霓。又云：半生窃禄鱼贪饵，四海无家鸟择栖。又云：未解作诗如见画，常忧读赋错呼霓。

    148

    梦中作诗或得句多清迈出尘余先祖龙山君尝梦得句云山路崭有壁松风清无尘先子梦中诗云落月浸天池余幼年梦中亦有作诗猿哭处江天暮白雁来时泽国秋如鬼语也
    　　先翰林罢御史闲居淮阳种五竹堂后自娯作诗云拨土移根卜日辰森森便有气凌云真成阙里二三子大胜樊川十万军影浸凉蟾牕上见声敲寒雨枕边闻林间故事传西晋不数山王咏五君以寄赵闲闲防闲闲亦于闲闲堂后种竹甚多一日礼部诏余曰昨夕欲和丈人竹诗牵于韵自作一篇答其意可也因出其诗云君家种竹五七个我亦近栽三四竿两地平分风月破大家留待雪霜看土膏生意叶犹卷客枕梦魂声已寒见此又思君子面何时相对倚阑

    Explanation

    148

    Dreams often yield verses of such clarity and transcendence that they rise above the mundane. My ancestor, Lord Longshan, once dreamt a line: "The mountain path has a steep and clear boundary, and the pine wind is fresh and free of dust." My father, in his dreams, composed: "The moonlight reflects on a lake or pool." Even in my youth, I too dreamt of writing poetry: "In the twilight over the river and sky, a monkey cries; when the white geese arrive in the marshy region, it is autumn." It was as if the dream content were spoken by a ghost.

    A former official, after retiring from his post, planted five bamboo trees behind his hall in Huaiyang for personal enjoyment and composed poetry. He wrote: "Digging up and transplanting the roots, choosing a favorable day, and the resulting growth that seems to reach towards the sky, creating a sense of grandeur. Truly, the bamboo is as elegant and strong as the disciples of Confucius, surpassing the army of Fan Zhongyan in terms of cultural and moral authority. The shadow of the moon seen through the window and the sound of rain heard from the pillow, creating a peaceful and intimate atmosphere. Stories from the Western Jin dynasty, specifically mentioning the 'Five Gentlemen,' and comparing them to the 'Mountain and Water' of the time, indicating a connection to the literary and cultural heritage of the era. To send a message or gift to Zhao Xianxian, who also planted many bamboo trees behind his hall, indicating a shared appreciation for bamboo and its symbolic significance."

    One day, the Ministry of Rites summoned me and said: "Last night, I intended to compose a poem in harmony with the bamboo, but was constrained by the rhyme. I will compose a poem myself to respond to your meaning." He then presented his poem: "In your home, you have planted five or seven bamboo trees; I too have recently planted three or four. The wind and moonlight are equally divided between the two places, and the beauty of the scene will be appreciated even in the harsh conditions of winter. The vitality of the earth and the curling leaves of the bamboo, while also evoking the coldness of a dream and the sound of a guest's pillow, suggesting a contrast between the natural world and human experience. Seeing this, I think of the face of a gentleman. When will we be able to face each other and lean against the railing?"

    149

    干先子后和其韵云我家陈郡子梁园不约同栽竹数竿清入梦魂千里共笑开诗眼几囘看幽资淡不追时好苦节相期保歳寒八坐文昌天咫尺得如闲客倚防干又李澥公渡因游园城防云中一僧曰德超谈及乡里名家刘雷事公渡留诗云邂逅云中老阿师思人许我话刘雷略谈近日诸孙事颇觉衰懐一笑开众道髯参宜帅幕【谓希顔】人怜短簿去霜台【谓先子】园城香火西庵地尝记秋髙雨后来后先子过园见之和其韵云上林春晚数归期轣辘车
    声病转雷翠幄防田桑叶密緑云夹路麦花开偶因假馆留萧寺试问游方指卮台【陈郡】白首衲僧同里闬亦知吾祖有云来余以示闲闲闲闲亦如其韵寄先子云屏山殁后使人悲此外交亲我与雷千里老懐何日写一生笑口几时开心知契濶留陈土时复登临上吹台目极天低雁囘处西风忽送好诗来先子复和云两地相望云与泥敢期胶漆嗣陈雷遥怜晓镜霜须满但对故人青眼开且趁梅芳醉梁苑莫因雁过问燕台上林花栁惊春晚蓬勃西风卷土来

    Explanation

    149

    After the original poem by the elder son, the younger son followed with a harmonized version:

    In my home, the son from Chenjun, we planted bamboo together in the garden without an agreement, and the clear bamboo entered our dreams. We shared laughter over poetry, keeping a clear perspective on life's deeper qualities, avoiding the pursuit of fleeting trends, maintaining integrity, and enduring through difficult times, even if close to the high officials in the capital, we could still enjoy the simplicity of a recluse.

    Another poet, Li Xie, on his journey through the city, met a monk named Dechao who spoke of the famous families and ancestors Liu and Lei. Li Xie left a poem:

    Encountering the old monk in the clouds, I thought of someone who allowed me to speak of Liu and Lei. We briefly discussed recent matters concerning the descendants, and I felt a sense of melancholy, but a smile opened up. The crowd said that the bearded man should serve in the military tent [referring to Xiyan], and people pitied the short man who left the frosty platform [referring to the elder son]. The garden and city, with the incense and fire of the western hermitage, I often remember the autumn rain. Later, the elder son visited the garden and saw it, and followed the original poem with a harmonized version:

    In the spring of the imperial forest, I counted the number of returns. The sound of the cart turning into a disease, the thunderstorm turning into a green curtain, the dense mulberry leaves, and the green clouds along the road, the wheat flowers blooming. I happened to stay at a temporary inn, leaving the Xiao Temple, and asked the monk traveling to point to the wine platform [referring to Chenjun]. The white-haired monk, like a fellow villager, also knew that my ancestor had come. I showed it to the idle person, and the idle person also followed the original poem and sent it to the elder son:

    After the death of Pingshan, it made people sad. Outside the family, I am friends with Lei. When will the old heart write down a lifetime of laughter? When will the open mouth be happy? Knowing that the bond is wide, I left the earth of Chen. I often climbed up to the blowing platform, looking at the low sky where the geese returned. The west wind suddenly brought good poetry.

    The elder son followed with a harmonized version:

    Looking at each other across the clouds and mud, how can we expect to inherit the legacy of Chen and Lei? From afar, I feel sorry for the morning mirror with frost on my beard. But facing old friends, I open my eyes. Let's take advantage of the plum fragrance and get drunk in the Liang garden. Do not ask about the swallows passing by the Yan platform. The imperial forest's willows and flowers are startled by the spring evening, and the vigorous west wind rolls up the soil.

    150

    正大初先君由叶令召入翰林诸公皆集余家时春旱有雨诸公喜而共赋诗以好雨知时节当春乃发生为韵赵闲闲得发字其诗云君家南山有衣鉢丛桂馨香老蟾窟从来青紫半门生今日儿孙牀满笏迩来云卿复秀出论事观书眼如月岂惟传家秉赐彪亦复生儿勮勔勃往时曽乗御史骢未害霜蹄聊一蹶双凫古邑试牛刀百里政声传马卒今年视草直金銮云章妙手看挥发老夫当避一头地有慙老骥追霜鹘座中三馆尽英豪
    健笔纵横建安骨已知良防得四并更许深杯辞百罚我辞不饮愿助勇政要青灯照华髪但令风雨破天悭未厌归途洗靴袜先君得好字因用解嘲其诗云春寒桑未稠歳旱麦将槁此时得一雨奚翅万金寳吾宾适在席喜气溢襟抱酒行不计觞花底玉山倒从来悭混嘲盖为俗子道北海得开尊天气岂常好况当生发辰霑足恨不早东风又吹檐滴干主人不悭天自悭是日诸公极欢皆霑醉而归后月余先君以病不起赵以天悭为诗谶云

    150

    In the early years of the Zhengda era, my father was summoned from his position as magistrate in Ye to join the Hanlin Academy. At that time, all the scholars gathered at my residence. It was spring, and there was a drought, but then it rained, which pleased everyone, and they composed poems together, using the line "Good rain knows its time, it falls in spring, making all things grow" as the rhyme. Zhao Xianxian got the character "fa" and his poem went:

    "Your family in the south has a legacy of robes and bowls, with fragrant osmanthus in the old toad's cave. Throughout history, half of the officials have come from your family. Today, your descendants are full of high-ranking officials. Recently, Yunqing has again excelled. His eyes are like the moon when he discusses matters and reads books. Not only did he pass on the family's legacy, but he also had sons who were outstanding. He once rode a gray horse, a symbol of a censor, and did not harm his reputation with a single stumble. He tested his skills in an ancient town like a sharp knife, and his political achievements spread among the soldiers. This year, he served in the imperial court, and his writing skills were superb and free-flowing. I should step aside, as he surpasses me. I feel ashamed as an old horse chasing a snowy falcon. All the scholars in the three academies were outstanding. His writing is vigorous and embodies the style of the Jian'an period. He knew how to manage multiple tasks effectively and could drink deeply and accept many penalties. I refuse to drink but wish to encourage bravery. The important thing is to illuminate our gray hair with the light of learning. As long as the rain breaks the drought, I am not tired of washing my boots and socks on the way home."

    My father received a good name and used it to mock himself. His poem went:

    "The spring cold makes mulberry leaves sparse, and the drought will dry up the wheat. At this time, even a small amount of rain is worth more than a fortune. My guests were present, and joy filled their hearts. They drank without counting the cups and were so drunk that they fell like a jade mountain. People often mock me for being stingy, because I am a common person. I opened the wine jar, but the weather is not always good, especially on the day of birth. It is too late to be satisfied. The east wind blows and the eaves are dry again. The host is not stingy, but the sky is. That day, all the scholars were very happy and returned drunk. After a month, my father fell ill and passed away. Zhao used the phrase 'the sky is stingy' as a poetic prophecy."

    元裕之李长源同乡里各有诗名由其不相下颇不相咸李好愤怒元尝云长源有愤击经元好滑稽李辄以诗讥骂元亦无如之何元尝权国史院编修官时末帝召故驸马都尉布萨阿哈【案旧作仆散阿海今改】女子入宫俄以人言其罪又放出元因赋金谷怨乐府诗李见之作代金谷佳人答一篇以拒焉一时士人传以为笑谈元诗云娃儿十八娇可怜亭亭袅袅春风前天上仙人玉为骨人间画工画不出小小油壁车轧轧出东华绣带盘绫结云裾踏雁沙娇云一片不成玉被风吹去落谁家岂无年少恩泽侯锦鞯貂帽亦风流不然典取鹔鹴裘四壁相如堪白头金谷楼台杳无主燕子不飞花着雨只知环佩作离声谁解琵琶得

    Explanation

    151

    Yuan Yuzhi and Li Changyuan were fellow townspeople, each renowned for their poetry. Because they refused to yield to each other, they were not very friendly. Li was prone to anger, and Yuan once remarked that Li had a tendency to express his anger through poetry. Yuan, on the other hand, was good at humor, and Li would often mock Yuan with his own poems, but Yuan could do nothing about it. Yuan once served as an official in charge of compiling the national history. At that time, the last emperor summoned the daughter of the former Imperial Son-in-Law, Bu Sa A Ha, to enter the palace. Soon, due to public opinion, she was accused of a crime and released. Yuan then wrote a poem titled "Resentment of Jin Gu" in the style of a folk song. Li saw it and wrote a reply titled "Reply to the Beautiful Lady of Jin Gu" to counter it. At the time, scholars passed it on as a joke. Yuan's poem goes: "The eighteen-year-old girl is charming and pitiful, standing gracefully in the spring breeze. She is a celestial being made of jade, beyond the reach of earthly painters. Her small oil-lacquered carriage creaks as it leaves the East Gate, her embroidered sash and cloud-like skirt trail behind her. A piece of tender cloud, not yet formed into jade, is blown away by the wind, where will it fall? Is there no young nobleman with grace and favor, wearing a brocade saddle and a fur cap, also fashionable? Otherwise, take out a purple silk robe, four walls of Sima Xiangru can turn white-haired. The pavilions and terraces of Jin Gu are now empty, the swallows no longer fly, the flowers are rained on. Only the sound of jade pendants and the parting voice are known, who understands the lute?"

    私语有情蜂雄蛱蝶雌无情鸡欺翡翠儿劝君满饮金屈巵明日无花空折枝李诗云石家园林洛水滨粉垣碧瓦迷天津楼台参差映金谷歌舞日日娇青春是时天下甲兵息江南已传归命臣永平以来本康治四海一家无穷人洛阳城中厌酺醵司隶夜过不敢嗔王门戚里争豪侈车马如水争红尘烧金斫玉延上客季伦岂输赵王伦两家炎炎贵相轧笙竽嘈嘈妓成列瑚红树鞭击碎步障青丝马踏裂因縁睚眦贵人怒诏下黄门促收捕邮夫防吏急喧驱河南牒系御史府钟鸣漏尽行不休生存华屋归山丘緑珠香魂涴尘土侍儿忍居楼上头君王慈明宥率土妾身窜居籍民伍平生作得健儿妇狗走鸡飞岂敢恶元和其诗先子称工

    Explanation

    152

    Intimate and meaningful conversations, like the interactions between bees and butterflies, are filled with emotion. Yet, even chickens, with their seemingly innocent nature, can bully the innocent, much like the jade (翡翠). I urge you to drink from the golden cup, for tomorrow, without effort or care, even the most beautiful things will wither away. As Li Bai's poetry once described, in the gardens by the Luo River, the white walls and green tiles were a sight to behold, with towers and buildings reflecting in the golden glow of the sun. Youth was full of joy and vitality, a time when the world was at peace, and the Eastern Han dynasty under Emperor Ming (永平) was known for its prosperity and unity. The capital city was filled with festivities and gatherings, and even officials were cautious and respectful at night. The wealthy and powerful competed in extravagance, their carriages and horses flowing like water, bustling through the dust of the city. Lavish hospitality was extended, with gold and jade burned and cut to welcome guests. Two historical figures, possibly comparing their wealth and power, vied for status, their families competing for influence. Music and entertainment filled the air, with performers arranged in rows, and a red coral tree shattered by a whip, its blue silk screen torn by horses. Even small grudges could lead to the anger of the powerful, and an imperial decree was issued to capture someone, with messengers and guards rushing to carry out the order. A document was sent to the Imperial Censorate in Henan, and the passage of time continued, with the clock striking and the water clock running out, yet the action persisted. Life, though lived in grand houses, ultimately returns to the earth, and the soul of Green Pearl (綠珠) was said to have been stained by the dust of the earth. A servant girl endured life on a high floor of a building, while the emperor's mercy extended to all the land. A woman, exiled and living among ordinary people, had once been a strong and capable wife, and even small animals were afraid of the powerful. The poet Yuan and his father, both skilled in poetry, were celebrated for their work.

    麻徴君知几在南州见时事扰攘其催科督赋如毛百姓不安尝题雨中行人扇图诗云幸自山东无赋税何须雨里太仓皇寻思此个人间世画出人来也着忙虽一时戏语也有味知几若见今日事又作何语耶又戏题太公钓鱼图云向使文王不猎贤一竿潦倒渭河边当时早随时世直吃羊羔八十年亦中时病也又有道人云太公寿命八十余文王一见便同车而今若有蟠溪客也被官中要纳鱼虽俚语可以想见时世也王翰林从之尝论黄鲁直诗穿凿太好异云能令汉家重九鼎桐江波上一丝风若道汉家一百年自严陵钓

    Explanation

    153

    Ma Zhiji, the Master of the Southern Region, observed the turmoil of the times and the oppressive nature of tax collection, which was as fine as hair, causing the people to be uneasy. He once inscribed a poem on a fan depicting travelers in the rain, saying, "Fortunately, there are no taxes in Shandong, so why should we be in a hurry in the rain? Thinking about this person in the world, it seems they are in a hurry to paint out a person," suggesting a metaphorical or allegorical interpretation. Though it was a playful remark, it had a certain depth. If Ma Zhiji were to see the current situation, what would he say? He also playfully inscribed a poem on a painting of Jiang Ziya fishing, saying, "If King Wen had not sought out talented individuals, Jiang Ziya would have been fishing alone by the Wei River. If he had adapted to the times, he might have had a life of ease for eighty years, but even that would have had its problems." There was also a hermit who said, "Jiang Ziya lived for more than eighty years, and King Wen saw him and traveled with him in the same carriage. If Jiang Ziya were still alive today, he would also have to pay taxes." Though this is a crude saying, it can give us a glimpse of the current times. Wang Hanlin followed this and once commented on Huang Tingjian's poetry, saying it could make the Han dynasty's power seem insignificant, like a light breeze on the Tongjiang River. If the Han dynasty had lasted for a hundred years, it might have been a different story, but in the end, it was still a case of Zhang Liang fishing.

    竿上来且道得【阙】　　　　又咏猩猩毛笔云平生几裲屐身后五车书此两事如何合得且一猩猩毛笔安能写五车书耶余尝以语雷丈希顔曰不然一猩猩之毛如何只作笔一管后以语先子大笑云
    　　金朝律赋之弊不可言大定间诸公所作气质浑厚学问深博犹可观其后张亟音行简知贡举惟以格律痛绳之洗垢求瘢苛甚其一时士子趋学模题画影至不成语言以是有甘【阙】泉水之【阙】文风寖衰故士林相传【阙二字】题小赋必曰国欲图治君当灼知隔句贴多用可得而知四字故文人见一举子必指曰入一可得而知者有人云闻一老师令席生作汉髙祖斩白蛇赋席生小赋破题云蛇不难斩君当灼知师改曰不然不国欲图治君当斩蛇又令作鸿雁来宾赋曰秋既云至雁当灼知此可以轩渠也

    154

    From personal experience, I can say that [the missing text]

    Additionally, there is a poem about a macaque's hair brush, which goes: "Throughout my life, I have worn few garments, yet my legacy is as vast as five carts of books. How can these two things be reconciled? How can a macaque's hair brush write such an extensive body of work?" I once shared this with Mr. Lei Xiyan, saying, "It is not so. How can the hair of a macaque be used to make only one brush?" Later, I told my father, who laughed and said, "That's true."

    The flaws in the Jin Dynasty's rules for composing regulated verse are numerous and cannot be fully described. During the Dading era, the works of the scholars were characterized by a robust and profound style, which was still admirable. However, after that, Zhang Qiji, the examiner for the imperial examinations, focused solely on strict adherence to form and structure, nitpicking with excessive rigor. As a result, scholars began to imitate and follow the patterns of the questions so closely that their writing became incoherent. Thus, there arose a preference for simple and pure writing, akin to sweet water, and the literary style gradually declined. Therefore, it is said among scholars that when composing short regulated verses, one must use the phrase "The state desires to govern well, and the ruler should be fully aware," and that the phrase "can be known" is often repeated. Consequently, when literati see a scholar, they often point and say, "He has entered the realm of 'can be known.'" Someone once heard a teacher instruct a student named Xi to compose an essay on Emperor Gaozu of Han beheading the White Snake. Xi began his essay with the line, "The snake is not difficult to behead; the ruler should be fully aware." The teacher corrected him, saying, "No, it should be: The state desires to govern well; the ruler should behead the snake." The teacher then asked Xi to compose an essay on "The Wild Geese Arrive as Guests," to which Xi replied, "Autumn has arrived, and the geese should be fully aware." This can be laughed at.

    许州有蘓嗣之者云东坡后裔盖子由久居颍川有族不南渡者也其人颇蠢騃富于财以赀入官交结权要短衣女直中士大夫多以为笑以其肥硕也呼为蘓胖余尝与雷希顔谈及之雷曰颇闻夜僵水牛之説乎余对不知也雷曰昔东坡生一夕眉山草木尽死今蘓胖生一夕郑村水牛尽死也此可大笑
    　　赵翰林周臣为学士杨之美为礼部尚书二公相得甚欢盖杨虽视赵进稍后且齿少赵以其学问政事过人雅重之而杨事赵亦谨正大初朝廷以夏国为北兵所废将立新主【案续通鉴宋理宗寳庆二年古主入夏城邑多降秋七月夏主徳旺忧悸而卒国人立其弟子晛是为金哀宗正大三年元太祖二十一年改元史太祖本纪二十一年十一月以后始破灵州等处至二十二年春始进攻夏王城六月晛始降则二十一年七月晛立之前仅失城邑数处又

    In Xuzhou, there is a man named Su Sizhi, who is said to be a descendant of Su Dongpo. It is said that Ziyu (Su Dongpo's brother) lived long in Yingchuan, and there were family members who did not move south. This person is somewhat dull and foolish, rich in wealth, and became an official through wealth. He befriended influential people and wore short clothing, typical of the Jurchen people. Scholars and officials often laughed at him because he was fat and bulky, and they called him Su Pangan.

    I once talked about him with Lei Xiyuan. Lei said, "Have you heard of the story of the night-stiffened water buffalo?" I replied, "I don't know." Lei said, "When Su Dongpo was born, one night all the grass and trees in Meishan died. Now when Su Pangan is born, one night all the water buffaloes in Zheng Village die." This is very funny.

    Zhang Zhongjing, the Hanlin Academy scholar, served as a scholar in the Imperial College, while Yang Mei served as the Minister of Rites. The two men got along very well. Although Yang Mei had joined the government slightly later and was younger than Zhang, Zhang held him in high regard due to his superior knowledge and administrative skills. Yang, in turn, treated Zhang with great respect. During the early years of the Zhengda era, the court decided to replace the ruler of the Western Xia Kingdom, who had been overthrown by the northern army, with a new leader. [According to the Continued History of the Song Dynasty, in the second year of Baoding (1226), the ancient ruler entered the Western Xia, and many cities and towns surrendered. In July, the Western Xia ruler, Dewang, died of fear. The people then installed his son, Xian, as the new ruler, who became known as Emperor Ai of Jin. In the third year of Zhengda, during the twenty-first year of the reign of Genghis Khan, the calendar was changed. According to the Annals of Genghis Khan, in the twenty-first year, in November, the armies began to attack Lingzhou and other places. By the spring of the twenty-second year, they started to besiege the capital of the Western Xia. In June, Xian finally surrendered. Therefore, before July of the twenty-first year, Xian had only lost a few cities and towns.]

    攷元圣武亲征録丙戌春至夏一歳间尽克其城丁亥灭其国丙戌实为正大三年丁亥为正大四年晛立在正大三年秋七月则城未尝尽克而国未尝废可知且夏因徳旺卒而更立新主非因国废而更立新主也此志云夏国为北兵所废将立新主与诸书有异又金史西夏云徳旺死嗣立者史失其名攷宋史夏国传德旺殂清平郡王之子南平郡王晛立元史太祖本纪亦云夏主李晛降而金史谓失其名盖皆由所传闻者未备】以赵公年德俱髙且中朝名士
    遂命入使册之既行馆阁诸公以为赵公此行必厚获盖赵素清贫也至界上朝议罢其事飞驿卒遣追囘当驿卒之行也杨公在礼部召至授以一卷书封印甚谨谕以直至学士面前开拆卒既至赵所先授以省符次白有礼部实封赵公疑讶不知为何事终之乃杨公诗一首也其诗云中朝人物翰林才金节煌煌使夏台马上逢人唾珠玉笔头到处洒琼瑰三封书贷州命半夜雷轰荐福碑自古书生多薄命满头风雪却回来赵公抚掌大笑后朝野喧传以为谈笑

    Explanation

    156

    Examining the Yuan Saint's Martial Campaign Record, it is noted that from spring to summer of the Bing Xu year, all the cities were captured, and in the Ding Hai year, the kingdom was destroyed. The Bing Xu year corresponds to the third year of the Zhengda era, and the Ding Hai year corresponds to the fourth year. Xian was established as the new ruler in the seventh month of autumn in the third year of the Zhengda era. However, the cities were not fully captured, and the kingdom was not completely destroyed. The Western Xia kingdom was overthrown by northern forces, and a new ruler was to be established, as recorded in the Jin Dynasty's history. However, the Jin Dynasty's records did not name the successor to Dewang. The Song Dynasty's history records that after Dewang's death, his son, the Prince of Nanping, Xian, became the ruler. The Yuan Dynasty's history also records that the Western Xia ruler, Li Xian, surrendered, but the Jin Dynasty's records did not name him. This discrepancy is likely due to incomplete historical accounts.

    Given Zhao Gong's advanced age and his status as a renowned scholar of the central court, he was appointed to lead the mission to confer the title of ruler. Upon his departure, the scholars of the imperial academy believed that Zhao Gong would gain much from this mission, as he was known for his frugality. However, the mission was halted at the border, and Zhao Gong was recalled by a fast messenger. When the messenger arrived, Yang Gong, from the Ministry of Rites, summoned Zhao Gong and gave him a sealed scroll, instructing him to open it only before a scholar. Upon arriving at Zhao Gong's residence, the messenger first presented the imperial seal and then revealed that the scroll was from the Ministry of Rites, sealed and unopened. Zhao Gong was puzzled and unsure of its contents. Finally, it was revealed that the scroll contained a poem by Yang Gong, praising Zhao Gong's talents and the hardships of being a scholar. The poem reads:

    "Scholars of the central court, men of the Hanlin Academy,
    Your golden credentials shine brightly as you serve in the Western Xia.
    On horseback, you meet people who offer you pearls and jade,
    Your brush strokes scatter like jade flowers wherever you go.
    Three letters were sent to Yangzhou, and in the dead of night,
    The Thundering Stele was erected with a thunderous sound.
    Since ancient times, scholars have often had thin fortunes,
    Yet you return with a head full of wind and snow, laughing."

    Zhao Gong clapped his hands in delight, and the poem later became widely known and discussed in the court and among the common people, becoming a topic of amusement.

    张特立字文举东明人少擢第有能声调莱州节度判官不赴居杞之圉城躬耕田野以经学自乐正大初侯左丞挚荐诸朝起为洛阳令称治召拜监察御史奉法无所私因劾省掾髙桢辈受请托饮娼家坐不实得罪【案金史张特立传躬耕杞之韦城正大初左丞侯挚参政师安石荐其才与此志所云居杞之圉城及专言侯挚之荐有异又本传既为御史拜章言□厉二宅不当久加禁锢又劾尚书右丞延扎舒噜与
    小民争田参知政事图克坦乌登谄事近习故当路者忌其直隂挤之此志亦缺载】盖初劾时尝以草示应奉王鹗伯翼共议之王乃其门生也事既行髙桢辈讼之谓当时同席并有省掾王宾德卿张以其进士也故不劾于是朝省疑其私并治文举德卿文举左迁邳州军事判官杖五十宾亦勒停士论皆惜文举之去宾因作诗有云王鹗既曽经手改髙桢自是着心攀就中最苦张文举收拾闲云返故山时人传以为笑

    Explanation

    157

    Zhang Te, also known as Wenju, was from Dongming. In his youth, he was selected for a high-ranking position and had a reputation for his talent. He was appointed as the assistant to the military governor of Laizhou but declined the position. Instead, he settled in Yucheng, Qi, where he worked the land himself and found joy in the study of Confucian classics. In the early years of the Zhengda era, Left Censor Hou Zhi recommended him to the court, and he was appointed as the magistrate of Luoyang, where he was praised for his good governance. He was later summoned and appointed as an Inspector of Censorship, upholding the law impartially. He accused officials like Gao Zhen for accepting bribes and drinking at brothels, but he was punished for false accusations. At the time of his initial impeachment, he had shown his draft to Wang E, a literary official, for discussion. Wang E was his student. After the accusations were made, Gao Zhen and others filed a complaint, claiming that there were other officials present at the time, including Wang Bin, who was not accused because he was a scholar. As a result, the court suspected Zhang Te of favoritism and punished him along with Wang Bin. Zhang Te was demoted to the position of military judge in Pizhou and was flogged fifty times, while Wang Bin was dismissed from office. Scholars all lamented Zhang Te's departure. Wang Bin later wrote a poem, saying, "Wang E had already revised it, and Gao Zhen was determined to pursue this matter. Among them, the most pitiable was Zhang Wenju, who retreated to a simple, reclusive life. People passed it on and laughed about it."

    髙丞相岩夫自南渡执政在中书十余年无正言直谏闻于外清论鄙之公性勤慎密以此为人主见知每朝入待漏院必先百官至有人云丞相方秉烛坐院中忽一朝士立于前公不识之问曰卿为谁其人曰吾欧阳修也尔为谁公曰吾丞相也卿岂不识耶其人曰修不识丞相丞相亦不识修朝野相传以为笑又为三司使时主行钞法出支军糗颇靳惜折支他物军民号不支及薨人又云丞相死既焚犹不支也【案金史髙汝砺传不及靳惜事且云时钞法不能流转汝砺随事上言多所更定民甚便之与此志回异】嗟乎士大夫得志不可不慎一有失众心其讥诮如此可畏也已

    Explanation

    158

    Translation

    Gao Yanchang, the chancellor, served in the central government for over a decade after the Southern Song relocated its capital southward following the Jin invasion. He was known for his lack of straightforward or bold advice, which led to disapproval from the clear and discerning opinions of the time. Gao Yanchang was diligent, cautious, and discreet, qualities that earned him the favor of the sovereign. He would arrive before all other officials each morning in the waiting room, often sitting there with a candle, indicating his punctuality and dedication.

    One day, a court official approached him, and Gao Yanchang did not recognize him. The official asked, "Who are you?" Gao Yanchang replied, "I am the chancellor. Do you not recognize me?" The official responded, "I do not recognize the chancellor, and the chancellor does not recognize me." The court and the common people passed this incident around and laughed about it, indicating widespread mockery.

    Gao Yanchang also served as the Three Departments Commissioner, responsible for implementing the system of paper money. He managed military supplies with strict frugality, often substituting other items for the original supplies. This led to complaints from both the army and civilians about the shortage of supplies. Even after his death, the shortage continued, suggesting a lasting impact of his policies.

    Alas, when scholars and officials achieve their ambitions, they must be cautious. If they lose the people's trust, the ridicule will be so terrifying.

    王翰林从之貎严重若不可亲然喜于狎笑酒间风味不浅崔翰林伯善性俭啬家居止蔬食为常故院中为之语曰崔伯善有肉不餐王从之无花不饮崔伯善有肉不餐却图个甚麽王从之无花不饮谁惯了你来又云崔伯善有肉不餐要餐也没王从之无花不饮不饮即休
    　　李屏山在燕都时与雷希顔张伯玉诸公宴游李嗜酒雷善饮啗因相戏言之纯爱酒如蝇希顔见肉如鹰伯玉好色如僧遂相与大笑
    　　李长源虽才髙然不通世事傲岸多怒交游多畏之李钦叔尝云长源上颇通天文下粗知地理中间全不晓人事也或者传为本谓王飞伯正大中长源过余淮阳因谈及飞伯余举钦叔言长源大笑曰此政谓我也李屏山视赵闲闲为丈人行盖屏山父与赵公同年进士也然赵以其才交之忘年屏山每见赵致礼或呼以老叔然于文字间未尝假借或因醉嫚骂虽愠亦无如之何其往刺寜边尝以诗送有云百钱一疋绡留作寒儒裩讥其多为人写字也又云一婢丑如鬼老脚不作温讥其侍妾也又送王

    Explanation

    159

    Wang Chongzhi, a Hanlin scholar, had a stern appearance that seemed unapproachable, yet he enjoyed casual laughter and found much enjoyment in drinking. Cui Bo Shan, another Hanlin scholar, was thrifty and stingy in nature, and his home life was characterized by a simple diet of vegetables. Thus, the court composed a saying about them: "Cui Bo Shan has meat but does not eat it; Wang Chongzhi drinks regardless of the presence of flowers." Another version of the saying went: "Cui Bo Shan has meat but does not eat it; why not eat it?" And yet another: "Wang Chongzhi drinks regardless of the presence of flowers; who has accustomed you to this?"

    Li Pingshan, while in Yanjing, hosted banquets with Lei Xiyang, Zhang Boyu, and other scholars. Li loved wine, and Lei was fond of drinking and eating, so they often joked about it. Chun, who loved wine as much as a fly loves its food, Lei, who saw meat as eagerly as an eagle sees its prey, and Zhang, who was as fond of beauty as a monk is—these were the subjects of their laughter.

    Li Changyuan, though highly talented, was ignorant of worldly affairs. He was arrogant and often angry, and many of his friends feared him. Li Qinshu once remarked that Li Changyuan was well-versed in astronomy, had a basic understanding of geography, but knew nothing about human affairs. Some attributed this to Wang Feibo. During the Zhengda era, when Li Changyuan visited Huaiyang, he mentioned Wang Feibo, and I quoted Li Qinshu's words. Li Changyuan laughed and said, "This is exactly what I meant."

    Li Pingshan regarded Zhao Xianxian as a senior figure, for Li Pingshan's father and Zhao Gong were the same year's jinshi (imperial examination graduates). However, Zhao valued Li's talent and treated him as an equal despite their age difference. Whenever Li Pingshan met Zhao, he showed respect, sometimes addressing him as "Old Uncle," but Zhao never let him off lightly in matters of writing, and even when drunk, he would scold Li harshly. Despite this, Li could do nothing about it. On one occasion, Li Pingshan went on a mission to Ningbian and sent a poem with the lines, "A hundred coins for a bolt of silk, left for the poor scholar's robe," criticizing Zhao for writing too much. He also wrote, "A servant as ugly as a ghost, old feet not warm," mocking Zhao's servant. He also sent a poem to Wang, but the specific content is not provided here.

    160

    从之南归有云今日始服君似君良独难惜花不惜金爱睡不爱官亦一时戏之也赵闲闲本好书以其名重也人多求之公甚以为苦尝于礼部厅壁上榜云当职系三品官为人书扇面失体请诸人知既致仕于宅门首书曰老汉不写字然燕居无客未曽不抄书相识辈强请亦不能拒夫其心所不喜者虽恳求竟不得也雷希顔得其书最多凡有求未尝拒盖公颇惮雷且雷善求其书时或邀公食复出古人墨迹使观之又出佳研精纸名墨在前或饮以一二杯待公有书兴引纸落笔俄顷数幅雷旁观辄称

    Explanation

    160

    Upon returning south, it was said: "Today I have come to appreciate that you are like a good friend, finding it hard to value flowers more than gold, preferring sleep over official duties. This was just a joke at the time." Zhao Xianxian is naturally fond of writing because of his reputation; many people seek his writing, which greatly troubles him. He once posted a notice on the wall of the Ministry of Rites, stating, "As a third-rank official, it is inappropriate for me to write on fans for others; please be informed." After retiring, he wrote on the gate of his residence, "An old man does not write," but when he is at home without guests, he has never stopped copying books. Even if acquaintances insist, he cannot refuse. If he does not like it, even earnest requests will not succeed. Lei Xiyuan has received the most of his writings; he has never refused any request because he fears Lei and Lei is good at asking for his writings. Sometimes he invites him to eat and shows him ancient calligraphy, also presenting fine stones, high-quality paper, and famous ink. Sometimes he offers one or two cups of wine, waits for him to get into the writing mood, and then he writes several sheets in a short while. Lei watches and praises.

    叹凡一防一画必曰此顔平原也此米元章也公既喜遂书不倦又雷与屏山皆不工书赵公尝笑之曰希顔堂堂如此而写如此字一日在礼部适公为王从之书末云某月日为从之天下士书髯雷在侧笑其不工也阖坐大噱又一日雷得郭恕先篆数幅甚珍之以示赵公公亦喜雷因求跋尾公跋云恕先篆不减唐人然迄宋百余年不经诸名士发雷希顔趣售之其鉴裁如此然其书不减李屏山此一夕后数日公壻张履求书余亦在坐公跋其尾云年月日微雨中为张倩书雷希顔欲以恕先篆相易雷

    Explanation

    161

    In every stroke and line, he would say it was either Yan Zhenqing or Mi Fu. Since he was pleased, he wrote without tiring. Lei Xiyang and Li Ping Shan were both not skilled in calligraphy. Zhao Gong once laughed and said, "Xiyang looks so dignified, yet writes such characters." One day at the Ministry of Rites, Zhao Gong was writing for Wang Congzhi, and at the end, he wrote, "On a certain day, I wrote for Congzhi, a scholar of the world." Lei Xiyang was beside him and laughed at his lack of skill. Everyone in the room laughed loudly. Another day, Lei Xiyang obtained several pieces of Guo Shuxian's seal script, which he treasured greatly and showed to Zhao Gong. Zhao Gong also liked them, and Lei Xiyang then asked for an inscription. Zhao Gong inscribed, "Guo Shuxian's seal script is not inferior to that of the Tang Dynasty. However, for over a hundred years since the Song Dynasty, it had not been praised by famous scholars." Lei Xiyang eagerly sold them. His judgment is like this, and his calligraphy is not inferior to Li Ping Shan's. This was a few days later. On a certain day in the rain, Zhao Gong wrote for Zhang Qian. I was also present, and Zhao Gong inscribed at the end, "On a certain day in the rain, I wrote for Zhang Qian." Lei Xiyang wanted to exchange Guo Shuxian's seal script for it.

    162

    愕然公徐曰刘京叔不可乃止因相与大笑又王武叔【文】出馆补外未赴甚贫防五月麦熟将出京求济于交友辈特索纯扇数十诣公求书公拒之武叔素嗜酒不检既出公门大叫呼公公闻而遽召为书之然每一扇头但书古诗一联有曰黄花入麦稀者有曰麦天晨气润者有曰麦陇风来饼饵香者盖嘲王求麦也然王竟以其书多所获又一日公在礼部白枢判文举诸人邀公饮丹阳观公将往先谓诸人曰吾今往但不写字耳如求字者是吾儿文举曰先生年德俱髙某等真儿行也公笑又为书之

    Explanation

    162

    The Scholar, startled, slowly said, "It cannot be done, so it was stopped," and they laughed together. Another scholar, Wang Wushu [Wen], had left the academy and was serving outside the capital but had not attended, being very poor. Anticipating the ripening of wheat in May, he was about to leave the capital and sought help from his friends, especially requesting several dozen plain fans to visit the Scholar and ask for his writing. The Scholar refused him. Wang Wushu usually loved drinking and was not self-disciplined. After leaving the Scholar's door, he shouted loudly and called out to the Scholar. The Scholar heard and immediately summoned him to write for him. However, on each fan, he only wrote a couplet from an ancient poem, such as "Yellow flowers enter the sparse wheat," "The morning air is moist in the wheat season," and "The wind from the wheat fields carries the fragrance of baked goods." This was probably mocking Wang's request for wheat. Yet, Wang ultimately gained much from his writings. Another day, the Scholar was at the Ministry of Rites and told the chief judge and others, including Wenju, that they had invited him to drink at Danyang Temple. The Scholar was going there and first told the others, "I am going now, but I will not write anything." If someone asked for writing, it was his son Wenju. The others, showing respect, said, "The master's age and virtue are both high; we are truly like children." The Scholar laughed and then wrote for them.

    李屏山平日喜佛学尝曰中国之书不及西方之书又曰学至于佛则无所学释迦赞云窃吾糟粕贷吾粃糠粉泽丘轲刻画老庄尝论以为宋伊川诸儒虽号深明性理发六经圣人心学然皆窃吾佛书者也因此大为诸儒所攻兴定间再入翰林时赵闲闲为翰长余先子为御史李钦止【献卿】钦叔【献能】刘光甫【祖谦】俱在朝每日见輙谈儒佛异同相与折难久之屏山因以禅语解中庸那着无多事只怕诸儒认识神先子和之亦书其后云谈政自伯阳孙佞佛真成次律身毕竟诸儒扳不去可怜饶舌费精神盖屏山尝言吾祖老子岂敢不学老庄吾生前一僧岂

    Explanation

    163

    Li Pingshan, who was fond of Buddhist studies, once said that Chinese books were inferior to Western books. He also said that once one reached Buddhism, there was nothing more to learn. He praised Shakyamuni Buddha, saying that he took the dregs and chaff of our teachings. He compared Confucius and Mencius to superficially embellished versions of Laozi and Zhuangzi. He argued that the Neo-Confucian scholars of the Song Dynasty, particularly those from the School of Principle, claimed to deeply understand the nature of human beings and the teachings of the Six Classics, but they secretly used Buddhist texts. As a result, they were greatly criticized by the scholars. During the year 1217, when Li Pingshan returned to the Hanlin Academy, Zhao Shizhong was the head of the academy, and my father was a censor. Li Qinzhi, Li Qinsu, and Liu Guangfu were all officials at court. Every day, they would discuss the differences and similarities between Confucianism and Buddhism, and debate with each other for a long time. Li Pingshan then used Zen language to explain the Zhongyong (Doctrine of the Mean), saying that there was little to fear from the scholars' understanding of the divine. My father agreed and wrote a response, saying that discussing the profound (玄) is best left to the descendants of Laozi, and that being a Buddhist is a secondary matter. The scholars cannot hold onto such things, and it is a waste of energy to argue about them. Li Pingshan once said that he respected Laozi and Zhuangzi and considered himself a Buddhist before anything else.

    164

    敢不学佛故先子及之屏山览之大笑且曰扳字如何下来先子曰公羊诸大夫扳隐而立之是也又屏山解道生一云一二三四五虾蟆打杖鼓大抵皆如此藤语及其属疾盖酒后伤寒至六七日发黄遍身如金迄卒色不变医所谓酒疸者交游因戏曰屏山平日喜佛今化为丈六金身矣而张介夫祭文直云公必乗云气骑日月为汗漫之游不然则西方之金仙矣赵闲闲本喜佛学然方之屏山顾畏士论又欲得扶教传古之名晚年自择其文凡主张佛老二家者皆削去号水集首以中和诚诸説冠之以拟退之原道惟杨礼部之美为序直推其继韩欧然其为二家所作文并

    Explanation

    164

    How dare I not learn Buddhism? Thus, my father and others discussed it, and Screen Mountain read it, laughing and saying, "How does the character '扳' continue?" My father replied, "According to the Gongyang Commentary, the ministers of the State of Qi held Duke Yin upright, which is the correct interpretation." Screen Mountain further explained the Daoist saying, "One, two, three, four, five," comparing it to a frog beating drums, generally indicating such meanings. Screen Mountain's commentary on Teng (藤) language, and when he fell ill, it was due to a cold after drinking alcohol, lasting six or seven days, turning his entire body yellow like gold until his death, with no change in complexion, which doctors call alcohol jaundice. His friends joked, "Screen Mountain, who usually loved Buddhism, has now transformed into a golden body of sixteen feet!" However, Zhang Jiefu's eulogy directly states, "He must ride on clouds and ride the sun and moon on a journey without a specific destination, or else he becomes a golden immortal in the West." Zhao Xianxian originally loved Buddhist studies, but compared to Screen Mountain, he feared public opinion and also wanted to gain the reputation of supporting the teaching and transmission of ancient doctrines. In his later years, he selected his own writings, removing all those that advocated Buddhism and Daoism, and titled his collection Water Collection (水集), placing Zhonghe Cheng (中和诚) and other teachings at the beginning, modeled after Han Yu's Yuan Dao (原道). Only Yang, the Minister of Rites, wrote the preface, directly praising him as a successor to Han Yu and Ouyang Xiu, but his writings advocating the two schools were still included.

    其藤诗句另作一编号闲闲外集以书与少林寺长老英粹中使刋之故二集皆行于世余尝与王从之言公既欲为纯儒又不舍二教使后人何以处之王文曰此老所谓藏头露尾身又深戒杀生中年断荤腥尝谓余曰凡人欲甘已之口舌而害生物彼性命与人何异也又曰吾先人晩年亦断荤腥临终闭目逝少顷复开目曰我见数人担肉数担过去盖吾命所得食而不食者也或者戏曰死则已矣不亦枉了此肉乎然推公之心本慈祥尝曰吾生前是一僧又曰吾生前是赵抃阅道盖阅道亦奉神也余先子自初登第识公公喜其政事既南渡喜其有直名后由公荐入翰林相

    Explanation

    165

    His poem "Teng" is separately numbered in the Xianxian Waiji (Idle Outer Collection) and was written and printed by the elder monk Ying Cui of Shaolin Temple. Thus, both collections circulated in the world. I once spoke with Wang Congzhi about this: the gentleman wanted to be a pure Confucian but did not abandon the two teachings. How should later generations deal with this? Wang replied, "This old man is known for his hidden and revealed aspects, and he also deeply forbade killing living beings. In middle age, he stopped eating meat. He once said to me, 'When people satisfy their mouths at the expense of living beings.' Isn't their life different from ours? My ancestors also stopped eating meat in their old age. At the moment of death, he closed his eyes, and shortly after, he opened them again, saying, 'I saw several people carrying several loads of meat past.' Someone jokingly said, 'If you're dead, isn't it a waste of this meat?' But considering his heart, it was fundamentally kind and compassionate. He once said, 'I was a monk in my past life,' and also said, 'I was Zhao Bian Yuedao in my past life.' Because Yuedao also worshipped the gods. My father first met him when he passed the imperial examinations. He was pleased with his governance. After the Southern Migration, he was pleased with his reputation for integrity. Later, he was recommended by him to become a Hanlin scholar and chancellor."

    得甚欢尝谓同僚曰吾将老而得此公入馆当代吾又曰其官业当为本朝第一未几先子殁公哭甚哀为文以祭为诗以挽又取诸朝士所作挽词亲书为一轴寄余余请表诸墓至于新修叶县学诗及先子惠政碑皆公笔也余兴定末因试南京初识公已而先子罢御史归淮阳余独留日从公游论诗讲道为益甚多然公以吾家父子不学佛议小不可且屡诱余余亦不能从也尝谓余曰学佛老与不学佛老不害其为君子桞子厚喜佛不害为小人贺知章好道教不害为君子元微之好道教不害为小人亦不可专以学二家者为非也余因悟公以吾父子不学二家恐其相疵病故

    Explanation

    166

    I found great joy and once told my colleagues, "When I am old, this gentleman will enter the academy and succeed me. I also said that his official career should be the best in our dynasty." Not long after, my father passed away, and this gentleman cried very mournfully. He wrote an article for the memorial service and a poem for the funeral elegy. He also collected the elegies written by court officials, wrote them personally into a scroll, and sent it to me. I asked to inscribe them on the tomb. The new poem about the school in Yexian and the stele commemorating my father’s benevolent governance were all written by this gentleman. At the end of the Xingding era, because of the examination in Nanjing, I first met this gentleman. Later, my father resigned as censor and returned to Huaiyang, and I stayed alone, spending days traveling with this gentleman, discussing poetry and philosophy, and gaining much benefit. However, this gentleman thought it was slightly inappropriate for my family not to learn Buddhism and repeatedly tried to persuade me, but I could not follow. He once said to me, "Learning Buddhism or not learning Buddhism does not harm one's status as a gentleman. Liu Zihou, who liked Buddhism, did not hinder him from being a small person. He Zhizhang, who liked Taoism, did not hinder him from being a gentleman. Yuan Weizhi, who liked Taoism, did not hinder him from being a gentleman. One cannot exclusively consider those who study these two schools as wrong." I realized that this gentleman was concerned that my father and I, not studying these two schools, might be criticized.

    有是论已而余亦归淮阳公又与余书曰慎不可轻毁佛老二教堕大地狱则无及矣闻此必大笑但足下未知大圣人作为耳余答书曰若二教岂可轻毁之自非当韩欧之任岂可横取谤议哉自非有韩欧之智岂可漫浪为哉君子者但知其反身则以诚处事则以义若所谓地狱则不知也然公终于余有所恨舒穆噜嵩企隆亦从公游学佛公甚爱之尝于慧林院谒长老公亲教企隆持香炉三棹脚作礼同语【阙】戸部斗南曰此老不亦壊了人家子弟耶士林传以为笑公既致仕苦人求书大书榜于门有一僧求公作化疏以钉钉其手于公门公闻遽出礼之为作疏且为书也

    Explanation

    167

    After having this discussion, I also returned to Huaiyang. The public then wrote to me, saying: "One must be cautious not to casually criticize the teachings of Buddhism and Daoism, for once fallen into the great hell, it is beyond remedy." Upon hearing this, one would certainly laugh, but you do not know what great sages have done. I replied in a letter: "If these two religions are to be criticized, how can one do so lightly? Unless one is in the position of Han Yu and Ouyang Xiu, how can one rashly invite criticism? Unless one possesses the wisdom of Han Yu and Ouyang Xiu, how can one act recklessly? A gentleman should only know to reflect on himself with sincerity and handle affairs with righteousness. If one refers to hell, then it is unknown. Although the public has some grievances, I still have some regrets. Shumu Lu Song Qilong also studied Buddhism under the public, and the public greatly loved him. He once visited Huilin Temple and personally taught Qilong to hold a three-legged incense burner and perform a ritual. The Ministry of Revenue, Dou Nan, said, 'This old man has not ruined the family's children?' The scholars spread this as a joke. After the public retired, people sought his calligraphy, and he wrote large signs to hang on the door. A monk asked the public to write a donation appeal and nailed it to the public's door. Upon hearing this, the public immediately went out, treated the monk respectfully, and wrote the appeal and the calligraphy.

    归潜志卷九
    <子部,小说家类,杂事之属,归潜志>
    　　钦定四库全书
    　　归潜志卷十
    　　元　刘祁　撰
    　　李屏山晩年多疑畏见后进中异常者必摩抚之雷公希顔本其门下士后见其锋铓气势恐其害已甚惮之常为檄以疏其过恶已而焚之李公钦止刘公光甫皆推挹屏山然屏山以为李有钩距刘谈论锋出皆惮之尝谓余曰若钦止之目希顔之髯光甫之牙皆可畏余每与先子言以为笑
    　　正大间雷希顔李钦叔俱在翰林王鹗伯翼以新进状元亦入院为应奉然其趋向各不同故当时馆中有云凡在院诸公有侯门戚里者有秦楼谢馆者有田夫野老者侯门戚里者谓雷交权要也秦楼谢馆者谓李狎歌酒也田夫野老者谓王为其乡人通请托也

    Records of Seclusion and Reflection, Volume Nine
    <Subclass: Fiction, Miscellaneous, Records of Seclusion and Reflection>
    Imperially Approved Complete Library of Four Treasuries

    Records of Seclusion and Reflection, Volume Ten
    Compiled by Liu Qi of the Yuan dynasty

    In his later years, Li Pingshan was often suspicious and fearful, especially when he encountered young people who displayed unusual qualities. He would often try to console and comfort them. Lei Gong Xiyan, once a student under him, later showed a sharp and imposing demeanor, which Li feared would harm him. He became very wary of Lei and often wrote a public denunciation to expose his faults, but then burned it. Both Li Qinzi and Liu Guangfu were held in high regard by others, but Li Pingshan believed that Li Qinzi had a cunning method and Liu Guangfu was sharp in conversation, and both were feared. He once told me, "The eyes of Li Qinzi, the beard of Lei Xiyan, and the teeth of Liu Guangfu are all to be feared." Whenever I spoke about this to my father, we would laugh together.

    During the Zhengda period, Lei Xiyan and Li Qinzi were both in the imperial academy. Wang E Boyi, a new状元 (zhuangyuan) or top imperial examination candidate, also entered the academy as an应奉 (should be translated as "attendant"). However, their inclinations were quite different. At the time, there was a saying in the academy: "Among all the officials in the academy, some were from noble families and relatives, some lived in palaces and mansions, and some were farmers and old villagers." The phrase "noble families and relatives" referred to Lei, who was close to powerful figures. "Palaces and mansions" referred to Li, who lived a luxurious and extravagant life. "Farmers and old villagers" referred to Wang, who was a local person and accepted favors and requests.

    169

    泰和大安以来科举之文敝盖有司惟守格法无育材心故所取之文皆猥弱陈腐茍合度程而已其逸才宏气喜为竒异语者徃徃遭绌落文风益衰及宣宗南渡贞祐初诏免府试而赵闲闲为省试有司得李钦叔赋大爱之盖其文虽格律稍疎然词藻庄严絶俗因擢为第一又擢麻知几为防论魁于是举子辈哗然愬于台省投状陈告赵公坏了文格又作诗讥之台官时道贞奏其事将覆攷久之方息俄钦叔中宏词科遂入翰林众始厌服正大
    中钦叔复为省试有司得史学优赋大爱之亦擢为第一于是举子辈复大噪盖史之赋比李尤疎第以学问词气见其为大手笔文赋中多用禽兽对属众言何攷官取此赋为魁盖其中口味多也又曰可号学优为百兽家俄学优对廷策中之议者亦息嗟乎士皆安卑习陋久矣一旦见其有轩昻峭异者其怪骇宜哉夫科举本以取天下英才格律其大约也或者舍彼取此使士有遗逸之嗟而赵李二公不循众好独所取得人彼议者纷纷何足较也

    Explanation

    169

    Since the late Jin dynasty, the imperial examination system has been in a state of decline. The officials have only adhered to the rules without a genuine heart for nurturing talent. As a result, the essays selected are vulgar, weak, and stale, merely conforming to the standards. Those with extraordinary talent and grand spirit, who enjoy using strange and unusual language, often suffer from being rejected, causing the literary style to further decline. During the Southern Migration of the Jin dynasty, in the early years of Emperor Xuanzong's reign, an edict was issued to exempt candidates from the prefectural examination. Zhao Xianxian, the provincial examiner, greatly loved Li Qinshu's essay, which, though slightly lacking in strict form, had dignified and extraordinary language. He was promoted to the top rank, and Ma Zhiji was also promoted to the top essay in the provincial examination. Consequently, the candidates raised a commotion, submitting petitions to the central government offices to complain that Zhao had ruined the literary style and wrote poems to mock him. The censor Shi Daogeng reported the matter, and after a re-examination, the controversy eventually subsided. Soon, Li Qinshu passed the advanced literary examination and entered the Hanlin Academy, and the public finally became satisfied and convinced.

    In the early years of Emperor Xuanzong's reign, Zhao Xianxian again served as the provincial examiner and greatly loved Shi Xueyou's essay, which was even more lacking in strict form than Li's. However, the depth of knowledge and style showed it to be a masterpiece. The essay frequently used animal imagery, and someone remarked that he could be called the best among all scholars. Soon, Shi Xueyou passed the imperial examination, and the critics also ceased. Alas, scholars are all content with mediocrity and accustomed to vulgarity. Once they see someone with an elevated and unique style, it is natural to be surprised. The imperial examination system is originally designed to select talented individuals from all over the country, with the rules serving as approximate guidelines. Some people abandon the rules and take this approach, making scholars lament the loss of talent. However, Zhang and Li did not follow the crowd but chose people based on their own judgment. All these criticisms are not worth considering.

    170

    金朝钱币旧止用铜钱正隆大定泰和间始铸新钱余皆宋旧钱及髙岩夫为三司副使倡行钞法初甚贵重过于钱以其便于持行也尔后兵兴官出甚众民间始轻之法益衰南渡之初至有交钞一十贯不抵钱十文用者富商大贾多因钞法用穷俗谓坐化官知其然为更造号曰寳劵新劵初出人亦贵之也已而复如交钞官又为更造号曰通货又改曰通寳又改曰通货【案金史食货志贞祐三年七月改交钞名贞祐寳劵兴定元年行贞祐通寳元光元年行
    兴定寳泉元光二年又以绫印制元光珍货天兴二年印天兴寳防于蔡州续文献通考与食货志同此更造号曰通货又改通寳曰通货均不见于食货志刘祁金人所传必不妄可补食货志之遗】曰寳泉珍寳珍防最后以绫织印造号珍货抵银一起一衰迄国亡而钱不复出矣予在淮阳时尝闻宋人喜收旧钱商贾徃徃以舟载下江淮贸易于是钱多入宋矣嗟夫钱为至寳自古流下今日弃置与瓦砾等而以诸帛相诳欺无怪乎天下之逺【案此下有阙文】

    Explanation

    170

    The Currency of the Jin Dynasty

    In the past, the Jin Dynasty exclusively used copper coins. During the reigns of Zhenglong, Dading, and Tahe, new coins were minted, while the rest were old Song Dynasty coins. Gao Yanfu, serving as the Deputy Director of the Three Departments, advocated for the introduction of paper money. Initially, this paper currency was highly valued, even more so than copper coins, due to its convenience in circulation. However, after the outbreak of war, the government issued a large number of paper money, leading the people to begin undervaluing it. The law governing its use gradually declined. In the early stages of the southern migration, there were cases where one ten-guan note of paper money was not worth ten copper coins. Wealthy merchants and traders often became impoverished due to the paper currency system, a phenomenon known as "sitting officials." Recognizing this, the government revised and renamed the currency, calling it "baojuan." When this new currency was first issued, it was also highly valued, but soon it faced the same fate as the previous paper money. The government then revised and renamed it again, calling it "tonghuo," which was later changed to "tongbao" and then back to "tonghuo" [According to the History of the Jin Dynasty: Annals of Finance and Trade, in July of the third year of Zhengyue, the name of the paper money was changed to "Zhengyue Baojuan." In the first year of Xingding, "Zhengyue Tongbao" was introduced. In the first year of Yuan Guang, "Xingding Baquan" was introduced. In the second year of Yuan Guang, "Yuan Guang Zhenhuo" was printed using fine fabric. In the second year of Tianxing, "Tianxing Baofang" was printed in Cai Zhou. The Continued Comprehensive Records of Literature and History and the Annals of Finance and Trade are consistent in this regard. The revision and renaming of the currency as "tonghuo" and the change of "tongbao" to "tonghuo" are not mentioned in the Annals of Finance and Trade. Liu Qi, a Jin Dynasty historian, must have had reliable information, which can supplement the Annals of Finance and Trade.]. It was finally called "baquan," "zhenbao," and "zhenfang," with the last form being printed on fine fabric and named "zhenhuo," equivalent to silver. Thus, the currency went through cycles of prosperity and decline until the dynasty's fall, after which copper coins were no longer issued. When I was in Huaiyang, I heard that the Song people favored collecting old coins, and merchants often transported them down the Yangtze and Huai rivers for trade, resulting in many coins entering the Song Dynasty. Alas, money is a precious treasure that has flowed down through the ages, but today it is discarded like broken pottery, while various fabrics are used to deceive. It is no wonder that such practices have spread far and wide [Note: There is a missing text here].
