    兴定末予在南京防屏山至钧台日游每从之多问以金朝旧事屏山备为予谈之其谈田瑴侍郎党事云熙宗时韩丞相企先辅政好奬进人材田瑴辈风采诚一时人士魁名士皆显达焉凡宴防谈集间羣以分别流品升沈人物为事时蔡丞相松年曹尚书望之许宣徽霖居下位欲附其中而瑴辈不许曰松年失节望之俗吏霖小人皆屏而不用三人者大恨之时太师辽王以皇叔当国三人者游其门甚言瑴等专进退人材用则将不利朝廷辽王信之将有以发怒防韩丞相病革辽王焉适瑴在内闻之趋避门后丞相属王

    Explanation

    171

    At the end of the Xingding era, I was in Nanjing, where I often visited Fang Bingshan and went to Jun Tai daily. I frequently asked him about the old affairs of the Jin Dynasty, and he prepared to talk about them with me. He spoke about the political faction of Tian Jue, a high-ranking official, during the reign of Emperor Xizong. At that time, Han Qianxian, the chancellor, was in power and favored rewarding and promoting talent. Tian Jue and his followers were truly admirable, and they all became prominent figures of their time. In all feasts, defenses, talks, and gatherings, they often discussed the ranking and status of people. Cai Songnian, the chancellor, and Cao Wangzhi, the minister, were in lower positions and wanted to join them, but Tian Jue and his followers did not allow it. They said that Songnian had lost his integrity, Wangzhi was a vulgar official, and Lin was a lowly person, and they were all rejected and not used. The three of them were greatly resentful. The Taishi (Grand Tutor) of the Liao State, being the emperor's uncle, held power, and they frequently visited his court and said that Tian Jue and his followers were too powerful in promoting and dismissing officials, which would be detrimental to the court. The Taishi believed them and was about to take action in anger. Just as Han Qianxian, the chancellor, was seriously ill, the Taishi waited for him. Just then, Tian Jue was inside and heard about it, so he hurriedly hid behind the door. The chancellor entrusted the matter to the Taishi.

    以后事曰田瑴可代吾辽王忿然曰是子当诛相公昏矣因起而出瑴闻之汗沾衣已而丞相薨瑴等失势三人者促辽王起党事奏闻熙宗曰党人何为辽王曰党人相结欲反耳上曰若尔当诛之于是收瑴等下狱且逺捕四方党与每得一人先漆其靣赴讯使不相识榜掠万状瑴具瞻皆死狱中而松年望之霖皆进用矣【案金史田瑴传瑴由吏部侍郎出为横海军节度使时选人龚夷鉴除名値赦赴吏部铨得预覃恩部吏以白瑴乃倒用月日署之许霖在省典覃恩员外郎张子周素与瑴有怨嗾许霖发之诋以专擅朝政诏狱

    Explanation

    172

    Afterwards, it was said that Tian Jue could replace me. The Liao King angrily said, "This son should be executed; the chancellor is deluded!" He then got up and left. Tian Jue heard this and his sweat soaked his clothes. Later, the chancellor died, and Tian Jue and others lost their power. Three people urged the Liao King to report party matters, and he reported it to Emperor Xizong. The emperor asked, "What are the party members doing?" The Liao King replied, "The party members have conspired to rebel." The emperor said, "If so, they should be executed." Thus, Tian Jue and others were arrested and imprisoned, and far-reaching arrests were made of party members throughout the land. Each person caught was first painted with pitch before being interrogated to prevent recognition during beatings, and they were subjected to countless forms of torture. Tian Jue and all his followers died in prison, while Song Nian and Wang Lin were promoted.

    [According to the Jin History, Tian Jue was appointed as the military governor of the Henghai region from his position as a deputy minister of personnel. A department official reported this to Tian Jue, who reversed the date and signed it. Xu Lin, while serving in the provincial office, and Zhang Zizhou, a deputy minister, had a long-standing grudge against Tian Jue. He incited Xu Lin to expose it, accusing Tian Jue of usurping the power of the court. This led to an imperial investigation.]

    The deaths of Jū Zhī, Yù Qiáo, Xī Yì, Xíng Jùzhān, Wáng Zhí, Gāo Fèngtíng, Wáng Liáng, Zhào Yìxīng, and Gōng Yíjiàn are recorded in this text, but the details vary in their level of detail. After this, Sōng Nián, who was in a high position, went to court in the morning and saw Yù Qiáo, who summoned him for a debate. Those around him only heard Sōng Nián say, "I must go." Wàng Zhī, who was in charge of the Ministry of Personnel, also saw Yù Qiáo and was summoned for a debate. Both of them died as a result, while Lín, who was ill, died with his neck broken. The retribution of heaven is also evident, as it is similar to the fate of Tián Fén and Guàn Fū. When Yù Qiáo was in power, those who sought to advance did not fail to flatter him, but my ancestor, the Old Man of the South Mountain, did not. When he encountered misfortune, many scholars were not spared, but my ancestor remained unscathed. He is compared to Guō Línzōng and Zhang Yùshǐ Jǐngrén, who inscribed his tomb, saying that those who were skilled in flattery and sought to advance through connections never helped him, and he did not care about it. Later, they all fell due to party affiliations, but my ancestor was not involved, and those who knew him praised him highly. This is indeed a true account.

    屏山乂谈赵闲闲初上言诸公坐诗讥讽得罪事云章宗诚好文奨用士大夫晚年为人谗间颇厌怒如刘左司之昻宗御史端修先以大中时坐谤议朝政谪外官其后路侍御铎周户部昻王修撰庭筠复以赵闲闲事谪绌每曰措大辈止好议论人故泰和三年御试上自出题曰日合天统以困诸进士止取二十七人皆积渐之所致也初赵秉文由外官为王庭筠所荐入翰林既受职遽上言云愿陛下进君子退小人上召入宫使内侍问当今君子小人为谁秉文对君子故相完顔守贞小人今参政胥持国也上复使语问汝何以知此二人为君子小人秉文惶廹不能对但言臣新自外来闻朝廷士大夫议论如此时上厌守贞直言由宰相出留守东京

    Screen Mountain Correct Discussion: Zhao Xianxian Initially Spoke Out About the Officials Punished for Their Poems Criticizing the Government, Saying That Emperor Cheng of the Jin Dynasty Loved Literature and Promoted Scholars, but in His Later Years, He Was Often Slandered and Became Very Angry. For Example, Liu Zuo Si (Left Censor) and Zhang Zong (Inspector) Duanxiu Were Demoted to Local Officials During the Dazhong Period for Criticizing the Government, and Later, Lu Shiyu (Inspector) Duozhou (Ministry of Household) and Wang Xiu (Editor) Tingyun Were Again Demoted Due to the Matter of Zhao Xianxian. They Often Said That Scholars Only Like to Criticize Others. Therefore, in the Third Year of the Taihe Era, the Imperial Examination Was Held, and the Emperor Himself Set the Question "The Sun and the Heavenly Order" to Test the Candidates, and Only Twenty-Seven People Passed, Which Was the Result of Gradual Accumulation. Initially, Zhao Bingwen, Originally an External Official, Was Recommended by Wang Tingyun to Enter the Hanlin Academy. After Accepting the Position, He Immediately Spoke Out, Saying, "I Hope Your Majesty Will Promote the Virtuous and Demote the Wicked." The Emperor Summoned Him to the Palace and Asked Through the Eunuchs Who the Current Virtuous and Wicked People Are. Zhao Bingwen Answered That the Virtuous Person Is the Former Prime Minister Wanyan Shouzhen, and the Wicked Person Is the Current Minister Xushi Guo. The Emperor Then Asked Through the Eunuchs How He Knew These Two People Are Virtuous and Wicked. Zhao Bingwen Was So Frightened That He Could Not Answer, and Only Said That He Had Just Come from Outside and Heard That the Officials in the Court Were Discussing This Way. At That Time, the Emperor Was Tired of Wanyan Shouzhen's Frank Words and Ordered Him to Leave the Capital and Stay in Dongjing as a Governor.

    向持国谄谀骤为执政闻之大怒因穷治其事收王庭筠等俱下吏【案金史赵秉文王庭筠传但详秉文庭筠下狱贬削事而未着胥持国之穷治胥持国本传则以罢黜完顔守贞等事一语槩之此志所云足补其缺略】且搜索所作讥讽文字复无所得独省掾周昂送路铎外补诗【案金史周昂传以诗涉谤讪坐停铨在拜监察御史后与此云省掾异当是为省掾时作诗及为御史乃追论其事】有云龙移防鳝舞日落鸱枭啸未须发三叹但可付一笑颇涉讥讽奏闻上怒曰此政谓世宗升遐而朕嗣位也大臣皆惧罪在不可测参知政事孙公铎从容言于上曰古之人臣亦有拟为龙为日者如孔明卧龙荀氏八龙赵衰冬日赵盾夏日宜无他于是上

    Xiang Chiguo, who flattered and rose to power as an official, heard of something and became greatly angry. He then thoroughly investigated the matter and arrested Wang Tingyun and others, sending them to the officials. He searched for any satirical writings they had produced but found nothing. Only the provincial clerk Zhou Ang's poem sending Lu Duo to an external appointment was found. The poem contained lines such as: "The dragon has moved, the eels dance; the sun sets, and the owls and screech owls cry. There is no need to sigh three times; one can just laugh it off." It was somewhat satirical. He reported it to the emperor, who became angry and said, "This was referring to the death of Emperor Shizong and my succession." All the ministers feared punishment, which was unpredictable. The Vice Premier Sun Gongduo calmly said to the emperor, "Ancient ministers also compared themselves to dragons and the sun. Like Zhuge Liang the Sleeping Dragon, the Eight Dragons of the Xun family, Zhao Cui the Winter Sun, and Zhao Dun the Summer Sun. There should be no other issue."

    胥参政持国由经童入仕得幸于章宗擢为执政一时权势赫然而张仲淹诸人游其门附以进用时号胥门十哲泰和南征宋人传檄有云经童作相监女为妃皆指以罪章宗监女者元妃李氏其家因罪没入官为奴婢属监户李氏少给事太后章宗见而悦之其即位大宠嬖专房拜为元妃势敌正后其兄锡尔【案锡尔旧作喜儿今改】少尝为盗夤缘至宣徽使弟特尔格【案特尔格旧作帖哥今改】至近侍局使【案金史李元妃传兄锡尔累官宣徽使安国军节度使弟特尔格累官近侍局使少

    Counselor-in-chief who holds the state, Xu, entered office through the path of a young scholar and gained favor with Emperor Xuanzong, who promoted him to the position of chancellor. At one time, he exerted great power, and scholars like Zhang Zhongyan were part of his circle, being promoted due to their association with him. They were collectively known as the "Xu Gate Ten Sages." During the southern campaign of Emperor Xuanzong, the Song people issued a proclamation that criticized Xu for becoming chancellor through unconventional means and his sister becoming a concubine, all of which were pointed out as guilty. The emperor's favorite concubine, who was also the sister of Xu, was known as the chief concubine Li. Her family was punished and became slaves, belonging to the palace household. Li, young and serving the empress dowager, was seen by Emperor Xuanzong and pleased him. Upon his ascension, he greatly favored her, and she dominated the palace, being made the chief concubine whose power rivaled that of the empress. Her brother, Xilai (formerly Xier, now corrected), was once a thief but rose through connections to become the envoy to the imperial court. Her younger brother, Teger (formerly Tiege, now corrected), became a high-ranking official in the imperial court.

    府监此志因当时宣徽使近侍局使视节度使少府监更优异从省文】一家权势熏天士大夫好进者徃徃趋附南京李按察炳中山李翰林着皆与妃家结为亲独李怀州晏辞不肯后章宗崩无子元妃等与宰相萨克蘓【案萨克蘓旧作撒速今改】定防立卫王王世宗子章宗叔也王既立萨克蘓欲专其功媒孽李氏罪恶以为尝为厌胜事卫王下诏赐元妃死【案金史卫绍王本纪大安元年四月杀章宗元妃李氏及承御贾氏攷李元妃传是月诏近者有防元妃李氏潜计负恩令承御贾氏诈称有身俟

    The governor's office intended to streamline the text due to the fact that the current Xuanwei Envoy and the Neishi Juzhishi were considered more distinguished than the Jiedushi and Shaofu Jianshi. One family's power was overwhelming, and scholars and officials who sought advancement often fawned upon this family. Li Ancha of Nanjing and Li Hanlin of Zhongshan both married into the Empress Dowager's family, while only Li Huizhou (晏辞) refused. After Emperor Zhangzong died without an heir, the Empress Dowager and the Chancellor decided to support and install Wei Wang, who was the son of Emperor Shizong and the younger brother of Emperor Zhangzong. After the king was established, the Chancellor wanted to claim all the credit and fabricated crimes against the Li family, alleging that they had practiced superstitious rituals. Wei Wang issued an edict ordering the execution of the Empress Dowager.

    179

    将临月于李家取儿以入月日不偶则规别取以为皇嗣先皇平昔或有幸御李氏嫉妬令女巫作纸木人鸳鸯符以事魇昧致絶圣嗣所为不遣大臣按问俱已款服云云不着萨克蘓媒孽罪恶之由与此志详畧互异】且废为庶人使天下止呼其小字李师儿其母王坐诛兄锡尔弟特尔格皆窜北边李氏一门灰灭矣当其盛时不减唐开元杨贵妃家然止于奢纵不能害政蠧民也世言李氏姿色不甚丽性慧頴能迎合人主意以此幸于章宗初不知书后见上好文遂能作字知文义妇人女子变化有此哉

    Explanation

    179

    During the imperial visitation period, a child was brought from the Li family to the palace to be raised as a potential heir. If the selected child was not auspicious, then another child would be chosen as the heir. The late emperor occasionally had relations with the Li family, and the Li family was jealous. They ordered a witch to make paper and wooden figures and double-headed fish symbols to cause harm and prevent the continuation of the imperial lineage. The emperor sent high-ranking officials to investigate, and they all confessed as stated. The reason for the slander and accusation of the evil deeds of Sakasu is not mentioned, and this differs from the detailed records in the annals. The person was demoted to commoner status, and the world was only allowed to call him by his nickname, Li Shier. His mother, Wang, was executed, and his brother Xiel and younger brother Telge were exiled to the northern border. The entire Li family was extinguished. At its peak, it was no less than the family of Yang Guifei during the Kaiyuan period of the Tang dynasty, but it was only about indulgence and did not harm politics or the people. It is said that the Li family was not particularly beautiful, but they were intelligent and could flatter the emperor's intentions, thus being favored by Emperor Zhangzong initially. They did not know how to read or write, but later, seeing that the emperor liked literature, they learned to write and understand the meaning of texts. How can women and girls change like this?

    张仲淹复亨少为进士同郭黼周询卢元中宏词科为文有体且长于吏事大为章宗所知登第不十年位三品擢中都路都转运使卒【案元好问同知河间府事张公着墓表张仲淹以趋附宰相起家不十年至大兴尹公薄其人众辱之明日而仲淹死则以大兴尹卒与此志以中都转运使卒冇异】时年方四十余不然大拜矣然以其附胥氏得进清论鄙之士大夫趋向不可不慎也
    　　赫舍哩执中小字呼沙呼【案呼沙呼旧作胡沙虎今改】世宗时为护卫得幸于章宗为人凶悍横为举朝所恶且莅官不法台谏屡有言上常右之每曰汝辈无他事何止言呼沙呼斯人止是跋扈耳孟参政铸时为御史中丞对曰圣世岂容有跋扈之臣上无以应然屡斥屡召恩宠不衰卫王即位北方兵起命执中为帅大败于古北口北兵由此犯燕都卫王疏其罪除名为民未几复起为四门都提控仍令参议省事执中既得兵柄遂有废立心【案大金国志赫舍哩执中起为右副元

    Explanation

    180

    Zhang Zhongyan, originally named Fu Heng, passed the imperial examination along with others (Gu Fu, Zhou Xun, and Lu Yuanzhong) in the "Hongci" category, demonstrating a distinct style in writing and being skilled in administrative affairs. He was highly favored by Emperor Zhangzong and rose to a high-ranking position within ten years of passing the examination. He was later promoted to the position of Director of Transportation for the Zhongdu Circuit and died at the age of forty or so. Had he lived longer, he might have reached a higher position. However, he rose to power by aligning himself with the Xusi family, which led to his being scorned by the scholarly elite. Scholars and officials must be cautious in their choices.

    Hesheri Zhi Zhong, also known by the nickname Husa Hu, served as a guard during the reign of Emperor Shizong and was favored by Emperor Zhangzong. He was cruel and violent, hated by the entire court, and acted unlawfully in office. The censors and remonstrators repeatedly spoke out against him, but the emperor often favored him, saying, "You have no other matters to attend to, why do you only speak of Husa Hu? This person is merely arrogant and domineering." Meng Shenzheng Zhu, a political figure, once served as a censor and remonstrator. When asked about the state of the empire, he replied, "In a holy age, how can there be a domineering minister?" The emperor had no response, but despite being repeatedly dismissed and summoned, Zhi Zhong's favor did not wane.

    When Emperor Wei ascended the throne, northern troops revolted. Zhi Zhong was appointed as commander and suffered a great defeat at the Gubeikou Pass. Northern troops subsequently attacked Yan capital (Beijing). Emperor Wei removed him from office and stripped him of his title. Not long after, he was reinstated as the director of the Four Gates and was also ordered to participate in provincial affairs. Having gained control of the military, Zhi Zhong harbored ambitions to overthrow the emperor.

    帅将武艺军三千至紫荆关开关迎敌执中至京上遣完顔纲御敌又败于易州纲奔还言执中受赂放敌入关执中惧诛遂谋反金史本传则云上使奉职即军中责执中止务驰猎不恤军事执中方饲鹞怒掷杀之与此志所云既得兵柄有废立心可互证】时驸马都尉南平衞王心腹也方用事判大兴府执中一旦勒兵言南平谋反杀之于街即诣宫斩关以入车载衞王还第自号监国元帅坐都堂百官无敢言者时完顔耀尼以参政将兵数万备北边【案耀尼旧作元奴今改金史完顔纲传

    Explanation

    181

    In a military campaign, the general led a force of three thousand troops to the Zijing Pass, opened the gates to meet the enemy. Zhi Zhong arrived in the capital, and the emperor sent Yan to defend against the enemy, but Yan was defeated again in Yizhou. Yan fled back, claiming that Zhi Zhong had accepted bribes and allowed the enemy to enter the pass. Fearing punishment, Zhi Zhong then plotted rebellion. According to the History of Jin, the emperor sent Zhi Zhong to serve his duty in the army, where he rebuked Zhi Zhong for only being concerned with hunting and neglecting military affairs. Zhi Zhong, while feeding a falcon, angrily threw it and killed it. At that time, Zhi Zhong was the trusted advisor of Prince Nanping, who was in power and governed the Grand Capital. One day, Zhi Zhong ordered the troops and claimed that Nanping was plotting rebellion, killing him in the street. He then immediately went to the palace, cut through the gates to enter, and loaded the prince onto a cart, returning him to his residence. Zhi Zhong self-proclaimed himself as the regent general, sat in the capital hall, and the officials dared not speak. At that time, Yan, as a chancellor, led tens of thousands of troops to prepare the northern border.

    谓纲之本名累官尚书左丞至宁元年行省事于缙山此作参政有异】执中惧其见讨使其家人好召之耀尼迟疑久竟赴阙执中执而诛之遂缢卫王死时丰王判彰德府即迎入立是为宣宗士论谓耀尼不入都执中必不敢弑逆政如皇甫嵩之就董卓征也庸人无识至误国家如此宣宗以执中为太师尚书令泽王进退百官自恣有震主之威宣宗拱手而已珠格髙琪者时为西南招讨使将兵执中命出都与北兵战髙琪败归见执中将诛之已而释之复命提兵以出又败髙琪惧诛号令军

    Explanation

    182

    During the reign of Emperor Ning, the person known as Gao was originally named Gao and held the position of Left Secretary of the Ministry of Works. He was appointed to act as provincial governor in Jinsan, where he was recorded as a Cishi (provincial governor), which was different from his actual title. Zhizhong, fearing that he would be pursued or punished, sent his family to invite Gao. Gao hesitated for a long time before finally going to the imperial court. Zhizhong seized him and executed him. The Marquis of Wei hanged himself at the time of his death. Feng Wang, who was the governor of Zhangde Prefecture, immediately welcomed the new emperor in and established him as Emperor Xuanzong. Scholars commented that if Gao had not entered the capital, Zhizhong would not have dared to commit regicide, just as Huangfu Song submitted to Dong Zhuo's command. Ordinary people lacking insight can mislead the country in this way. Emperor Xuanzong appointed Zhizhong as Grand Tutor and Chief Secretary. Zewang advanced and demoted officials at will, wielding authority that could shake the emperor. Emperor Xuanzong was passive and did nothing. Zhu Ge Gaoqi was at the time the commander of the southwestern region. He led troops and Zhizhong ordered him to leave the capital to fight against the northern army. Gaoqi returned defeated and was seen by Zhizhong, who was about to execute him but later released him. He was again ordered to lead troops out but suffered another defeat. Fearing execution, Gaoqi issued orders to the troops.

    士将顺众心诛执中众皆喏夕入执中第被甲胄露刃以前执中方濯足见大骇走入卧内高琪军士追杀之持其首赴宫门请罪宣宗大惧遽传诏赦之明日拜平章政事髙琪既为相复跋扈擅权南渡政事自己出宣宗甚惮之然其为人颇亷月俸计家所费外悉纳于官性忌忍多害其敌已者杀平章政事穆延尽忠杀东平帅伊喇图【案伊喇图旧作移剌都今改】其力也兴定初坐杀其夫人为家人讼言宰执将奏之法当退避髙琪忿然遽索马归宣宗即命亲兵擒下狱以大不敬论杀之

    Explanation

    183

    The officials followed public sentiment to punish Zhong. Everyone agreed. At night, they entered Zhong's residence, wearing armor and revealing their swords. Just as Zhong was washing his feet, he was greatly frightened, rushed into his inner chamber, and was chased and killed by Gao Qi's soldiers, who carried his head to the palace gate to ask for punishment. Emperor Xuanzong was greatly frightened and quickly issued an edict to pardon them. The next day, Gao Qi was appointed as the Chancellor of State Affairs. After becoming chancellor, he again became arrogant and seized power. The state affairs of the southern relocation were all decided by himself. Emperor Xuanzong was greatly intimidated by him, but he was quite frugal. The monthly salary, after deducting household expenses, was all handed over to the government. He was envious, cruel, and often harmed those who were his enemies, killing the Chancellor of State Affairs Mu Yanjinzhong and the commander of Dongping, Yilatu, by his own power. In the early years of Xingding, because he killed his wife, the family complained. The officials were about to report it to the emperor. By law, he should have stepped down. Gao Qi angrily quickly rode away. Emperor Xuanzong immediately ordered his personal guards to arrest him and put him in prison, charged with the crime of great disrespect and executed him.

    衞王初即位改元大安厯四年改元崇庆厯二年又改元至宁人谓三元大崇至矣俄有呼沙呼之变
    　　南京未破时一二年市中有一僧不知所从来持一布囊贮枣持以散市人无穷所在童儿从之又有一僧于街中拾破瓦子复用石击碎所在亦儿童聚焉人初不知何意后国亡方知散枣者使之早散击瓦者国家瓦解矣
    　　宣宗兴定六年夏彗星出西方长丈余朝廷下诏改元元光据汉武帝故事以厌之其年十一月宣宗崩【案大金国志兴定六年八月甲午彗星出氐九月壬戍彗再见金史天文志兴定六年八月己卯彗星出于亢宿右摄提周鼎之间指大角宣宗崩于元光二年十二月庚寅与大金国志二年十月及此志改元之年十一月均不合乂金史宣宗改元兴定止五年即以次年彗星出之后改元元光以元光二年崩通前贞祐四年凡十一年与大金国志所云在位一十二年不同而与此志合】已而宋帝亦崩天道竟谁应耶

    Explanation

    184

    The Wei King, upon his initial ascension to the throne, changed the era name to Da'an. Four years later, he changed it again to Chongqing, and two years after that, he changed it once more to Zhi Ning. People said that the three era names Da'an, Chongqing, and Zhi Ning were all grand and significant. Soon after, there was the uprising known as the "Husha Hu" rebellion.

    In the first or second year before the fall of Nanjing, a monk appeared in the market without anyone knowing his origin. He carried a cloth bag filled with dates and distributed them among the people. Everywhere he went, children followed him. Another monk was seen picking up broken tiles in the streets and smashing them with stones. Wherever he did this, children also gathered around him. At the time, people did not understand the meaning behind these actions. Only after the country fell did they realize that the monk who distributed dates was urging the people to disperse early, and the monk who smashed the tiles was symbolizing the disintegration of the nation.

    In the sixth year of the Xingding era of Emperor Xuanzong, a comet appeared in the west, measuring over ten feet in length. The court issued an edict to change the era name to Yuanguang, following the precedent of Emperor Wu of Han to suppress the calamity. In the eleventh month of that year, Emperor Xuanzong passed away. [According to the History of the Jin Dynasty, a comet appeared in the constellation of Di in the month of August of the sixth year of Xingding, and again in September. The Astronomical Records of the Jin Dynasty state that in the month of August of the sixth year of Xingding, a comet appeared in the constellation of Gang, near the Right Celestial Altar and the Zhou Ding, pointing towards Dajiao. Emperor Xuanzong died in the month of December of the second year of Yuanguang, which does not match the records in the History of the Jin Dynasty for the second month of the tenth year and the eleventh month of the year of the era name change. Furthermore, according to the History of the Jin Dynasty, Emperor Xuanzong changed the era name from Xingding to Yuanguang in the fifth year, and passed away in the second year of Yuanguang, which totals eleven years, including the four years of the Zhenyou era. This differs from the History of the Jin Dynasty which states he reigned for twelve years, but matches this record.] Soon after, the Song Emperor also passed away. Who will ultimately respond to the will of heaven?

    赵翰林可献之少时赴举及御试王业艰难赋程文毕于席屋上戏书小词云赵可可肚里文章可可三塲捱了两塲过只有这畨解火恰如合眼跳黄河知他是过也不过试官道王业艰难好交你知我时海陵庶人亲御文明殿望见之使左右趣录以来有旨谕攷官此人中否当奏之已而中选不然亦有异恩矣后仕世宗朝为翰林修撰因夜览太宗神射碑反覆数四明日防世宗亲飨庙立碑下召学士院官读之适可在音吐鸿畅如宿习然世宗异之数日迁待制及册章宗为皇太孙适可当笔有云念天下大器可不正

    Explanation

    185

    Zhao Hanlin Ke Xianzhi, in his early years, took the imperial exams and during the examination of the difficult imperial cause, after finishing his essay, he wrote a playful poem on the ceiling of the examination hall. The poem read: "Zhao, Zhao, the knowledge and skills in my belly, I passed two out of three trials, only this time I feel relieved, it's like leaping across the Yellow River with closed eyes, I don't know if I passed or not." The examiner said, "The imperial cause is indeed difficult, so that you know, when I was the prince of Haixing, I personally presided over the examination hall. I saw him and ordered the attendants to record his name, and issued an edict to the examiners to determine if he passed, and if he did not, he would receive special favor." Later, he served in the Shizong court as a Hanlin scholar and writer. Because he read the Shenzheshi stele of Emperor Taizong repeatedly at night, the next day, when Shizong personally attended the temple ceremony and stood under the stele, he summoned the scholars to read it, and Zhao read it fluently and smoothly, as if he had practiced it before. Shizong was impressed and promoted him to a higher position, and when he was appointed as the crown prince, Zhao was responsible for writing the decree, which read, "The great vessel of the world must be upright."

    其本欤而世嫡皇孙所谓无以易者人皆称之后章宗即位偶问向者册文谁为之左右以可对即擢直学士嗟乎献之三以文字遇知人主异哉献之少轻俊文章健捷尤工乐章有玉峯闲情集行于世晚年奉使髙丽髙丽故事上国使来馆中有侍妓献之作望海潮以赠为世所传其词云云垂余髪雾拖广袂人间自有飞琼三馆俊游百街髙选翩翩老阮才名银汉防双星尚相看脉脉似隔盈盈醉玉添春梦云同夜惜卿卿离觞草草同倾记灵犀旧曲晓枕余酲海外九州邮亭一别此生未卜他生江上数峯青怅断云残雨不

    Explanation

    186

    Is it not the case that the world's rightful heir, the imperial prince, is irreplaceable? People all praised him after. When Emperor Zhangzong ascended the throne, he happened to ask who wrote the previous imperial edict. His attendants replied that it was "Ke," and immediately "Ke" was promoted to the position of Zhi Xueshi (a scholar-official). Ah, how remarkable that "Xianzhi" thrice encountered a ruler who appreciated his writings! Xianzhi was young and agile, his writings vigorous and swift, especially skilled in composing music and lyrics. He had a collection of leisurely writings titled "Yufeng Xianqing Ji" that circulated in the world. In his later years, he was sent as an envoy to Goryeo (Korea). According to Goryeo's custom, when envoys from the superior state arrived, there were courtesans in the reception hall. Xianzhi composed "Wang Haichao" (A Gaze at the Sea) to give to her, and the poem became widely circulated. The words are as follows:

    Falling hair, mist draping broad sleeves, the world has its own fairy. Three halls for the elite, a hundred streets for high selection, graceful and elegant, the old talent of Lao Ruan, the Milky Way separating twin stars, still looking at each other, seeming to be apart. Drunken jade adds to the spring dream, sharing the night to cherish each other, parting hastily, pouring out together. Remembering the old melody of Lingxi, morning pillow with lingering intoxication. A thousand miles away in the nine states, a posthouse farewell, this life not foreseen, the next life uncertain. Green peaks on the river, lamenting the broken clouds and rain, not knowing what will happen.

    见髙城二月辽阳芳草千里路傍情归而下世人以为他生未卜之防云先是蔡丞相伯坚以尝奉使髙丽为馆妓赋石州慢云云海蓬莱风雾鬟不假梳掠仙衣卷尽霓裳方见宫腰纤弱心期得处世间言语非真海犀一防通寥廓无物比情浓与无情相博离索晓来一枕余香酒病赖花医却潋灔金尊收拾新愁重酌片帆云影载将无际关山梦魂应被杨花觉梅子雨丝丝满江干楼阁二词至今人不能优劣余谓萧闲之浑厚玉峯之峭拔皆可人然蔡之仙衣卷尽霓裳方见宫腰纤弱与赵之惜卿卿皆不免为人疵议之矣

    Explanation

    187

    Seeing the high city in February, the fragrant grass of Liaoyang stretches for a thousand miles; the sentiment of the roadside leads people to descend from the world, thinking it as a precaution for an uncertain future life. Previously, Cai Chenxiang Bojian, who once served as an envoy to Goryeo, wrote a poem titled "Shizhou Man" for a courtesan in the guesthouse. The cloud sea and Penglai, the wind and mist do not need to comb and style the hair, the heavenly robe is completely rolled up, revealing the colorful garments, only then can one see the slender waist of the palace; the heart's aspirations find that worldly words are not true, a sea rhinoceros connects the vast emptiness, nothing can compare to the intensity of emotion, to contend with the无情 (unfeeling), loneliness, in the morning, a pillow full of lingering fragrance, alcohol-induced illness is cured by flowers, rippling golden cup, gather new sorrows and drink again, a small sail and cloud shadow, to carry the boundless mountains and passes, the dream soul should be awakened by willow catkins, the rain of plum blossoms, thread-like, fills the riverbank, buildings. These two poems, to this day, people cannot determine which is superior. I believe that the "Xiao Xian" is rich and profound, and the "Yu Feng" is sharp and majestic, both are commendable. However, Cai's "heavenly robe is completely rolled up, revealing the colorful garments, only then can one see the slender waist of the palace" and Zhao's "cherishing the beloved" both cannot escape criticism and debate.

    王副枢晦子明自布衣时慷慨以侠闻其友人出游久妻与一僧私既归晦以告其友无如之何晦教之复为逺出计治装即岐而他寓夕造其家僧见之趋唘轩以逃晦伏轩外以铁简迎击僧脑出而毙明日晦诣有司自陈其事有司义而释之其后守顺州竟以节死金朝名士大夫多出北方世传云中三老图魏参政子平州顺圣人【阙】参政甫应州山隂人程参政晖蔚州人三公皆执政世宗时为名臣又蘓右丞宗尹天成人吾髙祖南山翁顺圣人雷西仲父子浑源人李屏山州人髙丞相汝砺应州人其余不可胜数余在南州时尝与交游谈及此余戏曰自古名人出东西南三方今日合到北方也
    　　周戸部徳卿尝论时人之文曰正甫之文可敬从之之文可爱之纯之文可畏也正甫名珪真定人尝为省都事有能声泰和南征军书羽檄皆出其手为文条畅有法余尝至栾城县署中有一遗爱碑正甫笔也余文不多见在南京时李屏山尝云正甫文字全散失不传以是知士大夫贵有良子弟也

    Explanation

    188

    Wang Fuchu Hui Ziming, a commoner by birth, was renowned for his bold and chivalrous deeds. One day, a friend of his went on a long journey, and while he was away, his wife had an affair with a monk. Upon returning, Wang informed his friend, but there was nothing they could do about it. Wang advised his friend to plan another trip, and they prepared for travel, splitting up to stay elsewhere. That evening, Wang visited his friend's house, and the monk saw him and fled quickly to the轩 (a type of building or structure). Wang hid outside the轩 and struck the monk with an iron ruler, causing the monk's brain to spill out and die. The next day, Wang reported the incident to the authorities, who released him out of justice. Later, Wang served as the governor of Shunzhou and ultimately died for his integrity during the Jin dynasty. Many famous scholars and officials of the Jin dynasty came from the north. It is said that there is a painting of three elders from Yunzhong, including Wei Zeping, a political figure from Hongzhou, and Cheng Huī, a political figure from Weizhou. These three men all held high positions and were famous ministers during the reign of Emperor Shizong. Another notable figure was Su Zongyin, a right chancellor from Tiancheng. My ancestor, the South Mountain Man, was also a figure from Shunsheng. There were many other notable figures, too numerous to count. I once interacted with them in Nanzhou and discussed this with them. I joked that since ancient times, famous people have come from the east, west, and south, and today it should be the north.

    Zhou Deqing, a minister of the household department, once commented on contemporary writings, saying that Zheng Fu's writings are respectable, Cong Zhi's writings are lovable, and Zhi Chun's writings are fear-inspiring. Zheng Fu, whose name was Gui, was from Zhending and once served as a provincial official with a good reputation. During the Southern Campaign of Taihe, all military documents and orders came from his hand. His writings were clear and well-structured. I once visited the county office in Luancheng and saw a stele commemorating a person's good deeds, which was written by Zheng Fu. I rarely see his writings. When I was in Nanjing, Li Pingshan once told me that Zheng Fu's writings were completely lost and not passed down. This is why scholars and officials value having good children.

    189

    赵闲闲于前辈中文则推党世杰怀英蔡正甫珪诗则最称赵文孺沨尹无忌【阙】尝云王子端才固髙然太为名所使每出一联一篇必要时人皆称之故止是尖新其曰近来陡觉无诗思纵有诗成似乐天不免物议也李屏山于前辈中止推王子端庭筠尝曰东坡变而山谷山谷变而黄华人难及也或谓赵不假借子端盖与王争名而李推黄华盖将以轧赵也屏山南渡后文字多杂禅语葛藤或太鄙俚
    不文迄今刻石镂板者甚众余先子尝云之纯晚年文字半为藤古来蘓黄诸公亦语禅岂至如此可以为戒又多为浮屠作碑记传赞文徃徃诋訾吾徒诸僧翕然归向因集以板之号屏山翰墨佛事传至京师士大夫览之多愠怒有欲上章劾之者先子尝谓曰此书胡不斧其板也屏山曰是向诸僧所镂何预我耶后屏山殁将板其全集闲闲为涂剔其伤教数语然板竟不能起今为诸僧刻于木使传后世惜哉

    Explanation

    189

    Zhao Xianxian praised Du Shi Jie, Huai Ying, Cai Zhengfu, and Gui in literature, and Zhao Wenru, Feng, and Yin Wuji in poetry. He once said that Wang Ziduan's talent was indeed high, but he was too influenced by fame. Every time he wrote a couplet or a poem, he must have everyone praise it, so his works were just sharp and novel. Recently, he suddenly felt he had no poetic inspiration, and even if he wrote a poem, it was like Bai Juyi, and he could not avoid criticism. Li Pingshan only praised Wang Ziduan among the predecessors, and Du Mu once said that Su Shi changed into Huang Tingjian, and Huang Tingjian changed into Huang Ruo, making it difficult for others to catch up. Some say Zhao does not lend a hand to Wang because he competes for fame with Wang, and Li promotes Huang Ruo in order to outdo Zhao. After Li Pingshan moved south, his writings often mixed in Zen sayings and entanglements, sometimes they were too vulgar. Unrefined writings are now widely engraved on stone and wood. My father used to say that in his later years, half of his writings were entangled with Zen. Ancient poets like Su and Huang also spoke of Zen. How could it be like this, which can serve as a warning. After Li Pingshan died, his entire collection was to be engraved, and Xianxian painted over some offensive words, but the engraving could not be completed. Now it is engraved on wood by the monks to be passed down to future generations. What a pity.

    190

    屏山之殁雷希顔志其墓赵闲闲表焉余先子之殁亦雷志其墓赵闲闲表焉【案王恽秋涧集浑源刘氏世徳碑亦云赵翰林秉文勒铭神道而滏水集但有故叶令刘君遗爱碑及祭刘云卿文而无所谓墓表或滏水集有所遗欤】皆刻于石矣迨雷赵之殁既而后元之志之其外表迄今皆阙也
    　　余髙祖南山翁未第时尝梦游山寺见佛衣纹隐隐如金字然细视之乃七言诗也觉而记其四句云喜逢汉代龙兴日髙谢南山豹隐秋蟾宫好养青青桂须占鼇头稳上游已而金朝初开进士举中魁甲继以二子西岩龙泉同擢第又继以孙洺州君又继以孙中奉君朝列君曽孙翰林君奉政君凡四世八人也在南京时中奉君尝求书八桂堂于赵闲闲闲闲曰君家岂止八桂而已耶为书丛桂桂窟四字

    Explanation

    190

    Upon the death of Ping Shan, Lei Xiyan inscribed his tomb, and Zhao Xianxian wrote a memorial tablet for him. My father's death was similarly inscribed by Lei, and Zhao Xianxian wrote a tablet for him as well. [According to Wang Yun's Qiu Jian Ji, the Dynastic Virtue Stele of the Liu Family from Hunyuan also mentions that Zhao Bingwen, the Hanlin scholar, inscribed the Shen Dao (Spiritual Path), while the Fushui Collection only contains the Legacy of Benevolence Stele of Lord Liu of Ye and the Eulogy for Liu Yunqing, with no mention of a tomb tablet. Perhaps the Fushui Collection is incomplete.] All of these were engraved on stone. Until the deaths of Lei and Zhao, after their burials, Yuan Zai inscribed the outer tablets, which are now all missing.

    My great-grandfather, the Old Man of Nanshan, before passing the imperial examination, once dreamed of visiting a mountain temple and saw the Buddha's robe patterns faintly resembling golden letters. Upon closer inspection, they were a seven-character poem. Upon waking, he remembered the four lines: "Happy to meet the day when the Han dynasty rose to power, highly appreciating the autumn retreat of the mountain leopard. The moon palace is good for nurturing lush osmanthus, must occupy the top position and ascend steadily." Later, when the Jin dynasty first opened the imperial examination, he passed and ranked first. His two sons, Xiyan and Longquan, both passed the examination together. Then his grandson, the Lord of Mingzhou, followed, and his great-grandson, the Hanlin scholar, the Fengzhengjun, and the Chaoliejun, making a total of four generations and eight people. In Nanjing, the Fengzhengjun once asked Zhao Xianxian to write "Eight Osmanthus Hall." Zhao said, "Your family is not just about eight osmanthus trees." He then wrote "Crown of Osmanthus" and "Cave of Osmanthus."

    191

    屏山之殁诸公祭文挽诗数十篇雷宋倡之已而余先子殁诸公祭文挽诗才数首后赵闲闲殁惟余及宋飞卿杨焕然作祭文挽诗也

    　　归潜志卷十
    　　钦定四库全书
    　　归潜志卷十一
    　　元　刘祁　撰
    　　録大梁事
    　　金正大八年辛夘冬十一月余居淮阳北兵由襄汉东下时老祖母老母在南京趋往省焉既至京师边声益急闻北兵阻荆江与平章政事完顔哈达等谋纵北兵东渡将以劲骑蹴入江【案完顔哈达旧作完顔合打今改】北兵既渡皆殊死战哈达兵不能遏遂帅八都尉退保钧州北兵袭之不进时朝廷忧惧不知所为然天下劲兵皆为二帅所统倚以决存亡【案二帅指完顔哈达与伊喇蒲阿而言上文未着伊喇蒲阿之名疑写有脱佚】又命防知政事圗克坦乌登殿前都防检完顔重喜提兵扼潼闗【案圗克坦乌登旧作徒单合典今改】九年正月下诏求言于东华门接受陈言文字日令一侍从官居门待言者虽多未闻有施行者盖

    Explanation

    191

    After the death of Ping Shan, numerous memorial essays and poems were written by various public figures, with Cao Cao leading the effort. Later, when my father passed away, only a few memorial essays and poems were written by various public figures. After Zhao Xianxian passed away, only I and Song Feiqing and Yang Huanner wrote memorial essays and poems.

    Volume Ten of Returning to Obscurity
    The Complete Library of the Four Treasuries
    Volume Eleven of Returning to Obscurity
    Compiled by Liu Qi of the Yuan Dynasty
    Recording Events in Daliang

    In the eighth year of the Zhengda era of the Jin dynasty, during the eleventh month of the year Xinmao, I was residing in Huaiyang. Northern troops advanced from the Xiang and Han regions towards Huaiyang. At that time, my grandmother and mother were in Nanjing, and I traveled there to visit them. Upon arriving in the capital, the situation at the border became increasingly urgent. I heard that northern troops were blocked at Jingjiang, and I consulted with Wang Yanhada, the Chief Councillor of State, and others. We planned to allow the northern troops to cross eastward in order to charge into the river with elite cavalry. After the northern troops crossed, they fought to the death, but Wang Yanhada's troops were unable to stop them. He then led eight military units to retreat and defend Junzhou. The northern troops attacked but did not advance further. At that time, the court was in a state of fear and uncertainty about what to do, though the strongest troops were under the command of two generals. We relied on these troops to decide the fate of the country. Additionally, Tuqudant Wudeng, the Chief Councillor of State, and Wang Zhongxi, the Commander of the Palace Guards, were ordered to lead troops to block the Tongguan pass. In the first month of the ninth year, the emperor issued an edict at the Donghua Gate, inviting public opinion. A court official was stationed at the gate to receive written opinions. Though many opinions were submitted, none were implemented.

    192

    凡得士庶言章先令诸朝贵如御史大夫费摩阿固岱户部尚书完顔努森等【案费摩阿固岱旧作裴满阿虎带完顔努森旧作完顔奴申今改】披详可然后进多为诸人革暌百无一达者余时亦愤然上书且求见口陈防翰林修撰李大节直于门余付之且与论时事李曰今朝廷之力全在平章副枢看此一战如何余无可奈何矣时正月十七日也翌日报闻十六日钧台与北兵战酣防天大雪没膝我师皆冻不能支转战良久北兵复自孟津南渡与南来诸兵防我师遂大败伊喇蒲阿就擒【案伊喇蒲阿旧作移喇蒲瓦今改金史本传云械至官山召问降否徃复数百言但曰我金国大臣惟当金国境内死耳遂见杀视此志所云就擒加详而与大

    Explanation

    192

    All the proposals or memorials submitted by officials and commoners are first reviewed by high-ranking officials such as the Grand Censor Feimoaguadi and the Minister of Revenue Wanyanusen. After careful examination, if they are deemed acceptable, they are then submitted. However, most are rejected by various people, and out of a hundred, only one is accepted. At the time, I also angrily submitted a memorial and sought an audience with the Hanlin Academician Li Dajie, speaking directly to him at his door. I entrusted him with my concerns and discussed current affairs with him. Li said, "Now the strength of the court lies entirely in the Chancellor and Vice-Chancellor. Let's see how this battle goes." I was at a loss as to what to do about it. It was the seventeenth day of the first month. The next day, I heard that on the sixteenth, at Juntai, our troops engaged in intense battle with the northern forces. A heavy snowfall covered the knees, and our troops were frozen and could not withstand the cold. After prolonged fighting, the northern troops crossed the Yellow River from Mengjin and met the southern troops. Our troops were then decisively defeated, and Yilapa was captured. He was shackled and taken to Guanshan, where he was questioned about surrendering. He responded with hundreds of words, simply saying, "As a minister of the Jin state, I will only die within the borders of the Jin state." And he was then executed.

    193

    金国志所云出降迥异似独得其实】完顔哈达窜于地穴中为所发见杀都尉苖英髙英樊泽中郎将完顔绰华善诸骁将皆死【案完顔绰华善旧作完顔陈和尚今改】京师大震下诏罪已改元开兴为守御京城计四面置帅府置行户工部和斯济雅博斯纳帅北面【案和斯济雅旧作和速甲博斯纳旧作蒲速辇今改】李新帅东面范正之帅南面完顔实讷阿巴帅西面【案实讷阿巴旧作习你阿不今改】富察君平张俊民张师鲁舒穆噜世勣分领戸工部事【案舒穆噜世勣旧作石抹世勣今改】时平章政事兼枢密使完顔巴萨枢密院副使持嘉哈希用事【案完顔巴萨旧作完顔白撒持嘉哈希旧作赤盏合喜今改】二人奸佞无逺

    Explanation

    193

    The Jin Guo Zhi (Record of the Jin Dynasty) states that the surrender was different, as if it alone captured the truth. Wang Yan Ha Da hid in a cave and was discovered and killed. Miao Ying, Gao Ying Fanze, and Wang Yan Chuo Hua Shan, along with other brave generals, all died. The capital was greatly shaken, and an edict was issued blaming himself. The era name was changed to Kai Xing, and plans for defending the capital were made. Commanders were placed in all four directions, and the Department of Household and Engineering was established. He Si Ji Ya Bo Si Na led the northern front, Li Xin led the eastern front, Fan Zheng Zhi led the southern front, and Wang Yan Shi Nei A Ba led the western front. Fu Cha Jun Ping, Zhang Jun Min, Zhang Shi Lu, and Shu Mu Lu Shi Ji were in charge of the Department of Household and Engineering. At this time, Wang Yan Ba Sa, who held both the position of Chancellor of State Affairs and Chief of the Military Council, and Chi Jia Ha Xi, the deputy of the Military Council, were in power. The two were treacherous and deceitful without limits.

    194

    略士庶皆恶之末帝信用不能斥去识者知其误国矣俄闻陷钧州又陷许州许帅布抡死之二月陷陈州陈帅纽赫努色尔死之【案纽赫努色尔旧作粘割奴申今改】京畿诸邑所至残毁末帝在宫中时聚后妃涕泣尝自缢为宫人救免又将坠楼亦为左右救免御史大夫费摩阿固岱吏部侍郎刘仲周等诣北兵告和不从三月北兵迫南京上下震恐朝议封皇兄荆王守纯子肃国公某为曹王命尚书右丞李蹊等奉以为质子于军前擢应奉翰林文字张本为翰林院侍讲学士从以北北兵留曹王营中李蹊等回具言彼虽受之待北援京城将不免攻明日北兵树礟攻城大臣皆分主方面时京城西南隅最急完顔巴萨主之西北隅尤急持嘉哈

    Explanation

    194

    The common people and scholars alike detested him, yet the last emperor trusted him and could not dismiss him. Those with insight knew that he was harming the state. Soon after, he captured Junzhou and then Xuzhou, where the commander of Xuzhou, Bulun, died in the process. In February, he captured Chenzhou, where the commander of Chenzhou, Niuhe Nusuer, also died. The areas around the capital were devastated wherever he went. While in the palace, the last emperor gathered his consorts and wept; he once attempted suicide by hanging, but was saved by the palace women. He also tried to jump from a tower, but was again saved by those around him. The Chief Censor, Feimo Agudai, and the Minister of Personnel, Liu Zhongzhou, among others, went to the northern army to plead for peace, but they were not heeded. In March, the northern army approached Nanjing, causing great fear among the people. The court decided to enfeoff the son of Prince Jing of Jing, who was the brother of the emperor, as the Prince of Cao, and ordered the Right Chancellor of the Board of Works, Li Xi, to take the prince as a hostage to the northern army. Zhang Ben, who served as an imperial scribe, was promoted to the position of Vice President of the Hanlin Academy. The northern army kept the Prince of Cao in their camp. Li Xi and others returned and reported that although they had accepted the hostage, the northern army was still waiting for reinforcements and would soon attack the capital. The next day, the northern army set up artillery to attack the city. The ministers were divided in their duties, with the southwest corner of the city being the most urgent, defended by Wang Yanba, and the northwest corner being even more critical, defended by Chijiaha.

    195

    希主之东北隅稍缓丞相完顔萨布主之【案萨布旧作塞北今改】独东南隅未尝攻时人情汹汹皆以为旦夕不支末帝亲出宫巡四面劳军故士皆死战帝出从数骑不张盖纵路人观余时在道左欲诣陈便宜忽见一士捧章以进帝令左右受之谕曰入宫看读当候之余谓此时当马上览奏行事今云入宫又虚文也遂趋去已而其事竟无闻北兵攻城益急礟飞如雨用人浑脱或半磨或半碓莫能当城中大礮号震天雷应之北兵遇之火起亦数人灰死军士又自城根暗门突出杀伤甚众总领富察古纳髙显刘奕皆以力战有功众庶推之【案富察古纳旧作蒲察官奴今改】皆擢为帅使分守四面相接应时自朝士外城中人皆为兵号防城

    Explanation

    195

    The northeastern corner of the main position was slightly relaxed, with Chancellor Wanyan Sabu in charge. Only the southeastern corner had not been attacked; at that time, people were in a state of panic, all believing they could not hold out for a day or two. The last emperor personally left the palace to tour the four sides and encourage the troops, so the soldiers fought to the death. The emperor left with several riders without spreading the canopy, allowing passersby to watch him. At that time, I was on the side of the road, intending to present a memorial. Suddenly, I saw a scholar presenting a memorial, and the emperor ordered his attendants to receive it, instructing, "Enter the palace to read it; wait for me." I thought that at this moment, one should read the memorial and act on it immediately, but now mentioning entering the palace is just empty formalities. I then hurried away. Later, the matter was never heard of. The northern army attacked the city with increasing urgency, cannonballs flew like rain, and people used clay pots or half-mills or half-stone mortars, none of which could withstand the attack. A large cannon in the city was called Thunder Shaker, which responded to the northern army's attack, causing fires to break out, killing several people instantly. Soldiers also emerged from secret doors at the base of the city wall, causing many casualties. Generals Fucha Gunan, Gao Xian, and Liu Yi all achieved merit through their fierce fighting, and the common people recommended them. All were promoted to commanders and assigned to guard the four sides, coordinating with each other. At that time, except for the officials, all the people in the city were soldiers, known as defenders of the city.

    196

    丁壮下令有一男子家居处死太学诸生亦选为兵诸生诉于官请另作一军号太学丁壮已而朝议以书生辈尫羸不任役将发为礮夫诸生刘百熙杨焕等数十人伺上出诣马前请自効上慰谕令分付四面户部工作委差官由是免礮夫之苦平章巴萨怒诸生之自见上也趣召赴部以缓期杖户部主事田芝又分令诸生监送军士饭食视医药书礮夫姓名又令于城上放纸鸢鸢书上语招诱胁从之人使自拔以归受官赏皆不免奔走矢石间又夜举灯毬为令使军士自暗门出劫战令诸生执役灯灭者死诸生甚苦之俄以灯毬未具杖刑部郎中舒穆噜世勣以前户部侍郎李涣代之巴萨本无守御才但以严刻立威誉夏四月八日始辍攻下诏

    Explanation

    196

    During the time of military conscription, an order was issued that any adult male found at home would be executed. Students from the Imperial Academy were also selected to serve in the military. The students appealed to the authorities, requesting to form a separate unit for themselves, known as the Imperial Academy's military contingent. However, the court debated that scholars were weak and unable to bear the burden of military service, and they were about to be assigned as gunners. In response, several dozen students, including Liu Baixi and Yang Huan, waited for the emperor to appear and approached him on horseback to offer their services. The emperor comforted them and ordered the Ministry of Revenue to assign them to various tasks, thereby exempting them from the hardship of being gunners.

    Pingzhang Basa, however, was angry that the students had approached the emperor directly. He hurriedly summoned them to the Ministry and delayed their punishment by flogging the Ministry of Revenue's chief clerk, Tian Zhi. Furthermore, he ordered the students to supervise the feeding of soldiers, provide medical care, and record the names of the gunners. He also instructed them to fly kites with messages from the emperor to encourage those who had been coerced to surrender and return to the government for rewards. All of these duties forced the students to run in the midst of arrows and stones. At night, he lit lanterns to signal the soldiers to emerge from secret doors and launch surprise attacks. The students were forced to perform these duties, and those whose lanterns went out were executed. Soon after, because the lanterns were not ready, the Minister of Justice, Shumulu Shiji, was flogged, and the former Vice Minister of Revenue, Li Huan, was sent to replace him.

    Basa himself lacked the ability to defend the city, but he only established his reputation through strict and harsh methods. On the eighth day of the fourth month of summer, the attack ceased, and a decree was issued.

    197

    改元天兴传闻北朝有命令勿击众谓攻三日不解城将隳已而城上望见北兵焚礮车众皆以相贺俄闻北兵不退驻兵逻之由是知祸未艾也士庶徃徃纵酒肉歌呼无久生心秋七月北兵遣唐庆等来使且曰欲和好成金主当自来好议之末帝托疾卧御榻上见庆等掉臂上殿不为礼致来防毕仍有不逊言近侍皆切齿既归馆饷劳是夕飞虎军数辈愤庆等无礼且以为和好终不能成不若杀之快众心夜中持兵入馆大噪杀庆等馆伴使鄂屯安济库二人及昼亦死【案鄂屯安济库旧作奥屯按出虎今改】迟明宰执趋赴馆视之军士露刃诣马前请罪宰相惶遽慰劳之上因赦其罪且加犒赏京师细民皆驩呼踊跃以为太平识者知其祸不

    Explanation

    197

    In the first month of the Tianxing era, there was a rumor that the Northern Court issued an order not to attack, and the troops believed that after three days of siege without success, the city would fall. However, when they looked up from the walls and saw the Northern soldiers burning their catapults, they all congratulated each other. Soon they learned that the Northern soldiers would not retreat and had stationed troops to patrol, realizing that the disaster was not yet over. Both officials and common people often drank and feasted, singing and shouting, without thinking long-term. In the seventh month of autumn, the Northern soldiers sent Tang Qing and others as envoys, saying that they wanted to achieve peace and friendship, and that the Jin ruler should come himself to negotiate. The last emperor pretended to be ill and lay on his bed, while Tang Qing and others waved their arms and went up to the throne, showing no respect, and completed their mission. They still spoke disrespectfully, and those close to the emperor were all furious. After returning to the guesthouse, they were provided with food and entertainment. That night, several members of the Feihu Army, angry at Tang Qing and others for being disrespectful and believing that peace and friendship would never be achieved, decided that killing them would satisfy the people. In the middle of the night, they held weapons and entered the guesthouse, causing a commotion and killing Tang Qing and others, as well as the two guesthouse attendants, Otu Anji and An Chuhu, who also died by day. The next morning, the prime ministers hurried to the guesthouse to see what had happened. The soldiers, with weapons drawn, approached the emperor's horse and asked for forgiveness. The prime ministers, feeling anxious and offering comfort, the emperor then forgave their crime and gave them additional rewards. The common people of the capital all cheered and rejoiced, thinking it was a time of peace. However, those who recognized the disaster knew that the danger was far from over.

    198

    可解矣八月恒山公武仙提兵自邓赴京师上命副枢哈希出兵援之至密县遇北兵喀齐喀遽退走【案金史持嘉喀齐喀传屯中牟古城凡三日弃辎重驰还与此所云至密县有异】仙兵与北兵转战于郑州之西南防图克坦乌登亦提兵东来相遇战久之由喀齐喀兵不相接皆败仙引余兵南归乌登亦西走【案金史哀宗本纪天兴元年二月图克坦乌登战败死与此所叙提兵东来及西走在八月后者迥异】喀齐喀还京师士庶罪其误国上不得已废为民时京师被围数月仓廪空虚尚书右丞李蹊坐粮不给下狱已而免死除名擢前戸部侍郎张师鲁为户部主粮储事时民间皆言官将捜百姓粮人情汹汹甚以为忧冬十月果下令自亲

    Explanation

    198

    The situation has become clear. In August, General Wu Xian of the Hengshan Principality led his troops from Deng to the capital city. The emperor ordered Deputy Chancellor Ha Xi to send reinforcements. Upon reaching Mi County, they encountered the northern forces led by Kaci Ka. Kaci Ka hastily retreated. [According to the Jin History, Kaci Ka's biography, he garrisoned Zhongmou Ancient City for three days before abandoning his supplies and rushing back, which differs from the account of reaching Mi County here.] Wu Xian's troops fought continuously with the northern forces in the southwestern part of Zhengzhou. General Fang Tu Kedan Uden also led his troops from the east and met them in battle, which lasted for a long time. Kaci Ka's forces did not engage and all failed; Wu Xian led the remaining troops south, and Uden also fled west. [According to the Jin History, the Chronicle of Emperor Aizong, in the second month of Tianxing Year One, Fang Tu Kedan Uden died in battle, which differs from the account of leading troops east and fleeing west in August here.] Kaci Ka returned to the capital city, and the common people blamed him for betraying the country. The emperor, unable to avoid it, demoted him to commoner status. At the time, the capital city had been besieged for several months, and the granaries were empty. Right Chancellor Li Xi was imprisoned for failing to provide food, but was later spared from execution and removed from the official register. Former Deputy Minister of Revenue Zhang Shilu was promoted to be in charge of grain storage at the Ministry of Revenue. At the time, the people all said that officials would search for grain from the common people, causing public sentiment to be turbulent and greatly worrying them. In the tenth month of winter, the emperor indeed issued an order to personally oversee the matter.

    王宰相以下皆存三月粮计口留之人三斗余入官【案续通鉴云先令各家自实壮者存石有三斗幼者半之与此所云人三斗有异】隐匿者处死命御史大夫费摩阿固岱率总知开封府图克坦伯嘉主之【案图克坦伯嘉旧作徒单百家今改】其余朝廷侍从官分领其事凡主者所徃剑防从焉戸阅人诘不少缓用铁椎监之石杵震之城中士庶人不爨以待或搜获隐匿者械于街虽皇兄后妃家皆不免军士突入妃主惊逃驱絷奴婢使之指陈所匿京师巨家着姓被罪者甚多总领富察鼎珠尤酷甚【案富察鼎珠旧作蒲察定住今改】杖杀无辜数人凶辈因之为奸利由是百姓离心识者知其必亡十二月朝议以食尽无防末帝亲出东

    Explanation

    199

    All officials below the prime minister were required to store three months' worth of grain, with each person keeping an additional three dou to be handed over to the government. Those who concealed grain were to be executed. The imperial censor-in-chief, Fei Mo'ao Guodai, was ordered to lead the investigation, assisted by Tuqudant Berjia, the governor of Kaifeng Prefecture. Other court officials were to assist in the investigation. Whenever the officials went, they were accompanied by guards armed with swords. Households were thoroughly inspected, and those who did not comply were monitored with iron hammers and stone pestles. The people in the capital city were not allowed to cook, waiting for the inspection. Those who were caught hiding grain were chained and displayed in the streets, and even members of the royal family and the imperial harem were not exempt from this investigation. Soldiers broke into the imperial harem, causing the ladies to flee, and forced the servants to reveal where the hidden grain was stored. Many prominent families in the capital were punished, and the chief inspector, Fuca Dingzhu, was particularly harsh. Several innocent people were beaten to death, and evil individuals took advantage of the situation to commit crimes for personal gain. As a result, the people lost faith in the government, and those with insight knew that the state would soon fall. In December, the court discussed the shortage of food and the lack of defenses, leading the last emperor to personally go east.

    征丞相萨布平章巴萨右丞完顔温绰【案温绰旧作斡出今改】工部尚书权参知政事李蹊枢密院判官白华近侍局副使李大节左右司郎中完顔进德张衮总帅图克坦伯嘉富察古纳高显刘奕皆从上与太后皇后诸妃别大恸誓以不破敌不归仪衞萧然见者悲怆留参知政事完顔努森枢密副使完顔实讷阿巴权行尚书省兼枢密事以余兵守南京上既出遇巩州帅完顔呼沙呼提兵转战来赴援【案完顔呼沙呼旧作完顔怱斜虎今改】因从以东初上疑东面帅李新跋扈有妄言先罢为兵部侍郎将出密谕二守臣羁絷已而上出二人者以事召新诣省新疑其见擒纵马突城门欲出门者止之新弃马逾城二人者遽命将追及堕湟水

    Explanation

    200

    Acting Chancellor Sabu, the Pingzhang of Basa, Right Chancellor Wangenchuo [Note: Wangenchuo was previously written as Wuchu but has been changed], Minister of Works Li Xi, Acting Vice-Premier Baihua, Judge of the Military Council Liba, Deputy Director of the Inner Service Bureau Li Da, Attendants of the Left/Right Office Wancheng, Zhang Gǔn, General Tuke Tan, Ba Jia, Fucha Guna, Gao Xian, and Liu Yi all followed the emperor,太后,皇后, and the various concubines in great grief, swearing not to return until the enemy was defeated. The imperial retinue was sparse, and those who saw it were filled with sorrow. Acting Vice-Premier Wangenchuo and Deputy Judge of the Military Council Wangeshena were left to act as the governor of the central government and the Military Council, to defend 南京 with the remaining troops. The emperor, after leaving, met the commander of 巩州 Wangeshahuhu, who raised troops and came to provide assistance. He then followed him eastward. Initially, the emperor suspected that the eastern commander Li Xin was arrogant and made wild statements, so he first dismissed him to serve as the Minister of War. He was about to leave secretly and give orders to two local officials to detain him. When the emperor left, the two officials summoned Li Xin to the province, and Li Xin suspected he would be captured. He galloped out of the city gate, but those who wanted to stop him did not. Li Xin abandoned his horse and jumped over the city wall. The two officials hastily ordered the general to pursue him, and Li Xin fell into the湟水 river.

    中斩其首时末帝既出人情愈不安日夜颙望东征之捷俄闻北渡前锋方交战有功取蒲城进取衞州巴萨等望见北兵遽劝上登舟船南渡从官多攀从不及死于兵而骁将图克坦伯嘉髙显刘奕辈初不知上去已而军士皆散没上以余兵狼狈入归德杜门京民大恐以为将不救矣二守臣素庸闇无谋但知闭门自守百姓食尽无以自生米升直银二両贫民徃徃食人殍死者相望官日载数车出城一夕皆剐食其肉净尽搢绅士女多行匄于街民间有食其子锦衣寳器不能易米数升人朝出不敢夕归惧为饥者杀而食平日亲族交旧以一饭相避于家又日杀乘骑马牛自防至于箱箧鞍韀诸皮物凡可食者皆煮而食之其贵家第宅与夫市中

    Explanation

    201

    During the time when the emperor's head was cut off, the people became increasingly uneasy, anxiously awaiting news of the eastern campaign's success. Soon after, they heard that the northern crossing had begun, and the front-line troops were engaged in battle, achieving victory by capturing cities such as Pucheng and advancing towards Weizhou. Upon seeing the northern forces, they hastily advised the emperor to flee south by boat. Many officials followed him but were left behind and perished in the fighting. The brave generals, including Tuketan, Berjia, Gao, Xian, and Liu Yi, were initially unaware of the emperor's departure, and soon afterward, the soldiers dispersed and fled. The emperor, with his remaining troops, entered Guide in a hasty and disorganized manner. The people of the capital were greatly alarmed, fearing that they would not be rescued. The two local officials, who were ordinarily incompetent and lacked strategy, merely knew to close the gates and defend themselves.

    The people had run out of food and could not sustain themselves; a measure of rice cost two ounces of silver, and poor people often resorted to cannibalism, with dead bodies lying everywhere. Officials daily loaded several carts of food out of the city, but by nightfall, they all slaughtered and ate the meat, consuming it all. Many nobles and high-ranking officials begged on the streets, and some even ate their own children, unable to exchange their luxurious clothing and valuable items for even a small amount of rice. People dared not leave their homes in the morning and feared to return at night, fearing they would be killed and eaten by those who were starving. In times of scarcity, people usually avoided meals with relatives and friends, and they also slaughtered their horses, cattle, and other livestock for protection. They even boiled and ate items such as boxes, saddles, and other leather goods that could be consumed. The luxurious homes of the wealthy and the markets were scenes of widespread desperation and survival.

    楼馆木材皆撒以爨城中触目皆瓦砾废区无复向来繁侈矣朝官士庶徃徃相结携妻子突出北归众谓不久当大溃二年正月末帝遣近侍局使图克坦色实等【案图克坦色实旧作徒单四喜今改】入南京取太皇后皇后诸妃嫔赴归德既出城与北兵遇复仓皇归宫于后色实独携其族以去末帝斩之时外围不解上下如在陷穽中且相继殍死议者以为上既去国推立皇兄荆王以城降庶可救一城生灵且望不絶完顔氏之祀是亦春秋纪侯大去其国纪季酅入于齐之义不得已者况北兵中有曹王也朝士皆知莫敢言二守臣但曰当以死守众愤二人无他策思有一豪杰出而为之救士民余夕见左司郎中杨居仁白其事杨云是事固善

    Explanation

    202

    The wood from the buildings was all used for cooking, and everything one sees in the city is ruins and rubble. There is no longer the former splendor and extravagance. Officials and common people often formed groups and fled north with their families, thinking it would not be long before a great collapse occurred. In the latter part of the second year, the last emperor sent the court attendants, including Tuoketan Seshi (formerly known as Tushan Sihui), to Nanjing to fetch the empress dowager, the empress, and the various concubines to Gui De. After they left the city, they encountered the northern forces and hurriedly returned to the palace. Tuoketan Seshi alone took his clan with him and left. The last emperor was executed at that time. The siege around the city had not been lifted, and people were trapped like in a pit, dying one after another. Some argued that if the emperor left the country and the crown prince of Jing Wang was established, the city could be surrendered to save the people and continue the Aisin Gioro lineage. This is also the meaning of the Spring and Autumn Annals where a prince left his country to preserve his family's name and lineage, which was unavoidable. Moreover, among the northern forces, there was a prince named Cao Wang. All court officials knew this but dared not speak out. The two city governors only said they would defend the city to the death. The people were angry because the two governors had no other strategy and hoped for a heroic figure to save them. Someone saw Left Censor Yang Jurin at night and informed him of the situation. Yang said this matter was indeed good.

    然孰敢倡者彼二执政亦知之而不敢言且不敢为也二十有一日忽闻执政召在京父老士庶计事诣都堂余同麻革潜众中以听二执政立都堂檐外杨居仁诸首领官从焉省掾元好问宣执政所下令告谕且问诸父老便宜完顔努森拱立无语独完顔实讷阿巴决复申谕以国家至此无可奈何凡有可行当共议且继以泣涕诸愚叟或陈说细微不足采余语麻革将出而白前事革言莫若以奏说密陈子归草之吾当共上也余以是退将明日同革献书其夕颇闻民间称有一西南崔都尉药招抚者将起事众皆曰事急矣安知无人余既归夜草书备论其事迟明怀以诣省庭且邀革徃自断此事系完顔氏存灭且以救余民虽死亦无愧矣是旦大

    Sure, here is the final translation:

    Who would dare to initiate it? Those two officials also know about it but dare not speak or act. On the twenty-first day, I suddenly heard that the officials had summoned elders and commoners from the capital to the capital hall to discuss matters. I went with Ma Ge, hiding among the crowd to listen. The two officials stood outside the eaves of the hall, while Yang Juren and other leaders were present. The provincial clerk Yuan Haowen announced the officials' orders and instructions, and asked the elders for advice. Wan Yan Nusen stood silently without speaking, while only Wan Yan Shen Nei and Aba Jue reiterated the instructions, followed by tears. The elders offered minor suggestions that were not significant. I told Ma Ge that I would report the previous events, and he suggested drafting a secret report to be submitted. I decided to draft the report and submit it the next day with Ma Ge. That evening, I heard that a general named Cui from the southwest was planning to rebel. The crowd said the situation was urgent and that no one knew what to do.     204

    Suddenly, the sky turned overcast and it began to rain. I took temporary refuge in a civilian home when I suddenly heard the sound of marching troops. The people in the city ran and spread the news, saying that the northern troops had entered the city. Realizing that the situation was beyond my control, I hurried back home. On the road, I learned that the troops were not the northern ones, but rather the southwestern troops had rebelled and surrounded the Shangshu Province. At that time, Cui Li, as the commander-in-chief of the western army, led his forces with his allies, including Han Duo, and raised an army against An Guo, a northerner known for his natural bravery and courage. He led the way, wielding his sword to enter the Shangshu Province, followed by Cui Li. Now, I have killed them to save the people of the city, and I have also prohibited all soldiers from taking even one coin from the people; if they do, they will be executed." The entire prefecture cheered and rejoiced, believing that they now had a way to survive. At mealtime, the sky suddenly turned overcast and began to rain, but then cleared up, and the sunlight shone brightly. Cui Li led his troops into the palace and explained the matter to the empress dowager.

The emperor appointed his younger brother as Chancellor of State Affairs, Zhang Song as the Chief Inspector of the Palace Guards, Han Duo as Deputy Commander-in-Chief and Governor of Kaifeng Prefecture, and Su Bolin Ji as the Deputy Director of the Left Office and Chief Censor. All of these individuals were part of the emperor's faction. Additionally, the emperor appointed Liu Zhongzhou, the Vice Minister of Personnel, and Zhang Zhenglun, the Councillor of State, as advisors to the provincial government, as the emperor had taken Liu Zhongzhou's daughter as his wife. Zhang Zhenglun was well-regarded. The emperor also appointed E Tun Agu Dai as the Right Vice Minister of the Board of Works and Wen Te Her Yi Shi as the Vice Minister of State Affairs. Furthermore, Diao Bi was appointed as the Minister of War and Left Commander of the Army. Initially, the emperor had planned to discuss matters with Diao Bi, but when the appointed time came, Diao Bi did not attend, which angered the emperor, causing him to lose his position. At that time, Diao Bi was highly regarded.

    士大夫退闲者皆以次迁擢台阁中其除拜无虚日俄立自为太师尚书令郑王闻钧汝间有众据西山不从命立遣韩铎帅兵讨之铎中箭死以折希顔知开封府立又封诸内藏库将以奉北兵亦徃徃取归其第又搜选民间寡妇处女亦将以奉北兵然入其家者甚众又括刷在京金银命百官分坊陌穷治之贵人富家俱被害陈国夫人王氏末帝姨也素富于财平章巴萨夫人亦富侈右丞李蹊旧以取积闻其妻子皆被搒掠拷讯死立又自诣军前求免剽掠又求纵百姓出城挑菜充饥于是人得出近郊采蓬子窠甜苣菜杂米粒以食又闻京西陈冈上有野麦甚丰立请百姓徃收之立又聚皇族皆入宫俄遣诣青城皆为北兵所杀如荆王梁王辈皆

    207

    The retired officials and literati were all promoted in turn to positions in the imperial government, with no day passing without appointments. Soon, he appointed himself as Grand Tutor and Chief Secretary.
