He immediately sent Han Duo to lead troops to suppress them. Han Duo was killed by an arrow. He then appointed Zhe Xiyan as the governor of Kaifeng Prefecture. He sealed and stored the imperial treasury to provide for the northern forces, and often took the wealth back to their own residences. He also searched and selected widows and unmarried women from the common people to provide for the northern forces. However, many entered their homes. He collected and confiscated gold and silver in the capital, ordering officials to divide the city into districts and thoroughly investigate. Wealthy and influential families all suffered harm. Chen Guo's Lady Wang was the aunt of the last emperor and had always been wealthy. Pingzhang Basa's Lady was also wealthy and extravagant. The Right Chancellor Li Xi was known for accumulating wealth, and it was known that his wife and children were beaten and interrogated to death. He then went to the front of the army to request exemption from looting and also requested to allow the people to leave the city to gather vegetables to eat. As a result, people were able to go to the outskirts to collect wild vegetables mixed with rice grains to eat. He also heard that in the western part of the capital, on Chen Gang, there was an abundance of wild wheat. He requested the people to go and collect it. He then gathered the royal family and brought them into the palace. Soon, he sent them to Qingcheng, where they were all killed by the northern soldiers, like King Jing and King Liang and others.

    208

    预焉独太后皇后诸妃嫔宫人北徙百姓初闻皇族当北徃有窜其间者亦被诛军前又取壬辰诸宰执家属治罪为杀唐庆事故相侯挚亦见杀四月二十日使者发三教医匠人等出城北兵纵入大掠立时在城外营中兵先入立家取其妻妾宝玉辇以出立归大恸亦不敢谁何大臣富家多被荼毒死者而三教医匠人等在青城侧亦被剽夺无遗俄复遣三教人入城许百姓与北兵市易城中人以所余金帛易北来米麦食之然多为北兵劫取莫敢语余时同诸生复入居八仙馆中五月二十有二日防使者召三教人从以北嗟乎此生何属亲见国亡至于惊怖劳苦万状不可数廼因暇日记忆旧事漫记于编若夫所传不真及不见不闻者皆不敢录

    208

    During the relocation northward, the empress, consorts, palace women, and commoners were forcibly moved. Initially, when the royal family was to be relocated north, some people attempted to hide among them and were subsequently executed. The military also took action against the families of officials from the year "Rénchén" and held them accountable for crimes, including the execution of former chancellor Hou Zhi due to his involvement in the death of Tang Qing. On the twenty-first day of the fourth month, envoys led monks, nuns, doctors, and craftsmen out of the city. The northern soldiers then entered and began a widespread looting. Soldiers from the camp outside the city entered first, taking the wives, concubines, and valuable treasures from the homes and carrying them out. Upon returning home, the person who witnessed this event was in great sorrow but dared not speak out against it. Many high-ranking officials and wealthy families were severely oppressed and killed, and even monks, nuns, doctors, and craftsmen near Qingcheng were looted and left with nothing. Shortly after, monks, nuns, and other religious figures were sent back into the city to allow the common people to trade with the northern soldiers. The people in the city used their remaining gold and silk to buy rice and wheat from the northern soldiers, but many of these items were seized by the soldiers, and no one dared to complain. At this time, the narrator, along with other students, returned to stay at the Eight Immortals Pavilion. On the twenty-second day of the fifth month, an envoy summoned monks, nuns, and other religious figures to accompany them north. The narrator reflected on their life, feeling as though they had no place in the world, having witnessed the fall of the nation and experiencing countless forms of terror and hardship. They decided to write down their memories during their spare time. Anything that was not true or that they had not seen or heard themselves, they would not record.

    209

    归潜志卷十一
    　　钦定四库全书
    　　归潜志卷十二
    　　元　刘祁　撰
    　　録崔立碑事
    　　崔立既变以南京降自负其有救一城生灵功谓左司员外郎元裕之曰汝等何时立一石书吾状耶时立国柄入手生杀在一言省庭日流血上下震悚诸在位者畏之于是乎有立碑颂功徳议数日忽一省卒诣余家赍尚书礼房小帖子云首领官召赴礼部余初愕然自以布衣不预事不知何谓即徃至省门外遇麻信之余因语之信之曰昨日见左司郎中张信之言郑王碑事欲属我辈作岂其然耶即同入省礼房省掾曹益引见首领官张信之元裕之二人曰今郑王以一身救百万生灵其功徳诚可喜今在京官吏父老欲为立碑纪其事众议属之

    Explanation

    209

    归潜志卷十二

    钦定四库全书

    元 刘祁 撰

    录崔立碑事

    崔立既变以南京降，自负其有救一城生灵之功。他对左司员外郎元裕之说：“你们何时为我立一块石碑，记录我的事迹呢？”当时，崔立已经掌握了国家大权，生杀予夺只在一言之间，朝廷内外血流成河，上下震动，所有在位者都对他感到恐惧。因此，有人提议为他立碑颂扬他的功德。几天后，一名省吏突然来到我家，带来了一份尚书礼房的小帖子，说首领官召我去礼部。我起初非常惊讶，自认为只是一个布衣百姓，不参与政事，不知道这是什么意思。于是，我立即前往礼部门外，遇到了麻信之。我向他询问，他说：“昨天我见到左司郎中张信之，他说关于郑王的石碑之事，想委托我们来做，难道是真的吗？”于是，我们一起进入礼房，省掾曹益引见了首领官张信之和元裕之二人。他们说：“现在郑王以一人之力拯救了百万生灵，他的功德确实值得称赞。现在在京的官员、老人和百姓都想为他立碑，记录他的事迹，大家的意见都支持这样做。”

    210

    二君且已白郑王矣二君其无让余即辞曰祁辈布衣无职此非所当为况有翰林诸公如王文从之及裕之辈在祁等不敢裕之曰此事出于众心且吾曹生自王得之为之何辞君等无让余即曰吾当见王丈论之裕之曰王论亦如此矣余即趋出至学士院见王丈时修撰张子忠应奉张元美亦在焉余因语其事且曰此实诸公职某等何预焉王曰此事议久矣盖以院中人为之若尚书檄学士院作非出于在京官吏父老心若自布衣中为之乃众欲也且子未仕在布衣今士民属子子为之亦不伤于义也余于是阴悟诸公自以仕金显达欲避其名以嫁

    Explanation

    210

    The two gentlemen have already informed the King of Zheng. They should not hesitate to let me handle this matter. I immediately said, "We are commoners with no official position; this is not something we should do, especially since there are esteemed officials like Wang Wenchong and Yu Zhi in the Imperial Academy. We dare not take on this responsibility." Yu Zhi replied, "This matter comes from the collective will of the people, and we, who have received our positions from the King, should not refuse. You gentlemen should not hesitate." I then said, "I will go to see the King to discuss this matter." Yu Zhi said, "The King’s opinion is the same as mine." I quickly left and went to the Imperial Academy to see the King. At that time, Zhang Zizhong, the compiler, and Zhang Yuanmei, the attendant, were also present. I then spoke about the matter and said, "This is truly the responsibility of the esteemed officials; what do we have to do with it?" The King said, "This matter has been discussed for a long time. It is being handled by the officials in the academy. If the Minister of Works issues an order to the Imperial Academy, it is not driven by the will of the officials and elders in the capital. If it is handled by commoners, it is what the people want. Moreover, you have not yet taken an official position and are still a commoner. Now the common people are looking to you. If you handle it, it would not be against the principles of righteousness." I then secretly realized that the esteemed officials, who have served the Jin dynasty and achieved prominence, wish to avoid their names being associated with this matter.

    211

    诸布衣又念平生为文今而遇此患难以是知子云剧秦美新其亦出于不得已耶因逊让而别连延数日又被督促知不能辞即畧为草定付裕之一二日后一省卒来召云诸宰执召君余不得已赴省途中遇元裕之骑马索余因刧以行且拉麻信之俱徃初不言碑事止云省中召王学士诸公防饮余亦阴揣其然既入即引诣左防政幕中见防政刘公谦甫举杯属吾二人曰大王碑事众议烦公等公等成之甚善余与信之俱逊让曰不敢已而谦甫出见王丈在焉相与酬酢酒数行日将入矣余二人告归裕之曰省门已锁今夕即当留宿省中余辈无如

    Explanation

    211

    The common people, reflecting on their writings throughout life, now find themselves in this difficult situation. They realize that Yang Xiong's Ju Qin Mei Xin was also written out of necessity. Because of humility and yielding, they parted ways, continuing for several days. They were again urged, knowing they could not refuse, they then roughly drafted it and gave it to Yu Zhi. A few days later, an official from the provincial government came to summon them, saying that various high officials had summoned you. I had no choice but to go to the provincial government. On the way, they met Yuan Yu Zhi riding a horse and demanding me. Because of the coercion, I went along and also took Ma Xing with me. Initially, they did not mention the stele matter, only saying that the provincial government summoned Mr. Wang and other scholars for a gathering. I also secretly suspected that this was the case. After entering, they led us to the office of the Left Censor. They met Mr. Liu, the Censor, who raised his cup and said to us two, "The matter of the stele for the Great King is complex, it is troublesome for you. If you can complete it, it would be very good." I and Xingzhi both humbly declined, saying we dare not. Afterwards, Mr. Liu came out and saw Mr. Wang there. They exchanged drinks, several rounds of wine, and the sun was about to set. We two asked to leave, and Yu Zhi said, "The provincial gate is already locked, we will have to stay overnight in the provincial government." We have no choice.

    212

    之何已而烛至饮余裕之倡曰郑王碑文今夕可毕手也余曰有诸公在诸公为之王丈谓余曰此事郑王已知众人请太学中名士作子如坚拒使王知书生辈不肯作是不许其以城降也则衔之刻骨缙绅俱受祸矣是子以一人累众也且子有老祖母老母在堂今一触其锋祸及亲族何以为智子熟思之余惧以非职辞久之且曰余既为草定不当诸公意请改命他人诸公不许促迫甚余知其事无可奈何则曰吾素不知馆阁体今夕诸公共议之如诸公避其名但书某名在诸公后于是裕之引纸落笔草其事王丈又曰此文姑使裕之作以为君作又何

    Explanation

    212

    As the candle arrived, the host of the banquet said, "The inscription for the Prince of Zheng can be completed tonight." I replied, "With all the gentlemen present, let the gentlemen do it." The respected elder said to me, "This matter is already known to the Prince of Zheng. The people asked a famous scholar from the Imperial Academy to write it. If you stubbornly refuse, it will make the Prince of Zheng know that the scholars are unwilling to write it, which is equivalent to not allowing him to surrender the city. Then he will bear a grudge against us deeply, and all the officials will suffer. This is you burdening many people with your actions. Moreover, you have your grandmother and mother at home. If you provoke him, the disaster will affect your relatives. How can this be considered wise? You should think carefully about it." I was afraid and tried to refuse for a long time, citing that it was not my duty. And I said, "I have already drafted it, but it does not meet the gentlemen's expectations. Please appoint someone else." The gentlemen did not agree and pressed me very much. I knew that there was nothing I could do and said, "I have never written in the official style. Let the gentlemen discuss it tonight. If the gentlemen want to avoid the name, just write my name after the gentlemen's names." Then Yu Zhi took out the paper and started writing the draft. The respected elder said, "Let Yu Zhi write it as a draft for you. What difference does it make?"

    213

    妨且君集中不载亦可也余曰裕之作政宜某复何言碑文既成以示王丈及余信之欲相商评王丈为定数字其铭词则王丈裕之信之及存余旧数言其碑序全裕之笔也然其文止实叙事亦无襃称立言时夜几四鼓裕之趣曹益甫书之裕之即于烛前焚其藁迟明余辈趋去后数日立坐朝堂诸宰执首领官共献其文以为夀遂召余信之等俱诣立第受官余辈深惧见立俄而诸首领官赍告身三通以出付余辈曰特赐进士出身因为余辈贺后闻求巨石不得省门左旧有宋徽宗时甘灵碑有司取而磨之工书人张君庸者求书刻方毕北兵入城纵剽

    Explanation

    213

    Moreover, if the collection of the respected individual (君集) does not include it, it is also acceptable. I said, if someone (裕之) is doing well in politics, what more needs to be said? After the memorial inscription was completed, it was shown to Wang and others for their evaluation and comments. Wang determined the number of characters for the inscription, and both Wang and the author (裕之) approved the content, retaining some old phrases. The preface of the memorial inscription was entirely written by the author (裕之). However, the text is purely factual and does not include praise or commentary. It was almost four o'clock in the early morning. The author asked Cao Yifu to write down the text. The author then burned the draft in front of the candle. Shortly before dawn, the author and others left. Several days later, while sitting in the hall of the government office, various officials presented the text as a birthday gift to someone in a high position. They were then summoned to receive official appointments. The officials were deeply afraid of meeting the person in power, but the chief officials gave them three copies of their official documents, saying they had been specially granted the status of Jinshi (进士). They congratulated each other. Later, they tried to find a large stone but failed. There was an old stele from the Song Dynasty's Huizong period on the left side of the provincial gate, which the authorities had polished. A skilled calligrapher named Zhang Junyong was asked to inscribe and carve it, but just as he finished, northern invaders entered the city and began looting.

    214

    余辈狼狈而出不知其竟能立否也嗟乎诸公本畏立祸不敢不成其言已而又欲避其名以卖布衣之士余辈不幸有虚名一旦为人之所刧欲以死拒之则发诸公嫁名之机诸公必怒怒而达崔立祸不可测则吾二亲何以自存吾之死所谓自经于沟渎而莫之知且轻杀吾身以忧吾亲为大不孝矣况身未禄仕权义之轻重亲莫重焉故余姑忍保身为二亲计且其文皆众笔非余全文彼欲嫁名于余余安得而辞也今天下士议徃徃知之所为且有曹通甫诗杨叔能词在亦不待余辨也因书其首尾之详以志年少之过空山静思可以一笑辩亡

    Explanation

    214

    We fled in a disheveled and desperate manner, unsure if we could possibly survive. Alas, the gentlemen originally feared the calamity of standing and were unwilling to let their words fail. Yet, they also wanted to avoid their names by selling out the common people. Unfortunate for us, we have a false reputation, and once we were taken hostage, we wanted to resist with death. But doing so would trigger the gentlemen to transfer their name to us, and they would surely be angry. Their anger could reach Cui Li, whose disaster is unpredictable. In that case, how could my parents survive? My death would be like hanging myself in a ditch, unknown to anyone, and lightly sacrificing my life for the sake of my parents' worry would be a great act of filial impiety. Moreover, my body has not yet received official rank or salary, and the balance of power and righteousness is not as important as my parents. Therefore, I temporarily endure and preserve myself for the sake of my parents. Furthermore, the text was written by many hands, not solely my own. They want to transfer their name to me, and how can I refuse? Today, the opinions of scholars and literati often know what I have done, and there are poems by Cao Tongfu and lyrics by Yang Shuneng, so I do not need to defend myself. I will write down the details of the beginning and end to record my youthful mistakes. In the quiet of the empty mountain, I can reflect on them with a smile, debating my downfall.

    215

    或问金国之所以亡何哉末帝非有桀纣之恶害不及民疆土虽削士马尚强而遽至不救亦必有説余曰观金之始取天下过于后魏后唐石晋辽然其所以不能长久者根本不立也当其取辽时诚与后魏初起不殊及取宋责其背约名为伐罪吊民收徽宗圗书车服襃崇元佑诸正人取蔡京童贯王黼诸奸党皆以顺百姓望由能用辽宋人材如韩企先刘彦能韩昉辈也及得天下其封建废置政令如前朝典章法度皆出于书生至海陵庶人虽淫暴自强然英鋭有大志定官制律令皆可观又擢用人材将混一天下功虽不成其强至矣世宗天资仁厚善于守成又躬自俭约以育士庶故大定三十年几致太平所用多敦厚谨勑之士如

    Explanation

    215

    Someone asked about the reasons for the downfall of the Jin State. The last emperor did not possess the wickedness of Jie and Zhou, and his harm did not reach the people; his territory was reduced, but his army remained strong. Yet, it suddenly reached a point where rescue was impossible, and there must be a reason. I said: Observe how the Jin State initially took control of the world—it was more powerful than the Later Wei, Later Tang, Later Jin, and Liao states. However, the reason it could not last long was that its foundation was not established. When it took control of the Liao state, it was truly similar to the early rise of the Later Wei. When it took control of the Song state, it blamed the Song for breaking the treaty and called itself a campaign to punish the guilty and comfort the people. It seized Emperor Huizong's books, vehicles, and clothing, honored the righteous people of the Yuan佑 era, and punished the corrupt officials like Cai Jing, Tong Guan, and Wang Fu—all to satisfy the expectations of the common people. Because it was able to use the talents of the Liao and Song states, such as Han Qixian, Liu Yanneng, and Han Fang. When it gained control of the world, its system of feudal enfeoffment was abolished, and its policies and laws were like those of the previous dynasty, all coming from scholars. Even Emperor Wanyan Liang, although he was licentious and violent, sought to strengthen himself, was sharp and had great ambitions, and established the official system and legal codes, all of which were noteworthy. He promoted talented individuals and aimed to unify the world, though his achievements were not realized, his strength was great. Emperor Shizong had a naturally kind and generous nature, was good at maintaining the status quo, personally practiced frugality to nurture the scholars and common people, and therefore, during the thirty years of the Dading era, it nearly brought about a period of peace. He mostly used honest and cautious officials.

    216

    石琚辈为相不烦扰不更张偃息干戈修崇学校议者以为有汉文景风此所以基明昌承安之盛也宣孝太子最髙明絶人读书喜文欲以变易风俗行中国礼乐如魏孝文天不祚金不即大位早世章宗聪慧有父风属文为学崇尚儒雅故一时名士辈出大臣执政多有文采学问可取能吏直臣皆得显用政令修举文治烂然金朝之盛极矣然文学止于词章不知讲明经术为保国保民之道以图基祚久长又颇好浮侈崇建宫阙外戚小人多预政且无志圣贤髙躅大臣惟知奉承不敢逆其所好故上下皆无维持长世之策安乐一时此所以啓大安贞祐之弱也卫王苛吝不知人君体不足言已而强敌生边贼臣得柄外内交病莫敢疗理宣

    Explanation

    216

    Shi Ju and his colleagues served as chancellors, governing without causing disturbance or making drastic changes, ceasing warfare, and promoting the establishment and development of schools. Some people believed that their governance style resembled that of the Han dynasty's emperors Wen and Jing, which laid the foundation for the prosperity of the Mingchang and Cheng'an eras. The heir apparent, the Prince of Xuan, was exceptionally intelligent and unique, enjoying reading and writing, and desiring to change customs and traditions by implementing Chinese rituals and music, akin to Emperor Xiaowen of Wei. However, due to a lack of divine favor, he did not ascend to the throne and died young. Emperor Zhangzong, known for his intelligence and resemblance to his father, favored literary pursuits and scholarly elegance, leading to the emergence of many distinguished scholars at the time. Ministers who governed were often praised for their literary talent and scholarly knowledge, and capable officials and upright ministers were all given prominent positions. Government policies were well-organized, and cultural achievements flourished, marking the peak of the Jin dynasty's prosperity. However, literature at the time was limited to ornamental writing, with little understanding of how to use Confucian teachings to protect the country and its people or to plan for a long-lasting dynasty. The emperor also had a fondness for extravagance and luxury, building grand palaces, and allowing relatives and unprincipled individuals to interfere in politics. Moreover, there was a lack of aspiration to follow the footsteps of sages and virtuous men, and ministers only knew how to flatter, fearing to oppose the emperor's preferences. As a result, neither the ruler nor the ministers had strategies for maintaining a long-lasting dynasty, leading to a period of temporary peace and happiness. This is why the later periods of Da'an and Zhenyou were weak. The King of Wei was stingy and lacked the qualities of a ruler, not worth mentioning. Powerful enemies emerged at the borders, corrupt officials gained power, and both the outside and inside of the government suffered, with no one daring to address the problems.

    217

    宗立于贼手本懦弱无能性颇猜忌惩权臣之祸恒恐为人所摇故大臣宿将有罪必除去不贷其迁都大梁可谓失谋向使守闗中犹可以数世况南渡之后不能苦心刻意如越王句践志报防稽之羞但茍安幸存以延嵗月由髙琪执政后擢用胥吏抑士大夫之气不得伸文法纷然无兴复逺畧大臣在位者亦无忘身徇国之人纵有之亦不得驰骋又偏私族疎外汉人其机宻谟谋虽汉相不得预人主以至公治天下其分别如此望羣下尽力难哉故当路者惟知迎合其意谨守簿书而已为将者但知奉承近侍以偷幸宠无効死之心幸臣贵戚皆据要职于一时士大夫一有敢言敢为者皆投置散地此所以啓天兴之亡也末帝夺长而立

    Explanation

    217

    The ruler, established by the hands of the enemy, was originally weak and incapable, with a nature quite suspicious. Punished by the disasters caused by powerful ministers, he always feared to be swayed by others. Therefore, when high-ranking officials and generals committed crimes, they were inevitably removed and not pardoned. His decision to move the capital to Daliang can be called a loss of strategy. If he had held onto Guanzhong, it could have lasted for several generations; after crossing south, he could not exert himself as much as King Goujian of Yue did to avenge the humiliation at Fucheng, but just tried to survive and prolong his days. Since Gao Qi took power, promoting clerks while suppressing the spirit of scholars, the legal system became chaotic without any plans for revival or long-term strategy. Those in high positions also lacked self-sacrificing individuals, even if there were any, they could not fully utilize their talents. Favoring one's own kind and alienating Han people, even Han prime ministers could not participate in secret plans. The ruler governed the world with utmost fairness, but the distinctions were so clear. Expecting subordinates to work hard is difficult, therefore, those in power only knew to flatter him and carefully keep records, while generals only knew to curry favor with those close to the ruler to gain temporary favor without a willingness to die for the cause. Favored officials and nobles held key positions at the time, while scholars and officials who dared to speak out were all relegated to peripheral positions. This is why Tianxing (the dynasty) perished. The last emperor seized power from the heir apparent.

    218

    出于爱私虽资不残酷然以圣智自处少为吏时全所教用术取人虽外示寛宏以取名内实淫纵自肆且讳言过恶喜听谀言又闇于用人其将相止取从来贵戚虽不杀大臣其骄将多难制不驯况不知大畧临大事辄退怯自沮此所以一遇勍敌而不能振也大抵金国之政杂用辽宋法令所以支持百年然其分别汉人且不变家政不得士大夫心此所以不能长久向使大定后宣孝得立尽行中国法明昌承安间复知保守整顿以防后忧南渡之后能内修政令以恢复为志则其国祚亦未必遽絶也尝记泰和间有云中李纯甫由小官上书万言大畧以为此政当有为日而当路以为迂阔笑之宴安自处以至土崩瓦南渡后复有以机

    Explanation

    218

    Arising from private affection, though not inherently cruel, he regarded himself as wise and sagacious. During his early days as an official, he employed tactics to select people, outwardly displaying generosity and magnanimity to gain fame, but internally indulging in licentiousness and unrestrained behavior, and avoiding mentioning faults and misdeeds, enjoying listening to flattering words. He was also obscure in the use of people, appointing only those of noble lineage, though not killing high officials, his arrogant generals were difficult to control and manage, and how much more so, lacking an understanding of the big picture, facing major events, they retreated and became discouraged. This is why, when encountering a strong enemy, they could not rally. Generally, the Jin state's governance mixed the laws of Liao and Song, thus supporting the state for a century, however, its treatment of Han Chinese and its household policies remained unchanged, it did not win the hearts of scholars and officials, this is why it could not last long. If, after the reign of Emperor Xuanzong, Emperor Shunzong had ascended the throne, to fully implement Chinese law, during the Mingchang and Cheng'an periods, there was a renewed effort to preserve and整顿 to prevent future troubles, after the southern relocation, if they had focused on internal reforms and aimed to restore the state, then the state's longevity might not have been cut short. I recall that during the Taihe period, Li Chunfu from Yunzhong, a minor official, submitted a ten-thousand-word memorial, roughly stating that this governance should have a period of action, those in power regarded it as impractical and laughed at it, living in ease and comfort until the state collapsed, after the southern relocation, there were again those who used cunning.

    219

    防宜急有备为言者而上下泰然俱不以为心以至宗庙丘墟家国废絶此古人所谓何世无竒材而遗之草泽者也金银珠玉世人所甚贵及遇凶年则不及菽粟何哉事有先后势有缓急也平时富贵之家求一珠玉犀玩好器物至发粟出帛惟恐其不得将以充其室夸耀于人以自乐者皆是也壬辰嵗余在大梁时城久被围公私乏食米一升至银二两余殍死者相望人视金银如泥土使用不计士庶之家出其平日珠玉玩好妆具环佩锦绣衣衾日陈于天津桥市中惟博鬻升合米豆以救朝夕尝记余家一毳袍极致宻鲜完博米八升金钗易牛肉一肩趋售之以是知明君贵五谷而贱金玉诚知其本也古人云薪如桂米如珠岂虚言哉

    Explanation

    219

    Those who should have been on high alert and prepared, yet both high and low were complacent and did not take it to heart, leading to the desolation of ancestral temples and the collapse of the state. This is what ancient people referred to when they said that every era has extraordinary talents but leaves them in the wilderness. Gold, silver, jewels, and precious stones are highly valued by the world, but when faced with a famine, they are not as valuable as beans and grains. Why is that? There is a sequence to things and a priority in urgency. In times of peace, wealthy families would go to great lengths to acquire precious items, even to the point of using grain and silk, fearing they might not get them. They would use these items to fill their homes, to show off to others, and to enjoy themselves. All of this is true.

    In the year Renchen, when I was in Daliang, the city had been under siege for a long time, and both public and private food supplies were scarce. A measure of rice cost two taels of silver, and the dead were everywhere. People treated gold and silver as if they were dirt, using them without counting. Both commoners and nobles would bring out their usual jewels, ornaments, and fine clothing and display them daily in the market of Tianjin Bridge, just to buy a little rice and beans to survive from day to day. I remember that one of my family's fur coats, which was extremely fine and almost new, was exchanged for eight measures of rice. A golden hairpin was traded for a shoulder of beef. From this, I understand that a wise ruler values grains and despises gold and jade, truly knowing the essence of things. As the ancients said, firewood is as expensive as cinnamon and rice is as valuable as pearls. Is this not a true statement?

    220

    文章各有体本不可相犯欺故古文不宜蹈袭前人成语当以竒异自强四六宜用前人成语复不宜生涩求异如散文不宜用诗家语诗句不宜用散文言律赋不宜犯散文言散文不犯律赋语皆判然各异如杂用之非惟失体且梗目难通然学者闇于识多混乱交出且互相诋诮不自觉知此虽一二名公不免也
    　　长于此者必短于彼优于大者或劣于小士君子穷处不能活妻子免饥寒及其得志则兼济天下使民物各得所太公困于鼓刀钓渔伊尹躬耕莘野彼岂不能妄营财利使生理优游耶耻不为也若夫韩淮阴少年乞食漂母人皆笑嗤及为将料敌制胜无遗策卒能佐汉祖定天下身享南面之乐岂昔之拙而今之巧耶材有所长志有所不为也因是以思吾侪今日遭大变遯于穷山荒野中日惟糊口之不给而不免有求于人亦不足怪但恨不能自渔樵亲耕稼以自给如古之人耳彼穷居妻子有愠言乡人贱人交游笑之又何病也理固然也

    Explanation

    220

    Different types of writing each have their own distinct styles, and they cannot be mutually violated or deceived. Therefore, ancient prose should not blindly imitate previous people's set phrases, but rather strengthen oneself by being unique and novel. Parallel prose, however, should use previous people's set phrases, but it is not advisable to seek novelty at the expense of readability. For example, prose should not use poetic language, and poetry should not use prose-like language. Regulated verse should not use prose-like language, and prose should not use regulated verse-like language. They are all clearly different. If they are mixed together, it is not only to lose the proper style but also difficult to understand. However, scholars are often ignorant of this, and they often mix things up, and they also criticize each other, not realizing this problem. Even some famous scholars cannot avoid this.

    Those who excel in one area must be deficient in another, and those who are better in the major aspects may be worse in the minor ones. Scholars and gentlemen in poverty cannot support their families and avoid hunger and cold. When they achieve their ambitions, then they can help the whole world, making people and things each find their proper place. For example, Jiang Ziya was poor and worked as a butcher and fisherman, and Yi Yin worked as a farmer. They could not have failed to seek wealth and profit to live a comfortable life, but they were ashamed to do so. As for Han Xin, he was a poor young man and was helped by a washerwoman, and people all laughed at him. When he became a general, he could plan and win battles without any mistakes, and he finally helped Emperor Gaozu to establish the Han dynasty, enjoying the pleasure of ruling. Is it not that he was foolish in the past and clever now? Talents have their strengths, and there are things they choose not to do. Therefore, thinking about our current situation of great changes, we hide in remote mountains and deserts, barely making ends meet, and cannot help but ask others for help, which is not surprising. We regret not being able to fish, cut wood, and farm to support ourselves like the ancients. They live in poverty, and their wives and children complain, and neighbors, lowly people, and friends all laugh at them. What is the problem with that? This is a natural thing.

    221

    国家养育人材当如养木彼楩楠豫章之材封植之防持之任其长成一旦可以为明堂太室之用如或牛羊囓之斧斤伐之则将憔悴惨淡无生姿或枯槁而死矣又安能有干霄拂云之势耶士大夫亦然国家以爵禄尊之以语言使之精神横出才气得伸鋭于有为然后得为用倘绳以文法索过求瑕为之则有议言之则有罪将括囊袖手相招为自全计矣国家何頼焉余先君尝为言如屏山之才国家能养挈提使议论天下事其智识盖人不可及惟其早年暂欲有为有言已遭摧折所以中年纵酒无功名心是可为国家惜也呜呼自非坚刚不防之志超世絶伦之人其遇忧患遭废绌而不变易者鲜矣哉

    Explanation

    221

    The state should nurture and develop talent as one would cultivate trees. Talented individuals, like the finest timber such as pine, cypress, and catalpa, should be protected and nurtured, allowing them to grow naturally. Once they have matured, they can serve important roles in society, much like the grand halls of the ancient palaces. However, if they are harmed by the likes of cattle and sheep or cut down by axes, they will wither, lose their vitality, and may even die. How then can they ever achieve a towering and impressive presence? Scholars and officials are similarly affected. The state honors them with titles and rewards, and encourages them to speak and act boldly, allowing their spirit and talent to flourish in their endeavors. Only then can they be truly useful. But if they are criticized and punished according to strict rules, seeking out faults and holding them to account, those who dare to speak out will face punishment. This will lead them to remain silent and inactive, preserving themselves from harm. What use is the state then? My late father often said that if the state could nurture and support individuals like Screen Mountain's talent, allowing them to discuss matters of the state, their wisdom and knowledge would surpass others. Yet in his early years, he wanted to achieve something and speak out but was suppressed. This is why, in his middle age, he indulged in drinking and lost his ambition for fame and success. It is a pity for the state. Alas, unless one has an unyielding and extraordinary spirit, few can remain unchanged when faced with adversity and setbacks.

    222

    曰人众亦能胜天天定亦能胜人余尝疑之诚以严冬在大厦中独立惨淡不能久居忽有人自外至共谈笑则殊暖燠盖人气胜也因是以思谓人胜天亦有此理岂特是哉深冬执爨或厚衣重衾亦不寒夏暑居髙楼以氷环坐而加之以扇亦不甚热大抵有势力者能不为造物所欺然所以有势者亦造物所使也
    　　人之生有三乐有志气之乐有形体之乐有性命之乐夫事业功名权势爵位乐志气也酒色衣食使令车马乐形体也仁义礼乐忠信孝弟乐性命也虽然事业功名权势爵位得时者之所有也酒色衣食使令车马富厚者之所备也惟仁义礼乐忠信孝弟虽不得时不富厚而于我皆具盖穷士之所有也今吾既不得时有志气之乐又不富厚有形体之乐居荒山之中日惟藜藿之为养其所享无一毫过于人舍性命其何乐哉士之生于世何其多品耶有为公卿宰辅以事业功名显于后代者有虽居下位不得柄用犹能以节义自著者又有浮沈闾里应物

    Explanation

    222

    The text says: "People can also overcome Heaven, and Heaven can also overcome people. I have often doubted this. Indeed, in a harsh winter, if one stands alone in a large building, they feel cold and cannot stay for long. But when someone comes from outside and they talk and laugh together, it suddenly feels warm. This is because human warmth overcomes it. Thus, I have thought that there is a way for people to overcome Heaven, but there is more to it than that. In deep winter, even if one is cooking or wearing thick clothes and quilts, they do not feel cold. In the summer heat, if one sits in a high-rise building with an ice ring and adds a fan, they do not feel excessively hot. Generally, those with power are not deceived by nature, but those with power are also instruments of nature.

    There are three kinds of joy in life: the joy of achieving goals, the joy of physical pleasures, and the joy of spiritual or moral fulfillment. Achievements and fame are what those who are in the right time have. Indulgences in alcohol, beauty, food, and clothing are what those who are wealthy and abundant have. Loyalty, righteousness, propriety, and music are what the poor scholar has, even in material poverty. Broad learning is beneficial in all areas of life.

    People in the world are so diverse: there are those who become high-ranking officials through their achievements and fame, there are those who, though not in high positions, uphold loyalty and righteousness, and there are those who live simple, unremarkable lives in the community."

    223

    持身但以徳善立名者有放浪山林草衣木食以髙洁自居者有抒心文史以著述吟讽有闻者又有研精技艺如阴阳医药卜筮字画绘画以名世者又有纵酒放歌拨弃礼法以乐其形体者又有抑情忘欲链身服气以觊飞升者要之各从所好且有定数亦安能一其迹耶今吾幼而苦学及于齿壮学虽粗成而未有所遇合穷居草野日惟衣食之不充将为事业功名而不可得又非居位当言且临事变可以立节义愿服链以懒惰不能放纵以拘窒不喜诸技艺皆非所専心平生以经籍文翰自娯顾后日穷达犹未可知然则独守吾残编断藁者犹未为痴计也

    Explanation

    223

    Those who establish their reputation solely through virtue and goodness include those who wander in the mountains and forests, living a simple life and considering themselves pure and noble; those who express their thoughts through literature and history, becoming known through writing and recitation; those who study and refine various skills such as divination, medicine, calligraphy, and painting, and become famous in the world; those who live a lifestyle of drinking and singing freely, discarding rituals and laws, and enjoying their bodies; and those who suppress emotions and desires, practice physical and spiritual cultivation, and aspire to ascend to heaven. In summary, everyone follows their own preferences, and there is a fixed destiny, so how could they all be made uniform? I studied hard from a young age, and by the time I reached adulthood, my learning was somewhat complete, but without encountering opportunities, I lived a life of poverty and isolation, barely having enough food and clothing, intending to achieve career and fame but unable to attain. Not being in a position to speak and facing changing circumstances, I still hoped to cultivate myself but was lazy, unable to be free but constrained, not liking various skills, and none of which were truly dedicated to. Throughout my life, I found pleasure in classical texts and literature, considering future success or failure still uncertain. Yet remaining alone with my incomplete and scattered writings is still not a foolish decision.

    224

    予生壮年其所厯多矣尝陪诸举子进取矣亦尝偕诸朋友讲学矣又尝视诸农夫耕获矣又尝同诸少年嬉逰矣又尝诣诸王公贵人干谒矣自是上为卿相行轻济之谋下为仆吏执奔走之役其于世故无所不涉今而时值乱离屏居故山之下回思向者之事扰扰胶胶于身初无少异所谓如梦觉如酒醒而不见纤毫形迹以此观之百年之内亦可以黙觉矣而独区区虑衣食之不充惧志意之不得而不能乐天知命坎止流行与万物同始终亦其学之不至也哀哉

    Explanation

    224

    I, in my prime, have experienced much. I have accompanied scholars in their pursuit of advancement, studied with friends, observed farmers plowing and harvesting, played with young people, and visited nobles and officials to seek favors. At the highest level, I have served as a minister and engaged in light and swift strategies; at the lower level, I have served as a low-ranking official and performed menial tasks. I have encountered all kinds of worldly affairs. Now, in times of chaos and separation, I live in seclusion in my hometown. Reflecting on past events, I find that my life has been troubled and entangled, with no significant difference. It is like waking from a dream or becoming sober, without seeing any trace or sign. Within a hundred years, one can also quietly realize it. But I am preoccupied with the worry of insufficient food and clothing, fearing that I will not achieve my aspirations, and cannot be content with fate, know my destiny, and flow with the current, sharing the beginning and end with all things. This is due to the lack of learning. How sad!

    225

    三国时士尚权诈其间不为风俗所移者陈实徐穉魏晋间士尚虚其间不为风俗所移者徐邈卞壸兹数人者或以道徳显或以节行闻或以智量称或以风义着立身行志卓尔不羣皆豪杰之士也
    　　余尝观道藏书见其练石服气以求长生登仙又书符呪水役使鬼神为人治病除祟且自立名字职位云主管天神而斋醮祈禳则乃能转祸为福大抵方士之术其有无谁能知又观佛书见谈天堂地狱因果轮回以为人与禽兽异且有千佛万圣异世殊刧而以持诵布施则乃生善地大抵西方之教其有无亦谁能知因思吾道天地日月明照山河草木蕃息其间君臣父子兄弟夫妇礼文粲然而治国治家焕有条理赏罚黜陟立见荣枯生死穷通互分得失其明白如此岂有惑人以不可知之事者哉而世之愚俗徒以

    Explanation

    225

    During the Three Kingdoms period, scholars valued cunning and deceit, yet there were those who remained steadfast and were not swayed by customs, such as Chen Shi and Xu Zhi. In the Wei and Jin dynasties, scholars valued the abstract and mystical, yet there were those who remained steadfast and were not swayed by customs, such as Xu Miao and Bian Ku. These several individuals were known for their morality, integrity and conduct, wisdom and capacity, or righteousness and virtue. They stood out and were unique, all being heroes and distinguished individuals.

    I have often read the Daoist canon and seen that it involves refining stones and breathing exercises to seek immortality and ascending to the heavens, as well as writing talismans and magical water to command spirits and deities, treating illnesses and removing evil spirits, and even establishing their own names and titles as overseers of heavenly gods. Through rituals and prayers, they could turn disasters into blessings. Generally, the techniques of Daoist practitioners are uncertain; who can truly know if they exist or not? I have also read Buddhist scriptures and seen that they discuss heaven and hell, karma and rebirth, believing that humans are different from beasts and that there are countless Buddhas and saints across different worlds and eras. Through recitation and giving alms, one can be reborn in a good realm. Generally, the teachings of Buddhism are uncertain; who can truly know if they exist or not? Therefore, I have thought about our own path: the heavens and earth, the sun and moon, clearly illuminating the mountains, rivers, grass, and trees, flourishing and abundant. Within this natural order, the hierarchical relationships of sovereign and minister, father and son, elder and younger brother, husband and wife, are clearly defined, and the rituals and ceremonies are orderly. Governing the state and managing the household are clearly organized, with rewards, punishments, promotions, and demotions immediately distinguishing between honor and disgrace. Life and death, prosperity and adversity, gains and losses are all clearly divided. It is so clear that there is no need to deceive people with unknowable matters. Yet, the foolish and vulgar of the world merely cling to these uncertainties.

    226

    二氏之诡诞怪异出耳目外则波靡而从之而饮食起居日在吾道中而恬不自知反以为寻常者良可叹也呜呼愚俗岂可责耶而士大夫之髙明好异者徃徃为所诱不亦悖哉举世之人日奔走经营惟以衣食为事士君子则安闲乐道不以衣食为忧举世之人所畏者饥寒患难死亡士君子则于饥寒患难死亡无所畏使道义充于中虽明日饥而死无歉于天地使行不义而动非礼虽贵于王公富积千金而内以愧于心外以怍于人然则士君子之所为所守诚举世之人所背而驰者也使俗人笑其迂而议其拙也宜哉

    Explanation

    226

    The strange and unusual doctrines of the two sects, which are beyond ordinary perception, spread like waves and are followed by the masses. In their daily lives, people are immersed in our moral principles but remain unaware and unconcerned, considering them ordinary. This is truly pitiable. How can one blame the ignorant and vulgar? Yet, scholars and officials who are sophisticated and fond of novelty are often lured by these doctrines, how perverse! All the people of the world rush around and plan, only concerned with food and clothing. Scholars and gentlemen, however, are at ease and enjoy the way, not worried about food and clothing. All the people of the world fear hunger, cold, difficulties, and death, but scholars and gentlemen have no fear of hunger, cold, difficulties, and death. If one is filled with righteousness within, even if one dies of hunger tomorrow, there would be no shame before heaven and earth. If one acts unjustly and behaves improperly, even if one is valued more than princes and has accumulated a fortune, one will feel ashamed in one's heart and be embarrassed before others. Thus, the behavior and principles of scholars and gentlemen are truly the opposite of what all the people of the world do. It is appropriate for common people to mock them as being foolish and clumsy.

    归濳志卷十二
    　　钦定四库全书
    　　归潜志卷十三
    　　元　刘祁　撰
    　　吾在南方时从父母仕宦家资颇温而吾则専心于学生事不一问食未尝不肉也寝未尝不帷也出游未尝无车马也役使未尝无僮仆也然不知温饱安逸之味也今遭防乱归故山四壁萧然日惟生事之见迫食或旬日无醯醢及一得之则觉其甘寝或终夜无衾裯及一得之则觉其暖出或徒行无驴及一得之则觉其便居或汲爨无人及一得之则觉其泰乃知夫温饱安逸者世之人亦未易得虽与向时异犹不足也惑矣因思一时富贵权势之人生长纨绮中或不遭患难摧折至老者非惟不知稼穑之艰难流于奢淫以蠧国病民抑又不知世间温饱安逸之正味为不少可胜叹哉吾故以自尝试者述之可为得志者戒

    Explanation
