    Records of a Hidden Return, Volume Twelve

    Qin Ding Si Ku Quan Shu (The Complete Library in Four Branches of Literature)

    Records of a Hidden Return, Volume Thirteen

    Yuan Dynasty, Liu Qi (刘祁) compiled

    When I was in the south, following my parents in their official careers, our family wealth was quite comfortable. Yet I focused solely on my studies and did not ask about other matters. My food never lacked meat, my sleeping never lacked curtains, my traveling never lacked carriages and horses, and my household never lacked servants and attendants. However, I did not know the taste of warmth, fullness, and ease. Now, facing turmoil, I returned to my hometown, where the four walls were empty, and daily life was pressured by necessities. Food sometimes lacked vinegar and soy sauce for ten days, and when I finally obtained them, I found them sweet. Sleeping sometimes lacked quilts and sheets all night, and when I finally obtained them, I found them warm. Traveling sometimes meant walking without a donkey, and when I finally obtained one, I found it convenient. Living sometimes meant no one to draw water or cook, and when I finally obtained help, I found it comfortable. Thus, I realized that warmth, fullness, and ease, which are common in the world, are not easily obtained. Even though they are different from what I had before, they are still insufficient, and this is perplexing. I then thought about those who grew up in luxury and power, who did not suffer from hardships and were not broken by adversity until old age. Not only did they not know the hardships of farming but also indulged in luxury and debauchery, harming the country and its people. Nor did they know the true taste of warmth, fullness, and ease in the world, which is abundant and deserves much lamentation. Therefore, I recount my own experiences to serve as a warning to those who have achieved their goals.

    228

    窃尝攷自古士风之变系国家长短存亡三代以前其风淳质修谨不必言三代以后世衰道防士大夫惟知功利为上故争尚权谋战国间游説纵横之流已而变为刑名掊克以法律控持上下失士庶心以至焚书坑儒毒流四海汉兴其风稍变多重厚长者然其权谋法律者犹相杂迨至武帝天下混同士风一变以学问为上故争尚经术文章一时如公孙董仲舒二司马枚乘之徒出文物大备元成以来经术之皆尚虚文而无事业可观浮沈委靡以茍容居位匡衡贡禹孔光之流重以謟谀故权臣肆志国随以絶东汉之初人主惩权

    Explanation

    228

    I have privately examined the changes in the moral climate of scholars throughout history and their impact on the rise and fall of states. Before the Three Dynasties, the moral climate was pure and upright, requiring no further comment. After the Three Dynasties, the world declined and the Way was obstructed, and scholars and officials only valued profit as the highest good, thus competing for the use of cunning and strategy. During the Warring States period, the itinerant strategists and diplomats were prominent, and later this evolved into the Legalist school of thought, which emphasized strict laws and harsh punishments, controlling the upper and lower ranks and losing the hearts of scholars and common people, leading to the burning of books and the burying of Confucian scholars, spreading poison throughout the land. When the Han dynasty rose, the moral climate changed somewhat, valuing weighty and honorable individuals, but the pursuit of power and strict laws still coexisted. By the time of Emperor Wu, the world was unified, and the moral climate changed again, with scholars valuing learning as the highest good, thus competing for the study of classics and literature. At that time, figures such as Gong Sun Hong, Dong Zhongshu, the two Simas, and Mei Cheng emerged, and culture and literature flourished. Since the reigns of Emperors Yuan and Cheng, the study of classics had become corrupt, favoring empty formalities without any notable achievements, floating and sinking, becoming enfeebled, and settling for mere survival in one's position. Figures such as Kuang Heng, Gong Yu, and Kong Guang were prominent, and flattery was prevalent, thus powerful ministers acted according to their own will, and the state followed in decline. In the early Eastern Han, the ruler punished power.

    229

    臣之祸以法令督责羣臣羣臣惟知守职奉法无过失及桓灵之世朝政淆乱奸臣擅权士风激厉以敢为敢言相尚故争树名节袁安杨震李固杜乔陈蕃之徒抗于朝郭泰范滂岑晊张俭之徒议于野国势虽衰而公议具存犹能使乱臣贼子有所畏忌已而诸豪割据士大夫各欲择主立功名如荀攸贾诩程昱郭嘉诸葛亮庞统鲁肃周瑜之徒争以智能自效晋初天下既一士无所事惟以谈论相髙故争尚虚王弼何晏倡于前王衍王澄和于后希髙名而无实用以至误天下国家南渡之后非有王导谢安辈稍务事业功名其頽靡亦不可救

    Explanation

    229

    The disaster of the minister stems from the strict enforcement of laws and regulations on the officials, who only know to fulfill their duties and obey the law without making mistakes. During the reigns of Emperor Huan and Emperor Ling, the court administration was chaotic with wicked ministers seizing power, and the scholars were encouraged by a风气 of daring to act and speak out, hence striving to establish a reputation for integrity. Figures like Yuan An, Yang Zhen, Li Gu, Du Qiao, and Chen Fan resisted in the court, while individuals such as Guo Tai, Fan Pang, Cen Zhi, and Zhang Jian debated in the countryside. Although the state was declining, public opinion still existed, which could make traitorous ministers and rebels fearful. Subsequently, various warlords carved out their territories, and scholars sought to choose a master under whom they could establish achievements and fame, like Xun You, Jia Xu, Cheng Yu, Guo Jia, Zhuge Liang, Pang Tong, Lu Su, and Zhou Yu, who competed to demonstrate their intelligence and abilities. In the early Western Jin Dynasty, when the empire was unified, scholars had little practical role to play, and they only engaged in discussions and debates, thus competing to value the abstract and mystical. Wang Bi and He Yan promoted this trend earlier, followed by Wang Yan and Wang Cheng, who continued it later. They sought high reputations but had no practical use, leading to the misguidance of the nation and the state. After the fall of the Jin Dynasty and the establishment of the Eastern Jin Dynasty, there were no figures like Wang Dao and Xie An who slightly engaged in the pursuit of achievements and fame, and the decadence and decline were also beyond redemption.

    230

    矣宋齐梁陈惟以文华相尚门地相夸亦不足观故国祚亦不能久唐兴士大夫复以事业功名为上贞观诸人有两汉风其权谋经术文章名节者错出间立故唐一代人材最多其扶支国势亦至三百载及其乱也死节者相望五代之间亦无可取宋初士大夫复驰骋智谋厥后混一其风大变经术文章不减汉唐名节之士继踵而出大抵崇尚学问以道义为先故维持国家亦三百载虽遭防夺尚能奄有偏方大抵天下乱则士大夫多尚权谋智术以功业为先天下治则士大夫多尚经术文章学问以名节为上国家存亡长短随之亦其势然也

    Explanation

    230

    The Southern Dynasties (Song, Qi, Liang, and Chen) valued only literary elegance and competed in family prestige, which was not worthy of admiration, and thus their dynastic rule could not last long. When the Tang Dynasty rose, scholars and officials again valued achievements and merit above all. The people of the Zhenguan era had the spirit of the Two Han dynasties; those skilled in strategy, classical learning, literary works, and moral principles emerged in succession, making the Tang Dynasty the era with the most talents, and its support for the national strength lasted for three hundred years. When the Tang Dynasty fell into chaos, those who died for their principles were numerous, and during the Five Dynasties period, there was nothing commendable. In the early Song Dynasty, scholars and officials engaged in strategic thinking, and later, the cultural and intellectual trends were integrated, with classical learning and literary works not falling short of those of the Han and Tang dynasties, and virtuous and principled individuals emerged in succession. Generally, learning was valued and moral principles were prioritized, so the Song Dynasty was able to maintain stability for three hundred years, even suffering from division and conquest, still able to dominate the peripheral regions. Generally, when the world is in chaos, scholars and officials tend to favor strategies and cunning, valuing achievements above all; when the world is well-ordered, scholars and officials tend to value classical learning and scholarship, prioritizing moral principles, and the rise and fall of the nation follow suit, it is the natural order of things.

    231

    余平生有二乐曰良友曰异书毎遇之则欣然忘寝食盖良友则从吾讲学见吾过失且笑谈游宴以忘忧异书则资吾见闻助吾辞藻属文著论以有益彼酒色膏梁如一时浮云过目竟何所得哉肥醲甘脆世所共珍使饱而遇之则食如泥土藜藿葵荠世所共贱使饥而遇之则食如饴糖乃知贫穷之士自乐富贵之人亦有苦是则我辈区区以空乏为忧者悖矣
    　　国之不可治犹可以治其家人不能正犹能正其身使家之齐而身之修虽居不仕犹可谓得志故吾尝曰虽天下未太平而吾一家独不可太平乎是诚在我者也

    Explanation

    231

    In my life, there are two joys: good friends and rare books. Whenever I encounter them, I forget sleep and food with joy. Good friends teach me and point out my mistakes, and we talk and enjoy feasts to forget our worries. Rare books enrich my knowledge and help my eloquence, and I write articles and essays that are beneficial. Those who indulge in luxurious living, such as fine wine, beautiful women, and rich food, are like fleeting clouds that pass before one's eyes—what lasting benefit do they bring? Rich, strong, sweet, and crisp things are universally cherished, but if one is already full and encounters them, they taste like mud. Humble vegetables like millet, chrysanthemum, and Chinese cabbage are universally despised, but if one is hungry and encounters them, they taste like honey. Thus, poor scholars find their own joy, while wealthy people also have their troubles. Those who worry about poverty are misguided. If the state cannot be governed, one can still govern one's family; if one cannot correct others, one can still correct oneself. By managing one's family well and cultivating oneself, even if one does not hold an official position, one can still be said to have achieved one's goals. Therefore, I often say that even if the world is not at peace, can my family not be at peace? It truly depends on me.

    232

    昔人云借书一痴还书亦一痴故世之士大夫有竒书多秘之亦有假而不归者必援此予尝鄙之以为君子惟欲淑诸人有竒书当与朋友共之何至靳藏独广已之闻见果如是量亦狭矣如蔡伯喈之秘论衡亦通人之一蔽非君子所尚不可法也其假而不归者尤可笑君子不夺人所好己所不欲勿施于人岂有假人物而不归之者耶因改曰有书不借为一痴借书不还又一痴也
    　　夫诗者本发其喜怒哀乐之情如使人读之无所感动非诗也予观后世诗人之诗皆穷极辞藻牵引学问诚美矣然读之不能动人则亦何贵哉故尝与亡友王飞伯言唐以前诗在诗至宋则多在长短句今之诗在俗间俚曲也如所谓源土令之飞伯曰何以知云予曰古人歌诗皆发其心所欲言使人诵之至有泣下者今人之诗惟泥题目事实句法将以新巧取声名虽得人口称而动人心者絶少不若俗谣俚曲之见其真情而反能荡人血气也飞伯以为然

    Explanation

    232

    The ancients said that lending a book is foolish, and returning a book is also foolish. Therefore, in the world, scholars and officials often keep rare books secret, and some borrow them but do not return them. I have always looked down on this, believing that a gentleman desires only to benefit others. If one has rare books, they should share them with friends; why hoard them to expand one's own knowledge alone? If one truly acts in such a way, their capacity is narrow. Even Cai Bojie's secret Lunheng is a blind spot of a learned person, not something a gentleman should aspire to or follow. Those who borrow books but do not return them are particularly laughable. A gentleman does not take away what others enjoy, and if one does not want something done to oneself, one should not do it to others. How can there be someone who borrows books from others and does not return them? Therefore, I say that not lending books is one kind of foolishness, and not returning borrowed books is another kind of foolishness.

    As for poetry, by its nature, it expresses joy, anger, sorrow, and pleasure. If reading it does not move the reader, it is not poetry. I observe that the poetry of later poets exhaustively uses elaborate language and draws on learning, which is indeed beautiful. However, if it cannot move the heart, what value does it have? I once discussed this with my deceased friend Wang Feibo. He said that poetry before the Tang dynasty was in the form of poetry, but by the Song dynasty, it was mostly in the form of ci poetry. Today's poetry is often found in popular folk songs and ballads, such as the so-called Yuantu genre. Wang Feibo asked how I knew this. I replied that ancient people's songs and poems expressed what they wanted to say from their hearts, and when others recited them, they sometimes wept. Today's poetry, however, is obsessed with adhering to titles, facts, and sentence structures, aiming for novelty and cleverness to gain fame. Although it may be praised by others, it rarely moves the heart. It is not as good as folk songs and ballads, which reveal true feelings and can even stir one's emotions. Wang Feibo agreed with me.

    233

    六经中莫难穷者易莫难断者春秋故予三十而学春秋以其壮而立志也四十而学易以长而多练事也余祖沂水君尝训子孙曰士之立身如素丝然慎不可使防汚少防汚则不得为完人矣屏山称之以为名言其作墓表也亦备载云
    　　老子之书孔子尝见之矣而未尝论其是非孟子亦尝见之矣而未尝言若庄子与孟子同时其名不容有不相知而亦未尝有一言相及而孟子所排者杨墨仪秦庄子所论者孔顔鲁史至于子始论老庄得失韩子则盛排之何哉夫老庄之书孔孟不言其偶然耶其有深意耶韩排之其得圣人微意耶其与圣人异见耶文中子一世纯儒其

    Explanation

    233

    Among the Six Classics, the I Ching (Book of Changes) is the most difficult to exhaust, and the Spring and Autumn Annals is the most difficult to interpret. Therefore, at thirty, I began studying the Spring and Autumn Annals because I was in my prime and had set my aspirations. At forty, I began studying the I Ching because I was older and had more experience in practical matters. My ancestor, Mr. Yishui, once taught his descendants: "A scholar establishes himself like a white thread; one must be careful not to let it become stained. If it becomes stained early on, then one cannot be a complete person." Screen Mountain praised this as a famous saying, and when he wrote the epitaph, he also included it.

    The Tao Te Ching (Dao De Jing) of Laozi, Confucius once saw it but never commented on its right or wrong. Mencius also once saw it but never commented. Zhuangzi and Mencius were contemporaries; their names could not have been unknown to each other, but they never mentioned each other. What Mencius criticized were Yangism, Mohism, and the strategies of the states of Qin and Wei, while what Zhuangzi discussed were Confucius, Yan Hui, and the history of Lu. Until Yang Xiong, he began to discuss the merits and faults of Laozi and Zhuangzi, and Han Feizi strongly criticized them. Why did Confucius and Mencius not comment on the books of Laozi and Zhuangzi? Was it by chance, or was there a deeper meaning? Why did Yang Xiong and Han Feizi criticize them? Did they grasp the subtle meaning of the sages, or did they have different views from the sages? Wen Zhongzi was a pure Confucian scholar of his time.

    234

    著述动作全法圣人虽未能造其域亦可谓贤而有志者遗书在世韩子亦不容不见之而未尝比数于荀子之列其意以为无足取耶其偶然耶至李翺则比诸世所太公家教以为无辞而粗有理亦轻之矣司马君实则论其失而取其长为有补传而程伊川则以为其议论尽髙有荀道不到处诸公皆名世大儒而异同如此皆学者所当深究也
    　　司马君实作文中子补怪隋书不为文中子立传而其子弟云凝为御史尝弹侯君集君集与长孙无忌善以此王氏不得用其修隋史者乃陈叔达魏征畏无忌故不为立传君子曰叔达固畏无忌征岂以畏无忌故掩其师名耶以是为疑余尝思使徴辈诚文中子门人其不为立传亦自有深意将非以拟师为圣人欲列于恐小之欲援孔子世家之例而隋书无他世家且恐时人议皆不纪以为其师之名不待史而乎如此然未可知也

    Explanation

    234

    In writing and action, completely emulating the sages, though they did not reach the realm of the sages, they can also be called virtuous and ambitious. Their writings remain in the world, and Han Feizi cannot be unseen, yet he has never been ranked alongside Xunzi. Is it because they are not worthy of consideration, or is it by chance? Li Ao, on the other hand, compares him to the Taigong's Teachings, deeming it somewhat reasonable but belittling it. Sima Guang discusses his shortcomings while taking his strengths, finding some benefit in transmission. Cheng Yi, however, believes that his arguments are all highly sophisticated, with places where they go beyond those of Xunzi and Yang Xiong. All are great scholars of the age, and the differences and similarities are like this; all are matters that scholars should deeply investigate.

    Sima Guang wrote a supplement to the biography of Wen Zhongzi, wondering why the Sui Shu does not have a biography of Wen Zhongzi. His descendants, Yun, served as a censor and once criticized Hou Junji, who was close to Changsun Wuji. Therefore, the Wang clan could not use Tchen Shuda and Wei Zheng to write a biography, fearing Changsun Wuji. A gentleman said that Tchen Shuda indeed feared Changsun Wuji, but did Wei Zheng also fear Changsun Wuji, thus concealing the name of his teacher? This is a matter of doubt. I have often thought that if Wei Zheng and others were truly disciples of Wen Zhongzi, their not writing a biography also had its own deep meaning. Perhaps they did not want to equate their teacher with the sages, fearing it would diminish him, or they wanted to follow the example of the biography of Confucius, but the Sui Shu had no other biographies, and they feared contemporary criticism, so they did not record it, believing that the name of their teacher did not need to be transmitted through history. This, however, is not known.

    235

    余读书至汤誓汤诰及泰誓牧誓观汤武伐桀纣之际谕众诲师无不以天为言如曰夏氏有罪予畏上帝尔尚辅予一人致天之罚天道福善祸淫降灾于夏肆台小子将天命明威不敢赦上天孚佑下民罪人黜伏俾予一人辑寜尔家今商王受弗敬上天降灾下民皇天震怒命我文考肃将天威商罪贯盈天命诛之予弗顺天厥罪惟钧惟天惠民惟辟奉天天其以予乂民戎商必克今商王受自絶于天结怨于民尔其孜孜奉予一人恭行天罚今予发惟恭行
    天之罚大抵以桀纣为恶逆天天絶之我则诛恶救民为顺天且若阴受上天之命而行者嗟乎圣人之心则天心也天之心则圣人心也天之所絶圣人则絶之天之所与圣人则与之初无一毫异有以见圣人以天自处也非徒以天自处其理诚一也故当时为圣人者权其轻重计其公私而不暇顾其君臣之分彼桀纣所行诚顺天耶吾则事之诚逆天耶吾则去之其事其去皆与天合既去彼而求其为天下主者舍己其谁哉故践位而伐之不辞而天下翕然亦无

    Explanation

    235

    As I read through the Shangshu chapters Tang Shì, Tang Gào, Tài Shì, and Mù Shì, observing the accounts of Tang and Wu's campaigns against Jie and Zhou, I noted that in instructing the masses and teaching the soldiers, all spoke of heaven. For example, it was said: "The Xia dynasty has committed crimes; I fear the Supreme Deity. You should assist me, the one person, to bring down the punishment of heaven. The way of heaven rewards virtue and punishes excess; it brings disaster upon the Xia. Thus, I, the young and humble one, will carry out the clear power of heaven's mandate and dare not pardon. The Supreme Deity faithfully protects the people below; the guilty are humbled and subdued, that I, the one person, may bring peace to your homes."

    Now, the Shang king Shou does not revere the Supreme Deity; he brings disaster upon the people. The Supreme Deity is greatly angered and commands my father, the virtuous, to solemnly carry out the power of heaven. The crimes of the Shang have reached their limit; heaven's mandate calls for their punishment. I do not follow heaven; their crimes are equal. Only heaven benefits the people, and only the ruler serves heaven. May heaven use me to govern the people; the Shang must surely be defeated. Now, the Shang king Shou has cut himself off from heaven and bound himself in enmity with the people. You must diligently serve me, the one person, and carry out the punishment of heaven with reverence. Now, I, Fa, will carry out with reverence the punishment of heaven.

    In general, it is seen that Jie and Zhou acted wickedly and were cut off by heaven; I, on the other hand, punish evil and save the people, which is in accordance with heaven. It is as if I were secretly receiving heaven's mandate and carrying it out. Ah, the heart of a sage is the heart of heaven; the heart of heaven is the heart of a sage. What heaven cuts off, a sage cuts off; what heaven bestows, a sage bestows. There is no difference between the two. This shows that a sage places himself under heaven, not just to place oneself under heaven, but because the principle is truly one. Thus, at that time, the sage considered the weight and the public/private aspects without having time to consider the distinction between ruler and subject. Did they truly follow heaven? Did I truly act against heaven? Their actions and departures were all in harmony with heaven. Having left them, to seek one who would be the ruler of the world, if not me, who else? Thus, taking the position and attacking them without hesitation, the world unites and there is none.

    236

    异议要之所行者天也又岂有歉然于心耶其曰惟有慙徳予恐来世以为口实者惧后之人臣不知天理妄干天位者援以为例耳亦惧后学之士求其名而遗其实者耳岂真有慙徳耶然则后之君子犹以臣伐君为疑者陋矣彼汤武之心求知于天而不求知于人者可见矣或者曰然则莽操之取汉司马氏之取魏若以天为言亦可乎曰不然彼汉魏之政如桀纣乎莽操司马氏之法如汤武乎有汤武之圣遇桀纣之恶然后可以言受天命不然则徒为篡逆而已
    　　吾道盛衰自有时吾尝攷之如循环相乗除也周衰诸侯不礼士至战国则魏文侯燕昭王辈拥篲筑台师事焉继以始皇坑儒之祸汉兴藩侯不礼士而光武则安车蒲轮征聘焉继有桓灵党锢之事唐朝士大夫徃徃为将相有势位后有白马之灾宋兴内外大小皆儒者显荣至宣政极矣至于金国士气遂不振而今日困顿摧頽亦何足怪但我辈适当此运者为不幸耳虽然穷达一也又何叹也

    Explanation

    236

    The important points of contention are determined by Heaven; how could one feel a sense of inadequacy in one's heart? To say that one has only a sense of shame, I fear that future generations might use this as a pretext for criticism. I also fear that those who, in the future, act without understanding the principles of Heaven and rashly attempt to usurp the position of Heaven, might use this as an example. I am also concerned that scholars of the future might seek its name but neglect its substance. Is it truly a matter of shame? Therefore, those later scholars who still doubt the legitimacy of a minister overthrowing his ruler are lacking in insight. The intentions of King Tang and King Wu were to seek knowledge from Heaven rather than from people, and this is evident. Someone might ask, "Then, can the actions of Wang Mang and Cao Cao in seizing the Han dynasty, and the Sima clan in seizing the Wei dynasty, also be justified by saying they received the mandate of Heaven?" I would say no; was the governance of the Han and Wei dynasties like that of the tyrannical rulers Jie and Zhou? Were the methods of Wang Mang, Cao Cao, and the Sima clan like those of King Tang and King Wu? Only when one possesses the virtue of King Tang and King Wu and encounters the wickedness of Jie and Zhou can one speak of receiving the mandate of Heaven. Otherwise, it is nothing more than usurpation and rebellion.

    The rise and fall of my way (Dao) has its own timing. I have observed that it is like a cycle of multiplication and division. During the decline of the Zhou dynasty, the feudal lords did not respect scholars. By the time of the Warring States period, rulers like Hui of Wei and Zhao of Yan swept the path for scholars and built platforms to honor them. This was followed by the disaster of Emperor Qin Shi Huang burning books and burying scholars. When the Han dynasty rose, the feudal lords again did not respect scholars, but Emperor Guangwu of Han used a special carriage with soft wheels to invite scholars, showing great respect. This was followed by the political purges during the reigns of Emperors Huan and Ling. In the Tang dynasty, scholars often became high-ranking officials, but this was followed by the White Horse Tragedy. In the Song dynasty, both inside and outside the court, scholars were honored and prominent, reaching their peak during the reigns of Emperor Huizong and Emperor Qinzong. By the time of the Jin dynasty, the spirit of the scholars had declined, and today we are in a state of decline and disarray. This is not surprising, but those of us who live in this era are unfortunate. Though poverty and prosperity are one and the same, what is there to lament?

    237

    贤人君子得志可以养天下如不得志天下当共养之分人以财有时而尽分人以善百世不磨
    　　凡将迎交接之际礼貎语言过则为谄为曲不及则为亢为疎所以贵乎得中也如或失中与其谄也宁亢与其曲也宁疎
    　　张平章万公弥学座右铭有云欲求子孙先当积孝欲求聪明先当积学此至言也
    　　为善而遇灾屯困窘者命也非分也为恶而遇灾屯困窘者分也非命也为善而得富贵亨达者分也非命也能辨之夫欲心不死道心不生若欲安时任命著书立言发前人所未见成后世之大名惟忘富贵利达外物可也
    　　寜使敬而疎毋使狎而亲人敬而疎不失为端士人狎而亲恐流而为小人独不见氷雪与脂韦乎其所喻可知
    　　厚于道味者必薄于世味厚于世味者必薄于道味士君子茍不为世味所诱何名之不成何节之不立哉士大夫多为富贵壊了名节吾尝为栁子厚元微之之徒惜也却死亡贫贱便做出好公事来不然终不能有所立

    Explanation

    237

    Virtuous and capable individuals, when in power, can nurture and govern the world; when they are not in power, the world should collectively support them. Sharing material wealth has its limits, but sharing goodness endures for a hundred generations.

    In all interactions, whether greeting or exchanging words, if one is overly polite, it becomes flattery and deceit; if one is insufficiently polite, it becomes arrogance and aloofness. Therefore, it is precious to find the middle way. If one fails to find the middle way, it is better to be arrogant than to be flattery, and better to be aloof than to be deceitful.

    Wan Gong Mi, the Right Chancellor, had a motto inscribed on his desk: "To seek descendants, one must first accumulate filial piety; to seek wisdom, one must first accumulate learning." This is profound wisdom.

    Those who do good and encounter misfortune are fated, not due to their actions; those who do evil and encounter misfortune are due to their actions, not fate. Those who do good and attain wealth and honor are due to their actions, not fate. One can distinguish between fate and due. If the desire for material gain does not die, the heart of the Way will not arise. If one wishes to accept one's fate and fulfill one's destiny, write books and make statements, revealing what was unseen by predecessors and achieving great fame for future generations, one must forget wealth, honor, and material possessions.

    It is better to be respectful but distant than intimate but close. Being respectful but distant does not lose one's dignity; being intimate but close may lead to becoming a petty person. Have you not seen the contrast between ice and snow and fat? The meaning is clear.

    Those who prioritize spiritual values will find worldly pleasures less satisfying; those who prioritize worldly pleasures will find spiritual values less satisfying. Gentlemen, if not tempted by worldly pleasures, can achieve greatness. How can one not achieve a name or establish a reputation? Many scholars and officials have ruined their names and integrity for wealth and honor. I have often lamented for Liu Zongyuan and Yuan Zhen. If one avoids death, poverty, and low status, good deeds can be accomplished; otherwise, one cannot achieve anything significant.

    238

    富贵爵禄世人所共嗜故忘身屈节而徇之惟君子视之为外物得失付自然茍与世人同安得为君子求合于圣贤必不合于世俗必欲与世俗合则于圣贤之道逺矣同于古必不同于今茍欲富贵与道义兼宁有是理是则忖己之所趋向嗜好又何愠乎贫贱哉以此自思便安
    　　士君子得志可以济天下不得志不能活一身故子思居卫緼袍无里荣公七十带索无依近世陈无巳妻子常寄妇翁家诚不肯非义而取也
    　　马援书诫兄子使之效龙伯髙无效杜季良所为则善矣虽然杜季良仇人讼书引援诫为证竟免官而梁松窦固因之被难梁松由是恨援死后搆陷至妻子不敢归葬若是则彼时戒子侄好论议人长短而不知先以此陷于祸也悲夫
    　　保养乎身勿以夀夭委之天勤俭乎家勿以有无付之命强勉乎政勿以否泰归诸时忠爱乎君勿以昏明托诸上此所谓先尽人事后言天道先尽其在己者在人者初不计也定心之法莫善于此

    Explanation

    238

    Wealth and noble rank are what the world commonly desires, hence people forget themselves and compromise their principles to pursue them. Only a gentleman regards them as external things, leaving gains and losses to nature. If one conforms to the world's desires, how can one be a gentleman? To seek harmony with sages and virtuous men necessarily means not conforming to the world; if one necessarily conforms to the world, then one is far from the path of sages and virtuous men. To be in agreement with the ancients necessarily means being different from the present. If one desires wealth and moral integrity simultaneously, is there such a thing? Therefore, considering one's own inclinations and preferences, why should one be angry about poverty and low status? Thinking about this and finding peace, one will be content.

    A gentleman with ambitions can save the world; without ambitions, one cannot even sustain oneself. Thus, Zisi lived in Wei state in a thin robe, and Rong Gongsun, at seventy, lived in a state of poverty. In recent times, Chen Wusi's wife and children often stayed with his mother-in-law's family. Truly, he would not take what is unjust. Ma Yuan wrote a letter to advise his nephew, instructing him to emulate Long Bao Gao and not to imitate Du Jiliang. If one follows this, it is good. However, Du Jiliang's enemies cited Ma Yuan's letter as evidence, leading to his dismissal. Liang Song and Dou Gu were implicated in a scandal, leading to their downfall. Liang Song resented Ma Yuan posthumously, fabricating charges against his family, preventing them from returning to bury him. Thus, at that time, Ma Yuan warned his nieces and nephews about discussing others' faults without realizing that this would lead to their downfall. Alas!

    To take care of oneself, do not leave life and death to fate; to be frugal and diligent in managing one's household, do not leave wealth and poverty to fate. To be diligent in governance, do not attribute success or failure to the times; to be loyal and loving to one's ruler, do not leave the clarity or obscurity of governance to the ruler. This is what is meant by first doing one's best and then speaking of fate, first doing one's best in what is within one's control and not initially considering what is outside one's control. The best way to calm the mind is through this approach.

    239

    凡事寜失之缓无失之急宁失之不及无失之过急者古人以为病前辈有云优柔和缓又云天下事孰不因忙里错了曷尝令君缓不及事宜深思之

    　　归潜志卷十三
    　　钦定四库全书
    　　归潜志卷十四
    　　元　刘祁　撰
    　　归潜堂记
    　　刘子朔方人生于云中之浑源山水之间髫龄从父祖仕宦大河之南初知诵读偶属为童子学少长习时文为科举计然亦时时阅古今词章窃读史书览古今成败治乱慨然有功名心未冠计偕试封礼部中之及廷而绌于是始大发愤以著述自力颇为先达诸公所知又结交当世豪杰未有不与以文字徃还者旧有田淮水之阳春夏在陈视耕获秋冬必入汴避乱且从诸公讲学已而先大夫下世遂经纪家事然读书为文未尝少休间四方交防来把酒论文谈笑连日夕或留之旬月不令去时虽少年未遂其进取心而防友著书亦自乐无歉岂知一旦时移事变流离兵革中生资荡然僮仆散尽从行惟骨

    Explanation

    239

    In all matters, it is better to err on the side of slowness than to rush and make mistakes, and it is better to fail to act than to act with excessive urgency, which the ancients considered a flaw. As前辈有云优柔和缓, it is said that a gentle and relaxed approach is preferable. And as the saying goes, in the world, who has not made mistakes due to haste? How often have I told you to think deeply about matters that require careful consideration?

    Volume Thirteen of Return to Seclusion Records
    Qinding Siku Quanshu
    Volume Fourteen of Return to Seclusion Records
    By Liu Qi of the Yuan dynasty

    Record of the Return to Seclusion Hall
    Liu Zi, a native of Shuofang, was born in the Huyuan mountains and waters of Yunzhong. From a young age, he followed his father and grandfather in their official duties in the south of the Yellow River. He began to learn to read and write, and occasionally attended school as a young scholar. As he grew older, he studied the prose of his time in preparation for the imperial examinations, but also frequently read ancient and modern literary works, secretly reading historical books and reflecting on the successes and failures of past dynasties. He felt a strong desire for fame and fortune, and before he had reached adulthood, he accompanied his peers to take the provincial examinations, passing the test of the Ministry of Rites, but failing the final imperial examination. At this point, he began to devote himself earnestly to writing, and was recognized by many esteemed scholars of the time. He also formed friendships with contemporary heroes, and none of them failed to exchange letters and writings with him. He once owned land on the north bank of the Huai River, where he would spend the summer and autumn seasons overseeing farming and harvests, and in the winter and spring, he would go to Bian to avoid chaos and to study with these scholars. After his father passed away, he took charge of managing the family affairs, but he never stopped reading and writing. Occasionally, friends from all directions would visit, and they would drink wine, discuss literature, and laugh together day and night. Sometimes they would stay for months, and he would not let them leave. At that time, although he was still young and had not yet achieved his ambitions, he found joy in his friends' writings and felt no regret. How could he have known that one day, circumstances would change, and he would be displaced by war, losing all his resources, and his servants would scatter. The only ones who accompanied him were his bones.

    Translation Explanation:

    1. Idiomatic Expressions:

      • "凡事寜失之缓无失之急宁失之不及无失之过急者古人以为病" is translated to emphasize the importance of patience and avoiding haste, as the ancients considered excessive urgency a flaw.
      • "优柔和缓" is rendered as "a gentle and relaxed approach," capturing the cultural value of calmness and moderation.
      • "天下事孰不因忙里错了" is translated to highlight the common human tendency to make mistakes when rushing.
      • "曷尝令君缓不及事宜深思之" is a rhetorical question emphasizing the need for thoughtful deliberation.

    2. Cultural and Historical Allusions:

      • The references to Return to Seclusion Records, Qinding Siku Quanshu, and Liu Qi are preserved as they are proper nouns.
      • The historical context of Liu Qi's life, including his early education, imperial examinations, and family responsibilities, is maintained to reflect the cultural and social setting of the text.

    3. Syntactic Ambiguities:

      • The complex sentences and idioms are broken down into clear, readable English while preserving their original meaning and structure.
      • The rhetorical questions and philosophical statements are translated to convey their intent and tone.

    4. Proper Nouns:

      • Names and titles such as "刘子朔方人," "归潜志卷十三," "钦定四库全书," and "归潜堂记" are rendered consistently throughout the text to ensure clarity and accuracy.

    This translation aims to balance fidelity to the original text with natural and accessible English, ensuring that the cultural and historical nuances are preserved while making the text accessible to modern readers.

    240

    肉数口旧书一囊由铜壶过燕山入武川几一载始得还乡里乡帅髙侯为筑室以居所居盖其故宅之阯四面皆见山若南山西岩吾祖旧游东为柏山代北名刹西则玉泉龙山山西胜处故朝岚夕霭千万状其云烟吞吐变化户间门前流水数支毎静夜微风有声琅琅使人清不寐刘子毎居室中焚香一炷置笔砚楮墨几上书数卷偃息啸歌起望山光寻味道腴为终日乐虽敝衣恶食不知也闲尝自念生而为儒忝学圣人之道其平昔所志修身治国平天下穷理尽性至于命进则以斯道济当时退则以斯道觉后世今当壮嵗遭此大变更頼先人之灵得返乡里幸而有居以自容将黙卷静学以休息其心力况

    Explanation

    240

    Several pieces of meat and an old book bag, I traveled from a copper pot, passing through Yan Mountain into Wu River. After nearly a year, I finally returned to my hometown. The local commander, Gao Hou, built a house for me to live in. The house is built on the site of my former home, surrounded by mountains on all sides. To the west is the cliff of Nan Mountain, where my ancestors used to visit. To the east is Baishan, a famous temple in the northern region. To the west is Yushui Longshan, a beautiful place in Shanxi. The morning mist and evening haze take countless forms, with clouds and smoke swirling and changing in the windows. Several streams flow in front of the door. Every quiet night, a gentle breeze makes a clear, ringing sound, making one feel clear and unable to sleep. Liu Zǐ often burns incense in the room, placing a brush, inkstone, paper, and ink on the table, reading several scrolls, lying down, singing, and looking at the mountain light, seeking the essence and richness as daily joy, even in ragged clothes and poor food, unaware. Occasionally, I think about being born as a scholar and feeling ashamed to study the ways of the sages, what I have always aspired to is to cultivate oneself, govern the state, and pacify the world, to exhaust understanding, fully express one's nature, and reach the ultimate, to advance by using this way to help the present era, to retreat by using this way to enlighten future generations. Now, in my prime, facing great changes, I rely on the spirit of my ancestors to return to my hometown, fortunately, I have a place to reside, I will quietly study and rest my mind and strength.

    241

    世路方艰未可为进取谋因榜其堂曰归潜且以张横渠东西二铭书诸壁客有过而诘之曰今吾子生当乱世政英雄奋发之秋大而可以分疆据土奉王命为诸侯下而可以附雄藩剧镇驰骋才谋取富贵或如终童请长缨入越羁其王致北阙下以功名著不然当蘓季子司马长卿以文词谈説于人主六印驷马耀乡俗吾子奚独韬光晦迹甘为弃物于一时使平日所学不见锋焰亦鄙陋之甚也刘子曰嘻若亦不闻君子之道乎盖君子之道以时卷舒得其时而不进为固失其时而强进为狂且先顾其内之所有何如亦不在夫外也吾平生苦学岂将徒老焉顾自鬻自求贤者所耻加之新罹蹇难始欲自修且

    Explanation

    241

    The path of the world is fraught with difficulties, not a time for planning advancement. Therefore, he posted a sign on his hall saying "Return to Seclusion," and also wrote the two inscriptions of Zhang Hengqu from east and west on the walls. A guest passed by and questioned him, saying, "Now that you are born in a time of chaos, it is the season for heroes to rise and strive. On a large scale, you can divide territories and hold land under the king's command as a feudal lord; on a smaller scale, you can attach yourself to powerful regional lords and display your talents to gain wealth and honor. Or like Zhong Tong, who requested a long rope to capture the king of Yue and bring him to the northern palace, thus establishing his fame through merit. Otherwise, you can emulate Su Qin and Sima Xiangru, who gained fame through eloquent speech and six seals and four horses, dazzling the local customs. Why do you alone conceal your talents and hide your tracks, content to be a discarded object for a time? If your daily studies do not show any brilliance, it is extremely vulgar."

    Liu Zi said, "Hmph, do you not know the way of the gentleman? The way of the gentleman is to roll up or unroll according to the times. Not advancing when the time is right is stubborn, and forcing advancement when the time is wrong is reckless. Moreover, first consider what is inside yourself; it does not lie in external things. I have suffered through a lifetime of study, not to grow old in vain. But to sell oneself for gain is a disgrace to the wise. Moreover, having recently encountered misfortune, I now wish to cultivate myself."

    242

    将扫除吾先祖丘墓果其后日为时所用亦安肯不致吾君泽吾民如或不然虽终身潜可也易曰龙徳而遯世无闷传曰君子若鳯治则见乱则吾虽非圣贤亦安敢不学乎若非知吾之志者也客既去遂书于堂以记之且歌曰南山漠漠兮浑水洋洋桂椒葱蔚兮松柏青苍清泉涌其下兮白石皦以如霜兕豹跧伏兮鸾鳯翩其来翔世溷浊而不照兮蹇驰骋夫先路荆榛蓊以防达兮野从横其豺虎矧余志之夐迂兮【阙】罕【阙】而畴伍归欤其潜于南山之下又歌曰潜于农挚之侣兮潜于渔望之徒兮顾惟不肖岂敢与俱兮惟兹一堂有琴有书兮学其所不知求进于圣途兮潜乎潜乎亦可以为娱兮嘻

    Explanation

    242

    I will sweep and clear my ancestors' graves. If indeed I am used by the times in the future, how could I not benefit my ruler and bless my people? If not, even if I remain hidden all my life, it is acceptable. The Yi says: "The dragon's virtue is to hide and retreat; the world is without worry." The Zhuangzi says: "A gentleman is like a phoenix, appearing in times of order and hiding in times of chaos." Although I am not a sage or a virtuous person, how dare I not learn? If they do not understand my aspirations, after the guest left, I wrote this on the hall to record it. And I sang:

    The South Mountain is vast and the turbid water flows, the cassia and cinnamon are lush, the pines and cypresses are verdant. The clear spring gushes below, the white stones shine like frost. The rhinoceros and leopard crouch and hide, the phoenix and crane gracefully fly. The world is turbid and does not shine, I am hindered in leading the way. The thorny bushes block the path, the wild animals roam. How much more so with my distant and lofty aspirations, return to me, to hide in the shade of the South Mountain.

    Return to me, to hide with the farmers and herders, hide with the fishermen and hunters. Considering myself unworthy, how dare I join them? Only this hall has a zither and books, learn what I do not know, seek progress on the path of sages. Hide, hide, it can also be a form of enjoyment.

    243

    麻信之游龙山记【案此首以后系祁附録他人所作】
    　　余生中条王官五老之下长侍先人西观太华迤东防洛因避地家焉如女几乌权白马诸峯固已厌登饱经穷极幽深矣革代以来自雁门逾代岭之北风壤陡异多山而阻色徃徃如死灰草木亦无容尝切慨叹南北之分何限此一领地脉遽断絶不相属如是耶越既留滞居延吾友浑源刘京叔尝以诗来盛称其乡泉石林麓之胜浑源实居代北余始而疑之虽然吾友著书立言蕲信于天下后世者必非夸言之也独恨未尝一游焉今年夏因赴试武川归道浑水修谒于玉峯先生魏公公野服萧然见余于前轩语未周浃骤及是诸山若南山若

    Explanation

    243

    Translation:

    Record of Ma Xinzhi's Journey to Long Mountain [Note: This section and those following are appended by Qi, recording works by others.]

    I was born in the shadow of the Five Elders of Wangguan in the Zhongtiao Mountains, serving my father as we traveled west to view Mount Hua and then eastward along the Luo River. We eventually settled in Luoyang to escape political turmoil. Having explored the peaks of Nüji, Wukuan, and the White Horse Mountains, I had grown weary of climbing and exploring their deepest recesses. Since the change of dynasties, traveling north from Yanmen Pass over the Dai Mountains, the climate and soil suddenly became harsh and rugged, with the scenery often appearing bleak and desolate, and the grass and trees struggling to survive. I often lamented the division between north and south, wondering how such a vast expanse of land could be so abruptly severed and disconnected. After staying in Ju Yan, my friend Liu Jingshu from Hunyuan sent me a poem highly praising the beauty of the springs, rocks, forests, and hills of his hometown. Hunyuan is indeed located in the north of Dai, and I initially doubted his claims. However, since my friend is a scholar whose writings aim to be trusted by future generations, his words must be true. What I regret is that I have never visited the place myself. This summer, on my way to take the exam in Wuchuan, I passed through Hunyuan and paid my respects to Mr. Wei, the Jade Peak Master. He appeared before me in simple, rustic attire, and as we spoke, he quickly mentioned the various mountains in the region, such as the Southern Mountains and others.

    244

    柏山业已防矣惟龙山为絶胜姑缺兹以须诸文士同之子幸来殊可喜乃选日为具且拉诸宾友骑自治城西南行十余里抵山下山无乍入谷来有竒沿溪曲折行数里草木渐秀润山竦出崭然露芒角水声锵然鸣两峯间心始异之又盘山行十许里四山忽合若拱而提环而卫者嘉木竒莽被之葱蒨醲郁风自木杪起纷披震荡山与木若相顾而坠者使人神骇目又行数里得泉之澄渟滀者焉洑出石罅激而为迅流者焉阴木荫其颠幽草缭其趾宾欲休咸曰莫此地为宜即下马披草踞石列坐诸生瀹觞以进酒数行客有指其西大石曰此可

    Explanation

    244

    Mount Bai has already been defended, but Dragon Mountain is absolutely superior. For now, we will leave this place for the scholars to enjoy together. It is very delightful that you have come. We will choose a day to prepare and invite friends and guests to ride, traveling southwest of the city for more than ten miles to reach the foot of the mountain. The mountain has no prominent features, but suddenly entering the valley reveals something remarkable. Following the stream for several miles, winding and twisting, the grass and trees gradually become lush and moist. The mountain rises abruptly, revealing sharp peaks, and the sound of water resounds between the two peaks. The heart begins to marvel at it. Then circling the mountain for about ten miles, suddenly, the four mountains converge as if they are supporting and encircling. Beautiful trees and strange plants cover it, lush and dense. Wind rises from the tips of the trees, causing them to sway and shake, and the mountain and trees seem to look at each other and fall. This makes the mind amazed and the eyes dazzled. After traveling several more miles, a clear and still pool of water is found. Water emerges from a crevice in the rock and becomes a rapid stream. Shady trees cover the top, and dark grass surrounds the base. The guests want to rest and all say that this place is the best. They immediately dismount, clear the grass, sit on stones, and the students prepare and serve wine. A few rounds of drinking are served. A guest points to a large stone on the west and says, "This is suitable."

    245

    识因命余余乃提笔书凡游者名氏及游之嵗月而去又行十许里大抵一峯一盘一溪一曲山势益竒峭树林益多杉桧栝柏而无他凡木也溪花种种金间玉错芬香入鼻幽逺可爱木萝松鬛罥人衣防又萦纡行数里得冈之髙遽涉而上马力殆不能胜行茂林下又五里两岭若岐中得浮屠氏之居曰大云寺有僧数辈来迎延入馆于寺之东轩林峦树石栉比楯立皆在几席之下憩过午谒主僧英公相与步西岭过文殊岩岩前长杉数本挺立有磴悬焉下瞰无底之壑危峯怪石巑岏巧鬭试一临之毛骨森竖南望五台诸峯若相聨络无间断西北而

    Explanation

    245

    识因命令我，我于是提笔写下所有旅行者的姓名和年龄，以及旅行的年份，然后离开。又前行了大约十里路，大体上是一峰一盘，一溪一曲，山势越来越奇特陡峭，树林也越来越多，全是杉树、桧树、栝树和柏树，没有其他种类的树木。溪边的花儿种类繁多，金黄与碧玉般的色彩交错，香气扑鼻，幽远而可爱。木萝和松树的枝条缠绕着衣襟，又蜿蜒前行了几里路，到达了一座高冈，急忙涉水上山，马几乎无法跟上。行走在茂密的森林下，又走了五里路，两座山岭像岔路一样，中间有一座佛教徒的居所，名叫大云寺。有几位僧人前来迎接，邀请我住进寺庙东边的轩室。林峦、树木和岩石整齐地排列着，仿佛都在几席之下。休息到午后，拜访了主持僧英公，一起步行上西岭，经过了文殊岩。岩前有几棵挺立的杉树，有石阶悬挂在旁边，向下俯瞰是一片无底的山谷，危险的山峰和奇怪的岩石相互争奇斗艳。试着登上岩顶，毛骨悚然，向南望去，五台山的诸峰仿佛相连不断，向西北延伸而去。

    246

    望峯豁而川明村墟井邑约微茫如弈局然徜徉者久之夤缘入西方丈观故侯同知运使雷君诗石及京叔诸人留题回乃径北岭登萱坡坡盖龙山絶顶也岭势峻絶无路可跻步草而徃深弱且滑甚攀条扪萝疲极乃得登四望羣木皆翠杉苍桧凌云千尺与山无穷此龙山胜概之大全也降乃复坐文殊岩下置酒小酌日既入轻烟浮云与暄色防少焉月出寒阴微明散布石上松楸翛然自万壑来客皆悚视寂听觉境愈清思愈逺已而相与言曰世有乐乎此者欤酒醺谈辩蜂起各主其家山为胜如郭主太华刘主兹余主王官五老更嘲迭难不少

    Explanation

    246

    Looking at the peaks, the view opens up, and the rivers become clear. The villages and towns are faint and indistinct, like a chessboard. Wandering for a long time, I climbed into the Western Hall of the Western Temple, where inscriptions were left by a former governor, a magistrate, a transport commissioner, and others like "京叔." Directly ascending the northern ridge, I climbed the An Slope, which is the summit of Long Mountain. The ridge is so steep that there is no path to ascend; I had to climb vines and grasp creepers, exhausted before finally reaching the top. From the summit, I looked around and saw that all the trees were tall and majestic, stretching endlessly into the sky. This is the grandest view of Long Mountain. Descending and sitting again under the Wenshu Rock, I set up wine for a light drink. As the sun set, light smoke and clouds mingled with the warm colors of the sunset, and the moon emerged to cast a faint, cool light on the rocks. The pines and cypresses seemed to come from the myriad valleys, and the guests were struck by the scene, becoming more attentive, feeling the environment becoming clearer and their thoughts more distant. Afterward, they spoke to each other, asking if there was anyone who could enjoy such a place. As the wine warmed them, the conversation became lively, with each person taking turns defending their favorite mountains, with jokes and challenges flying back and forth. Some favored Mount Hua, others the current location, and still others the Five Elders of Wangguan, with laughter and debate continuing without end.

    247

    屈玉峯坐上坐亦怡然一笑诗所谓善戏谑兮不为虐兮者政如是也至二鼓乃归卧东轩明旦复来各有诗识于石迨午饭主僧丈室已乃循岭而东径甚微木甚茂宻仅乃通马行又五里至玉泉寺山势渐颇隘树林渐稀阔顾非龙山比寺西峯曰望景台险甚主僧道客以登厯嵚崟坐盘石其傍诸峯罗列或偃或立或将仆坠或属而合或离而分贾竒献异不一状北望川口最寛肆金城原野分画条列厯厯可数桑干一水纡绕如玦观览旷达此玉泉胜处也从此归路崄不可骑皆步而下重谿复岭愈出愈竒抵暮乃得平地宿李氏山家卧念兹防之富

    247

    Qu Yu Feng sat on his seat and smiled contentedly. As the poem says, "good at jesting but not harmful," it is indeed so. By the time of the second drumbeat, he returned and slept in the eastern pavilion. The next morning, he came again, and each inscribed a poem on a stone. By the time of lunch, he visited the abbot's quarters. Then, following the mountain ridge eastward, he found a path that was very narrow with dense trees, allowing horse travel only then. Another five miles brought him to Yuquan Temple. The mountain terrain gradually became quite narrow, and the forest gradually became sparse and wide, but not comparable to Longshan. The western peak of the temple was called the Viewing Platform, which was very dangerous. The head monk invited the guests to ascend, passing through rugged terrain and sitting on a flat stone beside it. Various peaks were arranged, either lying down, standing, or about to fall over, either connected together or separated apart, displaying oddities and offering strange things in various forms. Looking north at the river mouth, which was the widest and most open, the plains of Jin City were divided into rows, clearly countable. The Sanggan River wound around like a jade ring, offering vast and open viewing. This is the famous place of Yuquan. The returning road from here was dangerous and could not be ridden, so all walked down. Repeated streams and mountain ridges became more and more strange, until evening, finally reaching flat land. He stayed overnight at the Li family's mountain house, laying down and thinking about the richness of this barrier.

    248

    与夫昔所经见而不能寐若太华之雄尊五老之巧秀女几之婉姸乌权白马之端重兹山固无之至于奥宻渊树林荟蔚繁阜不一览而得则兹山亦岂可少哉人之情大抵得于此而遗于彼用于所见而不用于所未见此通患也今中书令湛然公纪西域事称金山之秀李子微贻友书论和林之胜有过于中州者不知天壤间六合之内复有几龙山也因观山于是乎有得徒以文思浅狭且防之亟无以尽发山水之秘异时当同二三友幅巾藜杖于于而行遇佳处辄留更以笔札自随随得随纪庶几兹山之髣髴云己亥七夕后三日王官麻革为之记
    　　寂通居士陈时可秀玉归潜堂铭并序
    　　潜之为言也古之所谓君子者无江海而闲不山林而幽盖藏器待时乐天知命不潜而潜者也吾京叔之文之行有不可掩者而以归潜名所居堂第恐欲潜而不得耳且吾闻之易曰君子之道或出或处或黙或语应处而出非道应出而处亦非道语黙何异哉夫鱼不厌深矣龙徳则不然升潜以其时孔子圣之时者也乃

    Explanation

    248

    As for the sights of the past that could not be forgotten or slept through, such as the grandeur of Mount Hua, the grace of the Five Elders, the elegance of the Nüji Mountains, the dignity of the Uqian and Baima Mountains, this mountain indeed lacks none of these qualities. Its profound beauty and complexity, with its dense forests and abundant flora, cannot be fully appreciated in a single glance. Therefore, this mountain is certainly not to be overlooked. Human nature generally values what it has seen and neglects what it has not seen, using what it has experienced and not what it has not. This is a common failing. Now, the Vice Minister of the Central Secretariat, Mr. Zhanran, has recorded the beauty of the Western Regions, praising the Golden Mountains. Mr. Li Zimic has written a letter to a friend, discussing the beauty of Hulun, which surpasses that of the Central Plains. One wonders how many such mountains exist in the world. Thus, in observing the mountains, I have gained much, but my limited literary talent and the urgency of my duties prevent me from fully capturing the secrets of the mountains. At another time, I will join two or three friends, wearing a simple headband and walking with a staff, and when we encounter a fine spot, we will pause and take notes with our pens, hoping to capture the essence of these mountains. This is the record of the seventh day after the seventh day of the seventh month in the year Jihai, written by Wangguan Ma Ge.

    The Hidden Virtue Hermit, Chen Shike, and the Jade Hall of Retreat, Inscription and Preface

    The word "潜" means hidden. In ancient times, the so-called hidden virtuous men did not seek leisure in the rivers and seas or seclusion in the mountains and forests; they were like hidden treasures waiting for the right time, content with their fate and knowing their destiny. They were not hidden but hidden in their very nature. My uncle, whose writings and conduct are beyond reproach, has named his residence hall "Retreat," perhaps because he desires to be hidden but cannot. I have heard that the Book of Changes says, "The way of the gentleman is to come out or withdraw, to speak or remain silent, according to the situation. To withdraw when one should come out is not the way; to come out when one should withdraw is also not the way. Speaking and silence are not different." A fish does not tire of the depth of the water; the dragon's virtue is different. It rises and sinks according to the time. Confucius was a sage who knew the time.

    249

    所愿则学孔子谓顔渊曰用之则行舍之则藏其论逸民则曰我则异于是无可无不可艮止也圣人彖是卦曰时止则止时行则行动静不失其时其道光明庄周阳挤阴助者也至其举养生之道亦引仲尼曰无入而藏无出而阳柴立其中央岂有吾圣门弟子反转于潜之一字者耶京叔以书求铭老夫吿京叔能勿忘乎谨为铭曰
    　　仲尼驻车蚁立浆宜僚陆沈于其旁夫妻臣妾登屋梁季路徃视渠以亡但见虚室依頽墙古人潜徳不欲出那用此字书其堂况君年甫三十强撑肠拄腹经香文气浑尔诗笔昌户外屦满名飞吾恐自此饶荐章逺来乞铭何可当拈出圣语吾愿长用之则行舍则藏无入而藏出而阳得时思作天际翔勿以深贤庚桑归欤归欤且和光铭哉铭哉幸无忘

    Explanation

    249

    My wish is to emulate Confucius, who said to Yan Hui, "If I am used, I will act; if I am not used, I will hide." In his discussion of recluses, he said, "I am different from them; I can be present or absent as the situation demands." The hexagram "Gèn" (Mountain) in the I Ching symbolizes stillness, and the sage says, "When it is time to stop, stop; when it is time to move, move. Whether in action or in stillness, one does not miss the proper time, and thus the way is bright." Zhuangzi advocates for a balance between active and passive responses to life. Even in his teachings on the art of living, he quotes Confucius, saying, "Do not hide away; do not act rashly. Stand in the center, neither in nor out." How could my disciples of the sage, who follow Confucius's teachings, misunderstand the concept of "latent" (潛)?

    京叔 has asked for an inscription, and I, the old man, tell him, "Can you not forget this?" I respectfully write this inscription:

    Confucius stopped his carriage, and ants stood still as he poured water. Yí Liáo (宜僚) submerged himself in the water nearby. His wife, servants, and attendants climbed onto the roof beams. Zigong (季路) went to see him, but he had already passed away. All that remained was an empty room leaning against a crumbling wall. The ancients' latent virtues did not wish to be revealed. Why use this word to inscribe your hall? Especially since you are just thirty, strong-willed, and well-versed in the classics. Your writing is full of spirit, and your poetry is flourishing. Your fame flies high, and your footsteps are numerous. I fear that from now on, you will be praised in many writings. Far and wide, people come to ask for an inscription. How can I refuse? I will quote the sage's words: "Use me when I am needed, and hide me when I am not. Do not hide away; do not act rashly. Stand in the center, neither in nor out. When the time is right, soar like a bird in the sky. Do not be like Geng Sangzi, who lives in deep seclusion. Return to harmony. Inscription, inscription, may you not forget!"

    诗【案此系祁彚録他人投赠之作而诗首挽诗则又后人所録附】
    　　定庵老人吴章徳明

    Translation:

    Poems [Note: These are collected works of others dedicated to someone, and the first poem is a memorial written by a later person.]

    Ding'an Elder Wu Zhang Deming
    On the city wall, a bird rests, its tail fluttering; returning, it finds the world growing ever higher. Who can share in the lofty mountain and flowing stream? Under the bright moon and clear breeze, virtue is not lonely. Wealth and honor are but temporary to people; literary works illuminate the world and are surely enjoyable. When the temple hall suddenly seeks out the reclusive, one fears that the path of Zhongnan is the way to officialdom.

    Dingzai Recluse Li Xianqing Qin Zhi
    A unique and outstanding man, born with the ambition to travel far and wide. With grand strategies and a powerful bow, his sword is sharp as autumn water. He does not fond of trivial skills, nor does he act like a child or a woman in sorrow. Once indulged in wine in Chang'an market, his slaves are young and inexperienced. He seeks to sweep away the vast wilderness of dragons, crushing the islands of the western desert. He adjusts the golden cauldron for non-action, sitting by the Phoenix Pool, counting the years since the fall of the Li and Yue families. The world has lacked rituals and music for two hundred years, and he strives to emulate the three preceding dynasties. The auspicious birth of leaves and the dance of Tang flourish, making a measure of rice cost three or four coins. Who would have thought the heavens and earth would suddenly overturn, the vast sea surging and engulfing the flat land? Like fierce fire burning Kunshan, who can distinguish between a worthless stone and a true jade? What use is one's lifetime achievements? He takes his family and walks directly to the outskirts of Nan Mountain, wearing coarse clothes and eating simple food, mixing with fishermen. Having enough for wife and children, always happy and content. A few thatched cottages with a gate facing the water, spending all his time in writing. Sometimes looking up and down in the dust, the chaos of war is like ants fighting. The vast universe is truly a post station, one only feels the light of the heavens shining through a fixed universe. The trivial wealth and honor of the world, how different is it from a wasp and a caterpillar?

    A Collection of Sentences by Bai Hua from Hedong

    Heaven has not yet grown weary of the character "jin" (gold), and on the pond, there are still phoenix feathers today. Those with talent refuse to seek recognition or patronage, instead choosing to live in the mountains and forests, truly proud of their decision. Their clothes are as ragged as a sparrow's, and their horse as old as a dog. Wild vegetables fill their plates, and they might grow tired of eating them. They laugh loudly and leave, carefree and unburdened. In the spring breeze, they gather with friends over a cup of wine among peach and plum blossoms. High-ranking officials, historians, and secretaries of state, they wait for the morning bell, their boots covered in frost. How can one compare someone who has nothing but the bare necessities? Drunkenly, they walk through fallen flowers, leaving a trail of their scent. It is particularly difficult to find truly exceptional people in the present day. Life is like floating clouds and willow catkins, without a stable foundation. There is no need to struggle to achieve success, as it is often futile. Fish thrive in the cold, sandy waters.

    Xigang, Lü Dapeng, the one who soars

    The world is chaotic, and life is short and flickering like the light of a candle. Who can escape their fate? Even in one's hometown, it is inevitable. The fresh air and scenery fill the morning hunger, and the sound of ice cracking in the night creates a cold atmosphere. Is there solitude in the hall? There is enough leisure time with family members.

    太原元好问裕之
    　　南山老桂几枝分翰墨风流属两君共説人间似歆向争教茅屋着机云备尝险阻聊乗化力战纷华又策勋却恐声光埋不得皇天久矣付斯文

    Translation:

    Yuan Haowen of Taiyuan
    　　The old osmanthus trees of Mount Nanshan, with their branches divided by the brush and ink, belong to the two of you. Together they speak of the world as if it were Xun and Yang. Who would teach a thatched cottage to wear the clouds of a writing desk? Having experienced many dangers, they now accept transformation. Struggling against the world's distractions and achieving success, yet fearing that their fame and glory will not be buried. The Heavenly Emperor has long entrusted this culture.
    　　Wang Guan and Ma Ge
    　　Escaping to the deep waters, avoiding the arrows of the hunter, flying into the darkness. Since ancient times, the wise and virtuous have also sung about Picking the Wild Herbs. The ancestral houses on Mount Nanshan are in the midst of war. Missing the separation, the mountain is empty and no one lives there. Only seeing the lush vegetation. Gracefully, a thousand-year-old crane returns in a single day. Newly built near the muddy water, the path is protected by the clear stream, ringing out in front of the steps. White clouds enter the morning door, turning back, the mountains and valleys have changed, everything has suddenly become different. Writing books that delve into profound truths, obtaining sentences that exhaust the mysteries of heaven. The road ahead is naturally pressing, but this path still has some hope. Diligently holding the central jade, striving to retain the remaining light. But fearing that the desire to escape the world will still be criticized for practicing seclusion. Forever remembering, on the ancient stone, sharing a cup with you. Regretting the lack of soaring wings to fly far, not what is desired.
    　　Again,
    　　The dust of the world, endlessly soiling the traveler's robe. A hall that has lasted for a thousand years, entering the depths of seclusion. No noise of carriages and horses, no clouds greeting the door, only the quiet of the zither and books, the moon hanging from the eaves. The muddy water is clear and cold, passing through the bamboo, the green of Mount Nanshan merging with the sky. Far away, knowing the same singing and shouting, my brother in the clouds has new poems written on the walls.
    　　Ying Cui
    　　The two Lu's returning, finding true joy. A hall where the reclusive live, quiet and dust-free. Poetry and books are sufficient to teach young children. Cooking chicken and rice can still labor the old friend. The cool pine wind through three paths in the evening. The light rain fills the city with spring. Because of you, I realize my own clumsiness in my travels. Again, being tied to the floating reputation of this body.

    东城李微子微
    　　沧海成田后携家返故乡披蓁寻旧址借力搆新堂山给扉翠泉供枕簟凉故田依浑水别业胜淮阳侍御遗风在南山庆长芝兰宜并秀鸿雁自成行经史胸中业龙蛇笔下章行当依日月宁久事耕桑尚父终辞渭阿衡定佐商飞潜无定迹易道个中藏

    　　犇走红尘二十年归来防破净名禅忙开菊径成嘉遯静闭柴门草太千嶂云岚真辋谷一车风月小壶天旱时用商岩雨应遍齐州九防烟

    East City Li Weiziqi
    After the sea turned into fields, he returned to his hometown with his family. He cleared the underbrush to find the old site and used his strength to build a new hall. The mountains provided doors, and the green springs supplied cool bedding. The old fields relied on the Huainan River, and the secluded estate surpassed Huoyang, where the legacy of the imperial officials remained. In the southern mountains, he found joy in the long-lasting fragrance of orchids and lilies, which should flourish together. The geese formed their own lines, and his knowledge of classics and history was his profession. His writing, like dragons and snakes, flowed from his pen, and he should follow the path of the sun and moon rather than tilling the land for long. Jiang Ziya ultimately left the Wei River, and Shang Tang's advisor was destined to assist the Shang Dynasty. Flying and diving creatures have no fixed paths, and the principles of change are hidden within.

    析津 Li Weiyin Shunchen
    In the midst of vast wars, I sympathize with you for finding a place to settle. The clouds and mists of autumn make the bamboo mat cold, and the moon sets at night, leaving nothing but the years in a cup. My life is filled with books on the table, and there is true interest in the depths of my mind. I also love my humble abode, where the mind is far away and the heart is distant. When people are idle, things become quiet and secluded. Fame and wealth are truly worthless, like floating bubbles. Wild birds follow the noise and silence, and the mountain clouds come and go as they please. Outside a cup of cloudy wine, all matters are left to rest.

    蒲城 Xue Yuanweizhi
    Building a humble thatched hall to nurture the true way, he set aside mundane affairs that were full of complications. At night, he fished by the Panchi River, watching the moon in the center of the waves. In the spring, he tilled the fields in the Fen River valley, surrounded by clouds on the ridges. He laughed at the labor of bears and boars in dreams and would not let apes and monkeys resent the relocation of their habitat. He newly learned methods for achieving peace of mind, and the sound of wind through pine trees in the mountains reached his pillow.

    For twenty years, he rushed through the red dust of the world. Returning home, he broke through the Pure Land Zen, busy opening a path lined with chrysanthemums, forming a noble retreat. He quietly closed the wooden door, surrounded by the Tai Xuan Jing (Book of Supreme Mystery). The clouds and mists of a thousand peaks were real, and a cartload of wind and moonlight filled a small heavenly realm. In times of drought, he used the rain from the Shang River, which should spread throughout the nine barriers of Qizhou.

    254

    故山泉石栖迟纬国才名恐四驰节信情髙方著论渊明心逺更能诗素琴黄卷真余乐明月清风忽老时只恐葛龙潜不定一声雷雨跃天池
    　　金城兰光庭仲文
    　　几年踪迹寄兵尘且喜归家见在身满眼云山犹可一庭松筠未全贫定惭巧宦卢藏用却爱成名郑子真秖恐池中非久处伫看雷雨起天津
    　　渔阳赵着光祖
    　　万里烟埃气尚炎秋风携手赋归潜当时北望长劳梦今日南山副具瞻鸿雁不飞闲伴月鹡鸰无语静依檐遥思二陆犹如此自愧区区未属厌
    　　河东张纬纬文
    　　结庐髙谢尘埃浩气都从道学来北阙云烟无梦到南山草木觉春回四时风月供吟笔万古乾坤入酒杯却恐汉庭须羽翼书未许老岩隈
    　　太原髙鸣雄飞
    　　髙情谢氛壒归南山隈頽然一茅屋潇洒无纤埃胜概纷满前懐抱长好开舒啸野云乱浩歌空翠来瑶花晚夕静相对挥清杯天虚风露下幽兴何悠哉回首区中人扰扰良可哀

    Explanation

    254

    In the mountains, by the springs and stones, I have lived in seclusion, yet my talents and reputation may spread far and wide. With high moral integrity, I have written on important matters, following the example of Tao Yuanming, who found joy in simplicity and poetry. The simple zither and yellow scrolls are true joys, and the moon and clear winds pass by as if time has flown. I fear the hidden dragon may leap out with a sudden storm, and the sky pool may be disturbed.

    Jin Cheng Lan Guangting, courtesy name Zhongwen:
    For many years, my life has been entangled in military affairs, but I am glad to return home and find myself still alive. The mountains and clouds fill my eyes, and a courtyard of pine and bamboo is not entirely poor. I am ashamed of my cunning official career, but I love the fame of Zheng Zhen. I fear that I will not stay long in the pond, waiting for the thunderstorm to rise in Tianjin.

    Yuanyang Zhao Zheguang, courtesy name Guangzu:
    The smoke and dust of a thousand miles still burn with heat. In the autumn wind, we hold hands and compose poems of retreat. When I looked north in the past, I was always troubled by dreams. Today, I look at the south mountain with a secondary view. The wild geese do not fly, idly accompanying the moon, and the sparrow does not speak, quietly resting on the eaves. I think of the two Lus, and I am ashamed of my trivial self, not yet tired of the world.

    Hedong Zhang Wei, courtesy name Weiwen:
    I have built a thatched hut high to avoid the dust, and my grand spirit comes from the study of the Way. The clouds and smoke of the northern gate are not in my dreams, and the grass and trees of the south mountain feel the return of spring. The four seasons' winds and moons provide inspiration for writing, and the eternal universe enters the wine cup. I fear that the Han court will need wings, and I am not allowed to grow old in the rocky corners.

    Taiyuan Gao Ming, courtesy name Xiongfeng:
    With a lofty spirit, I retreat from the world to the south mountain, living in a humble thatched hut, free from the slightest dust. The wonderful sights fill my embrace, and I am always open-hearted. I let out a long sigh amidst the wild clouds, and I sing loudly amidst the greenery. In the evening, the jade flowers are still, and we drink clear cups together. Under the clear sky, the dew and wind fall, and the hidden pleasures are endless. I look back at the chaotic world, and I find it truly pitiable.

    255

    黄鹄入寥廓龙性何能驯英英刘处士天子不得臣卧老草堂月吟尽南山春野饭足藜藿幽兰充佩纫一杯石上酒静见天地春万虑此都寂孰知名与身灵运卧岩幽子陵钓渚滨神超物不违异世等达人我无豹姿亦欲事沦空歌紫芝曲早晚由东邻
    　　邢台刘徳渊道
    　　南国堂堂二鳯雏年来归旧茅庐四围山水境何胜一室琴书乐有余长啸松林月明夜行吟菜圃雨晴初荒芜庭院人休诮天下终期一扫除
    　　洺水刘肃才卿
    　　屠龙破千金梦觉人已非二陆不可作故山归采薇江湖鸿雁乐原隰鹡鸰飞惆怅朱门客思归不得归
    　　龙江张仲经
    　　羸短仆行夷犹西京才子云二刘荒山穷僻厌岑寂长裾遍谒东诸侯手中虽无丈八矛胸蟠河图与天球有时吐出作灵瑞坐令宇县还殷周忆昨长鲸吞古汴千里还家异乡县筑堂故址号归潜要使新诗走羣彦方今河朔藩镇雄衣冠徃徃罗其中两贤胡为独不出埋光彩为冥鸿朝亦潜暮亦潜东山不起吾何瞻山中为问谁相识白鸟孤云自入

    Explanation

    255

    The Crane Enters the Vast Sky; The Dragon's Nature Cannot Be Tamed. The Brilliant Liu Chushi, the Emperor Cannot Make Him His Subject. He Lies in His Thatched Hut by Moonlight, Singing the Spring of South Mountain to His Heart's Content. His Wild Diet Consists of Coarse Vegetables, and Fragrant Orchids Adorn His Belt. A Cup of Wine on the Stone, He Sees the Spring of Heaven and Earth in Stillness. All Worries Are Forgotten in This Silence. Who Understands Fame and the Self? Lingyun Lies in the Secluded Rock, and Zilin Fishes by the Shore. His Spirit Transcends the World Without Violating It; He Is Equal to the Wise of Other Ages. I Lack the Noble Demeanor of the Black Leopard, Yet I Wish to Live a Life of Seclusion. I Sing the Purple Mushroom Song, Hoping to Visit My Neighbor Soon.

    　　Liu Deyuan of Xingtai
    　　The Two Phoenix Chicks of the South Land Have Returned to Their Old Thatched Hut. The Surrounding Mountains and Waters Are Beyond Compare; A Single Room Filled with the Joy of Music and Books Is More Than Enough. He Longs in the Moonlit Pine Forest at Night, Walking and Reciting in the Vegetable Garden After the First Rain. Do Not Mock the Wastelanded Courtyard; One Day, the World Will Be Cleaned Up.

    　　Liu Su Caiqing of Ming Shui
    　　The Dream of Slaying the Dragon and Breaking Thousand Golds Awakens, but the Person Is No Longer the Same. The Two Lus Cannot Be Made; Returning to the Mountains, He Picks Wild Vetch. The Joy of the Wild Geese on the Lake, the Flight of the Skylark in the Plain, Lamenting the Guest of the Red Gate, Who Thinks of Returning but Cannot.

    　　Zhang Zhongjing of Longjiang
    　　A Weak and Short Servant Walks with Deliberation. The Talented Scholar of the Western Capital, the Two Lus, Are Tired of the Remote and Desolate Mountains, Bored by the Solitude. Their Long Robes Traverse the Eastern Princes, Though They Lack the Eight-Foot Spear, Their Minds Hold the River Chart and the Celestial Sphere. Sometimes They Emerge as Auspicious Signs, Making the Universe Prosperous Again. Remembering the Past When the Long Whale Swallowed the Ancient Bian, Returning Home After a Thousand Miles in a Foreign Land. Building a Hall on the Old Site, Naming It "Return to Seclusion," Hoping to Make New Poems Walk Among the Wise. Now the Factions of the River North Are Powerful, Their Attire Often Crowded in Their Midst. Why Do the Two Sages Not Come Out? Hiding Their Light and Color as Dark Geese, Hiding in the Morning and Evening. The East Mountain Does Not Rise, What Do I Look At? In the Mountains, Who Do I Know? White Birds and Lonely Clouds Enter the Void.

    256

    燕山张师鲁明道
    　　岐路荆榛万里夷丈夫出处不磷缁莫夸荀氏八龙集且羡陆家双鳯仪尘世浪随春夏改寸心惟有神知蒲团泽几炉烟静卧聼黄庭乐圣基
    　　东明张特立文举
    　　陵迁谷变海波翻筑室渠能返故村夜雨对牀闲练句春风满座共开樽却无北阙功名想且喜南山气象存才大到头潜不得已华萼出蓬门
    　　山东勾龙瀛英孺
    　　世路艰难已饱经归来一室晦虚名任他沧海掀天恶喜我南山照眼明云气冷侵吟砚润棣华香泛酒杯清故园未遂归休志惭愧刘家好弟兄
    　　追挽归潜刘先生　　　　　　　王　恽
    　　我自髧髦屡拜公执经亲为发颛防道从伊洛传心事文擅韩欧振古风四海南山青未了一丘洹水恨何穷然不为山阳笛老屋吟看落月空
    　　归潜志卷十四

    256

    燕山的张师鲁明道
    　　在崎岖的道路上，面对着万里的异国，真正的男子汉无论身处何地都能保持内心的纯洁，不要夸耀荀氏八龙的集会，而羡慕陆家双凤的仪态。尘世的生活随春夏更替而变化，但内心深处只有鬼神才能知晓。蒲团上几炉烟静静地燃烧，我静静地卧听黄庭乐的圣基。
    　　东明的张特立文举
    　　陵墓变迁，山谷改变，海波翻滚，筑室之人能否返回故乡？夜雨中对着床铺闲练诗句，春风中满座共开酒樽，却无北阙的功名之想，且喜南山的气象依然存在。才华横溢之人最终潜心隐居，不得已将华萼传出自蓬门。
    　　山东的勾龙瀛英孺
    　　世路艰难已饱经风霜，归来一室，晦暗虚名。任凭沧海掀起天大的恶浪，我喜南山的光明照耀着我。云气冷侵吟砚润，棣华香泛酒杯清，故园未遂归休志，惭愧刘家好弟兄。
    　　追挽归潜刘先生　　　　　　　王　恽
    　　我自幼多次拜见公，亲自执经为他发颛防，道从伊洛传心事，文擅韩欧振古风。四海南山青未了，一丘洹水恨何穷，然不为山阳笛，老屋吟看落月空。
    　　归潜志卷十四
